# fix-list.md — G13–G21 specialist + red-team fan-out (2026-05-16)

Appended from parallel specialist fan-out (8 specialists per slice excluding `comment-analyzer` and `code-simplifier` per user) + Claude red-team per slice, across batches **G13–G21** (PRs #55–#83). Each agent verified findings against current `main` before reporting.

**Severity thresholds applied:** all `critical` · `high` confidence ≥ 7 · `medium` confidence ≥ 8 · `low` confidence ≥ 9.

**Excluded specialists:** `comment-analyzer`, `code-simplifier` (per user request).

## G13 — PR #55 — Sprint 4 Intelligence Layer + Bridge V1

### CRITICAL (4)

#### G13-001 · _generate_alerts Sprint 4 alert rules (regime_shift, underperformance, concentration_creep) entirely untested
- **File**: `analytics-service/routers/portfolio.py:400`
- **Specialist**: `pr-test-analyzer` (confidence 10)
- **Summary**: The three new alert rules added in this PR — regime_shift (lines 400-431), underperformance (lines 433-456), concentration_creep (lines 458-471) — each compute non-trivial thresholds (rolling correlation delta > 0.15, vol-band trailing distance with second-place gap >= 0.005, weight_pct >= 1.5x equal-weight baseline). These are ALERT GENERATION rules — false positives spam users, false negatives miss intelligence-layer signals which is the entire selling point of Sprint 4. test_portfolio_router_logic.py::TestGenerateAlerts was only updated for the mock plumbing (select-then-insert), not for the 3 new rule branches. A regression that changes the 0.15 threshold to 0.015, swaps the sign on best_recent > best_prior in the direction computation, or drops the second-place gap guard would never be caught — the dedup-mock-fix masquerades as test coverage for the new logic.
- **Evidence**: `grep -rn 'regime_shift\|concentration_creep\|alert_type.*underperformance' analytics-service/tests/` returns zero matches inside test bodies (only file comments). Production code present in analytics-service/routers/portfolio.py:400-471.
- **Fix**: Append to analytics-service/tests/test_portfolio_router_logic.py::TestGenerateAlerts: test_regime_shift_fires_when_rolling_corr_delta_exceeds_015 (build rolling_corr={'s1-s2':[{'value':0.2}]*5+[{'value':0.5}]*5}, assert insert called with alert_type='regime_shift' and direction='tightened'); test_regime_shift_skipped_below_threshold (delta=0.10, assert no insert); test_underperformance_fires_when_worst_trails_by_more_than_band (attribution with worst contribution -0.05 and second -0.04 gap >=0.005, risk_decomp with vol_band=0.01, assert alert_type='underperformance'); test_underperformance_suppressed_when_second_place_too_close (gap < 0.005, assert no insert); test_concentration_creep_fires_when_top_weight_exceeds_15x_equal (risk_decomp 3 strategies with top weight_pct=55, equal_weight=33, assert alert_type='concentration_creep'); test_concentration_creep_skipped_with_only_2_strategies (len<3, assert no insert).

#### G13-002 · Bare `except Exception: pass` silently drops monthly_returns from narrative
- **File**: `analytics-service/routers/portfolio.py:281`
- **Specialist**: `silent-failure-hunter` (confidence 9)
- **Summary**: The monthly_returns build block catches ALL exceptions with no logging — `except Exception: pass # Monthly breakdown is best-effort`. Any failure (date parsing bug, missing portfolio_returns_series, KeyError, ZeroDivisionError, schema drift on `d.year`/`d.month`) silently drops the entire monthly breakdown from the persisted narrative. Operators get zero signal: no log line, no Sentry event, no metric. The MorningBriefing UI quietly omits the 'Monthly breakdown' section and users never know whether the monthly data is unavailable because it failed or because they have a new portfolio. This is exactly the debug-nightmare class the project bans.
- **Evidence**: analytics-service/routers/portfolio.py:269-282 — `try: ... monthly_returns[year_str][month_str] *= (1 + float(v)) ... analytics_payload['monthly_returns'] = monthly_returns\n        except Exception:\n            pass  # Monthly breakdown is best-effort`
- **Fix**: Narrow the catch to expected types (e.g. `except (AttributeError, ValueError, TypeError, ZeroDivisionError) as exc:`) AND emit `logger.warning('monthly_returns build failed for %s: %s', portfolio_id, exc, exc_info=True)` so failures surface in logs/Sentry. Re-raise unexpected errors so they're not hidden.

#### G13-003 · Bare `except Exception: pass` silently drops optimizer suggestions from narrative
- **File**: `analytics-service/routers/portfolio.py:293`
- **Specialist**: `silent-failure-hunter` (confidence 9)
- **Summary**: The optimizer_suggestions fetch wraps a Supabase SELECT in `try: ... except Exception: pass # Optimizer sentence is best-effort`. Any Supabase failure (transient network, RLS misconfig, schema drift in the `optimizer_suggestions` JSONB column) is swallowed with no log line. The 'If you trim ... expected Sharpe moves from X to Y' recommendation simply vanishes from the narrative with no operator signal. Worse, this catches programming errors like AttributeError on `.data[0].get(...)` if the table shape ever changes — masking real bugs as 'no suggestions available'.
- **Evidence**: analytics-service/routers/portfolio.py:285-294 — `try:\n            prev_analytics = supabase.table('portfolio_analytics').select('optimizer_suggestions')...execute()\n            if prev_analytics.data and prev_analytics.data[0].get('optimizer_suggestions'):\n                analytics_payload['optimizer_suggestions'] = ...\n        except Exception:\n            pass  # Optimizer sentence is best-effort`
- **Fix**: At minimum add `logger.warning('optimizer_suggestions fetch failed for %s: %s', portfolio_id, exc, exc_info=True)`. Catch only the specific Supabase exception types (`PostgrestAPIError`, `httpx.HTTPError`) rather than bare Exception so programming bugs (IndexError, AttributeError) bubble up.

#### G13-004 · POST /api/bridge has zero tests — all 7 branches (CSRF, auth, rate-limit, JSON, validation, ownership, scoring) untested
- **File**: `src/app/api/bridge/route.ts:7`
- **Specialist**: `pr-test-analyzer` (confidence 10)
- **Summary**: The bridge POST route handler ships with NO sibling route.test.ts. The handler has seven distinct branches that each gate access to a compute-intensive Python service: (1) CSRF rejection, (2) 401 unauthorized, (3) 429 rate-limit, (4) 400 invalid JSON, (5) 400 missing fields, (6) 404 portfolio not owned by user, (7) 500 on scoring failure plus the happy path. The ownership check at lines 44-49 is the ONLY guard preventing a logged-in user from triggering bridge scoring (and reading candidate strategy data) against another tenant's portfolio_id; the Python service uses a service-role client that bypasses RLS. A regression that flips .eq('user_id', user.id) into .or() or accidentally drops the .eq() would silently leak cross-tenant scoring and rate-limit-budget consumption. Other route.test.ts siblings in this PR family (api/bridge/outcome/route.test.ts, api/bridge/outcome/dismiss/route.test.ts, api/bridge/outcome/[id]/curves/route.test.ts) prove the test pattern exists.
- **Evidence**: `find src/app/api/bridge -name '*.test.ts*'` returns only the outcome/* siblings, never route.test.ts; `grep -rn '/api/bridge[^/]' src/ --include='*.test.ts*'` returns zero references to the new POST endpoint. Production code present at src/app/api/bridge/route.ts:7-68.
- **Fix**: Create src/app/api/bridge/route.test.ts mirroring src/app/api/bridge/outcome/route.test.ts. Describe block 'POST /api/bridge' with: (a) 'rejects when CSRF Origin missing → 403', (b) 'rejects when unauthenticated → 401', (c) 'returns 429 when rate-limited', (d) 'returns 400 on invalid JSON body', (e) 'returns 400 when portfolio_id or underperformer_strategy_id is missing', (f) 'returns 404 when user does not own the portfolio_id (cross-tenant attempt)' — assert .from("portfolios").select with both .eq('id', body.portfolio_id) AND .eq('user_id', session.user.id), (g) 'returns 500 with err.message when findReplacementCandidates throws', (h) 'returns JSON with candidates array on success'. Mock createClient, assertSameOrigin, checkLimit, findReplacementCandidates.

### HIGH (21)

#### G13-005 · WidgetProps.data: any erases all type safety on widget dataflow
- **File**: `/Users/helios-mammut/claude-projects/quantalyze/src/app/(dashboard)/allocations/lib/types.ts:80`
- **Specialist**: `type-design-analyzer` (confidence 9)
- **Summary**: WidgetProps.data is typed as `any` (with an eslint-disable). Every widget component (MorningBriefing, PortfolioAlerts, ConcentrationRisk, RegimeDetector, AllocationDonut, CorrelationMatrix, etc.) consumes this shape and reaches into it via `data?.analytics?.narrative_summary`, `data?.alertCount`, `data?.analytics?.total_aum` with zero compile-time guarantees. The Sprint-4 diff added a brand new field consumer (MorningBriefing.tsx:54 `data?.analytics?.narrative_summary`) under this `any` umbrella, and a sibling widget (PortfolioAlerts.tsx:21) duplicates a locally-defined `AlertCount` interface that should live alongside the producing payload type. A typo in any field name, a Python writer shape drift, or a producer-side rename will compile cleanly and render undefined silently — exactly the bug class this batch's contract (BridgeResponseSchema, etc.) was designed to prevent on the network boundary while letting the in-process props boundary stay wide open.
- **Evidence**: src/app/(dashboard)/allocations/lib/types.ts:78-84 `export interface WidgetProps { // eslint-disable-next-line @typescript-eslint/no-explicit-any\n  data: any;\n  timeframe: string; ... }`; consumers in src/app/(dashboard)/allocations/widgets/intelligence/MorningBriefing.tsx:52-54 `export function MorningBriefing({ data }: WidgetProps) { const narrative: string | null | undefined = data?.analytics?.narrative_summary;`
- **Fix**: Replace `data: any` with a discriminated payload union (e.g. `WidgetPayload`) or a generic `WidgetProps<TPayload>` where each widget declares the slice it reads. At minimum, define `interface WidgetPayload { analytics: PortfolioAnalytics | null; alertCount: AlertCount | null; metrics: ComputedMetrics; ... }` (mirroring the `data` object constructed in AllocationDashboard.useMemo) and use it as the default. Move the duplicated `AlertCount` from PortfolioAlerts.tsx and AllocationDashboard.tsx into a single source (src/lib/types.ts) and reference it from the payload type. This makes every widget reader checked against the producer and reuses the contract pattern the team already adopted for analytics-schemas.ts.

#### G13-006 · computePortfolioHealthScore conflates null with optimal value, producing false 'Healthy' for empty portfolios
- **File**: `/Users/helios-mammut/claude-projects/quantalyze/src/lib/health-score.ts:146`
- **Specialist**: `type-design-analyzer` (confidence 9)
- **Summary**: PortfolioAnalytics fields portfolio_max_drawdown and avg_pairwise_correlation are `number | null` (deliberately nullable for pending/empty portfolios). computePortfolioHealthScore coerces nulls to 0 with the `?? 0` pattern, then runs them through scaleComponent — and the inverted math makes 0 the BEST possible value. A portfolio with no drawdown data (null) gets 25/25 on the drawdown axis; null correlation also yields 25/25. Combined with the unconditional 20-pt CAPACITY_PLACEHOLDER, a brand-new or analytics-pending portfolio scores 70 = HEALTHY. The KpiStrip then renders a green badge over a portfolio that has no data, telling the allocator the portfolio is healthy when in fact nothing has been computed. The invariant the type design needed — 'health requires data presence' — is not encoded; the type allows null, the consumer treats null as max.
- **Evidence**: src/lib/health-score.ts:146 `const ddAbs = Math.abs(analytics.portfolio_max_drawdown ?? 0);` → 0.30 - 0 = 0.30 ≥ max(0.30) → 25 pts; line 151 `const corrRaw = analytics.avg_pairwise_correlation ?? 0;` → 0.8 - 0 = 0.8 > max(0.7) → 25 pts. Worked example: all-null analytics ⇒ 0 sharpe + 25 dd + 25 corr + 20 capacity = 70 ≥ HEALTH_THRESHOLD_HEALTHY → label='Healthy' (lines 158-163).
- **Fix**: Return `PortfolioHealthScore | null` when any required component is null (already supported by the return type union), or scale each null component to 0 explicitly: `const drawdown = analytics.portfolio_max_drawdown == null ? 0 : scaleComponent(0.30 - Math.abs(analytics.portfolio_max_drawdown), 0, 0.30);`. Better still, encode 'health requires X data' in the type by accepting a narrowed `Required<Pick<PortfolioAnalytics, 'portfolio_sharpe' | 'portfolio_max_drawdown' | 'avg_pairwise_correlation'>>` and lifting the null-check to the caller, so the function body cannot misinterpret missing data.

#### G13-007 · PortfolioInsight + BridgeTrigger contract enforced only by runtime guard + non-null assertion, not discriminated union
- **File**: `/Users/helios-mammut/claude-projects/quantalyze/src/lib/portfolio-insights.ts:19`
- **Specialist**: `type-design-analyzer` (confidence 8)
- **Summary**: PortfolioInsight declares strategy_id/strategy_name as `string | null | undefined` for ALL insight variants. BridgeTrigger requires a non-null strategy_id, enforced at runtime by isBridgeable() in InsightStrip and then peeled off with `insight.strategy_id!` non-null assertion in BridgeTrigger.tsx:61. Any caller that constructs a PortfolioInsight with key='underperformance' but no strategy_id, or that wraps a BridgeTrigger without going through isBridgeable, will pass type-check and crash at runtime when the non-null assertion is wrong. The bridgeable-vs-non-bridgeable invariant is a structural property of the insight type that should be encoded as a discriminated union (e.g. `BridgeableInsight extends PortfolioInsight { key: 'underperformance' | 'biggest_risk_concentration' | 'concentration_creep' | 'rebalance_drift'; strategy_id: string; strategy_name: string }`).
- **Evidence**: src/lib/portfolio-insights.ts:19-35 `export interface PortfolioInsight { key: ...; severity: ...; sentence: string; strategy_id?: string | null; strategy_name?: string | null; }`; src/components/portfolio/BridgeTrigger.tsx:61 `strategyId={insight.strategy_id!}` paired with src/components/portfolio/InsightStrip.tsx:65-71 `function isBridgeable(insight, portfolioId) { return insight.key === 'underperformance' && !!insight.strategy_id && !!portfolioId; }`.
- **Fix**: Convert PortfolioInsight to a discriminated union: a `BridgeableInsight` variant for keys that target a specific strategy (with REQUIRED strategy_id and strategy_name), and a `PortfolioWideInsight` variant for the rest. BridgeTrigger.tsx then takes `insight: BridgeableInsight` and the non-null assertion goes away; `isBridgeable` becomes a type predicate `(i: PortfolioInsight): i is BridgeableInsight` that narrows at the call site.

#### G13-008 · Bridge endpoint pulls unbounded published strategies + returns_series JSONB
- **File**: `analytics-service/routers/portfolio.py:858`
- **Specialist**: `performance` (confidence 8)
- **Summary**: Two queries fetch all published strategies (no LIMIT, no pagination) and then `strategy_analytics.in_(candidate_ids)` pulls the full `returns_series` JSONB for every one. Each `returns_series` is hundreds of date/value records. As the platform grows (10s -> 100s -> 1000s of published strategies) this becomes a multi-megabyte payload per Bridge call. Rate limit is 10/hour/user but Fluid Compute charges Active CPU + memory: parsing/holding all returns_series in pandas inflates request peak memory linearly with strategy count.
- **Evidence**: analytics-service/routers/portfolio.py:857-870 — `all_published = supabase.table("strategies").select("id, name").eq("status","published").not_.in_("id", strategy_ids).execute()` then `sa_cand_result = supabase.table("strategy_analytics").select("strategy_id, returns_series").in_("strategy_id", candidate_ids).execute()` — no `.limit()`, no chunking.
- **Fix**: Cap candidates with `.limit(50)` after ordering by a quality proxy (sharpe DESC), or split into a two-pass: first fetch only `id, name` + a cheap pre-filter column (e.g., sharpe), keep top-N by sharpe, then fetch returns_series only for the survivors.

#### G13-009 · O(N) select-then-insert loop in _generate_alerts replaces single batch insert
- **File**: `analytics-service/routers/portfolio.py:479`
- **Specialist**: `performance` (confidence 8)
- **Summary**: `_generate_alerts` runs once per portfolio recompute (cron-driven across every portfolio). For each of up to 5 alert types (drawdown, correlation_spike, regime_shift, underperformance, concentration_creep) it does SELECT then INSERT — 2 PostgREST round trips per type, up to 10 round trips per portfolio compute. PR #55 explicitly traded the prior single batch insert for this pattern. With 100 portfolios on the cron, that is up to 1000 PostgREST round trips per cron sweep just for alert generation.
- **Evidence**: analytics-service/routers/portfolio.py:479-495 — `for alert in alerts: existing = supabase.table("portfolio_alerts").select("id").eq(...).is_("acknowledged_at","null").limit(1).execute(); if existing.data: continue; supabase.table("portfolio_alerts").insert(alert).execute()`
- **Fix**: The partial unique index `portfolio_alerts_dedup_unacked` (migration 042) already gives DB-level dedup. Use a single batch INSERT ... ON CONFLICT DO NOTHING via PostgREST's `prefer: resolution=ignore-duplicates` header (supported on supabase-py's `upsert(..., ignore_duplicates=True, on_conflict="portfolio_id,alert_type")` against the unique index). One round trip instead of 10.

#### G13-010 · portfolio_bridge router endpoint has no integration test for ownership / no-candidate / no-returns gates
- **File**: `analytics-service/routers/portfolio.py:795`
- **Specialist**: `pr-test-analyzer` (confidence 9)
- **Summary**: The Python /api/portfolio-bridge endpoint (lines 798-893) is reachable from the Next.js bridge route and is the second layer of defense-in-depth ownership checks (.eq('user_id', req.user_id)). It also gates on (1) underperformer is in the portfolio, (2) returns data exists, (3) at least one published candidate exists. test_bridge_scoring.py covers the SCORING function only (find_replacement_candidates) — it does NOT exercise the router which is where the security-sensitive ownership/membership checks live. Only an AST-based audit-emission structural test (test_routers_audit_emission_structure.py) inspects this endpoint. A regression that drops .eq('user_id', req.user_id) on line 814 silently turns the service into a service-role-bypass tool that any authenticated caller can use to score any portfolio.
- **Evidence**: `grep -rn '/portfolio-bridge\|portfolio_bridge\|underperformer' analytics-service/tests/ --include='*.py'` returns only AST structural emission tests (test_routers_audit_emission_structure.py:114-144) and the unit-level bridge_scoring tests. No FastAPI TestClient invocation against the endpoint. Production code in analytics-service/routers/portfolio.py:795-905.
- **Fix**: Add analytics-service/tests/test_portfolio_bridge_router.py mirroring the pattern used by other router integration tests. class TestPortfolioBridgeEndpoint with FastAPI TestClient and Supabase mock: test_404_when_portfolio_user_id_mismatch (mock .eq('id').eq('user_id').single() returns data=None, assert 404); test_400_when_underperformer_not_in_portfolio (portfolio_strategies returns no row matching underperformer_strategy_id, assert 400); test_400_when_no_returns_data (strategy_analytics.in_ returns empty, assert 400); test_returns_empty_candidates_when_no_published_candidates (strategies.eq('status','published') returns empty, assert 200 with candidates=[]); test_hydrates_strategy_name_from_strategies_table (assert each candidate has strategy_name from candidate_names map); test_excludes_portfolio_members_from_candidates (assert .not_.in_('id', strategy_ids) invoked).

#### G13-011 · Alert dedup logic (select-then-insert per type) tested only via mock plumbing, never the dedup decision
- **File**: `analytics-service/routers/portfolio.py:480`
- **Specialist**: `pr-test-analyzer` (confidence 9)
- **Summary**: The new dedup loop (portfolio.py:480-499) replaces the broken batched upsert with: for each alert, SELECT existing unacknowledged of same type, skip if found, else INSERT. The accompanying test changes in test_portfolio_router_logic.py only updated the mock to return data=[] by default — they NEVER set existing data=[{...}] to verify the skip-when-existing branch fires. A regression that drops the `if existing.data: continue` check (or inverts it to `if not existing.data: continue`) would create infinite duplicate alerts of the same type. This is the entire reason migration 042's partial unique index exists; the application-level dedup is the first line and a regression there would slam the DB constraint and surface as generic insert errors.
- **Evidence**: `grep -n 'existing.data\|skip.*existing' analytics-service/tests/test_portfolio_router_logic.py` returns zero matches. The mock plumbing at test_portfolio_router_logic.py:54-66 sets data=[] (always passes dedup check). No test ever sets the select mock to return existing data and asserts insert was NOT called.
- **Fix**: Append to analytics-service/tests/test_portfolio_router_logic.py::TestGenerateAlerts: def test_skips_insert_when_unacked_alert_of_same_type_exists(self): sb = self._make_supabase_mock(); sb.table.return_value.select.return_value.eq.return_value.eq.return_value.is_.return_value.limit.return_value.execute.return_value = MagicMock(data=[{'id': 'existing-1'}]); _generate_alerts(sb, 'p-1', max_drawdown=-0.25, avg_pairwise_corr=0.85); sb.table.return_value.insert.assert_not_called(). Also: def test_inserts_when_existing_select_returns_empty(self) which is the only path the current mock exercises.

#### G13-012 · regime_shift alert crashes _generate_alerts when rolling_corr contains None entries from _safe_float(NaN) · _new_
- **File**: `analytics-service/routers/portfolio.py:413`
- **Specialist**: `red-team` (confidence 8)
- **Summary**: compute_rolling_correlation (portfolio_risk.py:39) writes `_safe_float(v)` into each rolling-corr entry's `value` field. `_safe_float` returns None when v is NaN — which happens routinely at the leading edge of a rolling window (insufficient data) or when two strategies have non-overlapping dates within the window. The Sprint 4 regime_shift branch then does `recent_vals = [p['value'] for p in series[-window:]]` (line 411) followed by `recent_avg = sum(recent_vals) / len(recent_vals)` (line 413). When any `p['value']` is None, `sum([None, 0.4, 0.5, ...])` raises `TypeError: unsupported operand type(s) for +: 'int' and 'NoneType'`. The exception propagates up through _generate_alerts → _compute_portfolio_analytics's outer try/except → portfolio analytics computation fails with status 'failed' and any sibling alert types (drawdown, correlation_spike, underperformance, concentration_creep) that would have fired in the same _generate_alerts call are silently lost. This is a per-portfolio recompute cascading failure that ALL specialists missed: silent-failure-hunter caught the monthly_returns swallow but not this rolling_corr None-crash, performance focused on O(N) inserts, and pr-test-analyzer flagged missing tests for the rule but did not pin the NaN/None input case.
- **Evidence**: analytics-service/routers/portfolio.py:411-414 `recent_vals = [p['value'] if isinstance(p, dict) else p for p in series[-window:]]\n            prior_vals = [p['value'] if isinstance(p, dict) else p for p in series[-window * 2:-window]]\n            recent_avg = sum(recent_vals) / len(recent_vals)\n            prior_avg = sum(prior_vals) / len(prior_vals)`. Combined with analytics-service/services/portfolio_risk.py:39 `result[key] = [{'date': d.isoformat(), 'value': _safe_float(v)} for d, v in rolling.items()]` where _safe_float returns None on NaN (services/metrics.py:72-80). Reproduces deterministically with any new strategy whose rolling-corr window straddles its first 30 days.
- **Fix**: Filter out None values before averaging: `recent_clean = [x for x in recent_vals if x is not None]; if not recent_clean: continue; recent_avg = sum(recent_clean) / len(recent_clean)`. Apply the same filter to prior_vals. Add a regression test that feeds rolling_corr with a leading-None series and asserts _generate_alerts does not raise.

#### G13-013 · Bridge composite_score wrong sign for dd_delta — drawdown improvements penalize ranking
- **File**: `analytics-service/services/bridge_scoring.py:96`
- **Specialist**: `code-reviewer` (confidence 9)
- **Summary**: `dd_delta = _delta(current_dd, new_dd) = current_dd - new_dd`. `_max_drawdown` (portfolio_optimizer.py:154) returns NEGATIVE values (e.g. -0.15 for 15% drawdown). When the replacement candidate IMPROVES drawdown (smaller absolute, e.g. current=-0.15, new=-0.10), `current_dd - new_dd = -0.05` (NEGATIVE). The inline comment claims `# positive = less drawdown (good)` and the composite `w3 * dd_delta` adds it with positive weight w3=0.3 — so an improvement subtracts from the score and a worse drawdown adds. Candidates that improve drawdown are ranked LOWER than candidates that worsen it on that axis. This inverts the REPLACE scoring on a key dimension.
- **Evidence**: analytics-service/services/bridge_scoring.py:96 `dd_delta = _delta(current_dd, new_dd)  # positive = less drawdown (good)`; analytics-service/services/portfolio_optimizer.py:154-160 `_max_drawdown` returns `drawdown.min()` which is <= 0. Example: current_dd=-0.15, new_dd=-0.10 → _delta=-0.05, but improvement should produce positive contribution. composite uses w3*dd_delta at line 98.
- **Fix**: Swap argument order to `_delta(new_dd, current_dd)` so positive delta corresponds to less drawdown (matches the docstring intent), OR use `abs(current_dd) - abs(new_dd)` so the magnitude difference is positive when drawdown shrinks. Mirror the same fix in `dd_improvement` in `portfolio_optimizer.find_improvement_candidates` (same pattern, same bug).

#### G13-014 · Bridge composite_score wrong sign on BOTH dd_delta and corr_delta — REPLACE ranking is inverted on two of three axes · _chain_ · refs: code-reviewer:1, code-reviewer:2
- **File**: `analytics-service/services/bridge_scoring.py:98`
- **Specialist**: `red-team` (confidence 9)
- **Summary**: code-reviewer caught the dd_delta sign error; this finding chains it with the corr_delta sign error which code-reviewer caught separately on the FRONTEND but missed on the BACKEND composite formula. Backend bridge_scoring.py:95 sets `corr_delta = _delta(current_corr, new_corr)` (positive when corr REDUCES, good) and bridge_scoring.py:96 sets `dd_delta = _delta(current_dd, new_dd)` (since _max_drawdown returns NEGATIVE values, positive when drawdown WORSENS — bad). The composite formula `composite = w1*sharpe_delta + w2*corr_delta + w3*dd_delta` (line 98) adds these with POSITIVE weights w2=0.3, w3=0.3. Result: a candidate that improves drawdown (dd_delta negative) loses 0.3*|delta| from its score; a candidate that improves correlation (corr_delta positive) gains 0.3*|delta|. So out of three improvement axes, ONE (corr) is correctly weighted, ONE (dd) is INVERTED, and the sign convention is also inconsistent. Top-5 candidates returned via the bridge will be the candidates that WORSEN drawdown the most, contradicting the user-visible 'Strong fit' badge.
- **Evidence**: analytics-service/services/bridge_scoring.py:94-98 `sharpe_delta = _delta(new_sharpe, current_sharpe)\n        corr_delta = _delta(current_corr, new_corr)  # positive = corr reduced (good)\n        dd_delta = _delta(current_dd, new_dd)  # positive = less drawdown (good)\n        composite = w1 * sharpe_delta + w2 * corr_delta + w3 * dd_delta`. _max_drawdown returns drawdown.min() which is <= 0 (analytics-service/services/portfolio_optimizer.py:154-160). When new portfolio has smaller drawdown (e.g. current=-0.15, new=-0.10), dd_delta = current_dd - new_dd = -0.15 - (-0.10) = -0.05, which is subtracted from composite — penalizing the improvement.
- **Fix**: Pick ONE sign convention and apply it uniformly. Recommended: positive delta = improvement on all three axes. Change line 96 to `dd_delta = _delta(new_dd, current_dd)` (new minus old, with both negative drawdown values, an improvement yields positive delta). Then frontend ReplacementCard.tsx must also flip MaxDD's invertedBetter from true to false (since positive becomes the improved direction). Same for corr if you want the convention to match: leave line 95 as is, and flip the frontend Corr invertedBetter to false. Add a unit test in test_bridge_scoring.py that asserts a candidate which strictly DOMINATES the incumbent (better sharpe, less corr, less drawdown) returns positive composite_score.

#### G13-015 · Fit-label thresholds are mis-calibrated against composite_score range — 'Strong fit' is effectively unreachable for realistic deltas · _new_
- **File**: `analytics-service/services/bridge_scoring.py:119`
- **Specialist**: `red-team` (confidence 9)
- **Summary**: composite = 0.4*sharpe_delta + 0.3*corr_delta + 0.3*dd_delta. Sharpe_delta units are Sharpe-ratio points (annualized), typically ±0.1 to ±0.4 for a single-strategy swap. Corr_delta is a Pearson correlation difference, typically ±0.05. dd_delta is a fractional drawdown difference, typically ±0.02. A realistic 'great' candidate produces composite ≈ 0.4*0.3 + 0.3*0.05 + 0.3*0.02 = 0.141 — which the _fit_label thresholds (>0.7 Strong, >0.4 Good, >0.2 Moderate, else Weak) maps to 'Weak fit'. To reach 'Strong fit' (>0.7) the candidate needs sharpe_delta ≈ 1.75 — a Sharpe-ratio swing larger than typical portfolio Sharpe ratios themselves. The unit tests in test_bridge_scoring.py use synthetic mu=0.001/0.003 returns that produce inflated sharpe_deltas of order 1+ and DO trigger 'Strong fit' — masking the production calibration issue. Allocators will see every candidate badged 'Weak fit', undermining the headline UX claim ('Find Replacement' surfaces Strong/Good fits) and devaluing the product.
- **Evidence**: analytics-service/services/bridge_scoring.py:119-126 `def _fit_label(score: float) -> str:\n    if score > 0.7: return 'Strong fit'\n    if score > 0.4: return 'Good fit'\n    if score > 0.2: return 'Moderate fit'\n    return 'Weak fit'`. Composite math at line 98 with w1=0.4, w2=0.3, w3=0.3 — combined with sharpe_delta units (Sharpe points) vs corr_delta units (correlation fraction) vs dd_delta units (drawdown fraction) producing composite values in the [-0.3, +0.3] range for realistic candidates.
- **Fix**: Either (a) normalize each delta to a [0,1] band before composing (e.g. sharpe_delta_norm = sharpe_delta / 2.0, corr_delta_norm = corr_delta / 0.5, dd_delta_norm = -dd_delta / 0.3 — with sign fixes from the chain finding) so the composite naturally lives in [0,1] and the >0.7 / >0.4 / >0.2 thresholds work; or (b) recalibrate thresholds to match the empirical distribution by running the scorer against 30 days of production data and picking quartiles. Add a test that pins 'a candidate with a 0.5 Sharpe improvement and 0.1 correlation reduction returns Good fit', not Weak fit.

#### G13-016 · POST /api/bridge swallows upstream 4xx as 500, breaks sister-route convention
- **File**: `src/app/api/bridge/route.ts:59`
- **Specialist**: `api-contract` (confidence 9)
- **Summary**: findReplacementCandidates() throws AnalyticsUpstreamError with a preserved .status, but the catch block flattens every upstream failure to 500 instead of forwarding 4xx semantics. The sister route /api/simulator (analogous compute proxy, established precedent) explicitly does the right thing at simulator/route.ts:100-102. Result: clients receive 500 for portfolio-already-archived (400), missing strategy (404), upstream rate-limit (429), and 422 validation errors — all surface as opaque 'something is broken' to the UI instead of actionable user errors.
- **Evidence**: src/app/api/bridge/route.ts:59-67  } catch (err) {     console.error("[bridge] Scoring failed:", err);     const message =       err instanceof Error ? err.message : "Bridge scoring failed";     return NextResponse.json({ error: message }, { status: 500 });   }   // vs simulator/route.ts:100-105 which explicitly forwards 4xx via `err instanceof AnalyticsUpstreamError && err.status >= 400 && err.status < 500`
- **Fix**: Import AnalyticsUpstreamError from @/lib/analytics-client and forward 4xx status codes through, mirroring src/app/api/simulator/route.ts:100-102 exactly. Keep 5xx→500 unchanged. Replace the generic Error.message echo with a static message for non-AnalyticsUpstreamError throws to also fix evidence leakage (separate finding).

#### G13-017 · POST /api/bridge echoes raw Error.message to client — upstream Python stack info leakage
- **File**: `src/app/api/bridge/route.ts:62`
- **Specialist**: `api-contract` (confidence 9)
- **Summary**: On any thrown error (DB error, analytics-service exception, JSON parse failure deep in fetch, Zod contract-drift errors from parseResponse), `err.message` is sent verbatim in the response envelope. parseResponse() inside analytics-client.ts:141-143 builds a multi-line message that embeds Zod issue paths AND messages from the Python boundary; AnalyticsUpstreamError likewise wraps the upstream `detail` payload, which can include FastAPI exception details. Authenticated allocators receive internal schema/exception hints they shouldn't see.
- **Evidence**: src/app/api/bridge/route.ts:62-66  const message =       err instanceof Error ? err.message : "Bridge scoring failed";     return NextResponse.json({ error: message }, { status: 500 });   // Compare contracted Python detail forwarded via AnalyticsUpstreamError; parseResponse() throws Error with the full Zod issue list.
- **Fix**: Return a static safe message for the 500 branch (e.g. 'Bridge scoring failed'), keep err.message confined to the server log. Mirror the redaction discipline already used in audit-aware routes — only forward known-safe AnalyticsUpstreamError.message for 4xx after status-code forwarding (fix in the same change).

#### G13-018 · /api/bridge flattens all upstream 4xx errors to 500
- **File**: `src/app/api/bridge/route.ts:62`
- **Specialist**: `silent-failure-hunter` (confidence 9)
- **Summary**: `findReplacementCandidates()` calls the analytics service via `analyticsRequest`, which throws `AnalyticsUpstreamError` preserving the upstream `.status` (400/404/422 etc.). The bridge route catches `err` generically and ALWAYS returns 500, losing the upstream status. When the Python service returns 400 ('No returns data available') or 404 ('Portfolio not found'), the client sees 500 + opaque message instead of an actionable 4xx. The class comment on AnalyticsUpstreamError (analytics-client.ts:36-40) explicitly says 'route handlers can forward 4xx semantics' — this route violates that contract.
- **Evidence**: src/app/api/bridge/route.ts:55-67 — `try { const result = await findReplacementCandidates(...); return NextResponse.json(result); } catch (err) {\n    console.error('[bridge] Scoring failed:', err);\n    const message = err instanceof Error ? err.message : 'Bridge scoring failed';\n    return NextResponse.json({ error: message }, { status: 500 });\n  }`
- **Fix**: Branch on `err instanceof AnalyticsUpstreamError` and pass through `err.status`. Branch on `AnalyticsTimeoutError` to return 504. Only flatten genuine unexpected exceptions to 500. Also use `logError` (Sentry) instead of plain `console.error` so the 500 path doesn't lose the breadcrumb in production.

#### G13-020 · ReplacementCard displays corr_delta improvement as red (negative) — sign convention disagrees with backend
- **File**: `src/components/portfolio/ReplacementCard.tsx:15`
- **Specialist**: `code-reviewer` (confidence 8)
- **Summary**: Backend `find_replacement_candidates` (bridge_scoring.py:95) computes `corr_delta = current_corr - new_corr` → POSITIVE when correlation REDUCES (improvement, good per its own comment). The frontend `deltaColor` (ReplacementCard.tsx:14-21) flips the sign with `invertedBetter: true` for 'Corr', treating `value <= 0` as the positive/green color. So a candidate that reduces correlation (positive corr_delta from backend) is rendered in red `text-negative`, and a candidate that worsens correlation is rendered green. The text rendered also shows '+5.0% Corr' (suggesting correlation went UP) for what is actually a reduction. Allocators reading this card will misjudge candidates.
- **Evidence**: src/components/portfolio/ReplacementCard.tsx:14-21 `function deltaColor(value, invertedBetter)` returns positive class when `value <= 0` and invertedBetter=true; line 74 sets `invertedBetter: true` for Corr; backend analytics-service/services/bridge_scoring.py:95 `corr_delta = _delta(current_corr, new_corr)  # positive = corr reduced (good)`. formatDelta (line 23-29) prints raw value with '+' for positive, which makes a corr REDUCTION render as '+X.X% Corr' (looks like worsening).
- **Fix**: Either change backend to emit `corr_delta = new_corr - current_corr` (negative=improvement, matching MaxDD direction), OR set `invertedBetter: false` for Corr in the frontend deltas array AND update formatDelta so that a corr drop is shown as a negative percentage with green color. The comment `// For MaxDD and Correlation, negative delta = improvement` is currently wrong for Correlation given the backend output.

#### G13-021 · ReplacementCard intro fetch swallows all errors into a generic 'Retry Intro' button
- **File**: `src/components/portfolio/ReplacementCard.tsx:67`
- **Specialist**: `silent-failure-hunter` (confidence 9)
- **Summary**: `handleIntro` wraps fetch + status checks in `try { ... } catch { setIntroState('error'); }` — empty catch, no parameter, nothing logged. Any failure (network error, 5xx, malformed JSON, schema mismatch, CSRF rejection 403, rate-limit 429) collapses to the same 'Retry Intro' button. Users can't distinguish 'try again in a minute' (429) from 'permanently blocked' (403) from 'service down' (network). Worse, the catch hides programming errors (TypeError on `candidate.composite_score.toFixed`) — they look like network failures. No Sentry event, no console output.
- **Evidence**: src/components/portfolio/ReplacementCard.tsx:45-70 — `const handleIntro = useCallback(async () => {\n    setIntroState('loading');\n    try { const res = await fetch('/api/intro', {...}); ...\n      if (!res.ok) { throw new Error(`${res.status}`); }\n      setIntroState('done');\n    } catch { setIntroState('error'); }\n  }, [candidate, replacementFor]);`
- **Fix**: Capture the error: `catch (err) { console.error('[bridge.intro] failed:', err); logError(err); setIntroState('error'); setErrorMessage(humanizeIntroError(err)); }`. Branch on the response status to render distinct UI for 429 ('Try again shortly'), 403 ('Sign in again'), and network failure. Show the error message to the user so they can act on it.

#### G13-022 · ReplacementCard treats HTTP 409 from /api/intro as success without verifying semantics
- **File**: `src/components/portfolio/ReplacementCard.tsx:58`
- **Specialist**: `silent-failure-hunter` (confidence 8)
- **Summary**: `if (res.status === 409) { setIntroState('done'); return; }` — the code assumes 409 means 'already requested' and shows the success UI 'Intro Requested'. But 409 is a generic HTTP conflict; the analytics-client's CSRF/dedup layers, future API revisions, or a different conflict (e.g. 'strategy is no longer published') would all surface as 409 and be misreported to the user as a completed intro. There is no body parsing to confirm the reason. If the server starts returning 409 for new reasons, users will think their intro was sent when it was not — a silent product failure.
- **Evidence**: src/components/portfolio/ReplacementCard.tsx:58-62 — `if (res.status === 409) {\n        // Already requested — treat as success\n        setIntroState('done');\n        return;\n      }`
- **Fix**: Parse the 409 body and only treat the 'already_requested' / 'duplicate' reason code as success. For other 409 reasons, render an explanatory message: `const body = await res.json().catch(() => ({})); if (body.code === 'duplicate_intro') { setIntroState('done'); } else { setIntroState('error'); setErrorMessage(body.error ?? 'Could not request intro'); }`

#### G13-024 · BridgeResponseSchema parse failures cannot be caught — no test for Zod validation of /api/portfolio-bridge response
- **File**: `src/lib/analytics-schemas.ts:2284`

There's no test verifying: (a) BridgeFitLabelSchema strictly accepts only the 4 enum values (mistyping 'Strong Fit' vs 'Strong fit' would slip the contract), (b) BridgeCandidateSchema requires all 7 fields, (c) BridgeResponseSchema.passthrough() is intentional. Also pin BridgeFitLabelSchema enum values so 'Strong fit'/'Good fit'/'Moderate fit'/'Weak fit' lock the contract.

#### G13-025 · computePortfolioHealthScore has zero tests despite driving green/yellow/red KpiStrip banding
