Pin the 25-point math so a bucket-flip is caught.

### MEDIUM (23)

#### G13-026 · /api/bridge route body parsed without Zod — relies on optional-field types instead of validating
- **File**: `/Users/helios-mammut/claude-projects/quantalyze/src/app/api/bridge/route.ts:28`
- **Specialist**: `type-design-analyzer` (confidence 8)
- **Summary**: The bridge route types the incoming body as `let body: { portfolio_id?: string; underperformer_strategy_id?: string };` and only checks truthiness on the two fields. Both are stringly-typed; a caller can pass `portfolio_id: 12345` (number) or any other JSON-coercible value and the type narrowing `if (!portfolio_id || !underperformer_strategy_id)` accepts it. The downstream `findReplacementCandidates(portfolio_id, ...)` parameter is `string` but the value travels through `JSON.stringify` and the analytics service receives whatever shape it was. This is exactly the failure mode the analytics-schemas.ts pattern was designed to prevent at the Python boundary, but the inbound Next.js route uses no Zod parsing. Every other field-validating route in this codebase (compute-queue, csv-finalize) already uses Zod request schemas.
- **Evidence**: src/app/api/bridge/route.ts:28-41 `let body: { portfolio_id?: string; underperformer_strategy_id?: string }; try { body = await req.json(); } catch ... const { portfolio_id, underperformer_strategy_id } = body; if (!portfolio_id || !underperformer_strategy_id) ...` — no runtime shape validation.
- **Fix**: Define `const BridgeRequestBodySchema = z.object({ portfolio_id: z.string().uuid(), underperformer_strategy_id: z.string().uuid() }).strict();` colocated with BridgeResponseSchema in analytics-schemas.ts. In route.ts: `const parsed = BridgeRequestBodySchema.safeParse(await req.json()); if (!parsed.success) return NextResponse.json({ error: 'Invalid request', issues: parsed.error.issues }, { status: 400 });`. This locks down the request contract at the trust boundary and also documents the API for callers.

#### G13-027 · ReplacementPanel parses fetch response without Zod — server-side contract guard not enforced in client
- **File**: `/Users/helios-mammut/claude-projects/quantalyze/src/components/portfolio/ReplacementPanel.tsx:55`
- **Specialist**: `type-design-analyzer` (confidence 8)
- **Summary**: ReplacementPanel.useEffect fetches /api/bridge and pulls candidates with `setCandidates(data.candidates ?? [])` where `data = await res.json()` is implicitly `any`. The same BridgeResponseSchema that validates the Python→Next boundary is NOT applied to the Next→Browser boundary. If anything in the Next.js route (or a future proxy layer, a service-worker mock, or an error envelope shape mismatch) returns `{ data: { candidates: [...] } }` or `{ candidates: null }` or `{ candidates: [{...different shape...}] }`, the client renders garbage with no warning. Same for error-path response on line 51-52 (`const body = await res.json().catch(...); throw new Error(body.error ?? ...)`) — body is any, body.error is any. The `BridgeCandidate[] | null` state type lies because it was never validated.
- **Evidence**: src/components/portfolio/ReplacementPanel.tsx:55-58 `const data = await res.json(); if (!controller.signal.aborted) { setCandidates(data.candidates ?? []); }` (no schema parse).
- **Fix**: Import BridgeResponseSchema in ReplacementPanel and parse: `const data = BridgeResponseSchema.safeParse(await res.json()); if (!data.success) { setError('Response contract violation'); return; } setCandidates(data.data.candidates);`. Same pattern for the error path — define an error envelope schema and parse before reading `.error`. This makes the client-side contract symmetric with the server-side guarantee.

#### G13-028 · BridgeResponseSchema uses .passthrough() despite comment promising a 'strict schema'
- **File**: `/Users/helios-mammut/claude-projects/quantalyze/src/lib/analytics-schemas.ts:168`
- **Specialist**: `type-design-analyzer` (confidence 8)
- **Summary**: The Sprint-4 docblock at lines 142-147 says 'Strict schema for /api/portfolio-bridge. Each candidate must match the BridgeCandidate shape in types.ts. Parse failures throw.' The actual schema (line 168) uses `.passthrough()` rather than `.strict()`. BridgeCandidateSchema also has no `.strict()`. Any Python-side shape drift that ADDS a new field on a candidate (e.g. `score_components`, `secrets_leaked`, or accidental PII like an emailed-at timestamp) will silently pass through into `BridgeResponse` and into client state without any signal. This is exactly the failure mode the file's own header documentation (lines 13-25) warns against and chose .strict() for TickJobsResponseSchema (line 139). The new endpoint should follow the contract-version/strict pattern declared as the migration direction.
- **Evidence**: src/lib/analytics-schemas.ts:166-168 `export const BridgeResponseSchema = z.object({ candidates: z.array(BridgeCandidateSchema), }).passthrough();` — compare to lines 123-139 where TickJobsResponseSchema explicitly uses `.strict()` with the same rationale.
- **Fix**: Either (a) drop `.passthrough()` from BridgeResponseSchema and add `.strict()` to BridgeCandidateSchema, or (b) update the lying docblock at lines 143-147 to say 'Loose schema; unknown fields are accepted'. The header at lines 13-25 already states new endpoints should prefer the strict style — Bridge is a new endpoint and should match. If allocator-safety motivated the choice (drop unknown server fields rather than fail), document that explicitly and consider `.strip()` rather than `.passthrough()` so unknown fields are removed instead of forwarded into client state.

#### G13-029 · BridgeFitLabel duplicated as TS literal union and Zod enum — silent drift risk
- **File**: `/Users/helios-mammut/claude-projects/quantalyze/src/lib/types.ts:638`
- **Specialist**: `type-design-analyzer` (confidence 8)
- **Summary**: BridgeFitLabel is defined twice: once as a TypeScript literal union in types.ts:638 (`'Strong fit' | 'Good fit' | 'Moderate fit' | 'Weak fit'`) and once as a Zod enum in analytics-schemas.ts:149-154 with the same four strings. Both are the source of truth for the SAME label set; nothing ties them together. If Python adds a 'Excellent fit' tier and someone updates types.ts only, FIT_STYLES in ReplacementCard.tsx (`Record<BridgeFitLabel, string>`) compiles but the Zod validator rejects 'Excellent fit' and clients see a contract violation. If Python adds a new tier and someone updates the Zod schema only, the candidate object's `fit_label` becomes a wider union than the TS type and the `Record<BridgeFitLabel, string>` lookup is incomplete at runtime.
- **Evidence**: src/lib/types.ts:638 `export type BridgeFitLabel = 'Strong fit' | 'Good fit' | 'Moderate fit' | 'Weak fit';` and src/lib/analytics-schemas.ts:149-154 `const BridgeFitLabelSchema = z.enum(['Strong fit','Good fit','Moderate fit','Weak fit']);`. ReplacementCard.tsx:7-12 uses `Record<BridgeFitLabel, string>` to map every variant to a CSS class.
- **Fix**: Make the Zod enum the single source of truth and derive the TS type: `export const BridgeFitLabelSchema = z.enum(['Strong fit','Good fit','Moderate fit','Weak fit']); export type BridgeFitLabel = z.infer<typeof BridgeFitLabelSchema>;`. Re-export from types.ts if needed for layering. Then `Record<BridgeFitLabel, string>` is guaranteed exhaustive at compile time and any addition forces an update to one schema only.

#### G13-030 · Bridge candidate scoring loop redoes full corr() per candidate
- **File**: `analytics-service/services/bridge_scoring.py:76`
- **Specialist**: `performance` (confidence 8)
- **Summary**: For each candidate (potentially 100s — see related finding) the loop calls `pd.concat([remaining_df, c_returns]).dropna()` then `_avg_corr(all_returns)` which executes `df.corr()` — an O(M² * T) Pearson correlation over the full time index, plus a sum/divide. With M remaining strategies, T = 252+ trading days, N candidates: cost is O(N * M² * T). Compounds with the unbounded candidate fetch above to make Bridge requests CPU-heavy on Fluid Compute (Active CPU billing).
- **Evidence**: analytics-service/services/bridge_scoring.py:72-92 — `for cid, c_returns in candidate_returns.items(): all_returns = pd.concat([remaining_df, c_returns.rename(cid)], axis=1).dropna(); ... new_corr = _avg_corr(all_returns)`. `_avg_corr` (portfolio_optimizer.py:145) calls `df.corr()` then sums every cell.
- **Fix**: Pre-compute the pairwise correlation block among remaining_df once (M×M matrix). For each candidate, only the new row/column (candidate vs each remaining) needs computing — that is O(M*T) per candidate, not O(M²*T). Then `_avg_corr` becomes (cached_sum + 2*sum(new_row) + 0_diag) / (M+1)*M total pairs. Drops scoring cost ~M× for portfolios with several holdings.

#### G13-031 · find_replacement_candidates compares baselines computed on different time windows — sharpe_delta is not apples-to-apples · _new_
- **File**: `analytics-service/services/bridge_scoring.py:48`
- **Specialist**: `red-team` (confidence 8)
- **Summary**: current_sharpe / current_corr / current_dd are computed from `port_df.dropna()` (line 39) — the intersection of dates where ALL portfolio strategies have data. Inside the per-candidate loop, new_sharpe / new_corr / new_dd are computed from `pd.concat([remaining_df, c_returns]).dropna()` (line 77) — a DIFFERENT, typically SHORTER intersection because the candidate's track record is usually shorter than the portfolio's. The delta `new_sharpe - current_sharpe` is therefore comparing Sharpe-over-2-years (incumbent baseline) against Sharpe-over-6-months (candidate slot) — different market regimes, different denominators, different annualization sample sizes. A candidate whose only history is a bull quarter will look spuriously great vs the multi-year incumbent. None of the specialists flagged the time-window mismatch (performance covered O(N) corr cost; pr-test-analyzer covered missing scoring tests; code-reviewer covered the sign on dd_delta).
- **Evidence**: analytics-service/services/bridge_scoring.py:39 `port_df = pd.DataFrame(portfolio_returns).dropna()`, lines 48-51 build current_* metrics on this full-portfolio intersection. Lines 76-78 build `all_returns = pd.concat([remaining_df, c_returns.rename(cid)], axis=1).dropna()` — a separate, typically shorter window. Lines 89-92 compute new_sharpe/new_corr/new_dd on this shorter window. The minimum 30-day check at line 79 doesn't enforce alignment with the current_* window.
- **Fix**: Reslice the incumbent baseline to the same time window as the candidate scoring: compute `current_returns_aligned = current_returns.reindex(all_returns.index).dropna()` inside the candidate loop and call `_compute_sharpe(current_returns_aligned)` per candidate. Slightly more expensive but eliminates the windowing bias. Alternatively, restrict candidates to those whose track records covers the same span as the portfolio (use `c_returns.reindex(port_df.index).dropna()` and require >=N overlap). Add a regression test with a portfolio history twice as long as the candidate and assert the sharpe baseline used in the delta is the candidate-aligned slice, not the full portfolio slice.

#### G13-032 · Narrative says '<strategy> drove X% of the gain' even when the portfolio LOST money — copy is sign-blind · _new_
- **File**: `analytics-service/services/portfolio_optimizer.py:108`
- **Specialist**: `red-team` (confidence 8)
- **Summary**: The Sprint 4 per-month breakdown sentence is unconditional: `f'In {month_name}, portfolio returned {ret * 100:+.1f}%. {top_contrib.get("strategy_name", "unknown")} drove {top_share * 100:.0f}% of the gain'`. When the month's return is negative (a LOSS), the second clause still says 'drove X% of the gain' — top_share is built from `abs(top_contrib.get('contribution', 0)) / total_abs`, so it's a SIZE share, not a directional share. Allocators reading 'In April 2026, portfolio returned -3.0%. Alpha drove 60% of the gain' get cognitively dissonant copy that undermines trust in the briefing widget. This is a copy bug that silent-failure-hunter found a related issue around (monthly returns being swallowed) but never flagged the wording problem when monthly returns succeed.
- **Evidence**: analytics-service/services/portfolio_optimizer.py:107-110 `parts.append(\n    f'In {month_name}, portfolio returned {ret * 100:+.1f}%. '\n    f'{top_contrib.get("strategy_name", "unknown")} drove {top_share * 100:.0f}% of the gain'\n)`. top_share is computed at line 100 from absolute contributions.
- **Fix**: Branch the copy on sign of ret: `noun = 'gain' if ret >= 0 else 'loss'; direction = 'drove' if (top_contrib.get('contribution', 0) >= 0 and ret >= 0) else 'absorbed' if ret < 0 else 'drove'`. Or simpler: `'drove' if ret >= 0 else 'led the loss'`. Pin in a narrative-generation unit test with a negative-month case.

#### G13-033 · generate_narrative builds 'If you trim ... Sharpe moves from X to Y' but silently emits no sentence when portfolio_sharpe missing
- **File**: `analytics-service/services/portfolio_optimizer.py:600`
- **Specialist**: `silent-failure-hunter` (confidence 8)
- **Summary**: The optimizer recommendation sentence is only appended when both `current_sharpe_str` and `new_sharpe_str` are truthy — both are populated only when `portfolio_sharpe` is non-null on the analytics dict. If the upstream caller forgets to thread `portfolio_sharpe` (or schema drift renames it), the entire recommendation sentence is silently dropped from the narrative with no log, no metric. Users see a narrative missing its actionable section and operators can't tell why. The 'if applicable' comment masks what is in fact a contract dependency that should be asserted, not silently degraded.
- **Evidence**: analytics-service/services/portfolio_optimizer.py:594-614 — `suggestions = analytics.get('optimizer_suggestions')\n    if suggestions and len(suggestions) > 0 and attr:\n        worst_attr = min(attr, ...)\n        ...\n        if portfolio_sharpe is not None:\n            current_sharpe_str = f'{portfolio_sharpe:.2f}'\n            new_sharpe_str = f'{portfolio_sharpe + sharpe_lift:.2f}'\n        if current_sharpe_str and new_sharpe_str:\n            parts.append(...)`
- **Fix**: When suggestions are present but the precondition fields are missing, emit `logger.warning('narrative.optimizer_sentence skipped: portfolio_sharpe missing for portfolio with suggestions')` so the asymmetric data flow is visible. Better: make `portfolio_sharpe` required in the analytics dict shape and assert it at the top of generate_narrative.

#### G13-034 · KpiStrip Health group + healthColor banding untested — green/yellow/red thresholds can silently shift
- **File**: `src/app/(dashboard)/allocations/components/KpiStrip.tsx:1080`
- **Specialist**: `pr-test-analyzer` (confidence 8)
- **Summary**: KpiStrip.tsx adds a 4th group 'Health' that only renders when computePortfolioHealthScore returns non-null, and uses healthColor() to apply #16A34A (>=70), #D97706 (>=40), #DC2626 otherwise. KpiStrip.test.tsx + KpiStrip.scenario.test.tsx + KpiStrip.warmup.test.tsx never reference health, healthColor, or HEALTH_THRESHOLD_*. A regression flipping the threshold ordering (return red before checking yellow) would silently paint healthy portfolios red. The Health group also requires the Tooltip wrapper, not the old native `title` attr — a regression that drops the conditional `if (health)` block would crash the Tooltip render on missing analytics.
- **Evidence**: `grep -rn 'Health\|healthColor\|computePortfolioHealthScore' src/app/(dashboard)/allocations/components/KpiStrip*.test.*` returns zero. Production code at src/app/(dashboard)/allocations/components/KpiStrip.tsx:1080-1090 (healthColor + Health group), 1183-1190 (group push).
- **Fix**: Append to src/app/(dashboard)/allocations/components/KpiStrip.test.tsx: it('renders the Health group when computePortfolioHealthScore returns non-null', () => mock with analytics that produces a score; assert getByText('SCORE') and that the Score label is present); it('applies green color when score >= 70', () => mock score=85; assert style.color matches #16A34A); it('applies yellow color when score in [40,70)', () => assert #D97706); it('applies red color when score < 40', () => assert #DC2626); it('omits the Health group entirely when analytics is null', () => assert queryByText('SCORE') is null). Use vi.mock('@/lib/health-score') to stub computePortfolioHealthScore so the test is hermetic from health-score internals.

#### G13-035 · MorningBriefing splitNarrative fragments monthly sentences — attribution clause routed to context section
- **File**: `src/app/(dashboard)/allocations/widgets/intelligence/MorningBriefing.tsx:24`
- **Specialist**: `code-reviewer` (confidence 9)
- **Summary**: `generate_narrative` in analytics-service emits each monthly entry as a SINGLE narrative part containing a '. ' mid-sentence: `'In {month}, portfolio returned {ret}%. {name} drove {pct}% of the gain'` (portfolio_optimizer.py:107-110). The TS `splitNarrative` then splits the whole narrative on `/\.\s+/` (line 25), which fragments each monthly part into TWO sentences. The first half ('In X, portfolio returned Y%') correctly routes to `monthly`, but the second half ('NAME drove Z% of the gain') does NOT match any startsWith pattern (it doesn't start with 'In ', 'If you trim', 'Your portfolio returned', or 'driven primarily by'), so it falls through to `context`. As a result, the attribution clauses for ALL months stack up together in the 'Context (correlation, risk)' paragraph, divorced from their month sentence in the 'Monthly breakdown' list. The reader sees orphaned 'X drove 50% of the gain' phrases that look like they belong to the correlation/risk paragraph.
- **Evidence**: src/app/(dashboard)/allocations/widgets/intelligence/MorningBriefing.tsx:24-27 splits raw on `/\.\s+/`; lines 34-46 only route 'In ' to monthly, leaving 'X drove Y% of the gain' in the else branch (context). analytics-service/services/portfolio_optimizer.py:107-110 produces parts with embedded '. ' between 'returned X%.' and 'NAME drove'.
- **Fix**: Either (a) change `generate_narrative` to emit each monthly part as a single clause without an internal period (e.g. join with comma: `f'In {month_name}, portfolio returned {ret * 100:+.1f}% — {top_contrib.get("strategy_name")} drove {top_share * 100:.0f}% of the gain'`), OR (b) extend `splitNarrative` to also route sentences matching `/drove \d+% of the gain$/` to the `monthly` bucket, OR (c) emit a structured narrative payload (array of sections) instead of joining and re-splitting a string.

#### G13-036 · MorningBriefing widget splitNarrative — monthly/recommendation/context buckets untested
- **File**: `src/app/(dashboard)/allocations/widgets/intelligence/MorningBriefing.tsx:17`
- **Specialist**: `pr-test-analyzer` (confidence 8)
- **Summary**: The new widget MorningBriefing (intelligence.tsx, NOT the simpler src/components/portfolio/MorningBriefing.tsx) parses a single narrative string into 4 semantic buckets via regex tests on sentence prefixes: 'In <Month>' + 'returned [+-]\\d' → monthly, 'If you trim' → recommendation, 'Your portfolio returned'/'driven primarily by' → headline, else → context. intelligence.test.tsx only tests heading + raw narrative_summary + placeholder — it never verifies a multi-sentence narrative gets split correctly, and never verifies the 'Monthly breakdown' label or the recommendation pill (rgba(27,107,90,0.06) background) renders for an optimizer sentence. A regression that adjusts the regex to /returned \\d/ (drops the +- group) silently classifies negative-return months as 'context' instead of 'monthly'. The split logic is the entire reason the new widget exists; without tests its purpose is invisible.
- **Evidence**: `grep -n 'splitNarrative\|Monthly breakdown\|If you trim' src/app/(dashboard)/allocations/widgets/intelligence/intelligence.test.tsx` returns zero matches. Production code at src/app/(dashboard)/allocations/widgets/intelligence/MorningBriefing.tsx:17-49.
- **Fix**: Append to src/app/(dashboard)/allocations/widgets/intelligence/intelligence.test.tsx (describe MorningBriefing): it('renders Monthly breakdown section when narrative contains "In April 2026, portfolio returned +1.2%"', () => render with narrative='Your portfolio returned +2.3% MTD. In April 2026, portfolio returned +1.2%. Alpha drove 50% of the gain.'; expect screen.getByText('Monthly breakdown').toBeInTheDocument()); it('renders the recommendation pill for "If you trim X and redistribute"', () => narrative includes 'If you trim Beta and redistribute to Gamma, expected Sharpe moves from 1.2 to 1.5.'; assert pill background); it('classifies negative-return months as monthly NOT context (regex must match -)', () => narrative='Your portfolio returned -1.5% MTD. In April 2026, portfolio returned -2.0%.'; expect text under Monthly breakdown); it('puts correlation/risk sentences under context bucket', () => narrative includes 'Correlation has tightened to 0.65 — diversification quality is degrading.'). These pin the regex contract so any future tweak surfaces immediately.

#### G13-037 · POST /api/bridge does not validate body shape — accepts any string, no UUID, no extra-field rejection
- **File**: `src/app/api/bridge/route.ts:28`
- **Specialist**: `api-contract` (confidence 9)
- **Summary**: The body is declared as a TS-only shape (`{ portfolio_id?: string; underperformer_strategy_id?: string }`) and the only runtime check is truthiness on each field. Sister routes (intro/route.ts:42, bridge/outcome/route.ts:21, simulator/route.ts:60, match/decisions/holding/route.ts:30) all run Zod safeParse. Real consequences: (a) underperformer_strategy_id is not validated as UUID, so an attacker can ship an arbitrary string ('; DROP TABLE...' or a 10MB payload) straight through to the Python /api/portfolio-bridge endpoint — the service has to defend itself; (b) extra body fields like `user_id` or `score_overrides` are not rejected — there's nothing structurally stopping a future refactor from spreading body into the downstream call (mass-assignment risk); (c) when portfolio_id is malformed-UUID, the supabase.from('portfolios').single() returns 22P02 and the route silently maps to 404 'Portfolio not found' (timing-undistinguishable from a real ownership failure, but the route doesn't preserve the 400-shaped contract upstream callers would expect).
- **Evidence**: src/app/api/bridge/route.ts:28-41  let body: { portfolio_id?: string; underperformer_strategy_id?: string };   try {     body = await req.json();   } catch {     return NextResponse.json({ error: "Invalid JSON" }, { status: 400 });   }   const { portfolio_id, underperformer_strategy_id } = body;   if (!portfolio_id || !underperformer_strategy_id) { ... 400 ... }
- **Fix**: Add a Zod schema co-located with the route (mirror simulator's @/lib/api/simulatorSchema.ts pattern): const BridgeRequestSchema = z.object({ portfolio_id: z.string().uuid(), underperformer_strategy_id: z.string().uuid() }).strict(); then `const parsed = BridgeRequestSchema.safeParse(rawBody)` and return 400 with issues on failure. .strict() blocks extra fields.

#### G13-038 · POST /api/bridge 429 response missing Retry-After header
- **File**: `src/app/api/bridge/route.ts:22`
- **Specialist**: `api-contract` (confidence 9)
- **Summary**: When the user hits the rate limit (userActionLimiter — 5/60s, a *tight* budget for a compute-intensive surface), the route returns 429 without a Retry-After header. The discriminated CheckLimitResult carries `retryAfter` (seconds until the window resets), and the sister route /api/simulator/route.ts:47-48 already plumbs it into both the JSON body and the standard HTTP header. Clients (ReplacementPanel) cannot disable the retry button for the correct duration and may hammer the limiter — wasting budget reserved for attestation/deletion paths that share userActionLimiter at 5/min.
- **Evidence**: src/app/api/bridge/route.ts:20-26  const rl = await checkLimit(userActionLimiter, `bridge:${user.id}`);   if (!rl.success) {     return NextResponse.json(       { error: "Too many requests. Bridge scoring is compute-intensive." },       { status: 429 },     );   }   // vs simulator/route.ts:46-50: `{ ..., headers: { "Retry-After": String(rl.retryAfter) } }` and `retryAfter: rl.retryAfter` in JSON body
- **Fix**: Mirror simulator/route.ts:40-51 exactly: include `retryAfter: rl.retryAfter` in the JSON body AND `headers: { 'Retry-After': String(rl.retryAfter) }` in the NextResponse options.

#### G13-039 · POST /api/bridge responses lack Cache-Control: private, no-store — violates audit-2026-05-07 Block D / P1947
- **File**: `src/app/api/bridge/route.ts:61`
- **Specialist**: `api-contract` (confidence 8)
- **Summary**: audit-2026-05-07 round-2 Block D / P1947 (the policy that motivated src/lib/api/headers.ts:13's NO_STORE_HEADERS) requires every authenticated route to stamp `Cache-Control: private, no-store` on both error AND success responses. The bridge route's 200 success body contains user-specific BridgeCandidate[] (strategy_id, sharpe_delta, etc. tied to the allocator's underperformer) — exactly the cross-tenant-leak surface the audit policy targets. None of the route's six response paths (401, 429, 400, 404, 200, 500) include NO_STORE_HEADERS. withAuth/withAllocatorAuth wrappers apply it automatically; this hand-rolled assertSameOrigin+getUser route bypasses that defense.
- **Evidence**: src/app/api/bridge/route.ts:14 (401), 19 (429), 32 (Invalid JSON 400), 38 (missing-field 400), 52 (404 Portfolio not found), 61 (200 success), 66 (500 — six total NextResponse.json calls; none pass `headers: NO_STORE_HEADERS`). Compare withAuth wrapper at src/lib/api/withAuth.ts:35.
- **Fix**: Either (a) refactor the route to use withAuth and remove the hand-rolled assertSameOrigin + supabase.auth.getUser block — this picks up NO_STORE_HEADERS on the 401 path automatically and aligns with the codebase convention used by bridge/outcome and bridge/outcome/dismiss; (b) failing the refactor, import NO_STORE_HEADERS from @/lib/api/headers and pass `{ status, headers: NO_STORE_HEADERS }` on every NextResponse.json call.

#### G13-040 · POST /api/bridge hand-rolls auth/CSRF instead of using withAuth, drifts from codebase convention
- **File**: `src/app/api/bridge/route.ts:7`
- **Specialist**: `api-contract` (confidence 8)
- **Summary**: The route open-codes the assertSameOrigin + supabase.auth.getUser sequence that withAuth (src/lib/api/withAuth.ts) encapsulates and that every other 2026-vintage bridge route uses (bridge/outcome/route.ts:92, bridge/outcome/dismiss/route.ts:13). The hand-rolled version is functionally similar but drifts in two observable ways: (a) the 401 envelope is `{ error: 'Unauthorized' }` without NO_STORE_HEADERS, where withAuth emits the same envelope WITH the audit-required headers; (b) any future hardening to withAuth (e.g., adding double-submit CSRF token check, body-size guard, Vary header) won't apply to this route. This is the canonical 'forks the wrapper silently' anti-pattern.
- **Evidence**: src/app/api/bridge/route.ts:7-18  export async function POST(req: NextRequest) {   const csrfError = assertSameOrigin(req);   if (csrfError) return csrfError;   const supabase = await createClient();   const { data: { user } } = await supabase.auth.getUser();   if (!user) {     return NextResponse.json({ error: "Unauthorized" }, { status: 401 });   }   // vs withAuth-using bridge/outcome/route.ts:92 export const POST = withAuth(async (req, user) => { ... })
- **Fix**: Refactor POST handler to `export const POST = withAuth(async (req, user) => { ... })` and drop the hand-rolled CSRF + auth lines. Brings NO_STORE_HEADERS, consistent 401 envelope, and future wrapper hardening at zero cost — only 6 of 11 bridge-related routes still hand-roll, this one should converge.

#### G13-041 · Cross-tenant scoring + service-key trust + missing route test = silent unauthorized scoring vector · _chain_ · refs: security:2, pr-test-analyzer:1, pr-test-analyzer:4
- **File**: `src/app/api/bridge/route.ts:44`
- **Specialist**: `red-team` (confidence 8)
- **Summary**: Chain of: security:2 (Python trusts client-supplied user_id), pr-test-analyzer:1 (no route.test.ts for /api/bridge), pr-test-analyzer:4 (no integration test for Python ownership gate). The Next.js bridge route at lines 44-49 does `.from('portfolios').select('id').eq('id', portfolio_id).eq('user_id', user.id).single()` — the SOLE tenant boundary. If a regression collapses the .eq('user_id', user.id) into .or() or drops it, the Python service trusts the body's user_id (security:2) so the cascading damage path is: TS bug → cross-tenant portfolio passes Next.js gate → Python's user_id check passes (it just checks the body's claimed user_id, not the session user) → arbitrary candidate scoring + the body-claimed user_id is stamped into audit_log (portfolio.py:886, 914). The combined effect: cross-tenant scoring + FORGED audit attribution. With zero route tests for the TS layer AND zero integration tests for the Python ownership gate (only AST emission tests), this regression ships green. No single specialist captured both halves of the chain.
- **Evidence**: src/app/api/bridge/route.ts:44-49 (single tenant gate, no test); analytics-service/routers/portfolio.py:815-817 (.eq('user_id', req.user_id) where req.user_id is the body-supplied value); analytics-service/routers/portfolio.py:884-894, 913-922 (log_audit_event(user_id=req.user_id, ...)).
- **Fix**: Three-part fix. (1) Add the pr-test-analyzer:1 route test set with explicit cross-tenant assertion: `it('returns 404 when portfolio belongs to another user, even with valid session', ...)` mocking session user X and a portfolio owned by user Y. (2) Add the pr-test-analyzer:4 Python integration test that asserts `.eq('user_id', req.user_id)` is invoked with the body's user_id matching the portfolio row's user_id. (3) Per security:2, harden the Python layer to verify req.user_id matches a session-derived principal — forward the Supabase JWT and validate sub claim, or sign (user_id, portfolio_id) with a secret HMAC in the Next.js route and verify on the Python side. Until (3) lands, the audit attribution is forgeable if any caller obtains the service key.

#### G13-042 · Bridge route uses console.error, not logError — failures don't reach Sentry
- **File**: `src/app/api/bridge/route.ts:63`
- **Specialist**: `silent-failure-hunter` (confidence 8)
- **Summary**: The 500 path logs via `console.error('[bridge] Scoring failed:', err)` rather than the project's standardized `logError`. Per project conventions (CLAUDE.md), production errors must use logError with an errorId from constants/errorIds.ts to reach Sentry. As written, a bridge scoring failure in production may print to a Vercel function log but does NOT raise a Sentry event with structured tags, so on-call won't be paged and there's no error-rate dashboard signal. Bridge is rate-limited at 10/hr precisely because it's expensive; silent failures here are exactly the class of regression that needs a tracked errorId.
- **Evidence**: src/app/api/bridge/route.ts:62-67 — `} catch (err) {\n    console.error('[bridge] Scoring failed:', err);\n    const message = err instanceof Error ? err.message : 'Bridge scoring failed';\n    return NextResponse.json({ error: message }, { status: 500 });\n  }`
- **Fix**: Replace with `logError(err, { errorId: 'BRIDGE_SCORING_FAILED', portfolioId: portfolio_id, userId: user.id });` and only fall back to `console.error` if logError isn't available in the route environment.

#### G13-043 · computeAllInsights re-runs on every parent rerender (not memoized)
- **File**: `src/components/portfolio/InsightStrip.tsx:82`
- **Specialist**: `performance` (confidence 8)
- **Summary**: `<InsightStrip>` calls `computeAllInsights(analytics, portfolioStrategies, portfolioAgeDays).slice(0, max)` directly in the function body. Although the file itself has no `"use client"`, every live caller (AllocationDashboardV2.tsx — `"use client"`) is a client component, so InsightStrip is rendered on the client and re-executes on every parent rerender. AllocationDashboardV2 has multiple useState (`pickerOpen`, plus parent state plumbed in), and `computeAllInsights` invokes 5 separate compute* helpers each iterating `attribution`, `risk_decomposition`, `rolling_correlation` arrays. Cheap per call but runs every time any unrelated state in the dashboard changes.
- **Evidence**: src/components/portfolio/InsightStrip.tsx:73-86 — `export function InsightStrip({analytics, portfolioId, ...}) { const insights = computeAllInsights(analytics, portfolioStrategies, portfolioAgeDays).slice(0, max); ... }`. No useMemo wrapper. Caller in `src/app/(dashboard)/allocations/AllocationDashboardV2.tsx:282` mounts it inside a `"use client"` shell.
- **Fix**: Wrap the call in `useMemo`: `const insights = useMemo(() => computeAllInsights(analytics, portfolioStrategies, portfolioAgeDays).slice(0, max), [analytics, portfolioStrategies, portfolioAgeDays, max])`. Add `"use client"` directive since the component must now use hooks.

#### G13-044 · ReplacementPanel fetch error has no telemetry — only inline UI
- **File**: `src/components/portfolio/ReplacementPanel.tsx:62`
- **Specialist**: `silent-failure-hunter` (confidence 8)
- **Summary**: When the /api/bridge call fails, the panel sets `error` state and renders it inline. But the catch block has no `console.error`, no `logError`, no Sentry breadcrumb. Operators have no visibility into how often bridge scoring fails in production. The user sees the message but ops can't aggregate failures or set alerts on a spike. Combined with G13 finding #3 (route flattens 4xx to 500), this means a configuration regression in the Python service would manifest as silent in-app error toasts with zero log signal.
- **Evidence**: src/components/portfolio/ReplacementPanel.tsx:59-64 — `} catch (err) {\n        if (err instanceof DOMException && err.name === 'AbortError') return;\n        if (!controller.signal.aborted) {\n          setError(err instanceof Error ? err.message : 'Failed to load candidates');\n        }\n      }`
- **Fix**: Add `console.error('[bridge.fetch] failed:', err); logError(err, { feature: 'bridge', portfolioId, strategyId });` before the setError call so operators get the breadcrumb and aggregate failure rate in Sentry.

#### G13-045 · Tooltip show() leaks timeouts on rapid hover
- **File**: `src/components/ui/Tooltip.tsx:29`
- **Specialist**: `performance` (confidence 9)
- **Summary**: `show()` assigns `timerRef.current = setTimeout(...)` without first clearing any prior pending timer. If two `onMouseEnter`/`onFocus` events fire before the 150ms elapses (e.g., focus-then-hover, or React's synthetic event re-fires), the first timeout's reference is lost and continues to run. When it fires, `setOpen(true)` triggers an extra render of an already-open tooltip. Low frequency but easy fix — and the component is used in the discovery/SimulateImpact path which can be hovered repeatedly.
- **Evidence**: src/components/ui/Tooltip.tsx:29-31 — `const show = useCallback(() => { timerRef.current = setTimeout(() => setOpen(true), 150); }, [])` — no `if (timerRef.current) clearTimeout(timerRef.current)` before assignment. `hide()` does clear, but a second `show()` before `hide()` overwrites the ref.
- **Fix**: At the top of `show()` add `if (timerRef.current) clearTimeout(timerRef.current)` to drop the old pending timer before queuing a new one. Also add a `useEffect` cleanup that clears on unmount so navigation away during the 150ms delay does not setState on an unmounted component.

#### G13-046 · Tooltip setTimeout fires setOpen after unmount, silently leaking state updates
- **File**: `src/components/ui/Tooltip.tsx:30`
- **Specialist**: `silent-failure-hunter` (confidence 8)
- **Summary**: `show` schedules `setTimeout(() => setOpen(true), 150)` but stores the handle in `timerRef.current` and never clears it on unmount — no `useEffect` cleanup. If the parent unmounts during the 150ms enter delay (which happens routinely when the KPI strip re-renders or the panel closes mid-hover), the timer fires after the component is gone, triggering React's 'state update on unmounted component' warning in dev and a memory leak in prod. The warning is suppressed in production builds so the leak is silent and only manifests under load.
- **Evidence**: src/components/ui/Tooltip.tsx:24-36 — `export function Tooltip({ content, children, className }: TooltipProps) {\n  const [open, setOpen] = useState(false);\n  const timerRef = useRef<ReturnType<typeof setTimeout> | null>(null);\n  ...\n  const show = useCallback(() => {\n    timerRef.current = setTimeout(() => setOpen(true), 150);\n  }, []);\n  const hide = useCallback(() => {\n    if (timerRef.current) clearTimeout(timerRef.current);\n    setOpen(false);\n  }, []);` — no useEffect with cleanup that clears `timerRef.current`.
- **Fix**: Add an unmount-cleanup effect: `useEffect(() => () => { if (timerRef.current) clearTimeout(timerRef.current); }, []);` so any pending show timer is cancelled when the Tooltip unmounts.

#### G13-047 · NEXT_PUBLIC_VERCEL_URL branch in csrf allowlist completely untested
- **File**: `src/lib/csrf.ts:27`
- **Specialist**: `pr-test-analyzer` (confidence 9)
- **Summary**: buildAllowedHosts() now reads NEXT_PUBLIC_VERCEL_URL and adds new URL(`https://${vercelUrl}`).host to the allowlist (csrf.ts:27-34). This exists specifically to fix preview-deployment 403s. A regression that drops the env var read or mis-parses it would silently re-break Vercel preview POSTs (allocator/admin testing on previews would all 403). The csrf.test.ts has neither a positive case ('accepts when Origin matches NEXT_PUBLIC_VERCEL_URL') nor a negative case ('malformed VERCEL_URL is gracefully skipped without crashing'). The host-set is built once and cached (which makes __resetAllowedHostsForTest essential), so a test that sets the env var must call reset before asserting.
- **Evidence**: `grep -n 'VERCEL_URL\|NEXT_PUBLIC_VERCEL' src/lib/csrf.test.ts` returns zero. Production code at src/lib/csrf.ts:27-34.
- **Fix**: Append to src/lib/csrf.test.ts: it('accepts Origin matching NEXT_PUBLIC_VERCEL_URL preview host', async () => { vi.stubEnv('NEXT_PUBLIC_VERCEL_URL', 'quantalyze-pr-55-abc123.vercel.app'); __resetAllowedHostsForTest(); const req = makeRequest({origin: 'https://quantalyze-pr-55-abc123.vercel.app'}); expect(assertSameOrigin(req)).toBeNull(); }); it('skips malformed NEXT_PUBLIC_VERCEL_URL without crashing', async () => { vi.stubEnv('NEXT_PUBLIC_VERCEL_URL', '%%not-a-host%%'); __resetAllowedHostsForTest(); const req = makeRequest({origin: 'http://localhost:3000'}); expect(() => assertSameOrigin(req)).not.toThrow(); }).

#### G13-048 · CSRF allowlist build silently swallows malformed NEXT_PUBLIC_VERCEL_URL
- **File**: `src/lib/csrf.ts:33`
- **Specialist**: `silent-failure-hunter` (confidence 8)
- **Summary**: When NEXT_PUBLIC_VERCEL_URL is set but malformed, the `try { hosts.add(new URL(`https://${vercelUrl}`).host); } catch { /* malformed — skip */ }` silently drops it from the allowlist. Unlike the sibling NEXT_PUBLIC_SITE_URL branch (line 25) which emits `console.warn`, this Vercel branch is completely silent. A Vercel preview deployment with a typo'd URL will 403 every POST request and operators will have no log line explaining why. The error masking exactly hides a misconfiguration that produces a confusing user-facing error (CSRF rejection).
- **Evidence**: src/lib/csrf.ts:29-34 — `const vercelUrl = process.env.NEXT_PUBLIC_VERCEL_URL;\n  if (vercelUrl) {\n    try {\n      hosts.add(new URL(`https://${vercelUrl}`).host);\n    } catch { /* malformed — skip */ }\n  }`
- **Fix**: Mirror the SITE_URL branch: `} catch { console.warn('[csrf] NEXT_PUBLIC_VERCEL_URL is not a valid URL:', vercelUrl); }`. This is module load-time code so emitting a warn is harmless and gives operators a single grep target.

### LOW (7)

#### G13-049 · Monthly returns build loop iterates twice; merge into single pass
- **File**: `analytics-service/routers/portfolio.py:271`
- **Specialist**: `performance` (confidence 9)
- **Summary**: During portfolio analytics compute, the monthly_returns dict is built in two passes over a derived structure: pass 1 multiplies daily (1+v) into a cumulative product per year/month; pass 2 subtracts 1.0. Hot path only in the sense it runs on every portfolio recompute, but D (days) is bounded — negligible CPU. Flagging because the diff explicitly hoisted other invariants and missed this one.
- **Evidence**: analytics-service/routers/portfolio.py:269-282 — first loop builds `monthly_returns[year][month] *= (1+v)` over `portfolio_returns_series.items()`, then a second nested loop `for year_str in monthly_returns: for month_str in ...: monthly_returns[year_str][month_str] -= 1.0`
- **Fix**: Single pass that accumulates cumulative product, then converts inline at finalize. Minor — only worth fixing if touching the surrounding code.

#### G13-050 · _records_to_series uses unsafe r['date'] / r['value'] access — KeyError on malformed strategy_analytics row crashes bridge endpoint · _new_
- **File**: `analytics-service/routers/portfolio.py:39`
- **Specialist**: `red-team` (confidence 9)
- **Summary**: _records_to_series at line 39-40 does `dates = [r['date'] for r in raw]; vals = [r['value'] for r in raw]` without .get(). If any row in strategy_analytics.returns_series has a malformed entry (missing 'date' or 'value' key — possible after a schema migration or a partial write), the comprehension raises KeyError. The bridge_endpoint at line 850 calls `_records_to_series(row.get('returns_series'), ...)` without a try/except; the KeyError propagates → FastAPI returns 500 → Next.js bridge route surfaces it. The bridge endpoint becomes unavailable for ANY portfolio that contains a single corrupted returns_series row. silent-failure-hunter caught two `except Exception: pass` swallows but missed this throw-the-other-way: an unguarded KeyError that takes down the endpoint instead of silently degrading.
- **Evidence**: analytics-service/routers/portfolio.py:35-41 `def _records_to_series(raw: list | None, name: str = '') -> pd.Series | None:\n    if not isinstance(raw, list) or not raw:\n        return None\n    dates = [r['date'] for r in raw]\n    vals = [r['value'] for r in raw]\n    return pd.Series(vals, index=pd.DatetimeIndex(dates), name=name)`
- **Fix**: Replace with .get and skip malformed records: `pairs = [(r.get('date'), r.get('value')) for r in raw if r.get('date') is not None and r.get('value') is not None]; if not pairs: return None; dates, vals = zip(*pairs); return pd.Series(list(vals), index=pd.DatetimeIndex(list(dates)), name=name)`. Add a unit test feeding a list with a missing-key dict and assert it returns a Series of the valid records.

#### G13-051 · Python analytics-service trusts client-supplied user_id for ownership check
- **File**: `analytics-service/routers/portfolio.py:817`
- **Specialist**: `security` (confidence 9)
- **Summary**: The /api/portfolio-bridge handler authenticates ownership by `.eq('user_id', req.user_id)` where req.user_id is a string field on BridgeRequest (analytics-service/models/schemas.py:34-37) supplied in the HTTP body. The X-Service-Key middleware authenticates the CALLER (Next.js), not the END USER. If the service key ever leaks (committed in .env, captured from CI logs, or any future caller besides /api/bridge) the attacker can call /api/portfolio-bridge with user_id=<victim_uuid> + portfolio_id=<victim's portfolio> and obtain a full bridge scoring on someone else's portfolio. The req.user_id is also written into audit_log (line 886, 914) — an attacker could forge audit attribution. The inline comment ('Defense-in-depth: Next.js layer already checks ownership') acknowledges this is a defense-in-depth gap. Today the Next.js layer at src/app/api/bridge/route.ts:59 correctly forwards `user.id` from authenticated session, so the LIVE exposure is bounded by the service-key secret, but the trust model is fragile.
- **Evidence**: analytics-service/models/schemas.py:34-37 `class BridgeRequest(BaseModel): portfolio_id: str; underperformer_strategy_id: str; user_id: str`. analytics-service/routers/portfolio.py:815-817 `portfolio_result = supabase.table("portfolios").select("id").eq("id", req.portfolio_id).eq("user_id", req.user_id).single().execute()`. log_audit_event called with user_id=req.user_id at lines 886 and 914.
- **Fix**: Bind the end-user identity to a verifiable token, not a body field. Either (a) require the Next.js layer to forward the user's Supabase JWT in an `Authorization: Bearer` header and validate it in the FastAPI middleware before populating req.user_id from the verified `sub` claim; or (b) keep user_id in the body but additionally verify the supplied user_id against a signed HMAC computed over (portfolio_id, user_id) with a separate signing secret. Until then, document the trust boundary explicitly and add an integration test that asserts X-Service-Key alone is NOT sufficient — every endpoint that takes user_id should reject when the user_id does not match a verified principal.

#### G13-052 · Analytics-service /api/portfolio-bridge rate-limit collapses to single bucket behind Next.js
- **File**: `analytics-service/routers/portfolio.py:799`
- **Specialist**: `security` (confidence 9)
- **Summary**: The decorator `@limiter.limit('10/hour')` uses slowapi's default key_func=get_remote_address (line 32 of the same file). All traffic to this endpoint arrives from the Next.js Vercel-functions pool, so get_remote_address returns the same handful of egress IPs (or one if Fluid Compute coalesces). A single noisy or malicious authenticated user can exhaust the 10/hour bucket for ALL other users on that IP — DoS amplification. The Next.js per-user `bridge:${user.id}` rate-limit (src/app/api/bridge/route.ts:20, userActionLimiter = 5/min per user) is the only EFFECTIVE quota. Most callers won't notice because they go through the Next.js path; but if the Next.js limiter ever degrades (Upstash outage) or is bypassed by a future caller, the Python tier provides no per-user cap.
- **Evidence**: analytics-service/routers/portfolio.py:32 `limiter = Limiter(key_func=get_remote_address)` and line 798-799 `@router.post("/portfolio-bridge") @limiter.limit("10/hour")`.
- **Fix**: Use a key_func that derives from the authenticated principal, e.g. `Limiter(key_func=lambda req: req.headers.get("x-end-user-id", get_remote_address(req)))` and have Next.js forward `x-end-user-id: <user.id>` on the analytics call (already passed in body as user_id). Alternatively run the limit at the (portfolio_id, user_id) granularity. Combine with the existing IP-based limit as a coarse outer ceiling.

#### G13-053 · Bridge route forwards raw internal error messages to client
- **File**: `src/app/api/bridge/route.ts:62`
- **Specialist**: `security` (confidence 9)
- **Summary**: The /api/bridge POST handler catches errors from findReplacementCandidates() (which proxies the Python analytics service) and returns err.message verbatim in the 500 response. Upstream messages can include Postgres column-not-found errors, Pydantic validation failure traces, or analytics-service-internal exception detail (e.g. 'AnalyticsUpstreamError: ... duplicate key value violates unique constraint portfolio_alerts_dedup_unacked'). An authenticated low-priv allocator can probe schema/internal state by crafting valid-looking but boundary inputs and reading the leaked 500 message — useful for chained exploitation reconnaissance (column names → SQL injection targeting elsewhere, internal hostnames in stack traces, etc.). Other routes in the codebase return generic 'Server error' or upstream-mapped status codes (see AnalyticsUpstreamError.status). The /api/intro and other adjacent routes do NOT forward err.message; this one does.
- **Evidence**: src/app/api/bridge/route.ts:62-67 `} catch (err) { console.error("[bridge] Scoring failed:", err); const message = err instanceof Error ? err.message : "Bridge scoring failed"; return NextResponse.json({ error: message }, { status: 500 }); }`
- **Fix**: Return a generic message to the client and keep the detail in server logs. If err is an AnalyticsUpstreamError, propagate the upstream status code but use a fixed user-facing message: `if (err instanceof AnalyticsUpstreamError) return NextResponse.json({ error: 'Bridge scoring failed' }, { status: err.status }); return NextResponse.json({ error: 'Bridge scoring failed' }, { status: 500 });`

#### G13-054 · Tooltip setTimeout not cleaned up on unmount
- **File**: `src/components/ui/Tooltip.tsx:29`
- **Specialist**: `code-reviewer` (confidence 9)
- **Summary**: `show` schedules a setTimeout to set state after 150ms but stores the timer only in a ref. If the component unmounts during the pending timer (e.g., fast hover then route change or parent re-render that removes the tooltip), the timer will fire after unmount and call `setOpen(true)` on an unmounted component. React 18 silently no-ops this, but the timer itself keeps a closure reference alive until it fires, and any future React-strict semantics tightening would surface this. Trivial cleanup missing.
- **Evidence**: src/components/ui/Tooltip.tsx:29-31 `show = useCallback(() => { timerRef.current = setTimeout(() => setOpen(true), 150); }, []);` — there is no useEffect cleanup that clears `timerRef.current` on unmount. `hide` clears it only on blur/mouseleave, not on unmount.
- **Fix**: Add `useEffect(() => () => { if (timerRef.current) clearTimeout(timerRef.current); }, []);` so the timer is cancelled on unmount.

#### G13-055 · BridgeResponseSchema is .passthrough() — silently accepts unknown fields from Python service
- **File**: `src/lib/analytics-schemas.ts:168`
- **Specialist**: `api-contract` (confidence 9)
- **Summary**: BridgeResponseSchema uses .passthrough() inherited from the loose legacy convention. The contract is otherwise locked — sister 'strict' versioned schemas (TickJobsResponseSchema at line 139) use .strict() so contract drift fails loudly. Today, if the analytics-service /api/portfolio-bridge endpoint adds a new top-level field (e.g. exposing internal scoring weights, candidate exclusion reasons, debug telemetry), passthrough silently surfaces it through findReplacementCandidates() and onto the wire, where any future client code that does Object.keys() on the bridge response will inadvertently process untyped fields. Block D leakage risk is low because the route does NextResponse.json(result) and the route itself doesn't transform; but the next consumer that maps or stringifies will broadcast surplus fields.
- **Evidence**: src/lib/analytics-schemas.ts:166-168  export const BridgeResponseSchema = z.object({   candidates: z.array(BridgeCandidateSchema), }).passthrough();   // Versus TickJobsResponseSchema at line 139 which uses .strict() and is documented as the migration direction.
- **Fix**: Replace .passthrough() with .strict() on BridgeResponseSchema AND BridgeCandidateSchema. Promote BridgeResponseSchema to contract_version literal style (mirror TickJobsResponseSchema at lines 123-140) when the next coordinated PR touches the analytics-service /api/portfolio-bridge writer.

## G14 — PR #57 — Sprint 5 Funding Cutover + /security

### CRITICAL (6)

#### G14-001 · run_sync_funding_job has zero direct tests
- **File**: `/Users/helios-mammut/claude-projects/quantalyze/analytics-service/services/job_worker.py:900`
- **Specialist**: `pr-test-analyzer` (confidence 10)
- **Summary**: The new analytics-worker entrypoint `run_sync_funding_job` (lines 900-958) is the per-strategy handler invoked by the cron-enqueued compute jobs. It contains the exchange-routing switch (binance/okx/bybit/unsupported→FAILED-permanent), the ccxt.RateLimitExceeded → `_stamp_429` circuit-breaker stamp, the finally-close-exchange path, the empty-rows DONE branch, and the upsert call. None of these branches are exercised. A regression where the unsupported-exchange branch silently returns DONE (or where _stamp_429 is skipped on a 429) would not be caught. The Python suite has `test_funding_fetch.py` for the normalizers and `test_funding_backfill_idempotency.py` for the shared upsert, but nothing for the worker handler itself.
- **Evidence**: `grep -rn run_sync_funding_job analytics-service/tests/` → zero hits. job_worker.py:900-958 is the only definition; dispatch wiring at job_worker.py:1758-1759.
- **Fix**: Create /Users/helios-mammut/claude-projects/quantalyze/analytics-service/tests/test_job_worker_sync_funding.py with describe 'run_sync_funding_job': assertions: (a) returns FAILED+permanent when key_row.exchange='kraken'; (b) calls _stamp_429 + re-raises on ccxt.RateLimitExceeded; (c) returns DONE with no upsert when fetch_funding_* returns []; (d) calls upsert_funding_rows with the rows on happy path; (e) ctx.exchange.close() is awaited in finally even on raise. Patch services.funding_fetch.fetch_funding_binance/okx/bybit and services.funding_fetch.upsert_funding_rows; mock _exchange_preflight to return a populated ctx.

#### G14-002 · funding_fees RLS policies have no integration assertions
- **File**: `/Users/helios-mammut/claude-projects/quantalyze/supabase/migrations/20260416081039_funding_fees.sql:135`
- **Specialist**: `pr-test-analyzer` (confidence 10)
- **Summary**: Migration 044 creates the `funding_fees_read` policy (joins through strategies.user_id = auth.uid()) plus three deny-everything policies for INSERT/UPDATE/DELETE (`WITH CHECK (false)`/`USING (false)`). These are the only barrier preventing cross-tenant leakage of perpetual-funding cashflow data and preventing authenticated users from forging rows. The migration's self-verifying DO block only checks the policy *exists* by name — it does not assert behavior. There is no integration / RLS test that connects as user A and confirms they cannot SELECT user B's funding_fees rows, or that an authenticated INSERT fails. A future RLS edit that loosens the predicate (or drops the deny policies) would ship silently.
- **Evidence**: `grep -rn funding_fees supabase/tests/` → zero hits. Only the migration itself references the policies. No pgTAP / vitest integration spec touches funding_fees.
- **Fix**: Add /Users/helios-mammut/claude-projects/quantalyze/supabase/tests/funding_fees_rls.test.sql (pgTAP) or extend the existing integration-rls suite. Tests: (a) user A inserts a strategy + funding_fees row via service role; (b) user A SELECT returns 1 row, user B SELECT returns 0 (cross-tenant leak guard); (c) authenticated INSERT/UPDATE/DELETE rejected (the deny policies). Mirror the pattern used for the api_keys/strategies tables in this repo.

#### G14-003 · OKX/Bybit daily_pnl still includes funding — new funding_fees attribution creates double-count on dashboards · _new_
- **File**: `analytics-service/services/exchange.py:485`
- **Specialist**: `red-team` (confidence 9)
- **Summary**: The PR comment in exchange.py (line 522) claims the Sprint 5.6 cutover stops FUNDING_FEE from routing into daily_pnl, but the gate is BINANCE-ONLY. For OKX (line 392-508) fetch_daily_pnl aggregates private_get_account_bills results without any type filter — it sums type=2 (trade pnl), type=8 (funding fee), type=fee, etc. into pnl_val = float(bill.get('pnl', 0)) + float(bill.get('fee', 0)). For Bybit (line 552-574), it uses private_get_v5_position_closed_pnl whose closedPnl field is, per the migration's own header comment at funding_fees.sql:10-11, 'the combined cashflow' (realized + funding). After this PR ships, OKX/Bybit perp strategies record funding TWICE — once aggregated into daily_pnl (consumed by transforms.py → Sharpe/Sortino/drawdown/equity curve at transforms.py:111-151 and equity_reconstruction.py:1851-1862) and once isolated in funding_fees → positions.funding_pnl (rendered in PositionsTab tooltip as Price ROI + Funding). The user-facing dashboard shows total ROI that already includes funding plus an explicit '+ Funding' line, inflating perceived economic P&L by the funding amount. Allocator factsheet numbers are now wrong for any OKX/Bybit perp strategy that pays/receives material funding.
- **Evidence**: exchange.py:485 OKX pnl_val = float(bill.get('pnl', 0)) + float(bill.get('fee', 0)) — no type=8 exclusion. exchange.py:556-569 Bybit uses position_closed_pnl which the migration's own preamble (funding_fees.sql:10-11) acknowledges 'returns the combined cashflow'. exchange.py:522 only Binance income gate dropped FUNDING_FEE. transforms.py:111 consumes daily_pnl for equity-curve math. position_reconstruction.py:464 separately writes positions.funding_pnl. PositionsTab.tsx:234 displays both.
- **Fix**: Either (a) extend the cutover: filter OKX account_bills by type != '8' AND switch Bybit from position_closed_pnl to a non-funding endpoint (or filter the combined number — but the migration header argues that's lossy); or (b) make this PR strictly Binance-only by gating positions.funding_pnl rendering on exchange === 'binance' until OKX/Bybit cutover lands. Currently the PR ships the double-count silently. Critical because the only data-quality flag in the funding code path is for missing/parse errors, not double-count.

#### G14-004 · Funding fetch errors mid-pagination silently truncate results to partial data
- **File**: `analytics-service/services/funding_fetch.py:183`
- **Specialist**: `silent-failure-hunter` (confidence 9)
- **Summary**: All three exchange fetchers (Binance, OKX, Bybit) catch any exception during a paginated fetch with `logger.warning(...)` then `break`/`return` — returning whatever rows were collected so far as if the run succeeded. A 500 from Binance on page 7 of 12 means pages 1-6 get UPSERTed and pages 8-12 are silently lost. The worker logs `inserted=N rows for strategy X` and returns DispatchResult(DONE). On the next cycle, since_ms advances based on last_sync_at, so the gap is never refilled. Position funding_pnl is now wrong forever and no flag is set on the position or strategy.
- **Evidence**: funding_fetch.py:177-183 (Binance): `try: data = await exchange.fapiPrivate_get_income(params) except Exception as exc: logger.warning('Binance funding fetch failed page %d: %s', page_idx, exc); break` — same pattern at lines 261-268 (OKX) and 347-355 (Bybit). job_worker.py:927-958 then logs DONE and reports inserted count with no knowledge of the truncation.
- **Fix**: Raise (or set ctx.exchange.last_error and re-raise after dedup) so the worker classifies the job as transient-failed and retries. At minimum, return a tuple (rows, partial: bool) and have run_sync_funding_job set a strategy-level data_quality_flag `funding_partial_fetch` so PositionsTab can show a warning banner.

#### G14-005 · sync-funding cron returns HTTP 200 when 100% of enqueues fail
- **File**: `src/app/api/cron/sync-funding/route.ts:101`
- **Specialist**: `silent-failure-hunter` (confidence 9)
- **Summary**: The cron handler always returns 200 OK with {failed: N, enqueued: 0} when every RPC call rejects. Vercel Cron monitors HTTP status; a 200 with all-failed body looks healthy in the dashboard. Funding ingestion can silently stop for ALL strategies (e.g. RLS regression on enqueue_compute_job, schema drift in compute_jobs, transient DB outage) while monitoring shows green. The per-row console.error is the ONLY signal, and Vercel log retention/alerting on stdout is opt-in.
- **Evidence**: src/app/api/cron/sync-funding/route.ts:101-107 — `return NextResponse.json({ enqueued, failed, total_candidates: rows.length, ...(errors.length > 0 ? { errors: errors.slice(0, 5) } : {}) });` with no status check on `enqueued===0 && rows.length>0` nor `failed === rows.length`.
- **Fix**: When failed > 0 AND enqueued === 0 (total failure), return HTTP 500 with the errors array so Vercel Cron's failure detection trips. When failed > 0 but enqueued > 0, return 207-style payload but still log a Sentry breadcrumb with errorId. Distinguish 'all candidates failed' from 'nothing to do' so silent failure modes generate pages, not green checkmarks.

#### G14-006 · /security page makes false promise: 'Raw fills older than 30 days are hard-deleted by a daily job' — no such retention job exists · _new_
- **File**: `src/app/security/page.tsx:89`
- **Specialist**: `red-team` (confidence 9)
- **Summary**: The new editorial /security page (line 89-92) states verbatim: 'Raw fills older than 30 days are hard-deleted by a daily job; aggregates remain because the factsheet needs them.' This is the lead bullet in the Data Handling section and a SOC2-prep promise to allocators. Verification: migration 056 (retention_crons.sql) installs retention pg_cron jobs for audit_log (2y), audit_log_cold (5y), notification_dispatches (180d), compute_jobs done/30d, compute_jobs failed-cancelled/90d. NO job touches trades or any fills table. grep -rn 'trades.*retention|prune.*trades|DELETE.*trades.*30 day' returns nothing. The only deletion of trades happens inside sync_trades RPC (migration 20260510172558_sync_trades_preserve_fills.sql) which scopes DELETE to is_fill=false rows on a per-strategy replacement — NOT a 30-day retention sweep. This is a material misrepresentation in a public security page that allocators and security researchers will diligence — and the same claim is restated in the downloadable security packet PDF. A pen-test or SOC2 auditor would flag this as a material posture misalignment.
- **Evidence**: src/app/security/page.tsx:89-92 (the new copy added by this PR): 'The data we persist is: read-only exchange API credentials (encrypted), raw trade fills for the last 30 days, and aggregate analytics... Raw fills older than 30 days are hard-deleted by a daily job; aggregates remain because the factsheet needs them.' Cross-check supabase/migrations/20260417110539_retention_crons.sql — covers audit_log, notification_dispatches, compute_jobs only. No cron.schedule job for trades.
- **Fix**: Either (a) implement the retention job before this page ships — add a pg_cron DELETE FROM trades WHERE timestamp < now() - interval '30 days' (consider impact on sync_trades cursor and the Phase 2 raw-fill ingestion's checkpoint); or (b) reword the /security page and security-packet.pdf to match reality (e.g. 'Raw fills are retained while your strategy is listed; deletion happens when you revoke a key or delete the strategy'). Shipping page 1 of the marketing surface with a false security claim is the worst case. This same claim text appears in build-security-packet.html and the linked PDF (committed in this PR).

### HIGH (26)

#### G14-007 · upsert_funding_rows batch-error accumulator path is untested
- **File**: `/Users/helios-mammut/claude-projects/quantalyze/analytics-service/services/funding_fetch.py:486`
- **Specialist**: `pr-test-analyzer` (confidence 8)
- **Summary**: funding_fetch.py:486-493 catches per-batch exceptions and accumulates them into `errors[]` (truncated to 200 chars), incrementing nothing in `total`. This is the shared error-handling contract used by both the job_worker and the backfill script. The only existing test of `upsert_funding_rows` is in test_funding_backfill_idempotency.py and it only asserts the happy path (call shape + batch sizes). A regression that turned the except into `raise` (so a single bad batch aborts the rest), or one that didn't truncate the error string (DB error containing a secret leaks through `errors`), would not be caught.
- **Evidence**: `grep -rn 'upsert_funding_rows' analytics-service/tests/` → only happy-path call-shape tests in test_funding_backfill_idempotency.py:90-91, 107, 146. Nothing exercises the `except Exception as exc` branch (funding_fetch.py:489).
- **Fix**: Add to /Users/helios-mammut/claude-projects/quantalyze/analytics-service/tests/test_funding_fetch.py a `TestUpsertFundingRowsErrors` class: (a) `test_partial_batch_failure_records_error_continues` — first batch raises, second succeeds → result['inserted']==len(second batch), result['errors'] has 1 entry; (b) `test_error_string_truncated_to_200` — raise Exception('x'*500); assert all(len(e)<=200 for e in result['errors']); (c) `test_empty_rows_short_circuits` (move from backfill-only).

#### G14-008 · serialize_funding_row has zero direct tests
- **File**: `/Users/helios-mammut/claude-projects/quantalyze/analytics-service/services/funding_fetch.py:433`
- **Specialist**: `pr-test-analyzer` (confidence 8)
- **Summary**: `serialize_funding_row` is the JSON-safety helper used before every UPSERT into funding_fees. It converts `Decimal` amounts to strings (preserving precision) and datetime timestamps to ISO strings. A regression that turned `str(row['amount'])` into `float(row['amount'])` would silently introduce float drift on financial cashflows — a class of bug that funding precision was specifically engineered to avoid (see the 'Preserved verbatim via Decimal to avoid float drift' comment at line 162). The serializer also has a non-isoformat fallback branch (`if hasattr(ts, 'isoformat')`) — if a caller passes a pre-stringified timestamp the function returns it as-is, which is also untested.
- **Evidence**: `grep -rn 'serialize_funding_row' analytics-service/tests/` → zero hits. Function defined at funding_fetch.py:433-451; used internally by upsert_funding_rows (line 477) and via backfill.
- **Fix**: Add /Users/helios-mammut/claude-projects/quantalyze/analytics-service/tests/test_funding_fetch.py::TestSerializeFundingRow: (a) `test_decimal_amount_stringified` — input row {'amount': Decimal('-0.012345678901234')} → output['amount']=='-0.012345678901234' (string, no float drift); (b) `test_datetime_isoformat` — input ts=datetime(2024,1,1,8,0,0,tzinfo=utc) → output endswith '+00:00'; (c) `test_string_timestamp_passthrough` — input ts='2024-01-01T08:00:00+00:00' → output equals input; (d) `test_raw_data_passes_through_unchanged`.

#### G14-017 · Route test does not assert is_active filter or PERP_EXCHANGES IN list
- **File**: `/Users/helios-mammut/claude-projects/quantalyze/src/app/api/cron/sync-funding/route.ts:39`

The test mock chains the same method names but doesn't assert what arguments were passed. A regression that drops the is_active filter (enqueues sync_funding for revoked keys) or expands the IN list (calls fetch_funding for an unsupported exchange and crashes inside the worker) would not fail any test. This is a payment-/billing-adjacent path: every spurious enqueue spends a compute job.
- **Evidence**: `grep -n 'is_active\|PERP_EXCHANGES\|api_keys!inner' src/app/api/cron/sync-funding/route.test.ts` → zero hits. The current mocks ignore all eq()/in() arguments.
