Also assert select('id, api_keys!inner(...)') string contains 'api_keys!inner' so a future drop of the inner-join contract fails.

#### G14-018 · Binance perps with 4-hour funding cycle silently lose half their events due to 8h match_key collapse · _new_
- **File**: `analytics-service/services/funding_fetch.py:234`
- **Specialist**: `red-team` (confidence 8)
- **Summary**: _bucket_8h deterministically buckets every funding event into one of three UTC windows per day (00, 08, 16). Binance's funding cadence is documented as '8 hours' in most pairs but a non-trivial subset of high-volume perps (BTCDOMUSDT, certain ALT perps under volatility regimes) pays funding at a 4-hour cadence — and Binance has been increasing the 4h roster over time as new pairs launch with the shorter cycle. Two funding events inside the same 8h window will collide on the same match_key (strategy:exchange:symbol:bucketed_ts) — the second event hits ON CONFLICT (match_key) DO NOTHING and is silently discarded. Position attribution then under-counts funding for those pairs by ~50%. No DQ flag is set; the logger.info at funding_fetch.py:219 reports the fetched count (which IS correct) — the loss happens at the UPSERT layer where postgres silently DROPs the duplicate.
- **Evidence**: funding_fetch.py:234-246 _bucket_8h hard-codes hour_bucket = (ts.hour // 8) * 8. funding_fetch.py:480-484 upsert(rows_to_insert, on_conflict='match_key', ignore_duplicates=True) silently drops collisions. Compare to Binance docs: funding rates can be 1h, 4h, or 8h depending on market conditions — and a single pair can switch cadence mid-history. supabase/migrations/20260416081039_funding_fees.sql header at line 56 acknowledges only '3× daily funding cadence' as the supported assumption.
- **Fix**: Include the EXACT event timestamp (rounded to ms or hour) in match_key instead of the bucketed cadence: f'{strategy_id}:{exchange}:{symbol}:{ts.isoformat()}' and rely on the exchange's own uniqueness (Binance returns one event per cycle). Alternatively, derive bucket size from a per-exchange config: Binance can be 4h; OKX/Bybit stay 8h. Add a regression test with two same-symbol events 4h apart and assert both land in the table.

#### G14-019 · Systemic: 10+ silent failure paths across funding pipeline return 'success' with no DQ flag — fail-loud rule violated · _new_
- **File**: `analytics-service/services/funding_fetch.py:1`
- **Specialist**: `red-team` (confidence 8)
- **Summary**: Pattern repeated across files in this batch (10+ instances visible in the diff): funding_fetch.py:183 break-on-exception (Binance); :247-249 silent return on missing endpoint; :263-268 silent return on per-page failure (OKX); :270-274 silent return on shape mismatch; :347-355 break-on-exception (Bybit); position_reconstruction.py:395-401 swallow then return; :414-420 silent skip parse failure; :442-443 swallow with continue; src/app/api/cron/sync-funding/route.ts:101 returns 200 on all-failed. Per CLAUDE.md Rule 12 ('Fail loud — Completed is wrong if anything was skipped silently'), the funding pipeline violates the rule at every boundary. The pattern compounds: one silent failure doesn't trigger an investigation; ten of them mean the pipeline can be 100% degraded for an exchange and the only visible signal is funding_pnl=0 in the UI for ALL strategies on that exchange. Allocators see clean numbers, no banner, no alert.
- **Evidence**: Files: analytics-service/services/funding_fetch.py (5+ silent paths), analytics-service/services/position_reconstruction.py (3+ silent paths), src/app/api/cron/sync-funding/route.ts (1 silent path). No aggregated_data_quality_flags writes in funding code, no Sentry calls, no metrics emit. Only logger.warning/info — which production filters at WARN+.
- **Fix**: Systemic policy: every silent-skip path in the funding pipeline must increment a per-strategy aggregated_data_quality_flags counter that surfaces in analytics.data_quality_flags. PositionsTab (and the public discovery page if/when positions become visible to non-owners) reads the flag and renders a banner. The cron handler 500s on total failure. The Python worker raises (not warns+continues) on ccxt regressions. This is one ~30-line patch across 3 files + a UI banner. Without it, the funding cutover is unreliable in production and the team won't know.

#### G14-020 · Bybit funding falls back to '0' when all three amount fields are missing
- **File**: `analytics-service/services/funding_fetch.py:366`
- **Specialist**: `silent-failure-hunter` (confidence 9)
- **Summary**: For each Bybit transaction-log item, the fetcher reads `item.get('funding') or item.get('change') or item.get('cashFlow') or '0'`. If Bybit changes their field names (they have already done so once — funding/change/cashFlow are three rotating names per the comment), this silently inserts a real row into funding_fees with amount='0' and a valid match_key. Position attribution then sees the bucket as 'funding present, value zero' rather than 'no data' and the on-conflict dedup BLOCKS the corrected row from a later fetch attempting to overwrite it (on_conflict='match_key', ignore_duplicates=True at line 482-484). This is a poison-pill: one bad fetch permanently records $0 for every Bybit perp funding event in that 8-hour window for that strategy.
- **Evidence**: funding_fetch.py:361-379 — `funding_raw = item.get('funding') or item.get('change') or item.get('cashFlow') or '0' ... rows.append(row)` followed by funding_fetch.py:475-484 — `supabase.table('funding_fees').upsert(rows_to_insert, on_conflict='match_key', ignore_duplicates=True)`.
- **Fix**: Skip the row when all three fields are missing (`if funding_raw is None: continue`) instead of inserting a zero placeholder. Or use upsert without ignore_duplicates and let later fetches overwrite. Or log.error + raise so the worker classifies the job as failed and retries — never silently inject $0.

#### G14-021 · upsert_funding_rows returns errors array but worker never reads it
- **File**: `analytics-service/services/job_worker.py:953`
- **Specialist**: `silent-failure-hunter` (confidence 8)
- **Summary**: upsert_funding_rows (funding_fetch.py:454-495) catches per-batch UPSERT failures into a `errors: list[str]` field of the return dict, then continues processing the next batch. job_worker.run_sync_funding_job reads `result['inserted']` for logging but completely ignores `result['errors']`. If 9 of 10 batches fail with 'connection reset' but the 10th succeeds, the worker reports `inserted=100` (the partial total), logs no warning, and returns DispatchResult(DONE). 900 funding rows silently missing.
- **Evidence**: funding_fetch.py:486-495 — `except Exception as exc: errors.append(str(exc)[:200]); logger.warning(...); ... return {'inserted': total, 'skipped': 0, 'errors': errors}`. job_worker.py:953-958 — `result = await upsert_funding_rows(...); logger.info('sync_funding: upserted %d funding rows for strategy %s', result['inserted'], strategy_id); return DispatchResult(outcome=DispatchOutcome.DONE)` — errors discarded.
- **Fix**: After the upsert call, if `result['errors']` is non-empty, return DispatchResult(outcome=FAILED, error_kind='transient', error_message=f"{len(result['errors'])} upsert batches failed: {result['errors'][:3]}") so the job is retried. Or at minimum, logger.error each entry with strategy_id so on-call has a searchable signature.

#### G14-022 · _attribute_funding() crashes with ValueError when all positions have null opened_at — outside try/except
- **File**: `analytics-service/services/position_reconstruction.py:362`
- **Specialist**: `data-migration` (confidence 9)
- **Summary**: `min_opened_at = min(p['opened_at'] for p in positions if p.get('opened_at'))` raises ValueError('min() arg is an empty sequence') if every position has falsy opened_at. The line sits BEFORE the try/except block (which starts at line 373 and only wraps the DB fetch). The exception escapes _attribute_funding and breaks the entire reconstruct_positions run for that strategy — funding attribution is supposed to fail soft (per the docstring 'positions will get funding_pnl=0') but actually fails hard for this case. Real risk on freshly-onboarded strategies before the first sync, or partial-data scenarios where all positions are open with NULL opened_at.
- **Evidence**: position_reconstruction.py:354-365. Line 354 returns if positions is empty. Lines 362-365 compute min_opened_at and max_closed_at OUTSIDE the try block. Line 373 starts `try:` only wrapping the funding_fees fetch. Lines 395-401's except only catches errors from the DB fetch, not from the bounding-window computation. Although _match_positions_fifo always assigns opened_at from a fill timestamp (line 564), a fill with NULL/empty timestamp would propagate as `position_open_time = None` (lines 766 reset path) — making this reachable.
- **Fix**: Wrap min/max in a try/except ValueError that returns early (matching the docstring contract), or compute defensively: `valid_opens = [p['opened_at'] for p in positions if p.get('opened_at')]; if not valid_opens: return; min_opened_at = min(valid_opens)`. Add a regression test exercising the empty-window path.

#### G14-023 · _attribute_funding range query uses unparsed/un-normalized opened_at string — corrupt closed_at poisons the whole-strategy range scan · _new_
- **File**: `analytics-service/services/position_reconstruction.py:362`
- **Specialist**: `red-team` (confidence 8)
- **Summary**: Lines 362-365 compute the outer query bounds min_opened_at and max_closed_at as raw STRINGS from the position dicts. These strings come from fill.get('timestamp') in _match_positions_fifo (line 564) — values that originate in raw exchange responses (Binance time-ms, OKX/Bybit ISO with offset). Even if normalized to UTC at the writer, ONE corrupt closed_at (non-ISO, e.g. '2026-04-15 10:00:00' without a 'T', or a Unix ms int as string) makes max_closed_at lexically-max but parsed-invalid by PostgREST when injected into .lte('timestamp', max_closed_at). PostgREST returns 400 → the broad except Exception at line 395 swallows it → ALL positions in that strategy keep funding_pnl=0 silently. The inner per-row parse loop (line 437-455) is defensive, but the OUTER bound computation is naive lexical min/max with no validation. A single bad position poisons the entire strategy's funding attribution without any DQ flag. The silent-failure-hunter caught the inner skip path but not this outer poison-pill.
- **Evidence**: position_reconstruction.py:362 min_opened_at = min(p['opened_at'] for p in positions if p.get('opened_at')) — no type or format check. Line 364 (p.get('closed_at') or now.isoformat()) returns raw string. Lines 383-385 inject directly into PostgREST. If any position has closed_at='2026-04-15 not-an-iso' the SELECT fails 400 → caught at 395 → ALL positions get funding_pnl=0 with one warning log.
- **Fix**: Validate bounds before the query: parse both into datetime, fall back to a sentinel like datetime(1970,1,1) / datetime.now(timezone.utc) if any position is corrupt, and log a DQ flag funding_window_corrupt_position. Better: compute the bounds AFTER per-position parsing — only positions that successfully parsed contribute to the range. Combined with chain finding below: add aggregated_data_quality_flags['funding_attribution_failed'] = True before the early return.

#### G14-024 · reconstruct_positions_atomic RPC payload mixes float-serialized funding_pnl with string-serialized money columns — silent precision drift · _chain_ · refs: data-migration:4, type-design-analyzer:10
- **File**: `analytics-service/services/position_reconstruction.py:464`
- **Specialist**: `red-team` (confidence 9)
- **Summary**: Line 464 writes pos['funding_pnl'] = float(round(total, 8)) while every other money column in the same payload (realized_pnl, fee_total, entry_price_avg) is round-tripped via str(...) so the RPC's (elem->>'realized_pnl')::NUMERIC cast accepts arbitrary-precision text. funding_pnl uniquely goes via Python float → JSON 1.23 → Postgres NUMERIC cast. This shouldn't matter for sub-million-dollar funding flows, BUT: the payload travels through supabase-py's json.dumps which writes float 1.0000000000000002 for IEEE-754 dust accumulated from Decimal → float conversion — this dust becomes ~10 silent extra digits in the stored NUMERIC column. Reconstruction is rerun every analytics tick so the digits drift on each run. The data-migration specialist (row 4) flagged the float-trip but missed that this CONTRADICTS the rest of the same JSONB payload's string-based round-trip — it's a 5-second fix to make funding_pnl match the established pattern but the inconsistency is a code-smell that will bite a future refactor.
- **Evidence**: position_reconstruction.py:464 pos['funding_pnl'] = float(round(total, 8)). Compare to the rest of the payload (e.g. line 716-722 for closed positions) where realized_pnl/entry_price/exit_price are NOT coerced to float. supabase/migrations/20260510181748_positions_atomic_rebuild_rpc.sql:145 accepts (elem->>'funding_pnl')::NUMERIC so the cast handles strings natively.
- **Fix**: Change to pos['funding_pnl'] = str(round(total, 8)) matching realized_pnl. One-line fix, no test changes needed (the cast in 113 RPC already accepts strings).

#### G14-025 · _attribute_funding swallows fetch failure and zeros funding_pnl with no DQ flag
- **File**: `analytics-service/services/position_reconstruction.py:395`
- **Specialist**: `silent-failure-hunter` (confidence 9)
- **Summary**: When the funding_fees SELECT fails (RLS regression, table missing on a stale staging DB, transient DB outage, PostgREST overload), the broad `except Exception` writes a logger.warning, returns early, and every position keeps funding_pnl=0 (the default seeded at lines 727 & 790). aggregated_data_quality_flags is NOT updated with a `funding_attribution_failed` counter — even though that exact pattern already exists for breakeven_positions and positions_missing_realized_pnl. PositionsTab.tsx:46-48 then computes `hasFunding = closedPositions.some((p) => p.funding_pnl != null && p.funding_pnl !== 0)` and the tooltip silently hides funding. Allocators see 'Price ROI excludes funding payments' which is a LIE when funding fetch errored — they'll assume the strategy didn't pay funding, when in fact we couldn't load it.
- **Evidence**: position_reconstruction.py:395-401 — `except Exception as exc: logger.warning('funding_fees fetch failed for strategy %s: %s — positions will get funding_pnl=0', strategy_id, exc); return` — note the comment explicitly admits the silent degradation, but no DQ flag is set. Compare with lines 287-294 where breakevens / missing_pnl DO get flagged.
- **Fix**: Add `aggregated_data_quality_flags['funding_attribution_failed'] = True` (or a counter) before the return. Plumb that through reconstruct_positions out['data_quality_flags'] so analytics_runner surfaces it on strategy_analytics.data_quality_flags. PositionsTab.tsx should read this flag and render an explicit warning banner like 'Funding data unavailable — ROI shown excludes funding payments'.

#### G14-026 · All-failed enqueue batch returns HTTP 200, hides cron-wide outage from Vercel alerting
- **File**: `src/app/api/cron/sync-funding/route.ts:101`
- **Specialist**: `api-contract` (confidence 9)
- **Summary**: When every enqueue rejects/errors (e.g. RPC permission revoked, _enqueue_compute_job_internal regression, transient DB outage), the route still returns 200 with `{enqueued:0, failed:N, total_candidates:N, errors:[...]}`. Vercel Cron's failure alerting only fires on non-2xx, so a totally-broken funding sync produces a green cron history. The sibling cron route reconcile-strategies/route.ts:121 already added an explicit `status = enqueued === 0 && errors.length > 0 ? 500 : 200` gate for exactly this reason; sync-funding never picked up the same fix, so the contracts diverge between two crons that share the same shape and same RPC.
- **Evidence**: src/app/api/cron/sync-funding/route.ts:101-106 returns the result envelope with no `{status}` argument (defaults to 200) even when `enqueued=0` and `failed>0`. Compare reconcile-strategies/route.ts:121-130 which conditionally returns 500 in the same situation.
- **Fix**: Mirror reconcile-strategies: compute `const status = enqueued === 0 && errors.length > 0 ? 500 : 200;` and pass `{ status }` to `NextResponse.json`. Add a regression test that mocks all RPC calls to reject and asserts `res.status === 500`.

#### G14-027 · Cron all-fail returns 200 + audit-skip + DB FK silent precondition = funding can stop without paging · _chain_ · refs: silent-failure-hunter:1, api-contract:1, silent-failure-hunter:2
- **File**: `src/app/api/cron/sync-funding/route.ts:101`
- **Specialist**: `red-team` (confidence 9)
- **Summary**: Chain: (1) silent-failure-hunter:1 + api-contract:1 — sync-funding cron returns 200 even when 100% of enqueues fail (compare reconcile-strategies/route.ts:121 which 500s correctly). (2) The route comment at line 64-69 (current main) explicitly @audit-skips audit logging because 'Vercel Cron requests don't carry a JWT'. (3) The cron path uses enqueue_compute_job which depends on compute_job_kinds having 'sync_funding' registered — but the migration's DO block (line 244-248) checks for the registry entry at migration-apply time, not at runtime. If a future schema-drift event drops the row (e.g. a compute_job_kinds prune script), every enqueue fails with FK constraint violation, cron returns 200 with errors[], no audit row, Vercel sees green checkmark. Funding ingestion is dead for ALL strategies until someone notices. The chain is: silent HTTP success + silent audit gap + silent DB FK precondition.
- **Evidence**: src/app/api/cron/sync-funding/route.ts:101-106 returns 200 envelope. Same route lines 64-69 acknowledge no audit. supabase/migrations/20260416081039_funding_fees.sql:244-248 only validates kind registration at MIGRATION time, not at every cron tick. compute_jobs.kind has FK to compute_job_kinds.name (migration 032).
- **Fix**: Three-line route fix: const status = enqueued === 0 && errors.length > 0 ? 500 : 200; return NextResponse.json({...}, { status });. Plus an integration-level smoke that asserts compute_job_kinds still contains 'sync_funding' at the start of each cron tick (or migration to make the row immortal via CHECK constraint preventing DELETE). Add a Sentry breadcrumb when status === 500 so on-call gets paged.

#### G14-028 · Promise.allSettled result with no .data and no .error silently dropped
- **File**: `src/app/api/cron/sync-funding/route.ts:96`
- **Specialist**: `silent-failure-hunter` (confidence 9)
- **Summary**: The enqueue dispatch counter only increments `enqueued` when `result.value.data` is truthy. If the RPC returns `{data: null, error: null}` (which happens when enqueue_compute_job is dropped/replaced or returns void), the row is counted as neither enqueued nor failed — it just vanishes. total_candidates !== enqueued + failed becomes the only signal, and nothing in the response or logs flags the discrepancy. Operators looking at {enqueued: 3, failed: 0, total_candidates: 10} would assume 7 strategies were intentionally skipped.
- **Evidence**: src/app/api/cron/sync-funding/route.ts:92-99 — `} else if (result.value.error) { failed += 1; ... } else if (result.value.data) { enqueued += 1; }` — the missing else swallows the (null data, null error) case.
- **Fix**: Add an explicit `else` branch that increments `failed` and pushes an error like `${row.id}: rpc returned null data with no error`, plus a console.error. Or assert `enqueued + failed === rows.length` before returning and 500 on mismatch.

#### G14-029 · Funding attribution silent zero + missing DQ flag + tooltip lie compound into allocator-facing misinformation · _chain_ · refs: silent-failure-hunter:4, silent-failure-hunter:5, code-reviewer:1, silent-failure-hunter:1

Allocator forwards the screenshot in diligence and the firm shows a number that's neither price-only nor total-economic. #### G14-030 · FundingFee.exchange duplicates SupportedExchange literal union instead of referencing the canonical type
- **File**: `src/lib/types.ts:450`
- **Specialist**: `type-design-analyzer` (confidence 9)
- **Summary**: `FundingFee.exchange: "binance" | "okx" | "bybit"` hardcodes the literal union instead of importing `SupportedExchange` from `src/lib/utils.ts` (line 122). When Sprint 6 adds a fourth exchange (e.g. Kraken) to `SUPPORTED_EXCHANGES`, `FundingFee.exchange` will silently fail to widen and downstream consumers will dead-code the new exchange. This already happened on `Position.side` historically — invariant must be canonical, not duplicated.

- **Fix**: Replace the inline union with `exchange: SupportedExchange;` and `import type { SupportedExchange } from "./utils";`. Single source of truth eliminates drift.

#### G14-031 · FundingFee has no Zod schema at the trust boundary — NUMERIC-as-string from PostgREST will silently NaN downstream math
- **File**: `src/lib/types.ts:447`
- **Specialist**: `type-design-analyzer` (confidence 9)
- **Summary**: `Position` rows are parsed through `PositionRowSchema` with `z.coerce.number()` on every NUMERIC column (lines 383-402) precisely because PostgREST returns DECIMAL/NUMERIC as strings when arbitrary precision matters. `FundingFee.amount: number` has no Zod guard at all. The moment a UI consumer reads `funding_fees` directly (the diff already extends the `positions` projection to include `funding_pnl`, and similar consumers will read funding_fees rows for breakdowns), `Number('123.45') === NaN` won't happen but arithmetic on the string will produce string concatenation or NaN.
- **Evidence**: src/lib/types.ts:447-458 defines `interface FundingFee { amount: number; ... }` with no companion `FundingFeeRowSchema`; PR added Zod hardening for Position rows (G12.E.1 comment at line 352) but did not extend the pattern to the newly-added type.
- **Fix**: Add `FundingFeeRowSchema` mirroring PositionRowSchema patterns: `z.coerce.number()` on amount, `z.string().datetime({ offset: true })` on timestamp, `z.enum(SUPPORTED_EXCHANGES)` on exchange, `.strict()` to surface drift. Export a `parseFundingFeeRows()` helper for the trust boundary.

#### G14-032 · funding_fees.exchange TEXT NOT NULL has no CHECK constraint — DB allows values the TS type forbids
- **File**: `supabase/migrations/20260416081039_funding_fees.sql:90`
- **Specialist**: `type-design-analyzer` (confidence 8)
- **Summary**: The DB column is `exchange TEXT NOT NULL` with no CHECK constraint pinning it to (binance, okx, bybit), while `FundingFee.exchange` narrows TS to those three literals. A misbehaving backfill script or a future exchange-name typo will write rows the TS type claims are impossible. Compare to migrations 020/032's compute_job_kinds registry which pins kind names via FK; the funding_fees table chose a free-text column and the only enforcement is in Python service code (`fetch_funding_binance` hardcodes `"binance"`).
- **Evidence**: supabase/migrations/20260416081039_funding_fees.sql:90 `exchange TEXT NOT NULL,` with no `CHECK (exchange IN ('binance','okx','bybit'))` and no FK to a kinds table. TS at src/lib/types.ts:450 narrows to the three literals.
- **Fix**: Either (a) add a CHECK constraint `CHECK (exchange IN ('binance','okx','bybit'))` to the column, or (b) FK to a small `funding_supported_exchanges(name)` lookup table mirroring `compute_job_kinds`. Option (a) is simpler and matches the surface area.

#### G14-038 · PositionsTab funding_pnl null/undefined handling untested

Next.js compiles the matcher string differently (path-to-regexp under the hood). A regression where Next.js silently parses the new pattern differently (after a framework upgrade) would not be caught.

#### G14-040 · OKX funding _paginate silently no-ops when the ccxt endpoint method is missing
- **File**: `analytics-service/services/funding_fetch.py:247`
- **Specialist**: `code-reviewer` (confidence 8)
- **Summary**: fetch_funding_okx wraps each endpoint call in a getattr(exchange, endpoint_name, None) check and returns silently if the method does not exist. Because private_get_account_bills_archive only exists when need_archive is true, a ccxt version bump that renames or removes the method drops all archive coverage (and similarly recent bills if the primary endpoint name changes) without any log warning. Combined with the broad `except Exception` swallowing on line 263-268 (logger.warning only), a ccxt API churn produces zero funding rows for OKX strategies with NO operator-visible error — silently understating funding_pnl in production until the next reconstruct surfaces 'positions get funding_pnl=0'.
- **Evidence**: analytics-service/services/funding_fetch.py:247-249 — `endpoint = getattr(exchange, endpoint_name, None); if endpoint is None: return` returns silently with no log. The dispatcher / job_worker sees empty rows and reports 'no funding rows' as a normal success path.
- **Fix**: Log a warning (or raise) when getattr returns None: at minimum `logger.warning('OKX endpoint %s missing on ccxt %s — funding ingestion incomplete', endpoint_name, ccxt.__version__)` so on-call sees the regression. The pattern repeats for `private_get_account_bills` too — silent miss means the archive-fallback path is the only one logged.

#### G14-041 · Bybit funding field fallback prefers truthy chain that drops legitimate zero values
- **File**: `analytics-service/services/funding_fetch.py:368`
- **Specialist**: `code-reviewer` (confidence 8)
- **Summary**: The Bybit normalizer at fetch_funding_bybit uses Python 'or' short-circuit fallback: `funding_raw = item.get('funding') or item.get('change') or item.get('cashFlow') or '0'`. If an exchange row has 'funding'=0 (numeric zero or float 0.0), the `or` chain falls through to 'change'; if 'change'=0 too, falls to 'cashFlow'. This corrupts the signed amount for any legitimate-zero funding row (rare but real on cycle boundaries where a perp position pays no funding for a window). Worse, if any of those fields contain a non-funding cashflow (e.g. realized PnL ledger entry that Bybit accidentally tags SETTLEMENT), the fallback uses the WRONG number. Should use explicit 'in' / `is not None` check, not truthy fallback.
- **Evidence**: analytics-service/services/funding_fetch.py:362-368 — `funding_raw = (item.get('funding') or item.get('change') or item.get('cashFlow') or '0')`. Strings '0' and '-0.0' are truthy in Python; numeric 0 and 0.0 are falsy. Inconsistent typing across Bybit responses → inconsistent fallback target.
- **Fix**: Use an explicit None check: `for key in ('funding','change','cashFlow'): val = item.get(key); if val is not None: funding_raw = val; break; else: funding_raw = '0'`. This isolates 'field missing' from 'field present but zero', the latter of which is a legitimate cycle row.

#### G14-042 · raw_data shallow dict() copy may carry non-JSON-serializable ccxt types — silent batch UPSERT drop on encode error · _new_
- **File**: `analytics-service/services/funding_fetch.py:119`
- **Specialist**: `red-team` (confidence 8)
- **Summary**: _normalize_funding_row writes dict(raw_item) (shallow copy) into the row's raw_data JSONB column. raw_item comes from ccxt's response parser, which can include Decimal, custom date types, and per-exchange ccxt-internal classes (e.g. ccxt's OrderType enum in some response variants). supabase-py's PostgREST client calls json.dumps(payload) which raises TypeError: Object of type X is not JSON serializable on the first non-coercible value. The upsert_funding_rows except clause at line 489 catches all exceptions and adds to errors[] — but truncates to 200 chars so the full traceback is lost. The error message itself only mentions the FIRST offending type; subsequent debugging is from cold memory. Worse, a future ccxt upgrade could quietly introduce a new non-JSON type and the batch UPSERT silently drops 100 rows per failure with no DQ flag.
- **Evidence**: funding_fetch.py:119 dict(raw_item) — shallow copy preserves Decimal/datetime/ccxt types. funding_fetch.py:486-493 except Exception as exc: errors.append(str(exc)[:200]) — truncated, no stacktrace, no row identification. No default= parameter passed to json.dumps anywhere in the call chain.
- **Fix**: Add a _sanitize_raw(value) helper that recursively converts Decimal→str, datetime→isoformat, sets→list, custom-class→str(...). Apply at the boundary in _normalize_funding_row. Or use json.dumps(payload, default=str) upstream (less surgical). Also: lift the truncation length to 1000 chars and add repr(rows_to_insert[0])[:200] to the error to identify which exchange's response shape regressed.

#### G14-043 · Bybit category='linear' filter excludes inverse perpetuals — strategies trading BTCUSD (inverse) silently get zero funding · _new_
- **File**: `analytics-service/services/funding_fetch.py:338`
- **Specialist**: `red-team` (confidence 8)
- **Summary**: fetch_funding_bybit hard-codes params['category'] = 'linear' (line 338). Bybit categorizes perpetuals into 'linear' (USDT-quoted: BTCUSDT) and 'inverse' (coin-margined: BTCUSD). A strategy that trades inverse perps gets zero funding rows fetched even though the underlying trades produce realized_pnl via the daily_pnl path. Position attribution then reports funding_pnl=0 for inverse perp positions and hasFunding=false, so the tooltip lies again. Bybit's API requires SEPARATE calls per category (no 'all' option). No DQ flag, no error log — just silently incomplete.
- **Evidence**: funding_fetch.py:338 'category': 'linear'. Bybit v5 docs: category is required and must be one of linear/inverse/spot/option — funding settlements live in both linear AND inverse. SUPPORTED_EXCHANGES in src/lib/utils.ts has only one bybit entry, with no inverse/linear distinction.
- **Fix**: Loop over ['linear', 'inverse'] and merge the results: for cat in ('linear', 'inverse'): result = await ...; items.extend(...). Optionally branch on whether the strategy's known symbols suggest inverse vs linear, but the safe default is to fetch both. Add a regression test with an inverse-perp Bybit fixture.

#### G14-044 · OKX bills-archive endpoint missing check returns silently — archive-only history (>90d) becomes invisible · _chain_ · refs: code-reviewer:3, silent-failure-hunter:8
- **File**: `analytics-service/services/funding_fetch.py:247`
- **Specialist**: `red-team` (confidence 8)
- **Summary**: Chain finding: code-reviewer:3 + silent-failure-hunter:8 flagged that getattr(exchange, endpoint_name, None) returns silently on missing endpoint. Combined with the need_archive branching at line 297 (if need_archive: await _paginate('private_get_account_bills_archive')), a ccxt version that drops private_get_account_bills_archive causes OKX strategies with > 90d history to receive ZERO archive rows. The recent endpoint runs successfully (silent miss for the archive call), but everything older than 90 days is silently absent. The OKX dedup at line 300-307 only operates over what was fetched — it can't recover missed pages. Backfill script then completes successfully with inserted=N where N excludes the archive segment. Result: any OKX perp strategy older than 90 days has incomplete funding history with NO operator-visible signal.
- **Evidence**: funding_fetch.py:247-249 silent return on missing endpoint. Line 297 if need_archive: await _paginate('private_get_account_bills_archive'). Line 309-311 logger.info only reports what WAS fetched, not what was attempted. Backfill scripts/backfill_funding.py:687 logs inserted=N — no operator-visible asymmetry warning.
- **Fix**: At funding_fetch.py:247-249 (and the recent endpoint path), raise instead of silently return: if endpoint is None: raise RuntimeError(f'OKX endpoint {endpoint_name} missing on ccxt {ccxt.__version__}'). Job_worker classifies this as transient or permanent based on the exception type — both surface in Sentry. Mirrors how sync_trades surfaces auth errors.

#### G14-045 · Challenge security:3 / data-migration:9 / type-design-analyzer:4 — OKX symbol normalization mismatch is NOT live; trades pipeline strips dashes consistently · _challenge_ · refs: security:3, data-migration:9, type-design-analyzer:4
- **File**: `analytics-service/services/funding_fetch.py:278`

- **Summary**: Three specialists raised this concern (security:3, data-migration:9, type-design-analyzer:4): OKX funding_fetch strips dashes (BTC-USDT-SWAP → BTCUSDTSWAP) and the implication is the trades pipeline keeps the hyphenated form, causing a silent join miss against position.symbol. Verification: analytics-service/services/exchange.py:799 symbol = fill.get('instId', '').replace('-', '') — OKX trades ALSO strip dashes when emitting fills. The normalization is consistent across producers in current main. The concern is therefore not LIVE — funding attribution to OKX positions works correctly in current code. The risk is FUTURE drift (one producer changes normalization, the other doesn't), which is a fair defense-in-depth concern, but it's not the silent zero-attribution claimed by the specialists.
- **Evidence**: funding_fetch.py:278 symbol = inst_id.replace('-', '') for OKX funding. exchange.py:799 symbol = fill.get('instId', '').replace('-', '') for OKX trades — same normalization. position_reconstruction.py:458 strict-match by_symbol.get(symbol, []) — both sides agree on the de-hyphenated form.
- **Fix**: Acknowledge the live-code is consistent. The defense-in-depth refactor (single normalize_symbol(exchange, raw) helper, brand type) remains a fair backlog item but is NOT a production correctness bug today. Downgrade severity from high/medium to low or close as 'consistent in main, file for future hardening'.

#### G14-046 · _normalize_funding_row silently drops rows on Decimal/timestamp parse failure
- **File**: `analytics-service/services/funding_fetch.py:105`
- **Specialist**: `silent-failure-hunter` (confidence 8)
- **Summary**: `_normalize_funding_row` returns None on bad symbol, bad amount, or bad timestamp. The three exchange callers all do `if row is None: continue` with no counter. If Binance regresses the `income` field format (e.g. returns 'NaN' as a string), every funding event for every strategy is silently dropped, the worker reports `inserted=0`, logs 'no funding rows', and returns DONE. The strategy's positions get funding_pnl=0 from the seeded default, with no DQ flag. The only signal is per-row logger.warning('Failed to parse timestamp') in _parse_ts_ms, which is per-row noise that nobody alerts on.
- **Evidence**: funding_fetch.py:100-105 — `if amount_raw is None: return None\n try: amount = Decimal(str(amount_raw))\n except Exception: return None`. Callers funding_fetch.py:203-204 (Binance), 288-289 (OKX), 377-378 (Bybit) — all `if row is None: continue` with no counter.
- **Fix**: Track `dropped: int` alongside `rows` in each fetcher. If dropped/total > 5% (or dropped > 0 in production), logger.error with strategy_id and a sample raw_item, AND surface as a per-strategy DQ flag `funding_normalize_dropped: N` so PositionsTab can warn.

#### G14-047 · OKX endpoint missing on ccxt object silently returns empty
- **File**: `analytics-service/services/funding_fetch.py:248`
- **Specialist**: `silent-failure-hunter` (confidence 8)
- **Summary**: `_paginate` inside fetch_funding_okx checks `endpoint = getattr(exchange, endpoint_name, None); if endpoint is None: return`. If ccxt drops or renames `private_get_account_bills` / `private_get_account_bills_archive` (these have been renamed before — e.g. ccxt v2 → v4), the function returns silently with zero rows. The worker reports `inserted=0` and DONE; OKX funding for every strategy stops being ingested. No warning is logged at the `endpoint is None` check.
- **Evidence**: funding_fetch.py:247-249 — `endpoint = getattr(exchange, endpoint_name, None)\n if endpoint is None:\n    return` — bare return, no logger call.
- **Fix**: `if endpoint is None: logger.error('OKX endpoint %s missing on ccxt — version drift', endpoint_name); raise RuntimeError(f'ccxt missing OKX endpoint {endpoint_name}')` so the worker classifies the job failed and on-call gets paged via Sentry.

#### G14-048 · OKX result-shape mismatch silently returns empty
- **File**: `analytics-service/services/funding_fetch.py:270`
- **Specialist**: `silent-failure-hunter` (confidence 8)
- **Summary**: After awaiting the OKX endpoint, the code does `if not isinstance(result, dict): return` and `data = result.get('data', []); if not data or not isinstance(data, list): return`. If OKX changes the response envelope, the fetcher exits silently with zero rows. No log line distinguishes 'OKX returned 0 funding events' (legit) from 'OKX returned a string we did not expect' (regression).
- **Evidence**: funding_fetch.py:270-274 — bare `return` on shape mismatch with no log.
- **Fix**: Replace `return` with `logger.error('OKX %s returned unexpected shape: type=%s', endpoint_name, type(result).__name__); return` (or raise) so we have a searchable signal when the envelope drifts.

#### G14-049 · FundingFee.symbol is stringly-typed across exchanges with inconsistent normalization — OKX strips hyphens, others do not
- **File**: `analytics-service/services/funding_fetch.py:449`
- **Specialist**: `type-design-analyzer` (confidence 8)
- **Summary**: `fetch_funding_okx` normalizes `BTC-USDT-SWAP → BTCUSDTSWAP` (line 449) while Binance/Bybit emit `BTCUSDT` unchanged. The `_attribute_funding` step in position_reconstruction.py joins funding rows to positions by exact `symbol` string equality (line 916+). If a position's symbol comes from the positions table (Binance-style `BTCUSDT`) but its funding rows come from OKX (now `BTCUSDTSWAP`), the symbol join silently misses every OKX funding payment. The TS type `FundingFee.symbol: string` has no constraint to surface this drift. This is precisely the kind of stringly-typed key that discriminated normalization should prevent.
- **Evidence**: analytics-service/services/funding_fetch.py:448-453: `inst_id = item.get("instId", "") or ""`; `symbol = inst_id.replace("-", "")` — OKX symbols stripped. position_reconstruction.py:916 `by_symbol[sym].append(...)` then position match at line 953 `for ts, amt in by_symbol.get(symbol, [])` requires exact string equality with position.symbol, which originates from a different fetch path entirely.
- **Fix**: Add a single canonical `normalize_symbol(exchange, raw)` helper used by every producer (trades, positions, funding_fees) and assert symbol shapes in tests. Document the canonical form on `FundingFee.symbol` JSDoc (e.g. "exchange-native instrument id, hyphens stripped"). Better: introduce a `Symbol` brand type to force callers to go through the normalizer.

#### G14-050 · Python funding_fetch returns dict[str, Any] instead of TypedDict — producer-side type contract is unenforced
- **File**: `analytics-service/services/funding_fetch.py:263`
- **Specialist**: `type-design-analyzer` (confidence 8)
- **Summary**: `_normalize_funding_row` returns `dict[str, Any] | None` and `serialize_funding_row(row: dict) -> dict`. The dict shape is exactly `FundingFee` minus `id`/`created_at`, but the Python type does not encode that. A producer typo (`'strategy_id'` → `'strategyId'`, swapping `amount` and `currency`) emits a dict that passes the dict-typed function signature, gets serialized to JSON, and silently inserts a malformed row that fails downstream parsing. The TS side has a strong type; the Python producer has none.
- **Evidence**: analytics-service/services/funding_fetch.py:263 `def _normalize_funding_row(...) -> "dict[str, Any] | None":` returning `{"strategy_id": ..., "exchange": ..., "symbol": ..., "amount": amount, "currency": ..., "timestamp": ts, "match_key": ..., "raw_data": dict(raw_item)}`. Line 604 `def serialize_funding_row(row: dict) -> dict:` accepts arbitrary dict and pulls expected keys via index access — KeyError at runtime if upstream drops a field.
- **Fix**: Define a `FundingFeeRow` `TypedDict` (or Pydantic BaseModel) with strict=True covering the 8 fields, narrow the return types to that TypedDict. Match the rigour the TS side already has.

#### G14-051 · funding_fees pagination uses .range() without explicit .order() — undefined ordering across pages
- **File**: `analytics-service/services/position_reconstruction.py:378`
- **Specialist**: `data-migration` (confidence 8)
- **Summary**: `_attribute_funding` paginates funding_fees in 1000-row pages using `.range(s, e)` but never calls `.order(...)`. PostgREST's default ordering is by primary key, but this is implicit and brittle: any future Supabase/PostgREST change to default ordering (e.g. to optimize for sequential scans) could cause duplicate or missed rows across page boundaries. Since the sum is over a deterministic [opened_at, closed_at] window, missed or doubled rows would silently corrupt funding_pnl.
- **Evidence**: position_reconstruction.py:378-388. The query chain `.select(...).eq('strategy_id', ...).gte('timestamp', ...).lte('timestamp', ...).range(s, e).execute()` has no `.order()`. Compare to sync_trades and other paginators in the codebase that explicitly `.order('timestamp', desc=True)` before `.range()`. PostgREST docs say ordering is undefined without an explicit order clause.
- **Fix**: Add `.order('id')` or `.order('timestamp')` to the chain. Use ascending order to keep page boundaries stable. Add a regression test with > _PAGE_SIZE funding_fees rows that asserts the sum is correct.

#### G14-052 · funding_pnl float-trip from Decimal loses NUMERIC precision before RPC insert
- **File**: `analytics-service/services/position_reconstruction.py:464`
- **Specialist**: `data-migration` (confidence 8)
- **Summary**: `pos['funding_pnl'] = float(round(total, 8))` converts the Decimal sum to Python float for the JSONB payload that ends up in reconstruct_positions_atomic's `(elem->>'funding_pnl')::NUMERIC`. Float has 53-bit mantissa (~15-17 significant digits); for funding amounts at 8 decimal places this loses fidelity (e.g. micro-funding flows from many positions sum into 9-10 significant digits). Other position fields (realized_pnl, fee_total) round-trip via NULLIF + NUMERIC and accept string representations; funding_pnl uniquely casts via float.
- **Evidence**: position_reconstruction.py:464 `pos['funding_pnl'] = float(round(total, 8))` vs the migration-113 RPC at supabase/migrations/20260510181748_positions_atomic_rebuild_rpc.sql:145 `COALESCE((elem->>'funding_pnl')::NUMERIC, 0)`. The funding_fees.amount column is NUMERIC (no precision specified, so arbitrary), but the float coercion loses precision before the JSONB serialization step in reconstruct_positions_atomic. database.types.ts:1868 `funding_pnl: number` is generated from the migration but reflects the lossy JS-side representation downstream.
- **Fix**: Serialize via `str(round(total, 8))` instead of `float(round(total, 8))`, mirroring how realized_pnl is round-tripped. The RPC reads via `(elem->>'funding_pnl')::NUMERIC` which already accepts string. Add a regression test with high-precision funding amounts that asserts no precision loss.

#### G14-053 · _attribute_funding range scan: min/max ISO string comparison is fragile with mixed-offset timestamps
- **File**: `analytics-service/services/position_reconstruction.py:362`
- **Specialist**: `data-migration` (confidence 8)
- **Summary**: `min_opened_at = min(p['opened_at'] for ... if ...)` uses Python's lexical string compare on ISO 8601. This is correct ONLY when all opened_at values are normalized to the same zone (UTC with 'Z' or '+00:00'). If a position has a string like '2026-04-15T10:00:00+02:00' and another '2026-04-15T08:00:00+00:00', they represent the same instant but '2026-04-15T08...' sorts before '2026-04-15T10...', so the min picks the second — correct in this example but undetermined in general. Then the gte/lte filter sends that string to PostgREST which compares as TIMESTAMPTZ.
- **Evidence**: position_reconstruction.py:362-365. Fill timestamps in this codebase are constructed by exchange.py / sync_trades and normalized to UTC ISO, so practical risk is low — but the contract is implicit. If any code path persists opened_at with offset != 00, lexical min can silently widen the range and pull extra funding_fees rows or miss them.
- **Fix**: Parse opened_at to a tz-aware datetime in the min/max generators (mirror what the later loop does at line 437), then take min/max on datetimes. Or assert opened_at always ends in '+00:00'/'Z' before lexical compare. Defensive only — current writers all emit UTC.

#### G14-054 · _attribute_funding uses OFFSET-based pagination instead of keyset
- **File**: `analytics-service/services/position_reconstruction.py:385`
- **Specialist**: `performance` (confidence 8)
- **Summary**: The funding_fees fetch paginates with PostgREST `.range(s, e)` which translates to SQL OFFSET/LIMIT. For positions with thousands of funding rows (long-lived strategies with many symbols), each successive page costs O(start) on the server because PostgREST has to skip `start` rows before returning. cost/frequency: reconstruct_positions runs on every analytics recompute. With ~10k funding rows over a long backfill, page-9 fetch is ~9x slower than page-1. Idx is (strategy_id, timestamp DESC) so keyset by (timestamp, id) tuple is feasible.
- **Evidence**: analytics-service/services/position_reconstruction.py:374-394         while True:             start = page * _PAGE_SIZE             end = start + _PAGE_SIZE - 1             def _fetch_funding(s=start, e=end):                 return (                     supabase.table("funding_fees")                     .select("symbol, amount, timestamp")                     .eq("strategy_id", strategy_id)                     .gte("timestamp", min_opened_at)                     .lte("timestamp", max_closed_at)                     .range(s, e)                     .execute()                 )
- **Fix**: Switch to keyset pagination: track last_timestamp + last_id from the previous page and replace `.range(s, e)` with `.gt("timestamp", last_ts)`. With the existing `(strategy_id, timestamp DESC)` index this gives O(log n) per page regardless of position. Alternatively raise _PAGE_SIZE to 10000 (well within PostgREST's max-rows = ~10k cap) so most strategies fit in one round-trip.

#### G14-055 · _attribute_funding does linear scan per position even when funding timeline is sorted
- **File**: `analytics-service/services/position_reconstruction.py:457`
- **Specialist**: `performance` (confidence 8)
- **Summary**: After sorting by_symbol[sym] by timestamp, _attribute_funding still runs a full O(F) linear scan over each symbol's funding list for every position. Total cost = O(P × F) where P = positions count and F = funding rows per symbol. The sort already establishes ordering — a bisect_left/bisect_right pair (or pre-built cumulative-sum) over the sorted timestamps would reduce this to O(P log F + F). For a 5-year strategy with 100 positions and 1500 funding rows per symbol, that's 150k comparisons per reconstruction call vs ~1.5k with bisect. Frequency: every analytics recompute (15min cron + on-demand).
- **Evidence**: analytics-service/services/position_reconstruction.py:423-460     for sym in by_symbol:         by_symbol[sym].sort(key=lambda x: x[0])     now_utc = datetime.now(timezone.utc)     for pos in positions:         ...         total = Decimal(0)         for ts, amt in by_symbol.get(symbol, []):             if opened_dt <= ts <= closed_dt:                 total += amt
- **Fix**: Build a prefix-sum array per symbol after sorting: `sums = [Decimal(0)]; for ts, amt in sorted: sums.append(sums[-1] + amt)`. Then per position, use `bisect_left(timestamps, opened_dt)` and `bisect_right(timestamps, closed_dt)` to get range indices, and `pos["funding_pnl"] = float(sums[hi] - sums[lo])`. O(P log F) overall.

#### G14-056 · _attribute_funding silently skips positions with malformed opened_at
- **File**: `analytics-service/services/position_reconstruction.py:443`
- **Specialist**: `silent-failure-hunter` (confidence 8)
- **Summary**: Inside the per-position loop, malformed opened_at_raw triggers `except Exception: continue` — the position is silently left with funding_pnl=0 (the seeded default at line 727/790). For a single corrupt row this is fine, but if a serialization regression hits all positions (e.g. opened_at stored as Unix ms instead of ISO), every position is skipped and the strategy quietly reports zero funding everywhere with no DQ flag. Tooltip lies again.
- **Evidence**: position_reconstruction.py:442-443 — `except Exception: continue` with no logger call and no counter; same pattern at 452-453 for closed_at where it falls back to now_utc which is also silent.
- **Fix**: Increment a `funding_skipped_positions` counter on each exception, push to aggregated_data_quality_flags after the loop, and logger.warning at least the first one with `pos.get('id')` and the raw value for debugging.

#### G14-057 · backfill_funding processes strategies serially — no parallelism
- **File**: `scripts/backfill_funding.py:173`
- **Specialist**: `performance` (confidence 8)
- **Summary**: main() loops `for strategy_row in strategies` and awaits `backfill_one_strategy` one at a time. Each strategy spins up a fresh CCXT exchange connection, fetches up to 90 days of funding (200 pages × 1000 rows = ~200k API time per strategy), then upserts. For a 90-day initial backfill across N strategies the wall time scales linearly. Frequency: every initial deploy / KEK rotation / disaster-recovery re-key. With 50 perp strategies × ~5-30s/strategy fetch, this is 4-25 minutes serial vs ~30s parallel.
- **Evidence**: scripts/backfill_funding.py:171-179     total_fetched = 0     total_inserted = 0     for strategy_row in strategies:         key_row = keys_by_id.get(strategy_row.get("api_key_id", ""))         fetched, inserted = await backfill_one_strategy(             supabase, kek, strategy_row, args.lookback_days, key_row=key_row         )
- **Fix**: Replace the serial for-loop with a bounded asyncio.Semaphore + asyncio.gather. Per-exchange rate limits cap per-IP concurrency at ~5-10 in-flight, but per-strategy each fetch is rate-limited internally by ccxt. A bounded concurrency of 5 brings a 50-strategy backfill from ~25min → ~5min. Caveat: keep a per-exchange semaphore (Binance/OKX/Bybit have separate rate buckets) so one slow exchange doesn't block the others.

#### G14-058 · Challenge pr-test-analyzer:13 — discovery page funding_pnl projection is dead code; positions RLS is owner-only · _challenge_ · refs: pr-test-analyzer:13
- **File**: `src/app/(dashboard)/discovery/[slug]/[strategyId]/page.tsx:44`
- **Specialist**: `red-team` (confidence 8)
- **Summary**: pr-test-analyzer:13 calls the discovery positions projection 'a key allocator-facing read path'. Verification disagrees: positions RLS (migration 114 / 20260510182439_positions_schema_rls_g12d.sql:140) is OWNER-ONLY (strategy_id IN (SELECT id FROM strategies WHERE user_id = (SELECT auth.uid())). The discovery page uses createClient() (user-context Supabase) not service-role admin (page.tsx:15, 24). So for any allocator browsing /discovery/[slug]/[strategyId] for a strategy they don't own, positionsResult.data is [] and PositionsTab renders its empty state. The funding_pnl projection added in this PR is dead code on the public discovery surface — the only path where it matters is the strategy owner's own dashboard. Either intentional or a missing service-role read seam, but the pr-test-analyzer characterization that this is 'allocator-facing' is incorrect, and the new code in the diff implies funding is visible in discovery when it isn't.
- **Evidence**: src/app/(dashboard)/discovery/[slug]/[strategyId]/page.tsx:15 import { createClient } from '@/lib/supabase/server' (user-context). Line 24 await createClient(). Line 43 .from('positions').select(...funding_pnl...). Cross-check supabase/migrations/20260510182439_positions_schema_rls_g12d.sql:140-147 — owner-only.
- **Fix**: Either (a) restructure the discovery page to fetch a redacted/aggregated positions view via service-role admin for non-owner viewers (mirror getStrategyDetail's published-strategy pattern), or (b) drop the funding_pnl from the discovery query since it's dead code there. Decision is product-side, but shipping the projection without surfacing the data is wasted bytes on the SSR payload and a misleading test target.

#### G14-059 · Response envelope shape drifts between empty and populated paths
- **File**: `src/app/api/cron/sync-funding/route.ts:55`
- **Specialist**: `api-contract` (confidence 9)
- **Summary**: The two success branches return structurally different JSON envelopes: the empty-rows branch returns `{enqueued: 0, skipped: 0}` (uses a `skipped` field that never appears anywhere else), while the populated branch returns `{enqueued, failed, total_candidates, errors?}`. Consumers (cron monitoring dashboards, future SDKs) that parse the response have to handle two unrelated schemas from the same route. `skipped` has no defined semantics in this route (nothing is ever skipped) and `total_candidates` is silently absent for the most common path. The same drift exists in the sibling reconcile-strategies route, so cleanup should land in both.
- **Evidence**: src/app/api/cron/sync-funding/route.ts:55 `return NextResponse.json({ enqueued: 0, skipped: 0 });` vs line 101-106 `return NextResponse.json({ enqueued, failed, total_candidates: rows.length, ...(errors.length > 0 ? { errors: errors.slice(0, 5) } : {}) });`
- **Fix**: Unify the envelope: the empty branch should return `{ enqueued: 0, failed: 0, total_candidates: 0 }`. Drop the orphan `skipped` field (or define and use it consistently). Optionally extract a `buildCronResult({enqueued, failed, errors, total})` helper and share with reconcile-strategies.

#### G14-060 · DB error message echoed back to caller in 500 response body
- **File**: `src/app/api/cron/sync-funding/route.ts:48`
- **Specialist**: `api-contract` (confidence 8)
- **Summary**: On a strategy-fetch failure, the route returns `{ error: fetchError.message }` directly to the client. PostgREST/Supabase error messages can include schema names, column names, and constraint identifiers (e.g. `relation "public.api_keys" does not exist`, `permission denied for table strategies`). The route is bearer-protected, so the immediate blast radius is small, but the same envelope leaks if the auth gate ever weakens or if logs are scraped by a third-party. The pattern also propagates to the per-row `errors` array (line 94: `${row.id}: ${result.value.error.message}`), which now includes raw PG/RPC errors plus a strategy UUID — useful debug surface for an attacker who has compromised CRON_SECRET.
- **Evidence**: src/app/api/cron/sync-funding/route.ts:48 `{ error: fetchError.message }` and line 94 `errors.push(`${row.id}: ${result.value.error.message}`);` — Supabase error objects carry `.message` strings that are not sanitised.
- **Fix**: Return a stable error code in the body (e.g. `{ error: "strategy_fetch_failed" }`) and keep the detail in `console.error`/Sentry. For the per-row errors array, either drop the raw message and surface only `${row.id}: enqueue_failed` or scrub via an allowlist of known error codes. Same hardening should be applied to reconcile-strategies for consistency.

#### G14-061 · Cron route handler /api/cron/sync-funding has implicit untyped response union — body shape differs across paths
- **File**: `src/app/api/cron/sync-funding/route.ts:27`
- **Specialist**: `type-design-analyzer` (confidence 8)
- **Summary**: `handle()` returns `Promise<NextResponse>` but the JSON body shape varies across four exit paths: {error: string} (401), {error: string} (500), {enqueued: 0, skipped: 0} (no strategies), {enqueued, failed, total_candidates, errors?} (happy path). No exported response type, no discriminated union, no zod schema. The companion test file `route.test.ts` reads `body.enqueued`, `body.total_candidates`, `body.failed`, `body.errors` directly as untyped property access — if a field is renamed, the test still compiles. The cron metadata observability story relies on every dispatch path being readable; today the contract is implicit.
- **Evidence**: src/app/api/cron/sync-funding/route.ts:31 returns `{error: "Unauthorized"}`; line 48 returns `{error: fetchError.message}`; line 55 returns `{enqueued: 0, skipped: 0}` (note: no `failed`/`total_candidates`); lines 101-106 returns the wider shape with optional `errors`. Test file route.test.ts:3308 destructures `body.enqueued` etc. as untyped `any`.
- **Fix**: Export a discriminated union response type: `type SyncFundingResponse = { kind: 'unauthorized' } | { kind: 'fetch_failed', error: string } | { kind: 'noop' } | { kind: 'enqueued', enqueued: number, failed: number, total_candidates: number, errors?: string[] }` and have `handle()` return `NextResponse<SyncFundingResponse>`. Or at minimum a single flat shape with required `enqueued`, `failed`, `total_candidates` on every success path so the test surface is stable.

#### G14-062 · PositionsTab ROI heading 'Total ROI (incl. funding)' is misleading — displayed Mean/Best/Worst rows still use price-only ROI
- **File**: `src/components/strategy/PositionsTab.tsx:221`
- **Specialist**: `code-reviewer` (confidence 8)
- **Summary**: When closedPositions contain any non-zero funding_pnl, the heading switches to 'Total ROI (incl. funding)' but the Mean/Best/Worst rows below it still pull from analytics.trade_metrics (tm.avg_roi, tm.best_trade_roi, tm.worst_trade_roi) which are price-only ROIs computed without funding. The tooltip dollar breakdown ('Price ROI: X + Funding: Y') is informational only — the headline metrics shown to allocators are still price-only despite the label promising funding is included.
- **Evidence**: src/components/strategy/PositionsTab.tsx:220-253 — heading switches to 'Total ROI (incl. funding)' at line 221 based on hasFunding, but lines 240-253 render avgRoi/bestRoi/worstRoi from tm (analytics.trade_metrics) which the worker computes from realized_pnl only, not realized_pnl + funding_pnl.
- **Fix**: Either (a) compute the Mean/Best/Worst client-side from (realized_pnl + funding_pnl) / notional when hasFunding so the values match the label, or (b) keep the heading as 'ROI' and surface a separate dedicated 'Funding P&L' row beneath it. The current state advertises a metric we don't show.

#### G14-063 · PositionsTab tooltip mixes dollar sums and ROI ratio labels in the same heading
- **File**: `src/components/strategy/PositionsTab.tsx:234`
- **Specialist**: `code-reviewer` (confidence 8)
- **Summary**: The tooltip text reads 'Price ROI: ${formatNumber(totalRealizedPnl,2)} + Funding: ${formatNumber(totalFundingPnl,2)}' — but totalRealizedPnl/totalFundingPnl are SUMS of position-level dollar values (realized_pnl, funding_pnl), not ROIs. formatNumber renders them as plain decimals with no $ prefix and no % suffix. Allocators reading the tooltip will see 'Price ROI: 15.00 + Funding: -2.50' under a heading called 'Total ROI (incl. funding)' next to 'Mean / Best / Worst' rows that ARE formatted as percentages. The two unit systems collide visibly.
- **Evidence**: src/components/strategy/PositionsTab.tsx:50-57 — totalRealizedPnl = sum of realized_pnl (dollars); totalFundingPnl = sum of funding_pnl (dollars). Then line 234 labels them 'Price ROI' / 'Funding' inside a tooltip attached to a heading containing the word 'ROI'.
- **Fix**: Either prefix with $ (formatCurrency) and rename the tooltip labels to 'Price P&L / Funding P&L' (the values ARE dollar P&L), or compute aggregate ROI ratios and format with formatPercent. Mixing 'ROI' label with raw dollar values is confusing on a metric that allocators screenshot for diligence.

#### G14-064 · Position.funding_pnl typed as NOT-NULL `number` but every consumer treats it as nullable — invariant is real, runtime checks are dead code
- **File**: `src/components/strategy/PositionsTab.tsx:47`
- **Specialist**: `type-design-analyzer` (confidence 8)
- **Summary**: `Position.funding_pnl: number` (NOT NULL DEFAULT 0 in the DB, `_coerceNumber` in the Zod schema) is documented at types.ts:347-348 as 'NOT NULL DEFAULT 0 — rows without funding carry 0'. But PositionsTab.tsx:47 reads `p.funding_pnl != null && p.funding_pnl !== 0` and line 51 reads `p.funding_pnl ?? 0`. Either (a) the invariant is real and the `!= null` / `?? 0` checks are unreachable defensive code (TS narrowing dead, suggests the dev didn't trust the type), or (b) the invariant is leaky and the type is lying. Both cases warrant fixing: tighten the type to `number` and remove the defensive nullish checks, OR loosen to `number | null` and fix the source. The contradictory pair makes future readers think the type is undertrustworthy.
- **Evidence**: src/lib/types.ts:348 `funding_pnl: number;` (non-null). src/components/strategy/PositionsTab.tsx:47 `p.funding_pnl != null && p.funding_pnl !== 0`; line 51 `s + (p.funding_pnl ?? 0)`. TS strictNullChecks would flag both as unnecessary if the type is accurate.
- **Fix**: Keep the type as `number` (matches DB), delete the `!= null` and `?? 0` runtime checks in PositionsTab. Add a type-narrowing test that confirms `PositionRowSchema.parse({...funding_pnl: null})` rejects (it does — `_coerceNumber` rejects null) so the boundary is enforced once at parse time.

#### G14-065 · FundingFee.match_key is opaque compound string with no type-level structure — typos silently produce duplicates
- **File**: `src/lib/types.ts:455`
- **Specialist**: `type-design-analyzer` (confidence 8)
- **Summary**: `match_key` carries the deduplication contract `strategy_id:exchange:symbol:8h-bucket(timestamp)` and is the UNIQUE constraint backing idempotency. It is typed as `match_key: string` with no parsing, no template literal type, no brand. A producer bug (e.g. forgetting to round the timestamp, swapping symbol/exchange order, missing the colon separator) will produce a valid-looking string that silently duplicates rows. `_build_match_key` in funding_fetch.py is the only producer in Python, but `scripts/backfill_funding.py` test fakes the format directly (`f"{STRATEGY_ID}:binance:BTCUSDT:bucket-{i}"` — uses 'bucket-{i}', not the canonical 8h timestamp). Type system gives zero help.
- **Evidence**: src/lib/types.ts:455 `match_key: string;` is a free string; analytics-service/services/funding_fetch.py:249-252 `_build_match_key` constructs the canonical form; analytics-service/tests/test_funding_backfill_idempotency.py:1140 fakes a different format (`bucket-{i}`) which would pass type checks but contradict the dedup invariant.
- **Fix**: Either (a) brand it: `type MatchKey = string & { readonly __brand: 'FundingFeeMatchKey' };` plus a constructor `buildMatchKey(parts)` that is the only legal source — same pattern as Position's parsePositionRows. (b) Use template literal types: `type MatchKey = \`${string}:${SupportedExchange}:${string}:${string}\`` so misordered concatenations fail to type-check. Either prevents the test-vs-prod divergence.

#### G14-066 · FundingFee.raw_data: Record<string, unknown> | null is a wide blob where a discriminated union by exchange is achievable
- **File**: `src/lib/types.ts:456`
- **Specialist**: `type-design-analyzer` (confidence 8)
- **Summary**: `raw_data` is the original exchange response row, preserved for audit/debug. Its shape is fully known per exchange (Binance income row with `incomeType/income/asset/time/tranId`; OKX bills row with `instId/type/pnl/ccy/ts/billId`; Bybit transaction-log row with `symbol/type/funding/currency/transactionTime/id`). Typing it as `Record<string, unknown> | null` discards that information. A debug consumer reading `raw_data.tranId` against an OKX row gets `undefined` with no type error. Given `exchange` already discriminates the row, the type should narrow.
- **Evidence**: src/lib/types.ts:456 `raw_data: Record<string, unknown> | null;` adjacent to `exchange: "binance" | "okx" | "bybit"` (line 450) which is the natural discriminator. analytics-service/services/funding_fetch.py:370, 459, 539 each pass exchange-specific dicts as `raw_item`.
- **Fix**: Define per-exchange raw types (`BinanceFundingRaw`, `OkxFundingRaw`, `BybitFundingRaw`) and refactor `FundingFee` as a discriminated union keyed on `exchange`. The amount/timestamp/strategy_id stay common; raw_data narrows automatically. Maintenance burden is one type per supported exchange, matching the count of normalizers.

#### G14-067 · ALTER TABLE positions ADD COLUMN NUMERIC NOT NULL DEFAULT 0 acquires ACCESS EXCLUSIVE lock on hot table
- **File**: `supabase/migrations/20260416081039_funding_fees.sql:166`
- **Specialist**: `data-migration` (confidence 8)
- **Summary**: `ALTER TABLE positions ADD COLUMN IF NOT EXISTS funding_pnl NUMERIC NOT NULL DEFAULT 0` is metadata-only in PG11+ for constant defaults, but still takes ACCESS EXCLUSIVE on the positions table. positions is heavily written by the analytics reconstruction path (DELETE+INSERT per tick) and read by allocator/discovery dashboards. The lock is short, but any in-flight reconstruct on a large strategy can block the migration (or vice-versa) and cause a brief read stall.
- **Evidence**: funding_fees.sql:166-167 adds the column in a single statement inside BEGIN; ... COMMIT. Migration 040 created positions with no batched-write contract. By 2026-05 the positions table is mutated by reconstruct_positions_atomic RPC (113), atomic delete+insert, and read by /discovery/[slug]/[strategyId]/page.tsx and PositionsTab.tsx. No CONCURRENTLY pattern is available for ADD COLUMN, but the migration could be issued with `SET lock_timeout = '5s'` to bail rather than queueing arbitrarily long.
- **Fix**: Either (a) deploy during a quiet window and accept the brief lock; or (b) prepend `SET LOCAL lock_timeout = '5s'; SET LOCAL statement_timeout = '30s';` inside the BEGIN so a stalled queue surfaces as a controlled failure rather than head-of-line blocking. Document the window in the runbook. (Now historical — column is already in main and types.ts; future migrations adding NOT NULL columns to hot tables should follow the pattern.)

### LOW (5)

#### G14-068 · funding_fees.raw_data JSONB stores full exchange response — minor PII/secret echo risk
- **File**: `analytics-service/services/funding_fetch.py:119`
- **Specialist**: `security` (confidence 9)
- **Summary**: _normalize_funding_row writes the entire raw exchange item (dict(raw_item)) into funding_fees.raw_data. While the read-side is RLS-protected to strategies.user_id = auth.uid() and the column is intended for audit/debugging, the raw payload from Binance/OKX/Bybit may include incidental account identifiers, masked-but-non-empty IDs, internal-only fields (e.g. uid, accountId), and per-row tranIds that combined with timing data could enable account linkage if the row ever leaks via an RLS misconfig or an admin export. Impact bounded by RLS today, but defense-in-depth would log only the fields actually needed (symbol, amount, timestamp, exchange fill_id) and drop the full blob.
- **Evidence**: funding_fetch.py:119 — `"raw_data": dict(raw_item)` stores every key the exchange returned, then serialize_funding_row(funding_fetch.py:450) carries it intact into the UPSERT payload.
- **Fix**: Whitelist the raw_data keys preserved: e.g. {"raw": {k: raw_item.get(k) for k in ("tranId","billId","id","income","pnl","funding")}}. Drop everything else. Aligns with the /security page promise that 'we read only the trade history' and reduces blast radius if RLS ever fails open.

#### G14-069 · _attribute_funding silently skips funding rows with malformed timestamp or amount
- **File**: `analytics-service/services/position_reconstruction.py:419`
- **Specialist**: `silent-failure-hunter` (confidence 9)
- **Summary**: When the funding_fees row's timestamp or amount fails to parse (`ts = datetime.fromisoformat(...) except Exception: continue` at line 414-420), the row is silently dropped from the per-symbol map. If a Bybit funding row stored an empty-string amount (which the `or '0'` fallback at funding_fetch.py:366 makes possible), it would parse fine — but if it stored 'NaN' or a non-numeric string, this skip drops it. No counter, no log. Combined with the on-conflict ignore_duplicates upsert, a poisoned funding_fees row sits in the table forever and is silently skipped at every reconstruction.
- **Evidence**: position_reconstruction.py:414-420 — `try: ts = datetime.fromisoformat(...) ... amt = Decimal(str(amt_raw)) except Exception: continue` with no log and no counter.
- **Fix**: Increment a `funding_rows_dropped` counter and add to aggregated_data_quality_flags. Optionally logger.warning with strategy_id and the bad row id so the upstream serialization regression can be hunted.

#### G14-070 · Per-row errors silently truncated to 5 with no indicator
- **File**: `src/app/api/cron/sync-funding/route.ts:105`
- **Specialist**: `api-contract` (confidence 9)
- **Summary**: When more than 5 enqueues fail, the response contains `errors: errors.slice(0, 5)` with no `errors_truncated: true` flag or total error count. A reader of the JSON envelope sees `errors.length === 5` and `failed === 12` and cannot tell which strategies are missing from the array. The summary counts (`failed`, `total_candidates`) are accurate, but the array is misleading — same pattern repeats in reconcile-strategies/route.ts:127. Low because the counts still reflect reality, but the response is harder to debug from a cron alert.
- **Evidence**: src/app/api/cron/sync-funding/route.ts:105 `...(errors.length > 0 ? { errors: errors.slice(0, 5) } : {})` — no `errors_total` or `errors_truncated` companion field.
- **Fix**: Add `errors_total: errors.length` (or `errors_truncated: errors.length > 5`) alongside the truncated array so consumers can detect the truncation without re-reading logs.

#### G14-071 · FundingFee.amount: number drops precision compared to Python's deliberate Decimal — DB is NUMERIC, JS number is IEEE-754
- **File**: `src/lib/types.ts:452`
- **Specialist**: `type-design-analyzer` (confidence 9)
- **Summary**: The Python service intentionally uses `Decimal` for `amount` (funding_fetch.py:274 `amount = Decimal(str(amount_raw))`) and serializes to string for UPSERT (line 617 `"amount": str(row["amount"])`) to avoid float drift. The DB column is `NUMERIC NOT NULL`. The TS contract is `amount: number` (IEEE-754 double), which silently loses precision on values requiring more than ~15 significant digits and on values not exactly representable in binary float (most decimal fractions). Funding payments are typically small (≤ 6 decimal places) so the practical risk is bounded, but the type design contradicts the producer's explicit precision choice — and a downstream sum across thousands of rows will surface rounding artifacts. Same concern applies to `Position.funding_pnl: number`.
- **Evidence**: analytics-service/services/funding_fetch.py:274 `amount = Decimal(str(amount_raw))` and line 617 `"amount": str(row["amount"])` deliberately preserve precision through the UPSERT. src/lib/types.ts:452 `amount: number;` accepts the wire string as a JS number via implicit coercion or future Zod `z.coerce.number()` — both lose precision.
- **Fix**: Either (a) type as `amount: string` and force consumers to opt into `Number(amount)` at the display boundary (mirrors how Position rows could be tightened), or (b) accept the precision tradeoff explicitly with a JSDoc note that funding amounts are clamped to JS-number precision and add a test asserting amounts ≤ 1e10 round-trip exactly. Option (a) matches the producer; (b) accepts current code.

#### G14-072 · funding_fees.raw_data JSONB unbounded — Bybit transaction-log items can be large; no row-size cap
- **File**: `supabase/migrations/20260416081039_funding_fees.sql:96`
- **Specialist**: `data-migration` (confidence 9)
- **Summary**: `raw_data JSONB` stores the full exchange response row per funding event. Binance/OKX/Bybit return rows that are typically 200-500 bytes, so the table grows ~1.5-2x the structured columns. Over 90 days × ~3 funding cycles/day × multi-symbol perp strategies, this can add up. No retention policy or partitioning is defined. Lower severity because volumes are modest, but it's a forward-only data growth concern.
- **Evidence**: funding_fees.sql:96 `raw_data JSONB` (nullable, no size limit). funding_fetch.py:119 stores `dict(raw_item)` unmodified. No retention sweep is registered alongside this table; the table only has the FK ON DELETE CASCADE from strategies, not a time-based retention.
- **Fix**: Either (a) trim raw_data to the fields actually needed for debugging (keep raw txn ID + amount + ts only), or (b) add a periodic retention job that deletes raw_data older than N days while keeping the row for the funding_pnl attribution math. Low priority — flag for capacity review.

#### G15-002 · No route.test.ts for POST /api/simulator — entire 7-branch route untested

It has 7 distinct response branches: CSRF reject (line 23-24), 401 unauth (line 31-33), 429 rate-limited (line 35-51), 400 invalid JSON (line 53-58), 400 bad shape (line 60-69), 404 portfolio-not-found (line 84-86), 500 + 4xx forwarding from AnalyticsUpstreamError (line 95-106). Existing routes like /api/preferences and /api/bridge/outcome have parallel route.test.ts with TC-style cases for each branch. A 4xx upstream that should forward as 4xx will silently regress to 500 with no test to catch it. The e2e/simulator-flow.spec.ts comment falsely claims 'the API route is covered by vitest' — it is not.
- **Evidence**: find src/app/api/simulator -name '*.test.ts' returns 0 results; grep -rn 'POST.*api/simulator' src --include='*.test.ts' returns nothing. e2e/simulator-flow.spec.ts:18 claims vitest coverage that doesn't exist.
