#### G15-050 · Math.min(...values) / Math.max(...values) spread on equity-curve arrays risks stack overflow and O(n) spread overhead
- **File**: `src/components/portfolio/PortfolioImpactPanel.tsx:518`
- **Specialist**: `performance` (confidence 9)
- **Summary**: EquityOverlayChart computes `Math.min(...values)` and `Math.max(...values)` where `values` is built from the merged current+proposed equity series. With business-day daily returns and 6mo–years of history, this can be 200–500+ values (the schema has no upper bound). The spread argument-passing copies every value onto the call stack and on engines that cap function-call argument counts can hit the 'too many arguments' threshold. Use a single linear scan instead.
- **Evidence**: src/components/portfolio/PortfolioImpactPanel.tsx:518-519 — `const minY = Math.min(...values); const maxY = Math.max(...values);` where `values = merged.flatMap(p => [p.current, p.proposed].filter(v => v !== null))`.
- **Fix**: Replace with a single linear scan: `let minY = Infinity, maxY = -Infinity; for (const p of merged) { if (p.current !== null) { if (p.current < minY) minY = p.current; if (p.current > maxY) maxY = p.current; } if (p.proposed !== null) { ... } }`. Also drops the separate values flatMap entirely. (See js-min-max-loop / js-combine-iterations rules.)

#### G15-051 · EquityOverlayChart re-derives minY, maxY, paths and closures on every parent re-render
- **File**: `src/components/portfolio/PortfolioImpactPanel.tsx:508`
- **Specialist**: `performance` (confidence 9)
- **Summary**: `EquityOverlayChart` does five non-trivial passes over `merged` on every render (flatMap to build values, Math.min/max, two `merged.map` calls to build path-point arrays, plus the buildPath linear scan inside each). None of this is memoized — even though `merged` is `useMemo`'d in the parent, any sibling state change in the parent dialog (loading/error/success transitions, ARIA announcement string changes) will re-render and re-execute the entire chart-derivation pipeline. The xAt and yAt closures are also re-allocated every render.
- **Evidence**: src/components/portfolio/PortfolioImpactPanel.tsx:508-575 — `function EquityOverlayChart({ merged }) { const values = merged.flatMap(...); ... const minY = Math.min(...values); ... const currentPath = buildPath(merged.map(...)); const proposedPath = buildPath(merged.map(...)); }`. No useMemo.
- **Fix**: Wrap the derived values (values, minY, maxY, currentPath, proposedPath) in `useMemo(..., [merged])`, or extract a tiny `function deriveChart(merged)` and memoize it. With ~200 daily points × 5 passes that's ~1000 array ops every render of an actively-mounted panel.

#### G15-052 · deltaChips() and buildDeltaAnnouncement re-allocate on every render
- **File**: `src/components/portfolio/PortfolioImpactPanel.tsx:368`
- **Specialist**: `performance` (confidence 8)
- **Summary**: `DeltaHero` calls `deltaChips(deltas)` directly inside the render body, allocating a fresh 4-element array of chip-config objects every render. Because the chips are passed to `DeltaChipCard` by reference, React.memo would not save the children even if added. Separately, `PortfolioImpactPanel`'s render body computes `announcement = buildDeltaAnnouncement(state.data.deltas)` on every render (line 115), allocating a 4-element parts array and four template-string concatenations every time. Neither is wrapped in useMemo despite the parent already using useMemo elsewhere in the file.
- **Evidence**: src/components/portfolio/PortfolioImpactPanel.tsx:115 — `const announcement = state.kind === 'success' && state.data.status === 'ok' ? buildDeltaAnnouncement(state.data.deltas) : '';`. Line 368 — `function DeltaHero({ deltas }) { const chips = deltaChips(deltas); ... }`.
- **Fix**: Wrap with `useMemo(() => deltaChips(deltas), [deltas])` and `useMemo(() => state.kind === 'success' && state.data.status === 'ok' ? buildDeltaAnnouncement(state.data.deltas) : '', [state])`. Equally cheap fix: hoist a `DELTA_CHIP_DEFS` array to module scope and look up values per-key instead of rebuilding the array.

#### G15-053 · PortfolioImpactPanel — retry button behavior on non-429 error untested
- **File**: `src/components/portfolio/PortfolioImpactPanel.tsx:2377`
- **Specialist**: `pr-test-analyzer` (confidence 8)
- **Summary**: The ErrorState retry button is disabled only when isRateLimited (retryAfter > 0). For non-429 errors (500, network failures, contract violations) the retry button must be enabled and clicking it must re-fire the fetch. The diff-included test asserts the button is present in error state (PortfolioImpactPanel.test.tsx:185-196) but does NOT click it to verify the retry path actually re-fires. A regression that, e.g., breaks the useCallback memoization of fetchImpact or fails to re-enable the button on a subsequent fetch would not be caught.
- **Evidence**: src/components/portfolio/PortfolioImpactPanel.test.tsx:185-196 — getByRole('button', {name:'Retry'}) is asserted but fireEvent.click is never called. PortfolioImpactPanel.tsx:2377-2386 declares the retry button.
- **Fix**: Add 'clicking Retry on a 500 re-fires the fetch and recovers' that: (1) mockFetch first returns 500, second returns 200 with valid buildResponse(); (2) renders the panel and waits for the retry button; (3) fireEvent.click(retryButton); (4) await waitFor(() => screen.getByText(/Projected impact/i)); (5) asserts globalThis.fetch was called twice.

#### G15-054 · PartialHistory threshold (126 business days) hardcoded twice with no shared constant — UI flag and Python flag can drift · _chain_ · refs: batch-G15.type-design-analyzer.jsonl:9, batch-G15.pr-test-analyzer.jsonl:21
- **File**: `src/components/portfolio/PortfolioImpactPanel.tsx:2426`
- **Specialist**: `red-team` (confidence 8)
- **Summary**: `PARTIAL_HISTORY_THRESHOLD = 126` lives in analytics-service/services/simulator_scoring.py:438. The TS side trusts the producer-emitted `partial_history` boolean (PortfolioImpactPanel.tsx:2414). type-design-analyzer.jsonl:9 flagged the boolean-vs-overlap_days inconsistency risk. The deeper chain: the threshold value is NOT documented anywhere user-facing OR in a shared TS constant. If the Python side ever changes to 90 days (different markets, more sensitive bar), the UI banner copy ('Partial history: only 40 overlapping trading days') won't reflect the new floor — the message is implicit ('only X days, lower than our threshold') with no explicit '<126' anchor. Worse: pr-test-analyzer.jsonl:21 flagged no boundary-case test at exactly 126 days. A user gets a partial-history warning at overlap=125 and not at overlap=126 with no UI explanation of why. The threshold should be in a contract module (e.g. src/lib/api/simulatorSchema.ts) and the UI should show the threshold explicitly in the banner copy ('only 40 of the 126 trading days we look for').
- **Evidence**: analytics-service/services/simulator_scoring.py:438 (`PARTIAL_HISTORY_THRESHOLD = 126`) — not exported anywhere; src/components/portfolio/PortfolioImpactPanel.tsx:2426-2436 (banner copy doesn't mention the threshold number). No TS-side constant for 126.
- **Fix**: Export from analytics-service/services/simulator_scoring.py via OpenAPI/constants module if the project has one (analytics-schemas.ts pattern). Add to src/lib/api/simulatorSchema.ts: `export const PARTIAL_HISTORY_THRESHOLD = 126;` with a comment 'must stay in sync with analytics-service/services/simulator_scoring.py'. Update the banner to read 'Partial history: only X of 126 overlapping trading days' so the threshold is visible. Add a parity test that asserts the Python value matches the TS constant via the OpenAPI export.

#### G15-055 · PortfolioImpactPanel catches all non-AbortError exceptions and shows raw error message as user copy
- **File**: `src/components/portfolio/PortfolioImpactPanel.tsx:79`
- **Specialist**: `silent-failure-hunter` (confidence 8)
- **Summary**: The catch block surfaces `err.message` verbatim as the user-facing error string. Network errors from `fetch` produce platform-specific strings ('TypeError: Failed to fetch', 'Load failed', 'NetworkError when attempting to fetch resource'). These are unhelpful and inconsistent across browsers. JSON parse failures on a malformed success response (e.g. `await res.json()` throwing on line 75) also fall into this catch and produce 'Unexpected token < in JSON at position 0' — confusing tech-debt-shaped text the user can do nothing with. The error is also not logged to console.error, so debugging requires the user to send a screenshot.
- **Evidence**: src/components/portfolio/PortfolioImpactPanel.tsx:79-88     } catch (err) {       if (err instanceof DOMException && err.name === 'AbortError') return;       if (!controller.signal.aborted) {         setState({           kind: 'error',           message:             err instanceof Error ? err.message : 'Failed to simulate impact',         });       }     }
- **Fix**: Distinguish branches: TypeError → 'Network error — check your connection'; SyntaxError (JSON parse) → 'Server returned an unexpected response. We have been notified.'; everything else → 'Simulation failed unexpectedly.' AND log every caught error with console.error so Sentry/Vercel logs capture it. Currently the user sees the error but the operator never does.

#### G15-056 · FetchState error variant — retryAfter optional but body.retryAfter is `any`
- **File**: `src/components/portfolio/PortfolioImpactPanel.tsx:52`
- **Specialist**: `type-design-analyzer` (confidence 8)
- **Summary**: Inside `fetchImpact`, `const body = await res.json().catch(() => ({ error: 'Simulation failed' }))` yields `any` (the Promise<any> from `.json()`). The code then does `typeof body.retryAfter === 'number' ? body.retryAfter : ...` which is the minimum reasonable guard, but `body.error ?? 'fallback'` also treats `body.error` as a free-form value — a server response of `{ error: { nested: 'object' } }` would coerce to '[object Object]' as the message. The schema for the error path is unspecified, so the UI cannot rely on `error: string`. Wider issue: error response shapes are uncovenanted across all routes.
- **Evidence**: src/components/portfolio/PortfolioImpactPanel.tsx:52-67 (`const body = await res.json().catch(...)` — body inferred as any; no schema)
- **Fix**: Define `const ErrorResponseSchema = z.object({ error: z.string(), retryAfter: z.number().nonnegative().optional() });` in `src/lib/api/errorSchema.ts` (or alongside SimulatorRequestSchema). Parse with safeParse before reading fields: `const parsed = ErrorResponseSchema.safeParse(body); const message = parsed.success ? parsed.data.error : 'Simulation failed'; const retryAfter = parsed.success ? parsed.data.retryAfter : undefined;`. Use the same schema for every API route's error response so the contract is reusable.

#### G15-057 · DeltaChip.format string union too narrow — drift-prone
- **File**: `src/components/portfolio/PortfolioImpactPanel.tsx:2447`
- **Specialist**: `type-design-analyzer` (confidence 8)
- **Summary**: `type DeltaChip = { ... format: 'ratio' | 'percent'; ... }` is fine, but `formatDelta(value, format: 'ratio'|'percent')` and `formatAnnouncementChip` both repeat the same string literal union inline. If a third format (e.g. 'currency') is added, three call sites must be updated. The literal is also weakly tied to the chip definitions — a typo in a config (`'percentage'` instead of `'percent'`) is caught by TS but the chip silently falls through the `if (format === 'percent')` to the ratio path. Tiny scope but recurring shape in this file.
- **Evidence**: src/components/portfolio/PortfolioImpactPanel.tsx:2447 (`format: 'ratio'|'percent'`), 2539 (`formatDelta(value: number, format: 'ratio'|'percent')`), 2733 (`formatAnnouncementChip(label, value, format: 'ratio'|'percent')`)
- **Fix**: Hoist `type DeltaFormat = 'ratio' | 'percent';` once and reuse. Even better, model formatters as a `Record<DeltaFormat, (n: number) => string>` so adding a new format adds one entry instead of editing three switch-like ifs. Use exhaustive `satisfies` to catch missing entries.

#### G15-058 · CHAIN: SimulateImpactButton renders for every row + StrategyTable deferred-load missing + PortfolioImpactPanel statically imported = ~25KB inflation on logged-out browser too · _chain_ · refs: batch-G15.performance.jsonl:1, batch-G15.pr-test-analyzer.jsonl:20
- **File**: `src/components/strategy/StrategyTable.tsx:86`
- **Specialist**: `red-team` (confidence 8)
- **Summary**: performance.jsonl:1 flagged PortfolioImpactPanel static-import (~20-30KB per render). Chain finding: StrategyTable is rendered on `/discovery/[slug]` (page.tsx:31 SSRed to logged-OUT users too — the auth redirect is at page entry but the SSR'd HTML still includes the SimulateImpactButton column with disabled state). pr-test-analyzer.jsonl:20 noted that the new portfolioId prop isn't tested but missed the bundle-inflation chain. So a CRAWLER hitting /discovery/crypto-sma gets back HTML with the disabled SimulateImpactButton column + the JS bundle is the same heavy bundle for every visitor. Performance: ~25KB cost x N rows x viewer-with-no-portfolio-anyway = wasted bytes for the 90% of /discovery visitors who can't actually use the feature. Best path: gate the SimulateImpactButton import behind `portfolioId !== null`, OR render a server-component placeholder until the panel is requested.
- **Evidence**: src/components/strategy/StrategyTable.tsx:18 (static import) + src/app/(dashboard)/discovery/[slug]/page.tsx:9-11 (auth redirect at line 9 BEFORE the table renders — so logged-out users never see this, BUT the table component itself is part of the bundle for /discovery/[slug] regardless of role). The redirect happens server-side; the question is whether the StrategyTable component code splits or ships with the page. Currently it's `"use client"` + static import → it ships in the client bundle for everyone.
- **Fix**: Per performance.jsonl:1: convert PortfolioImpactPanel to `dynamic(() => import(...), { ssr: false })`. Also conditionally render the SimulateImpactButton column header AND cell based on `portfolioId !== null` so the entire column disappears for users without a portfolio — saves the prop drilling and the click-handler bytes too.

#### G15-059 · StrategyTable.portfolioId optional with default null — invariant 'simulate=available iff portfolio≠null' not encoded
- **File**: `src/components/strategy/StrategyTable.tsx:40`
- **Specialist**: `type-design-analyzer` (confidence 8)
- **Summary**: `portfolioId?: string | null` defaults to `null`. The contract is: caller passes a UUID when the user has a portfolio, null otherwise. But `string | null` doesn't distinguish 'unknown/no portfolio' from 'present but empty string'. SimulateImpactButton then uses `!portfolioId` to disable — accidentally treating '' as 'no portfolio'. Combined with the missing `.uuid()` on the TS schema, an empty string could slip through from an upstream consumer mistakenly passing one. Minor in scope but the prop is now part of the StrategyTable contract that other callers will reuse.
- **Evidence**: src/components/strategy/StrategyTable.tsx:43-47 `portfolioId?: string | null` + 117 `portfolioId = null` + src/components/discovery/SimulateImpactButton.tsx:1745 `const disabled = !portfolioId;`
- **Fix**: Tighten the prop to `portfolioId: string | null` (required, force callers to be explicit), and branded as `PortfolioId | null` once branded IDs exist. Encode the invariant at the SimulateImpactButton boundary: `disabled = portfolioId === null` (so '' fails-loud as a contract violation, possibly with a console.warn). Even better, model as a discriminated union: `type SimulatorAvailability = { available: true; portfolioId: PortfolioId } | { available: false; reason: 'no_portfolio' | 'feature_disabled' }`.

#### G15-060 · Simulator delta types violate Zod contract when _safe_float collapses to None on Inf/NaN — `null` deltas would 500 the parseResponse path · _chain_ · refs: batch-G15.type-design-analyzer.jsonl:8 (metrics range), batch-G15.silent-failure-hunter.jsonl:1 (error envelope leak)
- **File**: `src/lib/api/simulatorSchema.ts:34`
- **Specialist**: `red-team` (confidence 9)
- **Summary**: `SimulatorDeltasSchema` requires `sharpe_delta: z.number()` (NON-nullable). But analytics-service/services/simulator_scoring.py:559-562 calls `_safe_float(sharpe_delta)` for each delta, and `_safe_float` (services/metrics.py:72-80) returns None for NaN/Inf inputs. The producer side has guards: `_delta(None, None) → 0.0` and `_compute_sharpe` returns None on std==0 → propagates None to `_delta` → 0.0. BUT `_max_drawdown` could return a -1.0 for a strategy that loses everything (cumulative hits 0 → drawdown of -1). If proposed_max_dd is -Inf or NaN from a numerically pathological returns series (cumulative goes through 0), `_delta(current_max_dd, proposed_max_dd)` propagates the Inf/NaN, and `_safe_float` returns None. The downstream `parseResponse(SimulatorResponseSchema, data, '/api/simulator')` in analytics-client.ts:228-231 then THROWS with a 'Expected number, received null' message. The route's catch block (route.ts:103-105) returns 500 with the raw err.message — leaking 'Analytics response contract violation on /api/simulator: deltas.sharpe_delta: Expected number, received null' as the user-facing error. Specialists noted .passthrough() and stringly-typed UUID risks but missed this nullable mismatch.
- **Evidence**: src/lib/api/simulatorSchema.ts:34-37 (deltas REQUIRED to be number, NOT nullable); analytics-service/services/simulator_scoring.py:559 `'sharpe_delta': _safe_float(sharpe_delta)`; analytics-service/services/metrics.py:72-80 (`_safe_float` returns None for NaN/Inf). Contract drift between producer (can emit null) and parser (rejects null).
- **Fix**: Two options. (A) Make the Python side coerce to 0.0 (not None) when the value is NaN/Inf — match the contract: `deltas: {'sharpe_delta': float(_safe_float(sharpe_delta) or 0.0)}`. (B) Make the Zod schema match producer reality: `sharpe_delta: z.number().nullable()` and update the UI's `formatDelta` to handle null. (A) preserves the meaningful-improvement chip semantics; (B) requires UI work but is the more honest contract. Either way add a regression test that feeds NaN-producing returns into simulate_add_candidate and asserts the response parses successfully.

#### G15-061 · SimulatorMetricsSnapshot lacks domain ranges — HHI/correlation/sharpe accept anything
- **File**: `src/lib/api/simulatorSchema.ts:26`
- **Specialist**: `type-design-analyzer` (confidence 8)
- **Summary**: `SimulatorMetricsSnapshot`/`SimulatorMetricsSchema` declare `sharpe`, `max_drawdown`, `avg_correlation`, `concentration` as `z.number().nullable()` with no domain constraints. But each metric has a well-known range: concentration (HHI) ∈ [1/N, 1] strictly bounded, avg_correlation ∈ [-1, 1], max_drawdown ≤ 0 (it's a drawdown). A Python regression that returns `concentration: 4.5` or `avg_correlation: 2.0` would pass the schema and propagate to the UI, where it would render as an absurd green chip without an error trail. The whole point of the trust-boundary schema is to make these invariants enforceable at the wire.
- **Evidence**: src/lib/api/simulatorSchema.ts:26-31 (`SimulatorMetricsSchema`: every field `z.number().nullable()`, no range) + analytics-service/services/simulator_scoring.py:593-603 (`_herfindahl` docstring says range [1/N,1] but the producer doesn't enforce it either)
- **Fix**: Tighten: `concentration: z.number().min(0).max(1).nullable()`, `avg_correlation: z.number().min(-1).max(1).nullable()`, `max_drawdown: z.number().max(0).nullable()`, `sharpe: z.number().finite().nullable()`. If `_safe_float`-coerced infinities are ever expected, add `.finite()` explicitly. Mirror in Pydantic with `Field(ge=-1, le=1, ...)`.

#### G15-062 · SimulatorStatus enum drift risk — Python returns string, TS validates with z.enum, no shared source
- **File**: `src/lib/api/simulatorSchema.ts:11`
- **Specialist**: `type-design-analyzer` (confidence 8)
- **Summary**: `SimulatorStatusSchema = z.enum(['ok', 'insufficient_data', 'already_in_portfolio', 'empty_portfolio'])` and Python emits these as string literals in `simulate_add_candidate`. No shared module — the Python side is plain string-typed (no `Literal['ok','insufficient_data',...]` annotation on the helpers, no `enum.StrEnum`). Adding a new status requires updating two source files + risking the TS schema rejecting a valid Python response on deploy if order-of-deploy is wrong (Python emits new status first, TS rejects until next deploy).
- **Evidence**: src/lib/api/simulatorSchema.ts:11-16 (4-variant enum) + simulator_scoring.py:464 (docstring: `status: 'ok' | 'insufficient_data' | 'already_in_portfolio' | 'empty_portfolio'`) + same literals scattered as bare strings at 489, 494, 555, 651
- **Fix**: In Python: `class SimulatorStatus(str, Enum): OK = 'ok'; INSUFFICIENT_DATA = 'insufficient_data'; ALREADY_IN_PORTFOLIO = 'already_in_portfolio'; EMPTY_PORTFOLIO = 'empty_portfolio'`. Use `SimulatorStatus.OK.value` in returns + type-annotate helpers `-> SimulatorResponse`. In TS, derive from one shared constants file or treat the Python side as canonical and import via the OpenAPI export (already used elsewhere per analytics-schemas.ts pattern).

#### G15-063 · checkLimit retryAfter return type allows undefined sneak-through
- **File**: `src/lib/ratelimit.ts:62`
- **Specialist**: `type-design-analyzer` (confidence 8)
- **Summary**: `CheckLimitResult` discriminated union (good!) gives `{ success: true } | { success: false; retryAfter: number }`. But the `simulator` route forwards `rl.retryAfter` directly into the JSON body and `'Retry-After': String(rl.retryAfter)` — this only works because we narrowed on `!rl.success`. The risk: if the rate-limit module ever returns `{ success: false }` without `retryAfter`, the body would carry `retryAfter: undefined` (Next.js strips this on serialization), but `String(undefined) === 'undefined'` lands in the `Retry-After` header. The type narrows correctly today, but the invariant 'on failure, retryAfter is always a positive integer' is not enforced in the union — it just declares `number`, which includes 0, NaN, negative.
- **Evidence**: src/lib/ratelimit.ts:62 `| { success: false; retryAfter: number }` (no positivity invariant) + src/app/api/simulator/route.ts:48 `headers: { 'Retry-After': String(rl.retryAfter) }`
- **Fix**: Either tighten to `retryAfter: number` with a runtime check inside `checkLimit` ensuring `Number.isFinite(retryAfter) && retryAfter >= 1`, or model the invariant in the type via a branded `type PositiveInteger = number & {__brand: 'PositiveInteger'}`. At minimum, add a Zod-style validator on the way out and a `Math.max(1, Math.ceil(rl.retryAfter))` coercion in the route. The route helper that builds the 429 response should be extracted so the header/body invariant is enforced once.

#### G15-064 · partial_history boolean decoupled from overlap_days — two sources of truth
- **File**: `src/lib/types.ts:702`
- **Specialist**: `type-design-analyzer` (confidence 8)
- **Summary**: `SimulatorCandidate` carries BOTH `overlap_days: number` and `partial_history: boolean`, where `partial_history := overlap_days < PARTIAL_HISTORY_THRESHOLD (126)`. The threshold is on the Python side (`simulator_scoring.py:438`). The TS schema can receive any `partial_history` value regardless of `overlap_days` — a producer bug or a future TS-side fake/test could set `partial_history=false` with `overlap_days=5` (or vice versa) and the schema accepts it. The UI keys conditional rendering off `partial_history` (`SuccessBody`, line 2414); the chart caption keys off `overlap_days` (line 2433). The two can disagree.
- **Evidence**: src/lib/types.ts:701-703 (`overlap_days: number; partial_history: boolean;`) + simulator_scoring.py:438 (`PARTIAL_HISTORY_THRESHOLD = 126`) + simulatorSchema.ts:51-52 (independent number + boolean)
- **Fix**: Make `partial_history` a derived getter on the client (or omit it entirely from the wire contract and compute it: `const partialHistory = data.overlap_days < 126`). If you keep both fields for forward-compat, add a Zod `.refine()` on the response schema: `.refine(d => d.partial_history === (d.overlap_days < 126), { message: 'partial_history inconsistent with overlap_days' })`. Same constant should be exported from the TS contract module.

#### G15-065 · SimulatorDeltas modelled as 4 unrelated numbers — sign convention only in docstring
- **File**: `src/lib/types.ts:678`
- **Specialist**: `type-design-analyzer` (confidence 8)
- **Summary**: `SimulatorDeltas { sharpe_delta: number; dd_delta: number; corr_delta: number; concentration_delta: number; }` — four bare numbers with the 'positive=improvement' sign convention baked into a JSDoc comment (lines 666-677). Same convention exists in Python (`simulator_scoring.py:478-487`). The convention is load-bearing for every visual decision in the UI (`DeltaChipCard.improving = chip.value > 0`, ARIA `direction = value > 0 ? 'improved' : 'regressed'`). If a future contributor adds a new metric and forgets to flip the sign for 'lower is better', the UI silently labels regression as improvement — a real correctness bug, not just a polish issue.
- **Evidence**: src/lib/types.ts:678-683 (no constraints, no brand, sign convention only in comments) + src/components/portfolio/PortfolioImpactPanel.tsx:2501 (`const improving = chip.value > 0;` — depends entirely on the convention)
- **Fix**: Introduce a `type Improvement = number & { __brand: 'Improvement' }` brand and a helper `asImprovement(rawDelta: number, direction: 'higher_is_better' | 'lower_is_better'): Improvement` that applies the sign flip in one place. Then `SimulatorDeltas` becomes `{ sharpe_delta: Improvement; ...}` and the UI's `improving` logic is correct by construction. Encode 'higher is better for sharpe, lower is better for HHI' as data, not docstring.

### LOW (9)

#### G15-066 · docs-link-check job — external links explicitly excluded but no test pins this contract
- **File**: `.github/workflows/ci.yml:42`
- **Specialist**: `pr-test-analyzer` (confidence 9)
- **Summary**: The CI job comment is explicit: 'External URL breakage should not fail CI because the runbooks reference third-party provider docs whose URLs we do not own. `--offline` resolves file:// and relative paths against the checked-out tree.' This contract — internal links checked, external skipped — is enforced by a single `--offline` flag. No test pins this. A future contributor removing --offline could silently start failing CI on Vercel docs URL changes, surprising the team.
- **Evidence**: .github/workflows/ci.yml:42-55 — only the inline YAML comment documents this. No test scoping.
- **Fix**: Add a tiny smoke test in scripts/smoke-docs-link-check.mjs that runs lychee with a fixture markdown containing both an internal-broken and an external-broken link, asserts the exit code is 1, AND asserts the failure reason is the internal one (so removing --offline would change the assertion failure). Wire it as a vitest test in src/__tests__/.

#### G15-067 · check-banned-packages.mjs reads ~/.claude/CLAUDE.md as the source of truth — script and CLAUDE.md drift silently · _new_ · refs: scripts/check-banned-packages.mjs:1121,1142-1164
- **File**: `scripts/check-banned-packages.mjs:1139`
- **Specialist**: `red-team` (confidence 9)
- **Summary**: The script's docstring says 'Keep in sync with the "Banned Packages" table in ~/.claude/CLAUDE.md.' That's a user-private file (per the harness CLAUDE.md preamble) and is NOT in the repo. So: (1) the CI cannot verify the in-repo BANNED constant matches CLAUDE.md, (2) any change to CLAUDE.md (e.g. a new banned package added 2026-04-20) only lands in CI when a contributor remembers to edit this .mjs file too, (3) the docstring lies — the file is not 'in sync' with anything, it's a copy. The TS-side BANNED array also doesn't include version pins; for axios, CLAUDE.md probably narrows the ban to 1.14.1 and 0.30.4 (per the script's reason text), but the script flags ANY axios version — a downgrade to 0.27.x (pre-compromise) would still be blocked.
- **Evidence**: scripts/check-banned-packages.mjs:1121 'Keep in sync with the "Banned Packages" table in ~/.claude/CLAUDE.md' — the file is not version-controlled. BANNED array at lines 1142-1164 flags axios by NAME with no version range.
- **Fix**: Either (a) move the banned-packages list into a CI-checked YAML in the repo (e.g. .github/banned-packages.yml) so it's a real source of truth and CI can grep it, or (b) update the docstring to say 'Mirrored from CLAUDE.md as of 2026-04-16; refresh when CLAUDE.md changes — there is no automatic sync.' For axios, gate by version range: `if (banned.name === 'axios' && (entry.version === '1.14.1' || entry.version === '0.30.4'))` to allow safe pre-compromise versions if a hypothetical legacy dep needs them.

#### G15-068 · Rate-limit token consumed before input validation on POST /api/simulator
- **File**: `src/app/api/simulator/route.ts:35`
- **Specialist**: `api-contract` (confidence 9)
- **Summary**: The route consumes a simulatorLimiter token (line 35) BEFORE parsing JSON (line 53-58) and BEFORE running Zod validation (line 60-69). An attacker (or a buggy client looping a 400) burns the user's 20/hour budget with malformed payloads, effectively DOS'ing the legitimate user from their own bucket without ever touching the analytics service. The Bridge route has the same ordering but its limiter is 5/min — much harder to exhaust accidentally than 20/hour.
- **Evidence**: src/app/api/simulator/route.ts:35 `const rl = await checkLimit(simulatorLimiter, ...);` runs immediately after auth. Lines 53-58 then `await req.json()` (can throw → 400 'Invalid JSON' while the token is already gone). Lines 60-69 SimulatorRequestSchema.safeParse → 400 same situation.
- **Fix**: Move the rate-limit check below the JSON parse + Zod parse so only semantically valid simulation attempts consume a token. The CSRF + auth checks should stay first (cheap, no token cost).

#### G15-069 · POST /api/simulator 500-branch leaks internal error details via error envelope
- **File**: `src/app/api/simulator/route.ts:103`
- **Specialist**: `api-contract` (confidence 9)
- **Summary**: The 500 fallback returns `err.message` verbatim. For AnalyticsTimeoutError this exposes `'Analytics service timed out after 15000ms on /api/simulator'` (internal path + timeout budget). For Zod response-shape violations bubbled from parseResponse in src/lib/analytics-client.ts:140-143, this exposes `'Analytics response contract violation on /api/simulator: deltas.sharpe_delta: Expected number, received null; ...'` — internal field names + schema details. Same shape applies to AnalyticsUpstreamError 5xx (line 100 condition is <500, so 5xx fall through to 500 with err.message which could be Python tracebacks turned into FastAPI 500 details).
- **Evidence**: src/app/api/simulator/route.ts:103-105 `const message = err instanceof Error ? err.message : 'Portfolio impact simulation failed'; return NextResponse.json({ error: message }, { status: 500 });`. Combine with src/lib/analytics-client.ts:26-30 (`AnalyticsTimeoutError` message includes path + ms) and src/lib/analytics-client.ts:140-143 (parseResponse throws with full issue paths).
- **Fix**: In the 500 branch return a fixed envelope: `NextResponse.json({error: 'Portfolio impact simulation failed'}, {status: 500, headers: NO_STORE_HEADERS})`. The server-side `console.error('[simulator] Simulation failed:', err)` on line 96 already captures the detail for operators. Only the 4xx forward branch (line 100-101) should propagate the upstream message since those are user-actionable ('Portfolio not found', 'Candidate is already in this portfolio').

#### G15-070 · <style> tag injected inside the dialog mount instead of hoisted to global CSS
- **File**: `src/components/portfolio/PortfolioImpactPanel.tsx:203`
- **Specialist**: `performance` (confidence 9)
- **Summary**: The slideInRight keyframes are inlined inside the dialog's JSX (`<style>{`@keyframes slideInRight { ... }`}</style>`). Each panel mount injects a fresh <style> tag into <head> and triggers a style recalculation. Mounting/unmounting the panel repeatedly (e.g., the user opens/closes for several rows) means repeated DOM <style> churn that the browser must parse/dedupe. Trivial perf cost but trivially fixable.
- **Evidence**: src/components/portfolio/PortfolioImpactPanel.tsx:203-208 — `<style>{`@keyframes slideInRight { from { transform: translateX(100%); } to { transform: translateX(0); } }`}</style>` inside the dialog's render tree.
- **Fix**: Move the keyframes into globals.css (or a CSS module) so they're parsed once and cached. The animation: rule on the panel keeps working unchanged. (See rendering-hoist-jsx / js-batch-dom-css guidance.)

#### G15-071 · PortfolioImpactPanel error body typed `any` after JSON.parse
- **File**: `src/components/portfolio/PortfolioImpactPanel.tsx:52`
- **Specialist**: `type-design-analyzer` (confidence 9)
- **Summary**: After `const body = await res.json().catch(() => ({ error: 'Simulation failed' }))`, every property access on `body` is implicitly `any` (parameter inference + no schema). `body.error`, `body.retryAfter` are read without runtime guards beyond `typeof === 'number'`. A typo on the server (`{ msg: '...' }` instead of `{ error: '...' }`) would surface as `undefined` text in the alert.
- **Evidence**: src/components/portfolio/PortfolioImpactPanel.tsx:52-66
- **Fix**: See finding on `ErrorResponseSchema` — same fix. At minimum, type the catch fallback as `{ error: string }` so the `body` variable is `unknown` rather than `any`, forcing explicit narrowing.

#### G15-072 · MergedPoint shape duplicates SimulatorMetricsSnapshot null-handling locally
- **File**: `src/components/portfolio/PortfolioImpactPanel.tsx:2619`
- **Specialist**: `type-design-analyzer` (confidence 9)
- **Summary**: `interface MergedPoint { date: string; current: number | null; proposed: number | null; }` is fine, but it's a private duplicate of the cross-cutting 'nullable metric point' concept already in `SimulatorMetricsSnapshot`. A future curve type that lifts the null discipline elsewhere will have two places to update.
- **Evidence**: src/components/portfolio/PortfolioImpactPanel.tsx:2619-2623
- **Fix**: Lift `MergedPoint` to a shared module alongside `TimeSeriesPoint`, or model it as `TimeSeriesPoint & { proposed: number | null }` to make the relationship explicit.

#### G15-073 · buildPath accepts `[number, number] | null` tuple — null-as-sentinel mixed with structural type
- **File**: `src/components/portfolio/PortfolioImpactPanel.tsx:2694`
- **Specialist**: `type-design-analyzer` (confidence 9)
- **Summary**: `function buildPath(points: ([number, number] | null)[]): string | null` uses `null` as a 'gap' sentinel inside the tuple array. This conflates two concerns (point vs gap) into a nullable union. A typed `type PathSegment = { kind: 'point'; x: number; y: number } | { kind: 'gap' }` would be more self-documenting and prevents the caller from passing `[NaN, NaN]` (currently legal). Scope is narrow but the pattern (null-as-flag inside a tuple array) is a smell.
- **Evidence**: src/components/portfolio/PortfolioImpactPanel.tsx:2694
- **Fix**: Either lift `null` out into a dedicated `Gap` literal type (as above) or have `buildPath` accept `Array<readonly [number, number]>` only and let the caller split contiguous runs upstream. Documenting 'null is a gap marker' in the inline JSDoc would help if the refactor is too invasive.

#### G15-074 · SimulatorRequestSchema accepts any non-empty string for UUID fields
- **File**: `src/lib/api/simulatorSchema.ts:20`
- **Specialist**: `api-contract` (confidence 9)
- **Summary**: portfolio_id and candidate_strategy_id correspond to UUID-typed Postgres columns (portfolios.id, strategies.id), but the request Zod schema accepts `z.string().min(1)` — any non-empty string passes. A 10 KB junk string, a SQL-shaped string, or a non-UUID identifier flows through validation, hits Supabase (.eq('id', portfolio_id)), and silently returns null → 404. Tightening to `.uuid()` gives defense-in-depth, surfaces validation failures with clearer messages, and avoids unnecessary DB round-trips for obviously malformed inputs.
- **Evidence**: src/lib/api/simulatorSchema.ts:19-22 `export const SimulatorRequestSchema = z.object({ portfolio_id: z.string().min(1), candidate_strategy_id: z.string().min(1), });` — no UUID format check despite both DB columns being UUID.
- **Fix**: Change to `z.string().uuid()` for both fields, matching the EnqueueComputeJobResponseSchema pattern in src/lib/analytics-schemas.ts:103. Update the 400 error message to reference 'valid UUIDs'.

## G16 — PRs #62-#63 — Vercel cron trim + gitignore

### HIGH (11)

#### G16-001 · PR #63 .gitignore is a no-op for 73 already-tracked .planning/ files · _new_
- **File**: `.gitignore:42`
- **Specialist**: `red-team` (confidence 10)
- **Summary**: PR #63 added `.planning/` to .gitignore claiming 'never in the repo', but `git ls-files` shows 73 .planning/ files currently tracked on main (REQUIREMENTS.md, ROADMAP.md, STATE.md, phase-19/*, phases/15-csv-unblock/*, phases/16-diagnostic-spike-observability/*, etc.). Git's .gitignore is silently ignored for files already tracked — adding the rule does NOT untrack them. Developers reading the .gitignore comment will (a) believe planning artifacts are safely local-only when they're being committed in every PR, and (b) skip the explicit `git rm --cached` step needed to retroactively detach them. The comment 'never in the repo' is false. (The .claude/ rule is fine — 0 files tracked.)
- **Evidence**: git ls-files | grep -c '^.planning/' => 73 files; .gitignore L41-43 adds '.claude/' and '.planning/' with comment '...never in the repo'
- **Fix**: Either (a) `git rm -r --cached .planning/` and commit the removal so the rule actually applies — but this loses planning history visible to PR reviewers, OR (b) drop `.planning/` from .gitignore and amend the comment to acknowledge `.planning/` is intentionally tracked while `.claude/` is the only local-only dir. Pick one; the current state lies in both directions.

#### G16-002 · Worker tick startup spike: 4 loops fire simultaneously on every restart
- **File**: `analytics-service/main_worker.py:332`
- **Specialist**: `performance` (confidence 8)
- **Summary**: `asyncio.gather` starts `daily_enqueue_loop`, `_scheduled_daily_loop("sync_funding")`, `_scheduled_daily_loop("reconcile_strategies")`, and `_scheduled_daily_loop("cleanup_ack_tokens")` together. Every one runs its `tick_fn()` immediately on startup (see scheduled_tasks.py module — `await tick_fn()` before entering the wait loop). Pre-PR, Vercel staggered these (00:00, 03:30, 03:00 Sun, 0/4*). Post-PR, every worker deploy/restart fires all 4 daily ticks in the same second — each one runs a `SELECT id FROM strategies JOIN api_keys` then loops `enqueue_compute_job` RPC per strategy. With N strategies and a worker that restarts on Railway redeploys (multiple times/day), this is a thundering herd against Supabase PostgREST + the postgres connection pool.
- **Evidence**: main_worker.py:332-339 asyncio.gather(daily_enqueue_loop(), _scheduled_daily_loop("sync_funding", ...), _scheduled_daily_loop("reconcile_strategies", ...), _scheduled_daily_loop("cleanup_ack_tokens", ...)). scheduled_tasks.py:82 `try: await tick_fn()` at loop entry, no jitter.
- **Fix**: Stagger initial ticks with `asyncio.sleep` jitter (e.g. each loop sleeps a different fixed offset before its first tick: 0s/30s/60s/90s). Or seed loops with the original Vercel UTC anchor times via `await asyncio.sleep((target_utc - now).total_seconds() % 86400)` so the worker re-creates a staggered daily schedule rather than concentrating load at startup.

#### G16-003 · _scheduled_daily_loop swallows tick failures forever — no alerting path
- **File**: `analytics-service/main_worker.py:75`
- **Specialist**: `silent-failure-hunter` (confidence 9)
- **Summary**: PR #62 wraps every relocated cron tick in `try/except Exception` that only logs `logger.error` and continues. Unlike the TS handlers it replaced (which return HTTP 500 to Vercel and trigger Vercel monitoring), the worker loop has zero downstream escalation: no Sentry capture, no portfolio_alerts insert, no Statsig event, no kill-switch. A permanently-broken tick (RPC permission revoked, schema drift, Supabase outage) will log identical errors every 24h indefinitely while operators see a green-process worker and a silent compute_jobs queue. The original TS reconcile handler explicitly returned 500 on all-failed batches `so monitoring catches the regression instead of treating an all-failed batch as a successful empty run` — that signal is lost when the loop catches and continues.
- **Evidence**: analytics-service/main_worker.py:75 `async def _scheduled_daily_loop(name: str, tick_fn, interval: float = 86400.0) -> None:` ... `except Exception as exc:  # noqa: BLE001` ... `logger.error("%s tick failed: %s", name, exc, exc_info=True)` (no Sentry, no alert insert, loop continues)
- **Fix**: Add Sentry capture (or portfolio_alerts insert) on tick failure, with a consecutive-failure threshold that promotes to critical. Mirror the TS handler's all-failed → 500 semantic: track consecutive failures per tick name, and after N (e.g. 3) raise a structured alert event the operator dashboard surfaces. Alternatively, re-raise after a threshold so asyncio.gather propagates and the supervisor restarts the worker — which at least triggers Railway alerts.

#### G16-004 · cleanup-ack-tokens cadence amplifies 7x weekly to daily without ceremony
- **File**: `analytics-service/services/scheduled_tasks.py:269`
- **Specialist**: `performance` (confidence 8)
- **Summary**: The original Vercel cron schedule for cleanup-ack-tokens was `0 3 * * 0` (Sundays 03:00 UTC, weekly). The replacement Python tick runs DAILY (`_scheduled_daily_loop("cleanup_ack_tokens", ...)` with default interval=86400.0s). This is a silent 7x increase in delete I/O on used_ack_tokens. The deleted set is the same (rows older than 30d), so steady-state daily churn is roughly 1/7th of weekly per tick — net cost is comparable, but the cadence change was not called out in the PR description and contradicts the original `// nightly cleanup` intent in src/app/api/cron/cleanup-ack-tokens/route.ts header (weekly).
- **Evidence**: vercel.json (before) `{ "path": "/api/cron/cleanup-ack-tokens", "schedule": "0 3 * * 0" }` (Sundays). main_worker.py:119 `_scheduled_daily_loop("cleanup_ack_tokens", cleanup_ack_tokens_tick)` with default 86400.0s interval = every 24h. scheduled_tasks.py:75 `async def _scheduled_daily_loop(name: str, tick_fn, interval: float = 86400.0)`.
- **Fix**: Either explicitly run weekly (`interval=604800.0` in the gather call) to match the original cadence, or document in the runbook that the worker version runs daily by design and update the route.ts header to match.

#### G16-005 · cleanup_ack_tokens_tick missing .select() — silent telemetry drift, deleted=0 reported even when GC fires
- **File**: `analytics-service/services/scheduled_tasks.py:281`
- **Specialist**: `silent-failure-hunter` (confidence 9)
- **Summary**: The TS handler chains `.delete().lt("used_at", cutoff).select("token_hash")` so PostgREST returns the deleted rows and `data.length` is the true delete count. PR #62's Python port drops `.select(...)` entirely: `_delete()` returns whatever the supabase-py client populates for a delete without RETURNING, which in practice yields `result.data = []` (or `None`). The subsequent `deleted = len(result.data or [])` then logs `deleted=0` on every tick — even when 100k rows were actually deleted. Operators inspecting the log line will conclude the GC is broken (or that no tokens are aging), and could either disable the loop or run a one-off cleanup that races the loop. The TS handler's count was load-bearing for the runbook's verification step.
- **Evidence**: analytics-service/services/scheduled_tasks.py:281 (PR #62 diff) `supabase.from_("used_ack_tokens").delete().lt("used_at", cutoff).execute()` — compare src/app/api/cron/cleanup-ack-tokens/route.ts:40-44 `await admin.from("used_ack_tokens").delete().lt("used_at", cutoff).select("token_hash")`
- **Fix**: Append `.select("token_hash")` (or `.select("*")`) to the delete chain so the count reflects reality. Then assert the value in a regression test (the diff's test_applies_30_day_cutoff verifies the filter shape but not that the count is faithful).

#### G16-006 · enqueue_*_tick drops correlation_id metadata — batch-tick forensic join lost
- **File**: `analytics-service/services/scheduled_tasks.py:177`
- **Specialist**: `silent-failure-hunter` (confidence 9)
- **Summary**: PR #62's `_enqueue_each` calls `supabase.rpc("enqueue_compute_job", {"p_strategy_id": sid, "p_kind": kind})` with NO `p_metadata`. The TS handlers (which the comment claims this mirrors `one-for-one`) explicitly pass `p_metadata: { correlation_id }` so every job from one cron tick shares a forensic batch id, queryable as `compute_jobs.metadata->>'correlation_id'`. This was a deliberate Phase-18 forensic thread (Day-2 Bug #1 follow-up). Dropping it means: a flaky worker tick can no longer be traced as a batch — operators have to time-window-correlate and guess. The TS comment at src/app/api/cron/sync-funding/route.ts:58 spells out the design intent explicitly. Silent loss of debuggability.
- **Evidence**: analytics-service/services/scheduled_tasks.py:177 (PR #62 diff) `supabase.rpc("enqueue_compute_job", {"p_strategy_id": sid, "p_kind": kind}).execute()` — vs src/app/api/cron/sync-funding/route.ts:72 which passes `p_metadata: { correlation_id }` per row
- **Fix**: Mint a per-tick correlation_id at the top of `enqueue_*_tick` (mirror `await getCorrelationId()` semantics, e.g. `correlation_id = str(uuid.uuid4())`) and thread it into `_enqueue_each(..., correlation_id)` then pass `p_metadata={"correlation_id": correlation_id}` to the RPC. Add a test asserting the metadata kwarg is present.

#### G16-007 · enqueue_*_tick treats all-failed batch as success — no 500-equivalent escalation
- **File**: `analytics-service/services/scheduled_tasks.py:228`
- **Specialist**: `silent-failure-hunter` (confidence 8)
- **Summary**: `src/app/api/cron/reconcile-strategies/route.ts:121` deliberately returns HTTP 500 when `enqueued === 0 && errors.length > 0`, with the comment `If every enqueue failed, the cron run produced zero useful work — surface that as a 500 so monitoring catches the regression instead of treating an all-failed batch as a successful empty run`. PR #62's Python tick loses this signal entirely: it returns a `{enqueued: 0, failed: N, total_candidates: N}` dict that `_scheduled_daily_loop` discards. From outside the worker process, an all-failed reconcile batch looks identical to a quiet day. The asymmetry between the routes-still-in-place (which curl-callers will see returning 500) and the scheduled invocation (silently logging) means manual ops checks lie about whether the schedule works.
- **Evidence**: analytics-service/services/scheduled_tasks.py:228 (PR #62 diff) returns `{"enqueued": enqueued, "failed": len(errors), "total_candidates": len(strategy_ids)}` with no escalation — vs src/app/api/cron/reconcile-strategies/route.ts:121 `const status = enqueued === 0 && errors.length > 0 ? 500 : 200;`
- **Fix**: Raise a typed exception (e.g. `ScheduledTaskAllFailed`) when `enqueued == 0 and errors`. `_scheduled_daily_loop` can catch a different exception class than generic `Exception` and route it to Sentry/portfolio_alerts as critical rather than a noise-level log.

#### G16-010 · cleanup-ack-tokens cron handler has zero test coverage

The TS route.ts has no colocated route.test.ts, and grep shows no integration coverage either. A regression in safeCompare, the cutoff math (off-by-one between `Date.now() - 30*24*60*60*1000` and a server clock skew), or the `.lt('used_at', cutoff)` filter (e.g. column rename) would ship silently — Vercel cron only logs non-2xx and the handler returns 200 with `{deleted: 0}` if the filter matches nothing. The replay-prevention table grows unbounded if cleanup silently breaks.
- **Evidence**: `find src/app/api/cron/cleanup-ack-tokens -name route.test.ts` returns no results; `grep -rln cleanup_ack_tokens|cleanup-ack-tokens src tests` returns only the route.ts and one comment in main_worker.py L550 noting the loop was removed; the four sibling crons (sync-funding, reconcile-strategies, warm-analytics, cleanup-wizard-drafts, founder-lp-report) each have route.test.ts.

Mirror sync-funding/route.test.ts mocking style.

Funding fee sync goes from 6x/day to 1x/day. ### MEDIUM (16)

#### G16-012 · Worker scheduled-task loop wrapper has no test for tick-failure isolation or SHUTDOWN exit
- **File**: `analytics-service/main_worker.py:279`
- **Specialist**: `pr-test-analyzer` (confidence 8)
- **Summary**: PR #62 added `_scheduled_daily_loop(name, tick_fn, interval)` in main_worker.py which catches Exception around tick_fn (`# noqa: BLE001`) and uses `asyncio.wait_for(SHUTDOWN.wait(), timeout=interval)`. The PR's added test_scheduled_tasks.py covers each tick function but NOT this wrapper. The wrapper has 3 failure modes that ship silently: (1) initial tick failure should not prevent the loop from continuing; (2) tick failures inside the loop should be logged but not crash the gather; (3) SHUTDOWN.set() should break the loop within `interval` (default 86400s — 24h). A bug where wait_for raises something other than TimeoutError, or where SHUTDOWN.wait() races the timeout incorrectly, leaves the worker stuck or crashed during shutdown. This is the exact failure class /api/cron/* had on Vercel that prompted the move.
- **Evidence**: analytics-service/tests/test_scheduled_tasks.py asserts each tick's behavior with a mock supabase but does not import or exercise `_scheduled_daily_loop` from main_worker.py. `grep -n '_scheduled_daily_loop' analytics-service/tests/*.py` returns nothing. The wrapper's `except asyncio.TimeoutError: pass` path is the only one that re-runs the tick; if a different exception class shows up (e.g. CancelledError in Python 3.11+ behavior change) the loop exits prematurely.
- **Fix**: Add tests in test_main_worker.py (or a new test_scheduled_daily_loop.py) covering: (1) initial tick raises -> loop continues to the wait_for branch; (2) tick raises mid-loop -> next iteration still fires after timeout; (3) SHUTDOWN.set() while wait_for is pending -> loop returns within ~50ms (use a short interval like 0.1s); (4) verify the 'exiting (shutdown)' log line fires exactly once. Use the same fakeclock pattern test_main_worker.py uses for dispatch_loop.

#### G16-013 · _enqueue_each serializes per-strategy RPCs in one thread; TS used Promise.allSettled
- **File**: `analytics-service/services/scheduled_tasks.py:167`
- **Specialist**: `performance` (confidence 9)
- **Summary**: The TS route at src/app/api/cron/sync-funding/route.ts:70 uses `Promise.allSettled(rows.map(row => admin.rpc('enqueue_compute_job', {...})))` — N strategies enqueue in parallel. The new Python `_enqueue_each` is a synchronous `for sid in strategy_ids:` loop that issues N RPCs sequentially, all wrapped inside ONE `db_execute(lambda: _enqueue_each(...))` call (line 214). `db_execute` is `asyncio.to_thread`, so the entire loop runs on a single thread pool worker. For N=100 strategies and ~50ms per RPC, the TS handler returned in ~50ms; the Python tick takes ~5s and occupies one threadpool slot the whole time, starving other db_execute calls (dispatch_loop, watchdog_loop) for that duration.
- **Evidence**: scheduled_tasks.py:167-186 `def _enqueue_each(supabase, strategy_ids, kind) ... for sid in strategy_ids: supabase.rpc(...).execute()`. scheduled_tasks.py:214 `enqueued, errors = await db_execute(lambda: _enqueue_each(supabase, strategy_ids, 'sync_funding'))`. db.py:17 `async def db_execute(fn): return await asyncio.to_thread(fn)`. Contrast src/app/api/cron/sync-funding/route.ts:70 `Promise.allSettled(rows.map(...))`.
- **Fix**: Wrap each per-row `supabase.rpc(...).execute()` in its own `db_execute(...)` call, then `await asyncio.gather(*tasks)` (or use `asyncio.Semaphore` to cap concurrency at e.g. 10). This restores parallelism, frees the thread pool between RPCs, and matches the TS route's wall-time behavior.

#### G16-014 · cleanup_ack_tokens_tick delete without .select() may always report deleted=0
- **File**: `analytics-service/services/scheduled_tasks.py:280`
- **Specialist**: `performance` (confidence 8)
- **Summary**: The tick computes `deleted = len(result.data or [])` to report progress, but the Supabase Python client's `.delete()` without `.select(...)` returns an empty `data` payload by default — the row count is conveyed in PostgREST `Content-Range` headers, not the response body. The metric `{"deleted": N}` will be 0 even when rows were actually deleted, masking growth of `used_ack_tokens` from operators. The original TS route uses `.delete().lt(...).select('token_hash')` exactly to surface the count.
- **Evidence**: scheduled_tasks.py:280-289 `def _delete(): return (supabase.from_('used_ack_tokens').delete().lt('used_at', cutoff).execute())` then `deleted = len(result.data or [])`. Contrast src/app/api/cron/cleanup-ack-tokens/route.ts:40-44 `.delete().lt('used_at', cutoff).select('token_hash')`.
- **Fix**: Add `.select('token_hash')` to the delete chain: `supabase.from_('used_ack_tokens').delete().lt('used_at', cutoff).select('token_hash').execute()`. This actually returns the deleted rows so `len(result.data)` matches the row count, restoring observability of cleanup throughput.

#### G16-015 · Worker daily ticks re-fire on every restart; no idempotency window
- **File**: `analytics-service/services/scheduled_tasks.py:82`
- **Specialist**: `performance` (confidence 8)
- **Summary**: `_scheduled_daily_loop` runs `await tick_fn()` immediately on startup before entering the wait loop. Each Railway redeploy of the worker (which can happen multiple times per day during active development) triggers a fresh `enqueue_sync_funding_tick` + `enqueue_reconcile_strategies_tick` + `cleanup_ack_tokens_tick`. Sync_funding and reconcile_strategies push compute_jobs into the queue — duplicate runs within the same day enqueue duplicate jobs that the worker then has to dispatch and dedupe (or do double work).
- **Evidence**: scheduled_tasks.py:82 `try: await tick_fn() except Exception as exc: logger.error(...)` runs unconditionally at the top of `_scheduled_daily_loop`. No persisted last-run timestamp guards re-firing on restart.
- **Fix**: Check `compute_jobs` for an existing same-day job per strategy before enqueueing (idempotency), OR persist a `scheduled_runs(name, last_ran_at)` row and skip the initial tick if the previous run was <24h ago. Either approach guards against deploy churn re-doing work.

#### G16-016 · CHALLENGE: 6 of 7 performance findings target Python scheduled_tasks.py — file does not exist on main, false-live · _challenge_ · refs: performance#1, performance#2, performance#3, performance#4, performance#5, performance#6, performance#7, silent-failure-hunter#1, silent-failure-hunter#2, silent-failure-hunter#3, silent-failure-hunter#4, silent-failure-hunter#5, silent-failure-hunter#6, silent-failure-hunter#8, pr-test-analyzer#5
- **File**: `analytics-service/services/scheduled_tasks.py:0`
- **Specialist**: `red-team` (confidence 9)
- **Summary**: Performance specialist findings #1-#7 and silent-failure-hunter findings #1-#6, #8 all reference analytics-service/services/scheduled_tasks.py which was deleted when the project upgraded to Vercel Pro. `ls analytics-service/services/scheduled_tasks.py` => No such file or directory. `grep _scheduled_daily_loop analytics-service/main_worker.py` returns nothing. The cleanup-ack-tokens TS route on main DOES use `.select('token_hash')` (route.ts:44) so the silent-failure-hunter 'deleted=0' finding (#2) is also wrong against the live code — that bug only existed in the deleted Python port. Without explicitly flagging which findings died with the file, downstream readers will spin cycles trying to fix code that isn't there. Live findings reduce to: (a) cleanup-ack-tokens has no test, (b) flag-monitor helpers have no colocated unit test, (c) vercel-cron-limits.test.ts has no negative tests, (d) loadCrons() permits empty array.

#### G16-017 · _enqueue_each only catches sync exceptions — supabase-py result.error path hidden
- **File**: `analytics-service/services/scheduled_tasks.py:182`
- **Specialist**: `silent-failure-hunter` (confidence 8)
- **Summary**: The TS handler examines BOTH `result.status === "rejected"` AND `result.value.error` because supabase-js can return a PostgREST error in `result.error` without throwing. PR #62's `_enqueue_each` only wraps the call in `try/except Exception`, then inspects `getattr(result, "data", None)`. If supabase-py's `.execute()` returns a result object with `data=None` and `error=<APIError>` instead of raising (PostgREST 4xx/5xx surfaces this way for some failure modes), the loop silently treats the row as `not enqueued` (no enqueued += 1, no errors.append) — neither counted in `enqueued` nor `failed`. The aggregated log `enqueued=X failed=Y total=Z` will silently violate the invariant `X + Y == Z`, and operators eyeballing the log won't notice.
- **Evidence**: analytics-service/services/scheduled_tasks.py:182 (PR #62 diff) `if getattr(result, "data", None):` ... `except Exception as exc:` — no inspection of `result.error`. Compare TS pattern in src/app/api/cron/sync-funding/route.ts:92 `} else if (result.value.error) { failed += 1; ...`
- **Fix**: After `result = supabase.rpc(...).execute()`, also check `if getattr(result, "error", None): errors.append(...); continue` before the data-truthy branch. Add a regression test that injects a mock returning `MagicMock(data=None, error=MagicMock(message="PG fail"))` and asserts it ends up in `errors`, not silently dropped.

#### G16-018 · fetch_result.data or [] masks fetch-time errors as 'no candidates'
- **File**: `analytics-service/services/scheduled_tasks.py:207`
- **Specialist**: `silent-failure-hunter` (confidence 8)
- **Summary**: After `fetch_result = await db_execute(_fetch)`, the diff does `rows = fetch_result.data or []` and short-circuits to `{"enqueued": 0, ...}` when empty. If supabase-py returns a result with `data=None` and `error` populated (PostgREST 5xx, RLS denial, schema cache mismatch) rather than raising, the tick silently emits `[scheduled/sync_funding] no candidates` — the operator sees a quiet log and assumes there genuinely were no eligible strategies that day. Meanwhile the underlying fetch outage may persist for weeks. The TS handler explicitly inspects `fetchError` and 500s.
- **Evidence**: analytics-service/services/scheduled_tasks.py:207 (PR #62 diff) `fetch_result = await db_execute(_fetch); rows = fetch_result.data or []` — vs src/app/api/cron/sync-funding/route.ts:45 `if (fetchError) { console.error(...); return NextResponse.json({ error: fetchError.message }, { status: 500 }); }`
- **Fix**: Inspect the result for an error before the data fallback: `if getattr(fetch_result, "error", None): raise RuntimeError(f"fetch failed: {fetch_result.error}")`. The exception will surface via `_scheduled_daily_loop`'s except block at minimum — far better than 'no candidates' lying to the log.

#### G16-019 · docs/architecture/adr-0008-cron-architecture.md L33/L59 claim warm-analytics runs every 5 minutes — bakes the lie into the ADR · _new_
- **File**: `docs/architecture/adr-0008-cron-architecture.md:33`
- **Specialist**: `red-team` (confidence 9)
- **Summary**: ADR-0008 (Status: Proposed) commits to 'Infra health pings (analytics warmup) -> Vercel Cron via vercel.json. Schedule: every 5 minutes.' (L33) and lists the job inventory at L59 with '*/5 * * * *' for warm-analytics. Actual schedule in vercel.json is `0 0 * * *` (daily). ADRs are the canonical decision record — when an ADR says 'we decided to run X every 5 minutes' and reality runs it daily, any future engineer cross-referencing the ADR for design context will be misled. Either the ADR was never enacted, or the schedule drifted without amending the ADR. Either way the ADR's authority is corrupted.
- **Evidence**: docs/architecture/adr-0008-cron-architecture.md:33 'Schedule: every 5 minutes.'; L59 '| Analytics warmup | */5 * * * * | Vercel Cron (1) | /api/cron/warm-analytics |'. Compare vercel.json L7 schedule '0 0 * * *'.
- **Fix**: Amend ADR-0008 with a Status update ('Implemented with deviation: warm-analytics moved to daily on 2026-MM-DD because <reason>') OR restore */5 * * * * and add warm-analytics to SUB_DAILY_ALLOWLIST. ADR conventions require explicit amendment, not silent drift.

#### G16-020 · docs/runbooks/bridge-outcome-cron.md inherits the stale Hobby narrative — 'fails CI on any third entry' · _new_

Either approach removes the half-state.

#### G16-022 · vercel-cron-limits.test.ts asserts quota shape but not that listed paths resolve to handlers
- **File**: `src/__tests__/vercel-cron-limits.test.ts:70`
- **Specialist**: `pr-test-analyzer` (confidence 9)
- **Summary**: The PR's regression test added in PR #62 (and still present on main with relaxed Pro-plan bounds) checks count<=10 and daily-schedule-or-allowlisted, but does NOT assert that each cron's `path` field resolves to an actual route handler on disk. A typo in vercel.json (e.g. `/api/cron/sync-fundings` instead of `/api/cron/sync-funding`, or `/api/alert-digest` vs `/api/cron/alert-digest`) would deploy a cron that 404s silently — Vercel doesn't validate the path against the build output and only retries non-2xx 3 times before giving up. This is exactly the silent-failure class the test was added to prevent. The integrity of `/api/alert-digest` (which lives at a non-`/cron/` path) is particularly fragile.
- **Evidence**: src/__tests__/vercel-cron-limits.test.ts L70-95 — only three `it()` blocks: max count, schedule frequency, and 'SUB_DAILY_ALLOWLIST entries are present in vercel.json'. No `it('every cron path resolves to a route handler')` block. `grep -n 'src/app' src/__tests__/vercel-cron-limits.test.ts` returns nothing.
- **Fix**: Add a fourth test in vercel-cron-limits.test.ts that maps each cron's `path` to a filesystem check: for path `/api/cron/foo`, assert `src/app/api/cron/foo/route.ts` exists; for non-/cron/ paths like `/api/alert-digest`, assert `src/app/api/alert-digest/route.ts` exists. Use `fs.existsSync` and accept either route.ts or route.tsx. This catches the typo class and PRs that delete a handler without removing the cron entry.

#### G16-023 · vercel-cron-limits.test.ts has no negative tests proving the guardrail catches regressions
- **File**: `src/__tests__/vercel-cron-limits.test.ts:70`
- **Specialist**: `pr-test-analyzer` (confidence 8)
- **Summary**: The CHANGELOG entry for PR #62 claims 'Proven to catch the exact breach that blocked PRs 57/58/61' but the test only reads the real vercel.json — there is no unit test asserting the predicate functions (`isDailyOrLessFrequent`, `MAX_CRONS_ALLOWED`) reject offending inputs. If someone refactors `isDailyOrLessFrequent` to be permissive (e.g. accidentally accepting `*` as numeric), the suite would keep passing against a clean vercel.json but fail to catch the next regression. The test is its own oracle — there's no way to know it works until production breaks again.
- **Evidence**: src/__tests__/vercel-cron-limits.test.ts L61-68 — `isDailyOrLessFrequent` has 5 branches (parts.length, looksNumeric(minute), looksNumeric(hour), parts.length !== 5 path, return true) but no `describe('isDailyOrLessFrequent')` block tests them. No `it('rejects "0 */4 * * *"')` or `it('rejects "*/15 * * * *"')` test exists. The Pro-plan relaxation kept MAX_CRONS_ALLOWED=10 untested — a future bump to 50 wouldn't be caught.
- **Fix**: Either (a) export `isDailyOrLessFrequent` and add a unit-test suite with positive cases (`'0 0 * * *'` accept, `'30 3 * * *'` accept, `'0 9 * * 0'` accept) and negative cases (`'*/15 * * * *'` reject, `'0 */4 * * *'` reject, `'* * * * *'` reject, `'0 0'` reject) or (b) add an `it('synthetic over-quota vercel.json fails')` test that loads a fixture string instead of the real file via dependency-injecting the loader.

#### G16-024 · vercel-cron-limits.test.ts silently passes if crons array is missing or empty
- **File**: `src/__tests__/vercel-cron-limits.test.ts:41`
- **Specialist**: `silent-failure-hunter` (confidence 8)
- **Summary**: `loadCrons()` uses `parsed.crons ?? []`. Both assertions (`length <= MAX_CRONS_ON_HOBBY` and `every schedule is daily`) trivially pass when the array is empty or absent. A regression that accidentally deletes the crons key in vercel.json — exactly the kind of breakage this test is supposed to guard against — would pass green. The PR description sells this test as 'Proven to catch the exact breach that blocked PRs 57/58/61', but it cannot catch the inverse breach (missing schedule = production cron silently un-scheduled, which is the bigger silent-failure risk).
- **Evidence**: src/__tests__/vercel-cron-limits.test.ts:41 (PR #62 diff) `return parsed.crons ?? [];` — both `it()` blocks then operate on empty array without any 'array exists and is non-empty' assertion
- **Fix**: Add a third test: `it('declares at least one cron', () => { expect(loadCrons().length).toBeGreaterThan(0); })`. Optionally lock the expected paths (warm-analytics, alert-digest) so they cannot be silently renamed/removed without test churn surfacing the regression in CI.

#### G16-025 · flag-monitor cron route.ts has no colocated unit tests despite high-risk auto-rollback logic
- **File**: `src/app/api/cron/flag-monitor/route.ts:278`
- **Specialist**: `pr-test-analyzer` (confidence 9)
- **Summary**: flag-monitor is the only sub-daily cron (`*/15 * * * *`) and is exempted via SUB_DAILY_ALLOWLIST in the test PR #62 added (later relaxed). The handler flips the production kill-switch row in feature_flags — wrong threshold math, wrong env filter on the Sentry query, or PostgREST error swallowing rolls back production unnecessarily OR fails to roll back during a real incident. Integration tests exist at tests/integration/cron-flag-monitor*.test.ts but there is no colocated route.test.ts unit test covering the helper functions (parseSentryCount shape rotation, isPostgrestResolutionError matcher, getNumerator rate-limit vs outage distinction, handleZeroDenominator streak counter ZERO_DENOMINATOR_ALERT_AFTER boundary, triggerAutoRollback D-3 fallback).
- **Evidence**: `find src/app/api/cron/flag-monitor -name route.test.ts` returns nothing; only `route.ts`. The route has 5 extracted helpers (parseSentryCount, isPostgrestResolutionError, getNumerator, getDenominator, handleZeroDenominator, triggerAutoRollback) with branching logic that integration tests cannot exercise exhaustively without complex Sentry/Supabase mocks. SUB_DAILY_ALLOWLIST in src/__tests__/vercel-cron-limits.test.ts L41 acknowledges this cron's elevated risk but doesn't verify behavior.
- **Fix**: Add `src/app/api/cron/flag-monitor/route.test.ts` covering: (1) parseSentryCount handles both `data[0]['count()']` and `data[0].count` shapes plus malformed payloads → 0; (2) isPostgrestResolutionError matches PGRST, 'function not found', 'schema cache' but rejects unrelated errors; (3) 429 + x-sentry-rate-limit-remaining header returns `sentry_rate_limited` not `sentry_unreachable`; (4) zero-denominator streak alerts only AFTER ZERO_DENOMINATOR_ALERT_AFTER (boundary: streak=2 silent, streak=3 alerts); (5) triggerAutoRollback's D-3 PostgREST fallback returns 500 with `kill_switch_unreachable_d3` AND sends SEV-2 email; (6) WARN threshold sends email but does NOT flip kill-switch.

The reconcile-strategies route docstring at line 23 compounds the lie: 'sync-funding's 4-hour cadence (runs at 00/04/08/12/16/20)' — used as the reason for placing reconcile at 03:30 to avoid the 04:00 tick (which IS now real, but for a daily cron, not 4-hourly). #### G16-027 · warm-analytics docstring claims 'every 5 minutes' but cron is daily — entire belt+suspenders rationale broken · _new_
- **File**: `src/app/api/cron/warm-analytics/route.ts:5`
- **Specialist**: `red-team` (confidence 9)
- **Summary**: The route docstring opens 'Vercel Cron — pings the Python analytics service /health every 5 minutes so the friend's forwarded /demo URL never lands on a cold-started worker.' Reality: vercel.json schedules `0 0 * * *` (daily at midnight). The docstring goes on to describe a 'belt + suspenders' design where the cron keeps the service warm during idle hours and a per-request warmup closes the gap 'if the cron last ran > 5 min ago' — that gap is now up to 24h on the cron side, so the suspender (per-request warmup at src/lib/warmup-analytics.ts) is doing essentially all the work. The architectural documentation (docs/architecture/adr-0008-cron-architecture.md L33: 'Schedule: every 5 minutes' and L59 '*/5 * * * *') matches the docstring lie. Daily warm-up of a Railway worker that hibernates is unlikely to keep it warm — this may be a real production issue masquerading as a doc drift.
- **Evidence**: src/app/api/cron/warm-analytics/route.ts:5 '...every 5 minutes...'; vercel.json L7 '{ "path": "/api/cron/warm-analytics", "schedule": "0 0 * * *" }' (daily 00:00); docs/architecture/adr-0008-cron-architecture.md L33 'Schedule: every 5 minutes' and L59 '*/5 * * * *'.
- **Fix**: Decide intent first: (a) if daily is correct, update the route docstring and ADR-0008 to reflect that the cron is a daily 'this exists in case the per-request warmup never fires' belt and the per-request warmup is the actual hot-keeping mechanism; (b) if 5-min is actually needed for cold-start avoidance, restore `*/5 * * * *` in vercel.json (Pro plan allows it; flag-monitor is already in SUB_DAILY_ALLOWLIST so add warm-analytics there too). Don't leave the conflict in place.
