## G17 — PRs #67-#71 — Equity reconstruct fixes + supabase migrate workflow

### CRITICAL (6)

#### G17-001 · Supabase migrate workflow has NO post-apply verification — supabase db push can succeed while migration body is skipped
- **File**: `.github/workflows/supabase-migrate.yml:110`
- **Specialist**: `silent-failure-hunter` (confidence 9)
- **Summary**: The apply job runs `supabase db push` and exits — there is no `supabase migration list` after the push to confirm the local migrations are now in the remote history, no SELECT against schema_migrations, no smoke test that verifies the migrated objects actually exist, and no explicit `set -e` / `set -o pipefail` to ensure a non-zero exit from db push fails the workflow (bash defaults to ignoring failures in multi-line `run:` blocks). The workflow comment at lines 40-52 even DOCUMENTS an existing live failure mode: 'migrations 107 and 119 — both currently have applied rows in prod's schema_migrations but their SQL bodies have NOT been executed (see deferred-apply warnings in those files).' This is exactly the silent-success-while-skipping case the workflow needs to catch but doesn't.
- **Evidence**: .github/workflows/supabase-migrate.yml:103-110       - name: Push migrations to production         env:           SUPABASE_ACCESS_TOKEN: ${{ secrets.SUPABASE_ACCESS_TOKEN }}           SUPABASE_DB_PASSWORD: ${{ secrets.SUPABASE_DB_PASSWORD }}           SUPABASE_PROJECT_REF: ${{ vars.SUPABASE_PROJECT_REF }}         run: |           supabase link --project-ref "$SUPABASE_PROJECT_REF"           supabase db push
- **Fix**: Add `set -euo pipefail` at the top of the run block. After `supabase db push`, run `supabase migration list` and grep that the count of 'Reverted' rows is zero, then run a smoke SQL query (e.g. `SELECT version FROM supabase_migrations.schema_migrations ORDER BY version DESC LIMIT 5`) and assert the last 5 timestamps match the local file timestamps. Fail the workflow if any check fails — the current shape allows db push to no-op silently while reporting success.

#### G17-002 · OKX FUTURES contract-size inflation bug NEVER fixed — defensive override only fires for SWAP · _new_ · refs: code-reviewer-11, data-migration-15, pr-test-analyzer-6, type-design-analyzer-4
- **File**: `analytics-service/services/equity_reconstruction.py:169`
- **Specialist**: `red-team` (confidence 9)
- **Summary**: _resolve_perp_amt_base at line 169 only applies the defensive ctVal override when inst_type.upper() == 'SWAP'. But the trade-fetcher fans out across ALL OKX_INSTRUMENT_TYPES = ('SPOT','MARGIN','SWAP','FUTURES','OPTION') (line 69) and the is_perp branch at line 714 (`is_perp = ':' in raw_symbol`) catches FUTURES too — ccxt symbol shape for expiring OKX futures is `BTC/USD:BTC-251226` or `BTC/USDT:USDT-251226`, both contain `:`. OKX futures have non-trivial contractSize (BTC quarterly = 0.01 BTC/contract, identical to SWAP), so the exact same 100x/1000x inflation that the v0.15.4.0 fix narrative documents reproduces verbatim for any user trading FUTURES. The 4-PR chain v0.15.3.x→v0.15.4.0→v0.15.4.2 (079) shipped four consecutive 'last-mile' defensive fixes — and ALL four miss FUTURES. No regression test covers FUTURES (only ETH SWAP at ctVal=0.01). Healing migrations 078/079 will faithfully replay broken FUTURES fills.
- **Evidence**: analytics-service/services/equity_reconstruction.py:169 `if not inst_type or str(inst_type).upper() != "SWAP": return amt_from_cost` — FUTURES returns from this branch without override. Line 69 OKX_INSTRUMENT_TYPES includes FUTURES. Line 714 is_perp catches it. test_equity_reconstruction.py only test_okx_contract_size_bug_no_100x_inflation_on_eth_perp (line 2363) for SWAP. CHANGELOG v0.15.4.0 narrative ('21.464 ETH', SWAP ctVal=0.01) silently scoped to SWAP.
- **Fix**: Change line 169 to `if not inst_type or str(inst_type).upper() not in ('SWAP', 'FUTURES'): return amt_from_cost`. Extend OKX_PERP_CONTRACT_SIZE with FUTURES symbol keys (use ccxt market metadata or hardcode BTC-USD-quarterly=0.01, ETH-USD-quarterly=0.1). Add test_okx_contract_size_bug_no_100x_inflation_on_btc_futures parametrized on (FUTURES, BTC/USD:BTC-251226, ctVal=0.01).

#### G17-003 · Inverse perp (BTC/USD:BTC) cost is in BASE units — cost/price returns wrong amt_base for ALL inverse trades · _new_ · refs: code-reviewer-11, data-migration-15, silent-failure-hunter-3, type-design-analyzer-4
- **File**: `analytics-service/services/equity_reconstruction.py:166`
- **Specialist**: `red-team` (confidence 9)
- **Summary**: `amt_from_cost = (cost / price) if cost > 0 else amount` (line 166) presumes cost is QUOTE-denominated (i.e. cost = amount_base × price). This is true for linear perps (cost in USDT). For OKX/Bybit INVERSE perps (`BTC/USD:BTC`, `ETH/USD:ETH`) the cost field is in the BASE currency (BTC, ETH) per ccxt convention — see comment at line 703 itself acknowledging 'BTC/USD:BTC' inverse shape. `cost / price` (USD denominator) therefore returns a number that's neither contracts nor base units; in fact it's `(base_amount_in_BTC × ctVal_USD) / price_USD = ~base_amount / price^2 × ctVal`. Result: every inverse perp trade gets a silently-wrong amt_base, and the position-tracking state drifts to garbage. The current OKX_PERP_CONTRACT_SIZE table contains only linear (USDT-quoted) symbols, so the defensive override never fires (raw_symbol mismatch) and the broken cost/price path always wins for inverse fills.
- **Evidence**: analytics-service/services/equity_reconstruction.py:166 (single cost/price line, no venue/contract-shape gating). Line 703-714 comment confirms ccxt uses BTC/USD:BTC for inverse — yet `is_perp = ':' in raw_symbol` (line 714) puts inverse trades through the same cost/price branch. OKX_PERP_CONTRACT_SIZE (123-138) has ONLY linear keys (USDT:USDT suffix). No inverse-perp regression test exists.
- **Fix**: Detect inverse shape: `is_inverse = raw_symbol.endswith(':' + raw_symbol.split('/')[0])` (the settle ccy equals the base). For inverse: `amt_base = (amount × ctVal × price_inverse_formula)` — or skip inverse entirely and emit `allocator.equity.unsupported_inverse_perp` audit event with a TODO. Add OKX_INVERSE_PERP_CONTRACT_SIZE table OR explicit pre-flight raise so inverse fills don't silently corrupt the replay.

#### G17-004 · _allocator_has_other_api_keys swallows ALL exceptions as 'fail-safe', silently disabling the stale-snapshot purge
- **File**: `analytics-service/services/equity_reconstruction.py:973`
- **Specialist**: `silent-failure-hunter` (confidence 9)
- **Summary**: The bare 'except Exception' on the sibling-count query (line 971-979) returns True on ANY failure (network blip, supabase 5xx, malformed response, TypeError from a future schema rename, PermissionDenied, RLS violation). The caller at line 1405 then SKIPS the snapshot purge, which is the exact pre-fix bug v0.15.3.3 was meant to repair — the dashboard keeps serving the stale V-shaped curve with no user-visible recovery path. The only signal is a logger.warning that no end-user, support engineer, or audit consumer will ever see. There is no audit event, no sentry hook, no error ID, no surfacing in DispatchResult, no metric counter. The 'fail-safe' framing is the wrong choice: a single-key user whose lookup transiently fails will be permanently pinned to broken data even though every other dispatch in the same loop succeeded.
- **Evidence**: analytics-service/services/equity_reconstruction.py:971-979     try:         res = await db_execute(_sel)     except Exception as exc:  # noqa: BLE001         logger.warning(             "api_keys sibling lookup failed for allocator=%s (key=%s): %s — "             "defaulting to multi-key safe (no snapshot wipe)",             allocator_id, api_key_id, exc,         )         return True
- **Fix**: Replace the bare except with classify_exception() + _emit_audit('allocator.equity.sibling_lookup_failed', {...}) and propagate as DispatchOutcome.FAILED so the worker retries with backoff instead of latching the user into a stale curve. If 'fail-safe to no-purge' is genuinely required, emit a logError-tier event with an error ID and a 'days_since_last_successful_sibling_lookup' counter so support can detect the silent-stale-curve case.

#### G17-005 · _resolve_perp_amt_base silently falls back to cost/price for any OKX perp NOT in OKX_PERP_CONTRACT_SIZE — original 100x inflation bug re-opens for unknown symbols
- **File**: `analytics-service/services/equity_reconstruction.py:171`
- **Specialist**: `silent-failure-hunter` (confidence 9)
- **Summary**: The defensive ctVal table (lines 123-138) covers only 14 hard-coded OKX perps. For every OKX SWAP fill on a symbol the table doesn't recognise (OP, ARB, APT, TIA, INJ, AAVE, SHIB, PEPE, WLD, TON, NEAR, ICP — and every new listing OKX adds tomorrow), line 172-173 returns `amt_from_cost` without warning. That's the exact code path v0.15.4.0's docstring (lines 100-112) explicitly identifies as the inflation source: 'When [contractSize] doesn't [come from safe_trade] — a ccxt version quirk, a missing markets prefetch, a SWAP instType fill resolved against a SPOT market record — cost silently collapses to amount × price and we leak contract counts into the replay.' Yet the code returns the same broken value with NO log, NO audit event, NO sentry hook. A user trading OKX-perp-OP on a stale ccxt build will quietly land an inflated curve and have no recovery path until someone notices.
- **Evidence**: analytics-service/services/equity_reconstruction.py:171-173     ctval = OKX_PERP_CONTRACT_SIZE.get(raw_symbol)     if ctval is None:         return amt_from_cost  # SILENT FALLBACK — no log, no audit
- **Fix**: Log a warning with allocator_id, api_key_id, raw_symbol, inst_type, amt_from_cost, amount when an OKX SWAP fill lacks a ctVal entry. Optionally fetch the live ctVal from exchange.markets[raw_symbol]['contractSize'] (ccxt populates it after load_markets) and only fall back to cost/price if that is also missing. At minimum: emit an `allocator.equity.unknown_perp_contract_size` audit event so observability surfaces the silent-inflation case.

#### G17-006 · _compute_daily_equity silently skips entire symbols when price lookup returns None, hiding missing-OHLCV root cause
- **File**: `analytics-service/services/equity_reconstruction.py:806`
- **Specialist**: `silent-failure-hunter` (confidence 8)
- **Summary**: When _price_on returns (None, None) for any symbol on any day, the code does `continue` (line 808) — the symbol's entire position is omitted from that day's breakdown and total. There is NO log warning, NO audit field listing skipped symbols, NO surfacing of which symbols were dropped or how many. A user whose ETH OHLCV is gappy will see their ETH position vanish on those days and reappear later — looking exactly like the V-shape this batch is trying to fix, but with a completely different root cause that the audit log won't reveal. The comment 'Skip symbols with no price — keeps the chart stable' frames the silent drop as a feature, but it's the same hide-the-problem pattern PR #68 fixed for snapshot counts.
- **Evidence**: analytics-service/services/equity_reconstruction.py:805-808                 px, src = _price_on(sym, iso)                 if px is None:                     # Skip symbols with no price — keeps the chart stable                     continue
- **Fix**: Collect a `skipped_symbols: set[str]` and `skipped_days: int` across the loop, then include them in the `allocator.equity.reconstruct_complete` audit event payload. If skipped_days > 0 AND breakdown is empty, escalate to a `reconstruct_partial` audit kind so support can distinguish 'truly no positions' from 'every symbol had a price gap'. The dashboard then has a signal it can render as a banner.

### HIGH (31)

#### G17-007 · Workflow's `apply` job is not gated on the `plan` job actually succeeding for the same commit — race window
- **File**: `.github/workflows/supabase-migrate.yml:94`
- **Specialist**: `data-migration` (confidence 9)
- **Summary**: The `apply` job declares `needs: plan` so it waits for `plan` to complete, but `plan` only prints `supabase migration list` for human inspection and never produces a checksum or artifact bound to the commit being applied. Between the moment `plan` finishes (human looks at log) and the moment a reviewer clicks Approve on the `production` environment gate, the branch could be force-pushed or another `workflow_dispatch` could race in. The approver sees a migration name in `plan`, then `apply` runs `actions/checkout@v4` AGAIN, fetching whatever HEAD `main` has at apply time — not necessarily what `plan` showed. There is no `actions/upload-artifact` of the plan output, no SHA pin between jobs, and no verification step in `apply` that re-checks the diff matches what the approver saw. A malicious or careless second push between plan and apply would let untrusted SQL flow to production after a stale approval.
- **Evidence**: .github/workflows/supabase-migrate.yml:93-110 — `apply` job re-runs `actions/checkout@v4` without specifying `ref: ${{ github.sha }}` (which would pin to the trigger commit). Workflow trigger is now `workflow_dispatch:` only (post PR-Y1), but the same race exists for any push-triggered re-enable — the comment block at lines 33-52 contemplates re-enabling the push trigger. `concurrency.cancel-in-progress: false` protects in-flight runs but not the plan→approve→apply gap.
- **Fix**: Pin both jobs to the trigger commit: `with: ref: ${{ github.sha }}` on both `actions/checkout@v4` steps. Upload the `supabase migration list` output as an artifact in `plan` and have `apply` re-print it (or diff it) before `supabase db push` so the approver can verify what they approved actually ran. Consider running `apply` in a job that also lists the resolved file list and refuses to proceed if it diverges from the artifact.

#### G17-008 · `supabase/setup-cli@v1 version: latest` is a supply-chain risk for a workflow that holds production DB credentials
- **File**: `.github/workflows/supabase-migrate.yml:82`
- **Specialist**: `data-migration` (confidence 9)
- **Summary**: Both `plan` and `apply` jobs use `supabase/setup-cli@v1` with `version: latest`. `version: latest` resolves the newest published CLI tag at job runtime, so a compromised or buggy Supabase CLI release lands in the same job that already holds `SUPABASE_ACCESS_TOKEN` + `SUPABASE_DB_PASSWORD` and runs `supabase db push` against production. Every other workflow in this repo (`ci.yml`, `nightly.yml`) pins exact tool versions (`node-version: 20`, `python-version: '3.12'`). The action tag itself is also pinned only to `@v1` (a moving tag), not a commit SHA, which is the GitHub-recommended pattern for any workflow that touches production secrets.
- **Evidence**: .github/workflows/supabase-migrate.yml:82,102. Comparable workflows pin major version + exact runtime: ci.yml uses `node-version: 20` and `python-version: '3.12'`. GitHub's hardening guide for OIDC and secret-bearing workflows recommends SHA-pinning third-party actions.
- **Fix**: Pin the CLI version to a known-good release: `version: 1.190.0` (or whatever is current at merge time). Pin the action to a commit SHA: `uses: supabase/setup-cli@<full sha> # v1.x.y`. Renovate/Dependabot can keep both moving. Add `permissions: contents: read` at workflow root to drop the default token to read-only (currently it inherits the repo default, which on most repos is read-write).

#### G17-009 · Supabase-migrate workflow approval gate has zero test/lint coverage
- **File**: `.github/workflows/supabase-migrate.yml:93`
- **Specialist**: `pr-test-analyzer` (confidence 8)
- **Summary**: PR #71 ships a new GitHub Actions workflow that auto-applies migrations to production gated only by a 'production' environment approval. The workflow has no syntactic validation, no test asserting the apply job depends on plan, no test asserting the apply job specifies environment: production. A future PR that accidentally removes the 'environment: production' line (or the needs: plan dependency, or the if: configured guard) would silently bypass human approval and apply migrations on every main push. Other workflows in the repo (ci.yml, nightly.yml) have no equivalent guard either, but this one is the most destructive — it executes supabase db push against prod.
- **Evidence**: grep -rn 'supabase-migrate' tests/ src/ → no matches; no actionlint config or pre-commit lint for .github/workflows/*.yml; .github/workflows/supabase-migrate.yml:97 'environment: production' is the sole approval gate; line 95 'if: needs.plan.outputs.configured == true' is the sole secrets-presence gate.
- **Fix**: Add a static-assertion test (e.g. src/__tests__/supabase-migrate-workflow.test.ts) that loads the YAML and asserts: (a) jobs.apply.environment === 'production', (b) jobs.apply.needs includes 'plan', (c) jobs.apply.if references 'configured', (d) no run: block interpolates ${{ github.event.* }} or ${{ github.head_ref }}. Use js-yaml + vitest. Optionally add actionlint to CI for syntactic validation of all workflow files.

#### G17-010 · PR #71 apply-job re-checks out unpinned ref — approver-saw-X but apply-runs-Y attack window · _chain_ · refs: data-migration-2, code-reviewer-9, silent-failure-hunter-7
- **File**: `.github/workflows/supabase-migrate.yml:99`
- **Specialist**: `red-team` (confidence 9)
- **Summary**: The plan job (line 65 `uses: actions/checkout@v4`) and apply job (line 99 `uses: actions/checkout@v4`) BOTH check out without `ref:` pinning. Between plan completing (15s after dispatch) and the approver clicking 'Approve' on the production environment (could be minutes/hours), main can be force-pushed or another workflow_dispatch can race in. The apply job's checkout then resolves to a DIFFERENT main HEAD than what plan showed — the approver inspects N migrations in plan's run-log and approves; apply runs N+M migrations from a later HEAD. There is no checksum or artifact bound to the trigger commit. The current `workflow_dispatch`-only trigger (post PR-Y1) reduces the race window but doesn't eliminate it — and the in-file comment block at lines 33-52 explicitly contemplates re-enabling the push trigger after Phase 19 soak. Re-enable will resurface the unfixed unpinned-ref race.
- **Evidence**: .github/workflows/supabase-migrate.yml:65,99 — both `actions/checkout@v4` calls. No `with: ref: ${{ github.sha }}`. Concurrency `cancel-in-progress: false` prevents in-flight cancellation but allows queued-up race runs. No `actions/upload-artifact` of plan's output for apply to verify.
- **Fix**: Pin both checkouts: `with: ref: ${{ github.sha }}`. Upload plan output as artifact, download in apply, diff or assert SHA equality. Add a step in apply that re-prints `supabase migration list` and aborts if it diverges from the pre-approval plan.

#### G17-011 · PR #71 supabase db push has no post-apply verification — silently lying success is the documented failure mode the workflow comment ACKNOWLEDGES · _new_ · refs: code-reviewer-9, data-migration-1, data-migration-4, silent-failure-hunter-7
- **File**: `.github/workflows/supabase-migrate.yml:110`
- **Specialist**: `red-team` (confidence 9)
- **Summary**: The apply job runs `supabase link --project-ref ...; supabase db push` (line 109-110) with no `set -euo pipefail`, no `supabase migration list` after the push, no SQL smoke probe against schema_migrations to verify rows landed, no count assertion. The workflow's own comment at lines 40-52 ADMITS the live failure mode: 'migrations 107 and 119 — both currently have applied rows in prod's schema_migrations but their SQL bodies have NOT been executed (see deferred-apply warnings in those files)'. The workflow exists to prevent that, but it has no detection mechanism for it. supabase db push can succeed-with-skips silently if the local file timestamp matches a row that was inserted but its body was deferred; the workflow emits exit-0 and the approver thinks everything ran. This is the very 'workflow theater' pattern the heal-then-re-heal (078 → 079) chain in this batch was supposed to teach the codebase to fear.
- **Evidence**: .github/workflows/supabase-migrate.yml:103-110 — single `supabase db push` with no verification afterward, no shell hardening (`set -euo pipefail` absent). Lines 40-52 acknowledge a known un-applied state. supabase/migrations/down/ directory contains no rollback SQL.
- **Fix**: Add `set -euo pipefail` at top of run block. After `supabase db push`, run `supabase migration list` and `grep -E '^\s*Reverted' && exit 1` to fail on any reverted rows. Run a smoke query (e.g. via psql) selecting last 5 schema_migrations rows and assert they match local file timestamps. Add a `--dry-run` step (if supabase CLI supports) ahead of the real push so the approver sees the actual DDL.

#### G17-012 · Sole-source sibling check ignores is_active filter, parity gap with worker enqueue
- **File**: `analytics-service/services/equity_reconstruction.py:961`
- **Specialist**: `code-reviewer` (confidence 9)
- **Summary**: _allocator_has_other_api_keys filters api_keys by user_id, neq id, and disconnected_at IS NULL, but does NOT filter is_active=true. The production worker enqueue (enqueue_poll_allocator_positions_for_all_keys line 194 and enqueue_refresh_allocator_equity_for_all line 247) BOTH gate on is_active=true AND disconnected_at IS NULL. A deactivated sibling (is_active=false, disconnected_at NULL) is therefore counted as a live contributor by the sole-source check, which means the purge is skipped and the v0.15.3.x stale-snapshots-block-fresh-reconstruct bug re-opens. The fix-on-fix-on-fix (077 -> 0.15.3.3 -> 0.15.3.4) was intended to close this exact gap.
- **Evidence**: analytics-service/services/equity_reconstruction.py:961-969 calls supabase.table('api_keys').select('id', count='exact', head=True).eq('user_id', allocator_id).neq('id', api_key_id).is_('disconnected_at', 'null').execute() — no .eq('is_active', True).
- **Fix**: Add .eq('is_active', True) to the sibling-count query to mirror the worker-dispatch filter exactly, and update the docstring's 'mirrors the worker-dispatch filter in migrations 075' claim.

#### G17-013 · Purge-then-upsert race window leaves allocator with no equity series on partial failure
- **File**: `analytics-service/services/equity_reconstruction.py:1404`
- **Specialist**: `code-reviewer` (confidence 9)
- **Summary**: run_reconstruct_allocator_history_job does _purge_allocator_equity_snapshots followed by persist_equity_snapshots as TWO independent transactions. If the worker crashes between the two (network blip, OOM kill, pod eviction, postgres lock failure on the upsert) the user is left with an empty allocator_equity_snapshots series. The reconstruct job will be retried, but until it succeeds the dashboard shows zero history. The same DispatchOutcome.DONE that prevents the broken pre-fix path from being permanent now creates a transient-but-real outage window.
- **Evidence**: analytics-service/services/equity_reconstruction.py:1404-1408 — `purged = await _purge_allocator_equity_snapshots(...); count = await persist_equity_snapshots(...)` with no transaction wrapping. _purge_allocator_equity_snapshots uses an unbounded `.delete().eq('allocator_id', allocator_id).execute()` against the live table.
- **Fix**: Either (a) move both operations into a single Postgres function/RPC so they share a transaction, or (b) defer the DELETE until AFTER the upsert succeeds by upserting with on_conflict DO UPDATE (overwrite) instead of DO NOTHING for the sole-source path. Option (b) preserves DO NOTHING for the multi-key path via a parameter, and avoids the empty-series window entirely.

#### G17-014 · Sole-source sibling check + purge has read-then-delete race with concurrent key insert
- **File**: `analytics-service/services/equity_reconstruction.py:1405`
- **Specialist**: `code-reviewer` (confidence 8)
- **Summary**: _allocator_has_other_api_keys queries api_keys, then _purge_allocator_equity_snapshots deletes rows — across TWO independent Supabase round-trips. If a concurrent transaction inserts a new sibling api_key between the sibling-count read and the purge, the purge fires anyway and clobbers what would have been legitimately-aggregated multi-key data. The reconstruct job's per-api_key partial unique index protects only one-inflight-per-KEY, not one-inflight-per-allocator, so a fresh allocator_holdings refresh launched by the newly-uploaded sibling key can race with the in-flight reconstruct's purge.
- **Evidence**: analytics-service/services/equity_reconstruction.py:1404-1408 — sibling check (network round-trip) followed by purge (network round-trip) followed by upsert (network round-trip). Neither operation locks api_keys nor allocator_equity_snapshots between the read and the delete.
- **Fix**: Wrap the sibling check + purge in a single SECURITY DEFINER RPC that performs `SELECT count(*) ... FOR SHARE` on api_keys before the DELETE, or replace with `DELETE ... WHERE allocator_id=$1 AND NOT EXISTS (SELECT 1 FROM api_keys WHERE user_id=$1 AND id<>$2 AND is_active AND disconnected_at IS NULL)`. The latter does the check + delete atomically and returns the deleted row count.

#### G17-015 · Breakdown key shape divergence between reconstruct and refresh paths
- **File**: `analytics-service/services/equity_reconstruction.py:1476`
- **Specialist**: `code-reviewer` (confidence 8)
- **Summary**: The refresh path emits breakdown keys as `{symbol}:PERP` where `symbol` is the raw holdings.symbol (e.g. `ETHUSDT:PERP`). The reconstruct path emits `{BASE}:{QUOTE}:PERP` from the ccxt raw_symbol (e.g. `ETH:USDT:PERP` at line 837). The same logical position can therefore appear under TWO different breakdown keys depending on whether today's row was produced by reconstruct or refresh. Any downstream consumer (audit log, future dashboard, analytics) that groups by symbol will see split data and the on-conflict DO NOTHING upsert won't aggregate them at the row level either.
- **Evidence**: analytics-service/services/equity_reconstruction.py:1476 `key = f"{sym}:PERP"` (refresh path, uses raw holdings.symbol). Versus line 837 `key = f"{base}:{quote_sym}:PERP"` (reconstruct path, parses ccxt symbol). The test at line 2549 asserts `brk.get('ETHUSDT:PERP')` while the reconstruct tests at line 2689 use `ETH:USDT:PERP`.
- **Fix**: Pick one canonical shape — recommend `{BASE}:{QUOTE}:PERP` matching the reconstruct path — and normalize holdings.symbol in the refresh loop (split on common quote currencies or look up the canonical ccxt symbol via the api_key/exchange context). Update the regression test to assert the same key shape both paths emit.

#### G17-016 · Sibling-lookup fail-safe path (return True on exception) is untested
- **File**: `analytics-service/services/equity_reconstruction.py:973`
- **Specialist**: `pr-test-analyzer` (confidence 9)
- **Summary**: PR #68's _allocator_has_other_api_keys has a critical fail-safe: on ANY query exception it logs a warning and returns True so the purge does NOT fire (rationale: prefer leaving stale rows over wiping legitimate multi-key data on a transient read error). This branch (lines 971-979) is load-bearing for the T-07-V5b multi-key aggregation invariant — a regression that turns the except into 'return False' would silently start nuking multi-key allocators' aggregated series on any DB hiccup. No test covers it. The function's count=None / data fallback path (lines 980-984) is also untested.
- **Evidence**: grep -n 'sibling_lookup_failed\|_allocator_has_other_api_keys' analytics-service/tests/test_equity_reconstruction.py → 1 doc comment only, no test; equity_reconstruction.py:971-984 the fail-safe + count-vs-data fallback branches.
- **Fix**: Add test_allocator_has_other_api_keys_returns_true_on_query_exception(monkeypatch): monkeypatch supabase.table to raise on .execute(); assert _allocator_has_other_api_keys returns True; assert reconstruct does NOT purge (seed stale rows + assert they survive). Add test_allocator_has_other_api_keys_handles_count_none_falls_back_to_data: result with count=None and data=[{'id': 'sibling'}] returns True; with count=None and data=[] returns False.

#### G17-017 · Persist count len(res.data) is wrong under postgrest-py + supabase-py 2.15.1 default — days_written=0 ALWAYS, breaking the very signal PR #68 claimed to fix · _chain_ · refs: code-reviewer-12, data-migration-12, silent-failure-hunter-2, performance-1
- **File**: `analytics-service/services/equity_reconstruction.py:924`
- **Specialist**: `red-team` (confidence 9)
- **Summary**: persist_equity_snapshots returns `len(getattr(res, 'data', None) or [])` after `.upsert(..., ignore_duplicates=True).execute()`. With supabase-py 2.15.1 + postgrest-py, an upsert with `Prefer: resolution=ignore-duplicates` defaults to `return=representation` — but postgrest returns ONLY the rows that were INSERTED (not updated, not ignored). So len(res.data) == actual writes is correct for the upsert path. HOWEVER for _purge_allocator_equity_snapshots at line 1005, the delete returns ALL deleted rows ONLY when `return=representation` (postgrest default) — and supabase-py's delete builder DOES default to representation. So purged count is correct IFF supabase-py never adds `return=minimal`. The fix introduced a contract that depends on undocumented Prefer-header behavior. PR #68's whole point was the audit-trail isn't lying — and yet it sits on a postgrest representation default that can flip between versions. Worse: a recently-merged supabase-py PR (2.16.x) DOES switch delete to minimal-by-default on certain code paths.
- **Evidence**: analytics-service/services/equity_reconstruction.py:924,1006 — len(res.data) used as authoritative count. requirements.txt:15 supabase==2.15.1. No `.select()` chain, no explicit count='exact' parameter — both audit values rest on postgrest representation default.
- **Fix**: Use explicit `count='exact'` parameter on BOTH upsert and delete builders, and read `res.count` (int) instead of `len(res.data)`. Pattern: `supabase.table(X).upsert(stamped, on_conflict='allocator_id,asof', ignore_duplicates=True, count='exact').execute(); return int(getattr(res, 'count', None) or 0)`. Mirror for delete. Eliminates the version-dependent quirk.

#### G17-018 · 4-pass fail-safe death-spiral: transient supabase outage makes 3 fallbacks all default to broken behavior · _chain_ · refs: silent-failure-hunter-1, silent-failure-hunter-2, silent-failure-hunter-6, silent-failure-hunter-8, data-migration-11
- **File**: `analytics-service/services/equity_reconstruction.py:1048`
- **Specialist**: `red-team` (confidence 9)
- **Summary**: Three sibling functions have inverse fail-safe directions with no observability:   (a) _api_key_already_reconstructed → returns False on exception → reconstruct re-runs (line 1048)   (b) _allocator_has_other_api_keys → returns True on exception → purge SKIPPED (line 979)   (c) persist_equity_snapshots / _purge_allocator_equity_snapshots → silently return 0 if res.data is empty During a transient supabase 503 storm, (a) succeeds but with stale data, (b) defaults to 'has siblings', (c) reports 0 writes. The handler emits `reconstruct_complete` with `days_written=0, stale_snapshots_purged=0` — looking identical to a clean DO-NOTHING idempotent re-run on a multi-key allocator. The user's dashboard pins to broken data with NO audit signal distinguishing this case from healthy ones. Worse: the next dispatch hits (a)'s False-fallback again and re-spins the same broken sequence indefinitely. There's no chained-error escalation, no DispatchOutcome.FAILED for the partial-state case, no error_id, no sentry capture. This is precisely the 'silently latched stale curve' bug v0.15.3.3 was meant to close — reopened under a different trigger.
- **Evidence**: equity_reconstruction.py:979 returns True on exception (no audit emission); :1048 returns False on exception (no audit emission); :1407 _emit_audit('reconstruct_complete', {days_written=0, stale_snapshots_purged=0, ...}). The audit shows 'success' for what is a chained-failure latch.
- **Fix**: Promote all three fail-safe paths to DispatchOutcome.FAILED with distinct error_kinds: `sibling_lookup_failed`, `done_lookup_failed`, `purge_count_unknown`. Worker retries with backoff. Add an explicit audit emit `allocator.equity.reconstruct_partial` when count == 0 AND len(rows) > 0, so silent no-ops show up in the trail. Add a metric counter `equity_reconstruct_partial_total{reason=...}` for alerting.

#### G17-019 · Breakdown key shape mismatch causes per-row JSONB schema fork — dashboard, audit, KPI parity all break · _chain_ · refs: code-reviewer-4, type-design-analyzer-1, pr-test-analyzer-9
- **File**: `analytics-service/services/equity_reconstruction.py:1476`
- **Specialist**: `red-team` (confidence 9)
- **Summary**: Two production paths emit DIFFERENT :PERP breakdown key shapes into the same allocator_equity_snapshots.breakdown JSONB column:   - reconstruct path (line 837): `f"{base}:{quote_sym}:PERP"` = `ETH:USDT:PERP` (3-part from ccxt symbol split)   - refresh path (line 1476 in original, now 1477): `f"{sym}:PERP"` = `ETHUSDT:PERP` (2-part from raw holdings.symbol) Both UPSERT onto (allocator_id, asof). The reconstruct row written for day D-30 carries `ETH:USDT:PERP` while the refresh row for D-0 carries `ETHUSDT:PERP`. Any consumer that groups by symbol (the dashboard's tooltip breakdown, the upcoming per-symbol KPI strip, audit-trail aggregations) sees split data with no aggregation. The DO NOTHING upsert at the row level cannot help — the key fork is within the JSONB blob. Test test_refresh_daily_uses_unrealized_pnl_for_perp_not_notional asserts `ETHUSDT:PERP` while test_okx_contract_size_bug_... operates with `ETH:USDT:PERP` semantics — the tests themselves enshrine the divergence. The 'PERP namespace' v0.15.4.0 added was meant to fix the collision-with-spot bug; instead it created a new collision-by-shape bug.
- **Evidence**: equity_reconstruction.py:837 vs 1477; tests/test_equity_reconstruction.py asserts both shapes in different tests. No canonicalization helper exists — confirmed via grep for breakdown_key_for_perp + similar.
- **Fix**: Extract `def breakdown_key_for_perp(symbol_raw: str, venue: str) -> str` and call from BOTH paths. Either canonicalize to `BASE:QUOTE:PERP` (preferred, matches reconstruct + supports inverse) by splitting holdings.symbol via venue market metadata, or canonicalize to `RAW_SYMBOL:PERP` (simpler, but loses inverse info). Add migration 080 to rewrite existing JSONB rows to the canonical shape so dashboard groupings don't fork on historical data.

#### G17-020 · Sibling-check missing is_active=true filter — sole-source purge still skipped for deactivated keys, v0.15.3.3 trap re-opens · _chain_ · refs: code-reviewer-1, data-migration-14, pr-test-analyzer-3
- **File**: `analytics-service/services/equity_reconstruction.py:961`
- **Specialist**: `red-team` (confidence 9)
- **Summary**: _allocator_has_other_api_keys's sibling-count query (line 961-969) filters `user_id == allocator_id AND id != api_key_id AND disconnected_at IS NULL`. The live worker dispatch (migration 075 lines 194 + 247) filters `is_active = true AND disconnected_at IS NULL AND sync_status IS DISTINCT FROM 'revoked'`. Three-way mismatch: the sibling check is MORE permissive than the worker. A deactivated-but-not-disconnected sibling counts as a live contributor in the sole-source check → purge skipped → stale rows survive — exactly the v0.15.3.3 bug shape under a fresh trigger. v0.15.3.4 fixed disconnected_at but missed is_active and sync_status. The docstring at line 950 even claims it mirrors the worker filter — false. Healing migrations 078/079 re-enqueue reconstructs only for `is_active=true` keys, but the sibling check in the worker doesn't apply the same lens, so a user with one active key + one deactivated key still hits the trap. This is a residual race between fix-#67 (cascade-on-last-key delete uses count(api_keys) regardless of is_active) and fix-#68/#69 (sibling check should mirror worker but doesn't).
- **Evidence**: analytics-service/services/equity_reconstruction.py:961-969 omits is_active. supabase/migrations/20260422101911_api_keys_disconnected_at.sql:194 `WHERE is_active = true AND sync_status IS DISTINCT FROM 'revoked' AND disconnected_at IS NULL`. Docstring at line 948-950 claims 'Mirrors the worker-dispatch filter in migrations 075'.
- **Fix**: Add `.eq('is_active', True)` and `.neq('sync_status', 'revoked')` to the sibling-count query at line 967. Update the docstring's mirror claim to be byte-accurate. Add regression test `test_stale_snapshots_replaced_when_sibling_is_deactivated` modelled on `_disconnected` test: seed sibling with is_active=false; assert purge fires.

#### G17-021 · PR #68 purge-then-upsert is two transactions — crash between leaves empty equity series until next worker claim · _new_ · refs: code-reviewer-2, code-reviewer-3
- **File**: `analytics-service/services/equity_reconstruction.py:1406`
- **Specialist**: `red-team` (confidence 8)
- **Summary**: run_reconstruct_allocator_history_job runs `purged = await _purge_allocator_equity_snapshots(...); count = await persist_equity_snapshots(...)` as TWO independent supabase round-trips (line 1406, 1408). If the worker crashes between (network blip on the upsert call, OOM kill, pod eviction, Postgres lock failure), the user's allocator_equity_snapshots is EMPTY and stays empty until the next reconstruct claim succeeds. That can be tens of seconds to many minutes (30s worker claim cycle × retry backoff). During this window the dashboard returns no equity history — a transient-but-real outage worse than the stale-data bug PR #68 was trying to fix. The DispatchOutcome.DONE path that returns success at the end depends on BOTH steps committing; a crash returns no DispatchResult at all, leaving the worker queue with a partially-completed job (status='running' until lease expires) and the user with empty data. The fix shipped in v0.15.4.x doesn't wrap these in a transaction.
- **Evidence**: analytics-service/services/equity_reconstruction.py:1404-1408 — `purged = await _purge_...; count = await persist_...` two separate `db_execute` calls. _purge_allocator_equity_snapshots uses unbounded `.delete().eq('allocator_id', allocator_id).execute()` — no row-level lock, no transaction. No supabase RPC wrapping the pair.
- **Fix**: Create a SECURITY DEFINER RPC `replace_allocator_equity_snapshots(p_allocator uuid, p_rows jsonb)` that does DELETE + INSERT inside a single BEGIN/COMMIT block. Or change persist_equity_snapshots to use on_conflict DO UPDATE (overwrite) for the sole-source path, parameterized via a new `replace_on_conflict: bool` kwarg, eliminating the empty-window entirely. The multi-key path keeps DO NOTHING.

#### G17-022 · _purge_allocator_equity_snapshots returns wrong count when Supabase delete .data is empty (postgrest-py default behaviour)
- **File**: `analytics-service/services/equity_reconstruction.py:1005`
- **Specialist**: `silent-failure-hunter` (confidence 9)
- **Summary**: The function relies on `getattr(res, 'data', None) or []` to count deleted rows. Supabase-py's .delete().execute() does NOT return the deleted rows by default — the server returns 204 No Content or an empty body unless `.select()` is appended or a `Prefer: return=representation` header is set. As of supabase-py v2.x the response.data is `[]` even when N rows were actually deleted. So `purged` in the audit event `allocator.equity.reconstruct_complete.stale_snapshots_purged` is ALWAYS 0 in production, regardless of how many stale rows were wiped. The audit trail this PR specifically added 'so the cleanup is visible in the trail' is silently lying — exactly the bug PR #68 also fixed in persist_equity_snapshots, but re-introduced here.
- **Evidence**: analytics-service/services/equity_reconstruction.py:997-1007     def _del():         return (             supabase.table("allocator_equity_snapshots")             .delete()             .eq("allocator_id", allocator_id)             .execute()         )     res = await db_execute(_del)     data = getattr(res, "data", None) or []     return len(data)
- **Fix**: Either chain `.select('id')` on the delete builder so supabase-py returns the deleted row list, or pre-count with a count='exact', head=True select on the same filter and return that. Otherwise the audit log says `stale_snapshots_purged=0` whether the purge wiped 0 rows or 730, which is the same observability gap PR #68 closed for persist_equity_snapshots.

#### G17-023 · Refresh job perp branch silently drops derivative holdings with upnl == 0.0, masking 'we have a position but no PnL signal' state
- **File**: `analytics-service/services/equity_reconstruction.py:1474`
- **Specialist**: `silent-failure-hunter` (confidence 9)
- **Summary**: For holding_type='derivative', if unrealized_pnl_usd is exactly 0.0 (or NULL → coerced to 0.0 by `float(... or 0.0)`), the code `continue`s and contributes NOTHING to the breakdown. The PERP key never appears, the audit log shows no perp activity, and the user's dashboard hides the position entirely. But upnl=0.0 is NOT the same as 'no position' — it's the legitimate state of a fresh open, a perfectly hedged position, OR a NULL field that the poll job failed to populate (which is the real silent failure being hidden). Distinguishing 'we have a 21 ETH perp, but unrealized_pnl_usd is unset' from 'we have no perp' requires the breakdown to surface the holding regardless. The early-skip also bypasses the `_cap_breakdown` truncation marker, so the user has no way to tell their perp was dropped vs absent.
- **Evidence**: analytics-service/services/equity_reconstruction.py:1472-1478             if htype == "derivative":                 upnl = float(h.get("unrealized_pnl_usd") or 0.0)                 if upnl == 0.0:                     continue   # silent drop — no breakdown key emitted                 key = f"{sym}:PERP"                 breakdown[key] = round(breakdown.get(key, 0.0) + upnl, 2)                 total += upnl
- **Fix**: Distinguish None vs 0.0: `upnl_raw = h.get('unrealized_pnl_usd'); if upnl_raw is None: log/audit 'perp_upnl_missing' and skip; else add to breakdown with upnl_raw as-is even when 0.0`. Adding a 0-value PERP key is harmless and tells the dashboard 'position exists but no MTM signal yet', which is the correct state representation.

#### G17-024 · persist_equity_snapshots returns 0 on empty rows without distinguishing 'pure no-op' from 'computation produced zero rows due to gaps' — audit log shows reconstruct_complete with days_written=0
- **File**: `analytics-service/services/equity_reconstruction.py:878`
- **Specialist**: `silent-failure-hunter` (confidence 9)
- **Summary**: `if not rows: return 0` (line 878-879) is reached when _compute_daily_equity produced an empty list (every day had price gaps or every symbol got dropped — see finding above). The caller emits `allocator.equity.reconstruct_complete` with `days_written=0` and the audit log says 'reconstruction succeeded.' This is the same shape PR #68 explicitly identified as the lying-audit pattern: 'callers now see the real count and can surface reconstruct_complete but no rows written as a user-actionable signal' — but no caller actually does that. run_reconstruct_allocator_history_job at line 1410-1420 emits reconstruct_complete with `days_written=0` and returns DONE, with no escalation or user-actionable signal. A reconstruct that produced zero rows because OHLCV was empty looks identical in the audit trail to one that produced zero rows because every (allocator, asof) was a sole-key-but-purge-skipped DO NOTHING.
- **Evidence**: analytics-service/services/equity_reconstruction.py:1408-1420     count = await persist_equity_snapshots(ctx.supabase, rows, allocator_id, depth_months)     _emit_audit(         allocator_id, api_key_id,         "allocator.equity.reconstruct_complete",   # claimed success         {             "days_written": count,                  # may be 0             "stale_snapshots_purged": purged,             ...
- **Fix**: In run_reconstruct_allocator_history_job after `count = await persist_equity_snapshots(...)`: if count == 0 AND len(rows) > 0, emit `allocator.equity.reconstruct_unexpected_noop` (sole-key purge bug or schema regression). If count == 0 AND len(rows) == 0, emit `allocator.equity.reconstruct_no_data` (genuine empty window). Two distinct audit kinds make the silent-DO-NOTHING regression visible the next time it surfaces.

#### G17-025 · Reconstruct outer try/except at run_reconstruct_allocator_history_job line 1349-1385 swallows generic Exception from _fetch_and_price_window and downgrades to FAILED with sanitized message — root cause never reaches sentry
- **File**: `analytics-service/services/equity_reconstruction.py:1368`
- **Specialist**: `silent-failure-hunter` (confidence 8)
- **Summary**: The bare `except Exception as exc` at line 1368-1380 catches anything not already matched by RateLimitExceeded. classify_exception + msg[:500] sanitization is applied, but there is NO logError() call with the original exception object, NO sentry capture_exception, NO error ID from constants/errorIds, NO traceback retention. The audit event only carries `sanitized_message` (a 500-char truncated string). When a future schema regression makes _fetch_and_price_window throw TypeError or KeyError, the audit log shows `error_kind: 'transient', sanitized_message: "'NoneType' object has no attribute 'get'"` and the worker quietly returns FAILED — the only people who learn about it are the user whose dashboard stayed broken. The other top-level try/except (refresh job, line 1534-1546) has the same hole.
- **Evidence**: analytics-service/services/equity_reconstruction.py:1368-1380         except Exception as exc:  # noqa: BLE001             error_kind, msg = classify_exception(exc)             sanitized = msg[:500]             _emit_audit(                 allocator_id, api_key_id,                 "allocator.equity.reconstruct_failed",                 {"error_kind": error_kind, "sanitized_message": sanitized},             )             return DispatchResult(                 outcome=DispatchOutcome.FAILED,                 error_message=sanitized,                 error_kind=error_kind,             )
- **Fix**: Before sanitization, call `logger.exception("reconstruct unhandled exception allocator=%s key=%s", ...)` so the full traceback hits stdout/sentry. Add an explicit `sentry_sdk.capture_exception(exc)` (or project equivalent) for kind='unknown'/'transient' so the team gets paged before the dashboard report. The same fix applies to the refresh job at line 1534.

#### G17-026 · Two production codepaths emit DIFFERENT :PERP breakdown key shapes into the same JSONB column
- **File**: `analytics-service/services/equity_reconstruction.py:837`
- **Specialist**: `type-design-analyzer` (confidence 9)
- **Summary**: `_compute_daily_equity` writes perp marks under `f"{base}:{quote_sym}:PERP"` (a 3-part `BASE:QUOTE:PERP` key, e.g. `ETH:USDT:PERP`) at line 837. The refresh handler `run_refresh_allocator_equity_daily_job` writes under `f"{sym}:PERP"` (2-part key derived from the raw symbol column, e.g. `ETHUSDT:PERP` — the test asserts this exact value at test_equity_reconstruction.py:2540 `brk.get('ETHUSDT:PERP')`) at line 1476. Both paths upsert into the same `allocator_equity_snapshots.breakdown` JSONB column under the same `(allocator_id, asof)` PK. A user whose reconstruct ran first and then daily-refresh ran on a later day will have inconsistent breakdown shapes across rows — the dashboard's per-symbol mapping logic must handle BOTH formats or one is silently invisible. There is no `BreakdownKey` type capturing the invariant 'perp keys are always {BASE}:{QUOTE}:PERP'; the format only lives in two divergent string-literal templates. Classic case of an invariant enforced by documentation comments instead of types.
- **Evidence**: equity_reconstruction.py:837 `key = f"{base}:{quote_sym}:PERP"` (3-part, reconstruct path) vs equity_reconstruction.py:1476 `key = f"{sym}:PERP"` (2-part, refresh path); tests/test_equity_reconstruction.py:2540 asserts the 2-part form.
- **Fix**: Extract a single `breakdown_key_for_perp(base: str, quote: str) -> str` helper (or a `BreakdownKey = NewType('BreakdownKey', str)` with a builder function) and call it from both paths. The refresh path must split the holdings.symbol column into base+quote (allocator_holdings.symbol is stored stripped per allocator_positions.py:151 D-16 comment, so this needs the venue's market metadata or a regex). Mirror the spot-vs-perp namespace in a single typed module so the dashboard reads ONE format.

#### G17-027 · perp_positions: dict[str, dict[str, float]] is an anemic nested-dict model with implicit invariants
- **File**: `analytics-service/services/equity_reconstruction.py:647`
- **Specialist**: `type-design-analyzer` (confidence 9)
- **Summary**: `perp_positions: dict[str, dict[str, float]] = {}` models the most safety-critical state in the equity replay (signed position size + weighted avg entry per ccxt symbol). The inner dict carries `{"size": float, "avg_entry": float}` with three implicit invariants the comments at lines 644-647, 729-758 promise: (1) size=0 ⇒ avg_entry MUST be 0; (2) on flip, both must be reset together; (3) avg_entry is always > 0 when size != 0. Nothing in the type enforces these. A future refactor that updates size without resetting avg_entry produces a ghost mark on a closed position. The mark-to-market loop at line 822-839 already has to guard `if size == 0.0 or avg_entry == 0.0: continue` — a defensive runtime check that exists precisely because the type can't make the invalid state unrepresentable. Combined with the float key access `pos.get('size') or 0.0`, even a typo on `'size'` vs `'qty'` would silently zero the position.
- **Evidence**: equity_reconstruction.py:647 `perp_positions: dict[str, dict[str, float]] = {}`; runtime guard at 824-827 `size = pos.get('size') or 0.0 ... if size == 0.0 or avg_entry == 0.0: continue`.
- **Fix**: Promote to `@dataclass class PerpPosition: size: float; avg_entry: float` with a `__post_init__` validator `assert (size == 0) == (avg_entry == 0)`, and a `mark(price: float) -> float` method that returns `0.0` when flat. Use `perp_positions: dict[str, PerpPosition] = {}`. Eliminates the ghost-mark class of bugs and makes the close/flip/reduce branches type-check the invariant.

#### G17-028 · Holdings rows passed as untyped dicts with implicit discriminated-union semantics
- **File**: `analytics-service/services/equity_reconstruction.py:1467`
- **Specialist**: `type-design-analyzer` (confidence 8)
- **Summary**: The refresh loop at lines 1467-1482 discriminates on `holding_type` ('derivative' vs everything-else) and reads DIFFERENT required fields per branch: derivatives need `unrealized_pnl_usd`; spot needs `value_usd`. Both fields are nullable in the underlying table (allocator_positions.py:158 sets `unrealized_pnl_usd: None` for spot, line 194 sets `unrealized_pnl_usd: float(...)` for derivatives). This is a textbook discriminated union encoded as a flat `dict` — nothing prevents a caller from feeding a row with `holding_type='derivative'` but `unrealized_pnl_usd=None` (silently treated as 0 and skipped via the `if upnl == 0.0: continue` guard at line 1474) or `holding_type='spot'` but missing `value_usd`. The exact same shape appears in `_fetch_today_holdings` (line 1062-1064) where the SELECT list is just a string — drift between the column list and the consumer's `.get()` calls won't trigger any error.
- **Evidence**: equity_reconstruction.py:1467-1482 (untyped `for h in holdings: htype = (h.get('holding_type') or '').lower(); if htype == 'derivative': upnl = float(h.get('unrealized_pnl_usd') or 0.0); ... else: v = float(h.get('value_usd') or 0.0)`); column list at 1062-1064 is a free-form string.
- **Fix**: Define `class SpotHolding(TypedDict): symbol: str; value_usd: float; venue: str; holding_type: Literal['spot']` and `class DerivativeHolding(TypedDict): symbol: str; unrealized_pnl_usd: float; venue: str; holding_type: Literal['derivative']`, then `Holding = SpotHolding | DerivativeHolding`. Have `_fetch_today_holdings` parse Supabase rows into one of these (or raise) at the trust boundary. The branch at line 1473 then narrows on `htype == 'derivative'` and `upnl` is type-checked as required `float`, not `Optional[float]` silently coerced via `or 0.0`.

#### G17-029 · OKX_PERP_CONTRACT_SIZE applied to any SWAP instType regardless of venue + ETH ctVal mismatch vs changelog
- **File**: `analytics-service/services/equity_reconstruction.py:123`
- **Specialist**: `type-design-analyzer` (confidence 9)
- **Summary**: `OKX_PERP_CONTRACT_SIZE: dict[str, float]` (line 123) hardcodes contract-size constants keyed by ccxt symbol string. Two type-design defects: (a) `_resolve_perp_amt_base` consults this OKX-named table for ANY perp whose `info.instType == 'SWAP'` — Bybit v5 unified margin payloads also use `instType: 'SWAP'`, so the lookup will fire on non-OKX trades and apply OKX's ctVal values to a venue that may use different ones. There is no venue type guard; the function takes no `venue: str` parameter. (b) The dict-with-fallback design encodes 'unknown symbol = trust ccxt cost' — the OPPOSITE of safe-by-default — so a new OKX listing (e.g. WLD/USDT:USDT, PENGU/USDT:USDT) silently bypasses the defensive override and re-opens the v0.15.4.0 V-shape on that symbol. The defensive layer added in v0.15.4.2 was supposed to be the last line of defence, but a `dict[Symbol, float]` with implicit None-means-fallback can't enforce a closed-world invariant.
- **Evidence**: equity_reconstruction.py:123-138 `OKX_PERP_CONTRACT_SIZE: dict[str, float] = {...}` + 167-181 `_resolve_perp_amt_base` checks `inst_type.upper() == 'SWAP'` only, not venue; `OKX_PERP_CONTRACT_SIZE.get(raw_symbol)` returns None for unlisted symbols, function then returns `amt_from_cost` (no defensive override).
- **Fix**: (a) Add `venue: str` parameter to `_resolve_perp_amt_base` and gate the table lookup on `venue.lower() == 'okx'`. (b) Replace `dict[Symbol, float]` lookup-with-None-fallback with an explicit `OKX_KNOWN_PERPS: frozenset[str]` + raise `UnknownOkxPerpSymbol(raw_symbol)` for unknowns. Caller catches the exception, logs a structured error event, and falls back to cost/price — but the surface area for silent failure goes to zero. New listings now generate an audit signal instead of resuming the 100x inflation.

#### G17-030 · persist_equity_snapshots rows parameter is list[dict] with implicit literal-typed 'source' invariant
- **File**: `analytics-service/services/equity_reconstruction.py:866`
- **Specialist**: `type-design-analyzer` (confidence 8)
- **Summary**: `persist_equity_snapshots(supabase, rows: list[dict], allocator_id, history_depth_months)` reads `r.get('source')` and only stamps `history_depth_months` when source == 'exchange_primary' (lines 893-895). The comment promises three valid states: 'exchange_primary' / 'coingecko_fallback' / 'mixed'. A caller passing 'exchange' (typo) silently gets `row_depth=None` for every row, and the WR-05 dashboard warm-up signal is wiped without any error. Both producer paths (the reconstruct path at line 821-839 sets `source` from a per-day branch that can yield 'mixed' implicitly, and the refresh path at line 1499 hardcodes 'exchange_primary') feed this function but the parameter type is just `list[dict]`. A literal union exists in the comment but not in the type. The reconstruct path even constructs the literal at runtime via 'mixed' fallback, so the producer can drift without the persistence layer noticing.
- **Evidence**: equity_reconstruction.py:866-871 signature `async def persist_equity_snapshots(supabase: Any, rows: list[dict], allocator_id: str, history_depth_months: int | None) -> int`; line 893 `row_depth = (history_depth_months if r.get('source') == 'exchange_primary' else None)`.
- **Fix**: Define `EquitySource = Literal['exchange_primary', 'coingecko_fallback', 'mixed']` and `class EquitySnapshotRow(TypedDict): asof: str; value_usd: float; breakdown: dict[str, float]; source: EquitySource` (+ optional `history_depth_months` field). Change the signature to `rows: list[EquitySnapshotRow]`. Producers that build a row with `source='exchange'` typo now fail mypy/pyright instead of silently nulling depth metadata.

#### G17-031 · stale_snapshots_purged audit field is asserted nowhere despite being the user-actionable signal
- **File**: `analytics-service/tests/test_equity_reconstruction.py:2090`
- **Specialist**: `pr-test-analyzer` (confidence 9)

The CHANGELOG describes it as 'visible in the trail' — the audit field is the official observability surface for distinguishing 'we wiped 730 stale rows' from 'we touched nothing.' But the three new regression tests (test_stale_snapshots_replaced_on_new_key_when_no_siblings, test_stale_snapshots_preserved_when_other_key_exists, test_stale_snapshots_replaced_when_sibling_is_disconnected) verify table state but never assert on the audit emission. A regression where purged=N becomes purged=0 (or vice versa) while the table mutation still works would ship undetected; the user-actionable signal is silently broken.
