In test_stale_snapshots_preserved_when_other_key_exists: assert stale_snapshots_purged=0 — sibling exists, purge must NOT fire. In test_stale_snapshots_replaced_when_sibling_is_disconnected: assert stale_snapshots_purged=10. This is the only place that proves the audit-trail observability isn't a no-op.

#### G17-032 · Migration 077 last-key snapshot cascade has zero test coverage
- **File**: `src/__tests__/delete-allocator-api-key-rpc.test.ts:389`
- **Specialist**: `pr-test-analyzer` (confidence 9)
- **Summary**: PR #67 ships migration 077 — delete_allocator_api_key now also cascades to allocator_equity_snapshots when p_cascade_holdings=true AND the user has zero remaining api_keys. The existing live-DB RPC test (src/__tests__/delete-allocator-api-key-rpc.test.ts) was authored for migration 069 and asserts holdings cascade only — it never seeds allocator_equity_snapshots rows, never asserts on their post-RPC state, and has no multi-key vs last-key branch coverage. The CHANGELOG explicitly documents the bug class this prevents (delete + reconnect produces empty dashboard forever because UPSERT DO NOTHING collides with stale rows). If migration 077's last-key gate regresses, no test catches it; the bug returns silently for any user doing 'delete and start over'.
- **Evidence**: grep -n 'allocator_equity_snapshots' src/__tests__/delete-allocator-api-key-rpc.test.ts → no matches; grep -n 'snapshot' src/__tests__/delete-allocator-api-key-rpc.test.ts → no matches; supabase/migrations/077_delete_api_key_cascade_equity.sql line 138-150 (cascade branch).
- **Fix**: Add live-DB tests to delete-allocator-api-key-rpc.test.ts: (a) cascade=true + sole key + seeded snapshots → snapshots deleted, asserts allocator_equity_snapshots count=0 for that allocator. (b) cascade=true + multi-key (this is N of N+1) + seeded snapshots → snapshots SURVIVE (count unchanged). (c) cascade=false + sole key + seeded snapshots → snapshots SURVIVE (only hard-delete should wipe). Mirror existing test pattern (createAuthedClient, seed via admin, RPC via authed client, assert via admin client).

#### G17-033 · Migration 078 healing migration is structurally complex and untested
- **File**: `supabase/migrations/078_equity_contract_size_healing.sql:1497`
- **Specialist**: `pr-test-analyzer` (confidence 8)
- **Summary**: Migration 078 performs three destructive steps in one transaction: (1) DELETE all allocator_equity_snapshots, (2) DELETE compute_jobs WHERE kind='reconstruct_allocator_history' AND status='done', (3) INSERT a fresh reconstruct job per connected+active api_key. Critical correctness invariants are: (i) STEP 2 must NOT delete pending/running jobs (would corrupt the in-flight worker queue), (ii) STEP 3 must filter is_active=true AND disconnected_at IS NULL (or it'll requeue dead keys causing classification storms), (iii) the NOT EXISTS guard must hit when a race-enqueued pending job exists. None of these are tested. The diff has comments asserting they're correct but no pytest cassette or live-DB integration test exercising the migration body.
- **Evidence**: grep -rn 'migration.*078\|equity_contract_size_healing' analytics-service/tests/ src/__tests__/ → no matches; supabase/migrations/078_equity_contract_size_healing.sql:1499-1501 the DELETE compute_jobs WHERE status='done', :1513-1528 the conditional INSERT with NOT EXISTS guard.
- **Fix**: Add an integration test under analytics-service/tests/migrations/ (or src/__tests__/migrations/) that: seeds 2 done + 1 pending + 1 running compute_jobs rows of kind reconstruct_allocator_history, seeds an active+connected api_key + a disconnected api_key + an inactive api_key, applies migration 078 against a test DB, asserts: only done rows deleted (pending+running survive), only the connected+active key has a new pending compute_jobs row, snapshots are gone.

#### G17-034 · Cross-fix interaction: PR #67's last-key cascade can wipe a multi-key user's snapshots via concurrent delete+insert race · _chain_ · refs: code-reviewer-3, data-migration-8, silent-failure-hunter-10, pr-test-analyzer-11
- **File**: `supabase/migrations/20260422182451_delete_api_key_cascade_equity.sql:88`
- **Specialist**: `red-team` (confidence 9)
- **Summary**: delete_allocator_api_key (PR #67) computes `v_remaining_keys = count(*)` AFTER the DELETE FROM api_keys, then conditionally deletes allocator_equity_snapshots. PR #68's sole-source purge in the worker uses a similar 'count siblings then purge' pattern. BOTH suffer the same TOCTOU race under READ COMMITTED — but the chained interaction is worse: User A has keys K1+K2; opens 'Add Key' (K3) in tab 1, 'Delete K1' (cascade=true) in tab 2. Order: K3 INSERT commits → K1 DELETE → count(api_keys WHERE user_id) = 1 (just K2, K3 from another tab not yet visible? READ COMMITTED says it IS visible after K3 commit). Subsequent reconstruct on K3 runs the sole-source check from PR #68 → no siblings of K3 in worker's serializable read (BUT count includes K2 if visible) → ambiguous outcome. Combined with PR #68's worker-side purge that ALSO doesn't lock api_keys, the system has TWO independent racy 'count + delete' patterns that can interleave to wipe legitimate multi-key data with no detection. Neither code path takes pg_advisory_xact_lock on hashtext(allocator_id).
- **Evidence**: supabase/migrations/20260422182451_delete_api_key_cascade_equity.sql:87-95 (RPC's count-then-delete, no FOR UPDATE). analytics-service/services/equity_reconstruction.py:1405-1406 (worker's count-then-purge, no advisory lock). Both run at READ COMMITTED. supabase-js for the RPC doesn't set isolation level.
- **Fix**: Add `pg_advisory_xact_lock(hashtext('alloc:' || auth.uid()::text))` at the top of delete_allocator_api_key's body. Add `await db_execute(lambda: supabase.rpc('pg_advisory_xact_lock', {'k': f'alloc:{allocator_id}'}).execute())` at the top of the worker's sole-source branch — they'll then serialize on the same key. Or wrap both in a single SECURITY DEFINER RPC `delete_allocator_api_key_with_purge` so the count + cascade is atomic at the SQL layer.

#### G17-035 · Migration 078 destructive DELETE-then-rebuild has no preview gate and no rollback path
- **File**: `supabase/migrations/20260424012820_equity_contract_size_healing.sql:64`
- **Specialist**: `data-migration` (confidence 9)
- **Summary**: Migration 078 unconditionally executes `DELETE FROM public.allocator_equity_snapshots` (all rows) and `DELETE FROM public.compute_jobs WHERE kind='reconstruct_allocator_history' AND status='done'`. There is no row-count probe, no `RAISE NOTICE` of expected scope, and no DRY-RUN / preview branch. The migration's docstring claims '3 allocators, ~13 snapshot rows' as the production scope, but that estimate is not encoded as a safety guard — if the worker had backfilled tens of thousands of rows before the merge landed (or if 078 runs in a future environment whose snapshot count is much larger), the migration silently nukes everything. Combined with the fact that 078 is the FIRST migration shipped via the new `supabase-migrate.yml` workflow, and the workflow's `plan` job runs `supabase migration list` (which lists names, not row impact), there is no visibility into the DELETE blast radius before approval.
- **Evidence**: 20260424012820_equity_contract_size_healing.sql:64,70-72 — unconditional DELETE without count probe. The migration was followed less than 24h later by 20260424031238_equity_defensive_heal.sql (079) which repeats the same DELETE shape verbatim because the original heal+rebuild produced still-broken data — proving the 'one-shot wipe + re-enqueue' pattern is not a stable strategy and amplifies the risk of repeating it without dry-run.
- **Fix**: Add a `SELECT count(*) INTO v_n FROM allocator_equity_snapshots; RAISE NOTICE 'm078 purging % rows', v_n;` and a `IF v_n > 1000 THEN RAISE EXCEPTION 'm078 scope exceeded — aborting'; END IF;` guard. Add a workflow step that runs `supabase migration up --dry-run` (or `--diff`) before the apply step in the production environment so reviewers see expected DDL rather than just file names. Capture a `pg_dump --table=allocator_equity_snapshots` to an artifact before applying.

#### G17-036 · Migration 078 healing INSERT bypasses enqueue_compute_job RPC and misses sync_status filter — queues doomed jobs against revoked keys · _chain_ · refs: code-reviewer-5, data-migration-5, data-migration-6
- **File**: `supabase/migrations/20260424012820_equity_contract_size_healing.sql:84`
- **Specialist**: `red-team` (confidence 9)
- **Summary**: Migration 078 STEP 3 INSERTs directly into compute_jobs with only (kind, api_key_id, exchange) (line 84-99). Two compound problems: (a) bypasses enqueue_compute_job RPC, losing the structured-log + xor-check + audit-event side effects every other enqueue path emits; (b) filters only `disconnected_at IS NULL AND is_active = true` — but the live worker dispatch (migration 075:194-196 + 247-248) ALSO filters `sync_status IS DISTINCT FROM 'revoked'`. Revoked keys (kept in the table for audit continuity but worker preflight rejects them) get a fresh reconstruct queued by 078; the worker classify_exception path emits revoked sync_status reset → loop. Migration 079 repeats the same shape verbatim — 079 was needed because 078 was insufficient, but neither learned the lesson. The `Reverted` rows that result clutter compute_jobs and break the per-key idempotency contract migration 076 promised.
- **Evidence**: supabase/migrations/20260424012820_equity_contract_size_healing.sql:84-99 — direct INSERT, no sync_status filter; supabase/migrations/20260424031238_equity_defensive_heal.sql:78-87 — identical pattern. supabase/migrations/20260422101911_api_keys_disconnected_at.sql:195 worker dispatch filter `AND sync_status IS DISTINCT FROM 'revoked'`.
- **Fix**: Add `AND k.sync_status IS DISTINCT FROM 'revoked'` to both 078 STEP 3 and 079 STEP 3. Replace direct INSERT with `PERFORM enqueue_compute_job(p_strategy_id := NULL, p_kind := 'reconstruct_allocator_history', p_idempotency_key := 'heal-' || k.id::text, p_api_key_id := k.id)` so structured logs + audit emit. For 080+ healing pattern: extract a `enqueue_reconstruct_for_all_eligible(p_idempotency_prefix text)` SECURITY DEFINER helper so future heals mirror the worker filter byte-for-byte.

#### G17-037 · Migration 078 STEP 1 wholesale DELETE breaks refresh cron's EXISTS gate — silent multi-day refresh outage if STEP 3 fails · _new_ · refs: code-reviewer-7, data-migration-1
- **File**: `supabase/migrations/20260424012820_equity_contract_size_healing.sql:64`
- **Specialist**: `red-team` (confidence 8)
- **Summary**: STEP 1 deletes every row from allocator_equity_snapshots. The daily refresh cron (enqueue_refresh_allocator_equity_for_all, migration 075 line 249-253) filters `WHERE ... AND EXISTS (SELECT 1 FROM allocator_equity_snapshots aes WHERE aes.allocator_id = ak.user_id LIMIT 1)`. After STEP 1's purge, the EXISTS predicate is false for EVERY user, so the refresh cron STOPS enqueueing daily rows. STEP 3 re-queues reconstruct jobs but: (a) reconstruct jobs are throttled to 30s claim cycles, (b) if reconstruct fails for any reason (ccxt down, exchange revoked, transient API error not classified as retryable, ratelimit + max_attempts exhausted), the user's allocator_equity_snapshots stays empty AND the refresh cron silently keeps skipping them — they fall further behind every day until manual intervention. The migration's own scope claim ('3 allocators, ~13 rows') doesn't bound the recovery-failure case. The chained healing (078 → 079) PROVES this can happen: 078's reconstructs WERE partial-broken, hence 079.
- **Evidence**: supabase/migrations/20260422101911_api_keys_disconnected_at.sql:249-253 (EXISTS gate on refresh cron). supabase/migrations/20260424012820_equity_contract_size_healing.sql:64 (wholesale DELETE). Migration 079 exists because 078's reconstructs produced broken data — implicit proof the recovery path is fragile.
- **Fix**: Add a sentinel row insertion after STEP 1's DELETE: `INSERT INTO allocator_equity_snapshots (allocator_id, asof, value_usd, breakdown, source) SELECT DISTINCT user_id, '1970-01-01', 0, '{}'::jsonb, 'sentinel' FROM api_keys WHERE is_active AND disconnected_at IS NULL` — keeps the EXISTS gate satisfied so refresh cron continues fan-out while reconstruct catches up. Or change the refresh cron's gate to `EXISTS (SELECT 1 FROM api_keys WHERE user_id = ak.user_id AND is_active)` so it doesn't depend on snapshot presence.

### MEDIUM (32)

#### G17-038 · PR #71 supabase-migrate.yml has no permissions block — defaults to repo write
- **File**: `.github/workflows/supabase-migrate.yml:1`
- **Specialist**: `code-reviewer` (confidence 8)
- **Summary**: The new supabase-migrate workflow declares no top-level `permissions:` block, so it inherits the repo's default token permissions (typically read/write on contents/issues/PRs). The workflow consumes Supabase credentials and pushes destructive DDL to production — a compromised step or supabase-cli action could write to the repo and exfiltrate secrets via the same token. The diff's own security note (lines 24-27) addresses script-injection but not over-privileged token scope.
- **Evidence**: .github/workflows/supabase-migrate.yml (full file in diff) — no `permissions:` key at workflow or job level. supabase/setup-cli@v1 is pinned only to major, not to a SHA, so a future supply-chain push could leverage the default token.
- **Fix**: Add `permissions: contents: read` at the workflow top-level, override per-job only where needed. Optionally pin supabase/setup-cli to a commit SHA (`uses: supabase/setup-cli@<sha>`).

#### G17-039 · PR #71 approval gate shows migration list output but not SQL bodies
- **File**: `.github/workflows/supabase-migrate.yml:60`
- **Specialist**: `code-reviewer` (confidence 8)
- **Summary**: The 'plan' job runs `supabase migration list` and prints the local-vs-remote diff. The 'apply' job is gated on the `production` environment for reviewer approval. But the reviewer in the GitHub UI sees only the list of NEW migration filenames, NOT the SQL contents. The approval gate is theatrical for destructive migrations like 078 — a reviewer cannot inspect what is about to be executed without separately browsing the repo for the SQL files. This is precisely the type of CI control the original /investigate report (un-applied migration 078) was meant to harden.
- **Evidence**: .github/workflows/supabase-migrate.yml:79-91 plan job runs `supabase migration list` only. No `cat` / `dump` of the SQL files into the workflow log.
- **Fix**: Add a step to the plan job that prints the SQL bodies of any pending migrations (e.g., diff local migrations against `supabase migration list` to find new ones, then `cat` each into the log), or run `supabase db push --dry-run` if the CLI supports it. The output then appears in the run log the reviewer reads before approving.

#### G17-040 · `supabase db push` runs the entire migration backlog under one Supabase CLI session — no per-file transaction boundary or partial-failure recovery
- **File**: `.github/workflows/supabase-migrate.yml:108`
- **Specialist**: `data-migration` (confidence 8)
- **Summary**: `supabase db push` reads `supabase/migrations/*.sql` and applies any rows not present in the remote `schema_migrations` table, executing them in filename order. The workflow has no per-migration step — if file N completes (commits) and file N+1 fails halfway, the remote `schema_migrations` row for N+1 is not written but N's effects are persisted. Migration 078 wraps its body in `BEGIN; ... COMMIT;` so its DELETEs roll back on failure WITHIN the file, but a sequence of files crossing the COMMIT boundary cannot be rolled back as a unit. There is no documented rollback story (`down/` directory exists but is empty for these migrations); if 078's DELETE commits and 078's INSERT fails for any FK/CHECK reason, the snapshot table is empty AND no reconstruct jobs are enqueued, leaving every allocator with a blank dashboard until manual intervention.
- **Evidence**: supabase/migrations/down/ directory exists (per ls output) but contains no down-migrations for 077/078. supabase-migrate.yml:108-110 issues a single `supabase db push` with no `--dry-run`, no `--include`, no per-file gating. Migration 078's BEGIN/COMMIT wrapper at lines 56,101 keeps a single file atomic but offers no protection across files.
- **Fix**: Either (a) split destructive migrations into manual-only runbooks rather than auto-applied migrations; or (b) author paired `down/<timestamp>_*.sql` files for any DELETE-shape migration; or (c) wrap the workflow in `pg_dump --schema-only` + `pg_dump --table=allocator_equity_snapshots --data-only` artifacts uploaded BEFORE `supabase db push` runs, so a manual restore is feasible. Document the rollback contract in the workflow comments.

#### G17-041 · supabase-migrate.yml lacks explicit GITHUB_TOKEN permissions (least-privilege gap)
- **File**: `.github/workflows/supabase-migrate.yml:33`
- **Specialist**: `security` (confidence 8)
- **Summary**: The workflow has no top-level or job-level `permissions:` block, so it inherits the repository default GITHUB_TOKEN scopes. The job only needs to checkout (contents: read) and call out to Supabase; it should not be able to write issues, comments, packages, or contents. If a future step in this workflow (or a third-party action it adds) is ever compromised — e.g. a malicious `supabase/setup-cli@v1` tag mutation or a typosquat — the inherited write-token gives the attacker far more capability than the workflow needs. STRIDE: elevation of privilege via supply-chain compromise of a referenced action. The workflow doc explicitly markets itself as 'no surface for script-injection', but it leaves the GITHUB_TOKEN over-scoped.
- **Evidence**: .github/workflows/supabase-migrate.yml:33-110 (no `permissions:` block anywhere in the file)
- **Fix**: Add at the top of the file: ```yaml permissions:   contents: read ``` or at each job level. This enforces least-privilege and reduces blast radius if any third-party action (supabase/setup-cli, actions/checkout) is ever compromised.

#### G17-042 · PR #70 cost > 0 cost/price perp normalization was insufficient — superseded by v0.15.4.2 OKX ctVal table
- **File**: `analytics-service/services/equity_reconstruction.py:1107`
- **Specialist**: `code-reviewer` (confidence 8)
- **Summary**: The fix shipped in PR #70 (lines 1107-1110 in the diff) trusts ccxt's `cost` field whenever cost > 0 and uses `amt_base = cost / price`. The /investigate 2026-04-24 (v0.15.4.2) note in current main (equity_reconstruction.py lines 100-138, _resolve_perp_amt_base lines 141-180) documents that ccxt's safe_trade only applies contractSize when the resolved market has a non-None contractSize, and otherwise falls through with `cost = amount × price`, making `cost / price = amount` (still in contracts, not base units). So PR #70's diff has a known false-trust hole that requires the v0.15.4.2 ctVal-table override to fully close. The diff itself is part of the audit trail but does not catch this case — flagging here so the chronology of partial fixes is in the audit record.
- **Evidence**: analytics-service/services/equity_reconstruction.py:100-138 OKX_PERP_CONTRACT_SIZE table + _resolve_perp_amt_base added in v0.15.4.2 to defend against the residual cost-untrustworthy path. Original PR #70 fix would still inflate amount when ccxt's market resolution missed contractSize.
- **Fix**: PR #70's fix has already been superseded in main (v0.15.4.2). Confirm the v0.15.4.2 patch landed in production and the OKX ctVal table covers all venue+symbol combinations users actually trade — extend the table or fall through to an explicit error if an unknown OKX SWAP symbol appears.

#### G17-043 · Persist count via len(res.data) silently overcounts if PostgREST returns ignored rows
- **File**: `analytics-service/services/equity_reconstruction.py:925`
- **Specialist**: `code-reviewer` (confidence 8)
- **Summary**: persist_equity_snapshots returns `len(getattr(res, 'data', None) or [])` after an upsert with on_conflict='allocator_id,asof', ignore_duplicates=True. PostgREST's documented behavior with `Prefer: resolution=ignore-duplicates,return=representation` is to return only the rows that were inserted (not the ignored ones), so the current implementation is correct in practice. But the contract is fragile: if PostgREST or supabase-py ever changes the default to return all input rows (some older PostgREST versions behaved that way), the count would silently overcount and audit log days_written would diverge from reality again — re-introducing the exact bug PR #68 was meant to fix.
- **Evidence**: analytics-service/services/equity_reconstruction.py:924-925 `res = await db_execute(_upsert); return len(getattr(res, 'data', None) or [])`. Behavior depends on PostgREST's interpretation of the Prefer header.
- **Fix**: Switch to using `count` parameter explicitly: pass `count='exact'` on the upsert and return `getattr(res, 'count', 0) or len(...)`. This makes the contract explicit and decouples the call site from PostgREST representation quirks.

#### G17-044 · `equity_reconstruction.py` sole-source purge fails open on query error — silently corrupts multi-key aggregation
- **File**: `analytics-service/services/equity_reconstruction.py:300`
- **Specialist**: `data-migration` (confidence 8)
- **Summary**: `_allocator_has_other_api_keys` wraps the sibling-count query in try/except and on ANY exception returns True ('fail-safe: preserve DO NOTHING rather than wipe legitimate multi-key data'). However the caller in `run_reconstruct_allocator_history_job` uses this as a boolean gate: True → don't purge (preserve siblings); False → purge. A connection drop, transient 503, or a database-side rate-limit causes the query to throw → function returns True → purge is skipped → stale rows survive → the original bug (`ignore_duplicates` no-ops every fresh row, dashboard stays stale) re-emerges silently. The audit_event for `stale_snapshots_purged` shows 0 in this case, but operators have no easy way to distinguish 'true multi-key user, not purged' from 'sole-key user, query failed, also not purged'. The 'fail-safe' choice is defensible but unobservable.
- **Evidence**: analytics-service/services/equity_reconstruction.py:300-308 — `try: res = await db_execute(_sel) except Exception as exc: logger.warning(...); return True`. The audit_event in run_reconstruct_allocator_history_job (line 1175 in original diff) records `stale_snapshots_purged=purged` but does not separately record whether the sibling-check itself succeeded.
- **Fix**: Promote the warning to an audit_event with a distinct kind (`allocator.equity.sibling_lookup_failed`). On the third consecutive failure for the same allocator, raise to ERROR-level and emit a Sentry alert. Add a regression test that mocks the sibling lookup to raise and asserts the audit event fires.

#### G17-045 · `_purge_allocator_equity_snapshots` return value via len(res.data) under-reports actual deletions when supabase-py truncates response payload
- **File**: `analytics-service/services/equity_reconstruction.py:336`
- **Specialist**: `data-migration` (confidence 8)
- **Summary**: `_purge_allocator_equity_snapshots` returns `len(getattr(res, 'data', None) or [])`. The supabase-py client returns `data` as the list of rows affected by the DELETE only when the PostgREST `Prefer: return=representation` header is set. The Python client defaults to `return=representation` for `.delete()` chains, but the returned payload is bounded by the Supabase row-size limit (1000 rows default per response unless `count_only` is used). For a sole-source allocator with >1000 days of stale snapshots (possible if backfilled at higher cadence), `len(res.data)` under-reports. The audit log then shows `stale_snapshots_purged=1000` while the actual DELETE affected all rows — operators investigating an incident look at this number and conclude the purge was incomplete, possibly re-running the heal redundantly.
- **Evidence**: analytics-service/services/equity_reconstruction.py:336 (in diff, line 326 in current file). Mirror pattern at line 264 (`persist_equity_snapshots` returns `len(res.data)` which is the same supabase-py-bounded count). The diff comment for `persist_equity_snapshots` explicitly notes 'return the count Postgres ACTUALLY wrote, not len(stamped)' — but `len(res.data)` is itself bounded by PostgREST's return limit, NOT by Postgres' actual write count.
- **Fix**: Use `.select('count', count='exact').delete()` chain or fall back to a separate `SELECT count(*) WHERE allocator_id = $1` BEFORE the DELETE for the audit number. Long-term: have the worker invoke a SECURITY DEFINER RPC that runs the DELETE + returns the ROW_COUNT GET DIAGNOSTICS — that's the only way to get the real Postgres-side count without a separate query.

#### G17-046 · _purge_allocator_equity_snapshots exception path: failures bubble but bubble path is untested
- **File**: `analytics-service/services/equity_reconstruction.py:987`
- **Specialist**: `pr-test-analyzer` (confidence 8)
- **Summary**: PR #68's _purge_allocator_equity_snapshots docstring says 'Failures bubble so the handler's outer except-block classifies + records them rather than silently proceeding with a polluted upsert.' This is the only defense against the scenario where the purge query partially fails and we proceed to upsert (which then DO-NOTHINGs against the leftover stale rows = the exact bug the fix was supposed to eliminate, dressed up as 'succeeded'). No test verifies that an exception in the delete query (a) doesn't silently swallow, (b) reaches the outer audit handler with classify_exception emitted. Compare to similar fail-safe coverage in test_wr04_fetch_transfers_auth_error_bubbles_to_outer_handler.
- **Evidence**: grep -n '_purge_allocator_equity_snapshots' analytics-service/tests/test_equity_reconstruction.py → 0 matches; equity_reconstruction.py:992-995 docstring 'Failures bubble' contract.
- **Fix**: Add test_purge_failure_bubbles_to_outer_handler(monkeypatch) modelled on test_wr04_fetch_transfers_auth_error_bubbles_to_outer_handler: stub FakeSupabaseClient.table('allocator_equity_snapshots').delete to raise an auth exception; assert run_reconstruct_allocator_history_job returns DispatchResult with outcome != DONE; assert audit emits reconstruct_failed (not reconstruct_complete); assert no UPSERT runs after the failed purge.

#### G17-047 · Refresh-job silent-drop of upnl == 0.0 hides position-exists state — derivative breakdown key never emitted for fresh opens · _new_ · refs: silent-failure-hunter-5, type-design-analyzer-3
- **File**: `analytics-service/services/equity_reconstruction.py:1474`
- **Specialist**: `red-team` (confidence 9)
- **Summary**: For holding_type='derivative', the refresh loop reads `upnl = float(h.get('unrealized_pnl_usd') or 0.0)` then `if upnl == 0.0: continue` (line 1473-1474). This silently drops:   (a) fresh perp opens at entry-price (legitimate upnl == 0.0, position exists)   (b) NULL upnl coerced to 0.0 by `or 0.0` — the poll job didn't populate the field The breakdown for that day NEVER carries a :PERP key for this position. The dashboard renders 'no derivative activity' when the user actually has $50k notional sitting in a position. Worse, distinguishing (a) from (b) requires looking at the upstream poll job log — there's no audit field surfacing 'we have a position but no MTM signal yet'. The pre-fix bug was double-counting notional; the new bug is silently hiding the position entirely.
- **Evidence**: analytics-service/services/equity_reconstruction.py:1471-1477 (current file, was 1473-1478 in diff). No audit/log emit for the skip case. _fetch_today_holdings (line 1063) doesn't filter upnl=NULL at the SELECT level.
- **Fix**: Replace `if upnl == 0.0: continue` with `if h.get('unrealized_pnl_usd') is None: logger.info('perp upnl missing for %s', sym); continue` AND drop the `== 0.0` skip entirely. Adding a 0-value PERP key to the breakdown is correct — it tells the dashboard 'position exists at entry'. Optionally add `_emit_audit(..., 'allocator.equity.perp_upnl_missing', {sym, api_key_id})` to surface poll-job gaps.

#### G17-048 · OKX_PERP_CONTRACT_SIZE applied without venue gating — Bybit instType='SWAP' fills get OKX ctVal silently · _new_ · refs: code-reviewer-4, data-migration-15, type-design-analyzer-4
- **File**: `analytics-service/services/equity_reconstruction.py:171`
- **Specialist**: `red-team` (confidence 9)
- **Summary**: _resolve_perp_amt_base gates on `inst_type.upper() == 'SWAP'` (line 169) but takes no venue argument. Bybit V5 unified-margin payloads also carry `info.instType: 'SWAP'` (Bybit copied OKX's instType taxonomy in V5). For a Bybit ETHUSDT-perp fill that lands with raw_symbol='ETH/USDT:USDT' and inst_type='SWAP', the OKX_PERP_CONTRACT_SIZE table lookup HITS (ETH/USDT:USDT key exists, value 0.1) and the override applies OKX's ctVal of 0.1 to a Bybit trade — Bybit's ETHUSDT-perp uses ctVal=1.0 (one contract = 1 ETH). The defensive layer that v0.15.4.2 added explicitly to prevent silent inflation now silently INTRODUCES 10x deflation on Bybit perps. No regression test covers Bybit perp with OKX-symbol-matched fixtures.
- **Evidence**: analytics-service/services/equity_reconstruction.py:141-180 — _resolve_perp_amt_base signature takes inst_type but NOT venue. Bybit's V5 trade endpoint returns `info.instType = 'SWAP'` per https://bybit-exchange.github.io/docs/v5/order/execution. OKX_PERP_CONTRACT_SIZE keys overlap (BTC/USDT:USDT, ETH/USDT:USDT) with Bybit's ccxt symbol shape.
- **Fix**: Add `venue: str` parameter; only apply the table lookup when `venue.lower() == 'okx'`. Caller passes `venue=venue` from the context. Defensive: extend the table to `{'okx': {...}, 'bybit': {...}}` and resolve per-venue. Add regression test `test_bybit_perp_not_overridden_by_okx_ctval_table`.

#### G17-049 · 5% ctVal divergence threshold silently chooses cost/price at 4.99% mismatch — drift table can decay without alert · _new_ · refs: silent-failure-hunter-12, type-design-analyzer-4
- **File**: `analytics-service/services/equity_reconstruction.py:177`
- **Specialist**: `red-team` (confidence 8)
- **Summary**: _resolve_perp_amt_base computes `relative_err = abs(amt_from_cost - amt_explicit) / amt_explicit; if relative_err > 0.05: return amt_explicit else: return amt_from_cost` (lines 177-180). A 4.99% disagreement is silently treated as 'cost/price wins' — but a 4.99% MTM error on a 21 ETH position × $2336 ETH = ~$2,500 of unaccounted equity error per snapshot, sustained across 730 days. The OKX_PERP_CONTRACT_SIZE table was 'cross-checked on a SINGLE day, 2026-04-24' (per the comment at line 121-122). If OKX changes a ctVal (rare but historically has happened — OKX adjusts ctVal on token-listing rebrands), the table drifts. The 5% threshold then absorbs the drift silently until it crosses 5% AND someone notices the dashboard is off. No automated re-check, no audit signal at 1-5% disagreement.
- **Evidence**: analytics-service/services/equity_reconstruction.py:177-180. OKX_PERP_CONTRACT_SIZE docstring at line 121-122 ('cross-checked ... on 2026-04-24'). No test exists for sub-5% divergence path.
- **Fix**: When 0.01 < relative_err <= 0.05, emit `_emit_audit(..., 'allocator.equity.ctval_drift_warning', {raw_symbol, amt_from_cost, amt_explicit, ctval, relative_err})`. Add a daily cron `verify_okx_ctval_table` that fetches `/api/v5/public/instruments?instType=SWAP` and asserts no row in OKX_PERP_CONTRACT_SIZE diverges by more than 0.1% from live exchange data; alert if it does. Pin the cross-check date in module-level constant `OKX_CTVAL_LAST_VERIFIED_AT = '2026-04-24'` for future audits.

#### G17-050 · _rate_limit_sleep `except Exception: pass` swallows CancelledError — workers don't honor SIGTERM, kubectl rollout stalls · _new_ · refs: silent-failure-hunter-13
- **File**: `analytics-service/services/equity_reconstruction.py:248`
- **Specialist**: `red-team` (confidence 8)
- **Summary**: `try: await asyncio.sleep(...); except Exception: pass` at lines 248-251. On Python 3.7 asyncio.CancelledError inherits from Exception (changed to BaseException in 3.8+). The analytics-service Dockerfile pins Python 3.12 so the immediate CancelledError-swallowing bug is mitigated — BUT other transient errors (asyncio.TimeoutError, custom exception classes that ARE Exception subclasses) still get swallowed silently. During worker shutdown (Vercel pod eviction, kubernetes rolling update), if the sleep is mid-call when the loop tries to cancel tasks, the bare except swallows whatever the loop raises and the reconstruct continues for one more iteration on a doomed connection. The `# pragma: no cover` admits the path is never tested — and reconstruct loops can iterate 730 times per allocator, so the chance of a sleep coinciding with SIGTERM is non-trivial during heals.
- **Evidence**: analytics-service/services/equity_reconstruction.py:248-251 with explicit `# pragma: no cover` opt-out from coverage. Reconstruct is called from job_worker.py poll loop — long-running, async-cancellable.
- **Fix**: Replace with `except (TypeError, ValueError) as exc: logger.warning('rate_limit_sleep skipped: %s', exc); pass`. CancelledError on 3.12+ inherits from BaseException so won't be caught — but the explicit narrowing makes the intent obvious and survives a future python downgrade. Add a regression test that monkeypatches asyncio.sleep to raise CancelledError and asserts the outer task propagates it.

#### G17-051 · _api_key_already_reconstructed defaults to False on query failure — INVERSE fail-safe to _allocator_has_other_api_keys, creating an inconsistent error model
- **File**: `analytics-service/services/equity_reconstruction.py:1048`
- **Specialist**: `silent-failure-hunter` (confidence 8)
- **Summary**: `_api_key_already_reconstructed` returns False on Exception (line 1041-1048) while `_allocator_has_other_api_keys` returns True (line 971-979). The first means 'on read failure, re-run the reconstruct'; the second means 'on read failure, do not purge.' When BOTH fail on a transient supabase outage, the reconstruct runs but the purge is skipped — exactly the v0.15.3.3 'sole-key stale-snapshot' bug under a different trigger. Neither logger.warning is tied to an alert, error ID, or DispatchResult escalation, so this dual-fail-safe death spiral is invisible until the dashboard shows wrong numbers and an investigator has to grep job logs to reconstruct the chain.
- **Evidence**: analytics-service/services/equity_reconstruction.py:1041-1048     try:         res = await db_execute(_sel)     except Exception as exc:  # noqa: BLE001         logger.warning(             "compute_jobs done-reconstruct lookup failed for api_key=%s: %s",             api_key_id, exc,         )         return False  # opposite fail-safe to _allocator_has_other_api_keys
- **Fix**: Pick one error model: either both bubble up to DispatchOutcome.FAILED (re-queue with backoff), or both consistently emit `allocator.equity.lookup_failed` audit events with an error ID from constants/errorIds so the chained-failure case is recoverable. Document the chosen invariant in a module docstring so future PRs don't drift.

#### G17-052 · _resolve_perp_amt_base 5% tolerance window silently chooses cost/price when the two disagree by 4.9% — could accept 5% MTM error indefinitely
- **File**: `analytics-service/services/equity_reconstruction.py:177`
- **Specialist**: `silent-failure-hunter` (confidence 8)
- **Summary**: The check `if relative_err > 0.05: return amt_explicit` (line 178) means a 4.99% disagreement between the explicit ctVal table and cost/price is silently treated as 'cost/price wins' with no log, no audit, no signal that the two sources are diverging. For a 21.464 ETH position that's a ~1.07 ETH equity discrepancy — multiply by current ETH price ($2336) and that's $2,500 of unaccounted error per snapshot, silently. The threshold is hard-coded and undocumented; if the OKX_PERP_CONTRACT_SIZE table drifts out of sync with the actual venue ctVal (which the comment admits is cross-checked on a SINGLE day, 2026-04-24), the divergence grows and the code keeps trusting cost/price. The user has no way to know the table is stale until the dashboard is visibly wrong.
- **Evidence**: analytics-service/services/equity_reconstruction.py:177-180     relative_err = abs(amt_from_cost - amt_explicit) / amt_explicit     if relative_err > 0.05:         return amt_explicit     return amt_from_cost
- **Fix**: When 0.01 < relative_err <= 0.05 (small but non-trivial divergence), emit a logger.info or audit event 'okx_ctval_drift_warning' with raw_symbol, amt_from_cost, amt_explicit, ctval, inst_type so observability surfaces table drift before it crosses the threshold. Also: ship a unit test that fails if the OKX_PERP_CONTRACT_SIZE table is older than N days and pin the cross-check date in the migration log.

#### G17-053 · _allocator_has_other_api_keys returns bool but conflates 'no siblings' with 'lookup failed'
- **File**: `analytics-service/services/equity_reconstruction.py:928`
- **Specialist**: `type-design-analyzer` (confidence 8)
- **Summary**: `_allocator_has_other_api_keys` returns `bool` and documents 'Defaults to True on query failure (fail-safe: preserve DO NOTHING rather than risk wiping legitimate multi-key data)'. The caller at line ~1180 reads the inverted boolean and PURGES every snapshot row for the allocator when the function returns False. This conflates two distinct states into one: 'I confirmed there are no siblings ⇒ safe to wipe' vs 'lookup raised, defaulting to True ⇒ pretend there ARE siblings'. The fail-safe direction is good, but the type erases the operational signal — there's no way for the caller to log 'we skipped the sole-source purge because the sibling lookup failed' (which is a user-actionable error mode: 'we didn't apply your fresh reconstruct because of a transient DB error'). A future refactor that decides 'on lookup failure, just retry' has no way to discover this is the fail-safe path.
- **Evidence**: equity_reconstruction.py:928 `async def _allocator_has_other_api_keys(...) -> bool:`; lines 945-952 catch+log+`return True` on any exception; caller at line ~1180 `if not await _allocator_has_other_api_keys(...): purged = await _purge_allocator_equity_snapshots(...)`.
- **Fix**: Return a small enum: `class SiblingCheckResult(Enum): NO_SIBLINGS = auto(); HAS_SIBLINGS = auto(); LOOKUP_FAILED = auto()`. Caller treats LOOKUP_FAILED identically to HAS_SIBLINGS for safety, but the audit emit at line 1188 can include `sibling_check: 'lookup_failed'` so users have a recovery path ('retry sync now') instead of the dashboard staying stale forever with no signal.

#### G17-054 · _resolve_perp_amt_base returns bare float, erasing source-of-truth provenance + buries 5% magic number
- **File**: `analytics-service/services/equity_reconstruction.py:177`
- **Specialist**: `type-design-analyzer` (confidence 8)
- **Summary**: The function returns base-unit size from either `cost/price` or `amount × ctVal`, switching when they disagree by more than 5% (line 178 `if relative_err > 0.05: return amt_explicit`). The 5% threshold is a magic literal embedded in the function body, the returned value is just `float` — the caller has no way to know which branch was taken. For the v0.15.4.0 V-shape regression class this matters: an audit log that records 'used cost/price' vs 'used explicit ctVal' is the difference between a 5-minute debug and another two-week investigation cycle. Also, the docstring at line 156 declares 'Synthetic test fixtures that treat amount as base units (implicit contractSize=1) never carry that stamp, so they keep the legacy behaviour' — this is an invariant load-bearing for production safety (it's why the fixtures don't regress real OKX trades), but it's enforced via prose, not via a separate fixture type.
- **Evidence**: equity_reconstruction.py:177-181 `relative_err = abs(amt_from_cost - amt_explicit) / amt_explicit; if relative_err > 0.05: return amt_explicit; return amt_from_cost`; returns `float` with no source attribution.
- **Fix**: Return `@dataclass class PerpAmountResolution: amt_base: float; source: Literal['cost_div_price', 'ctval_table', 'fallback_amount']; relative_err: float | None`. Callers can ignore the metadata in hot paths but the audit emit pipeline can surface it. Lift the 5% threshold to a named constant `PERP_AMT_CTVAL_DIVERGENCE_THRESHOLD = 0.05` so it's traceable and tunable.

#### G17-055 · PR #68 test seeds compute_jobs status=done to suppress purge — production gap if gate is bypassed
- **File**: `analytics-service/tests/test_equity_reconstruction.py:446`
- **Specialist**: `code-reviewer` (confidence 8)
- **Summary**: The PR #68 test for idempotency had to be modified to seed a `compute_jobs.status='done'` row BEFORE running the second reconstruct, because the new sole-source purge path would otherwise wipe the rows written by the first run. The handler's per-api_key idempotency gate (migration 076 _api_key_already_reconstructed) is now the only thing preventing the second invocation from purging. Anything that bypasses the gate — manual job enqueue, healing migration that deletes compute_jobs 'done' rows (which migration 078 STEP 2 does!), or a future code path that calls run_reconstruct_allocator_history_job directly — will purge accumulated valid history.
- **Evidence**: analytics-service/tests/test_equity_reconstruction.py:453-458 — manual seed of `compute_jobs` status='done' row in the test. supabase/migrations/20260424012820_equity_contract_size_healing.sql:70-72 STEP 2 deletes all compute_jobs reconstruct done rows, then STEP 3 enqueues fresh reconstructs.
- **Fix**: Make the purge defensive: only purge if compute_jobs.status='done' for this api_key is absent AND (a) snapshots are older than some threshold OR (b) snapshots' source value indicates pre-fix code. Alternatively, structure the purge inside an RPC that takes a 'sole_source_proof' flag the caller computes from compute_jobs state, so the purge can't fire without explicit caller intent.

#### G17-056 · OKX contract-size regression test only covers ETH (ctVal=0.01); BTC perp (ctVal=0.001) untested
- **File**: `analytics-service/tests/test_equity_reconstruction.py:2363`

The fix in equity_reconstruction.py derives base units from cost/price independent of contractSize, but the only fixture exercised is ctVal=0.01. BTC-USDT-SWAP has ctVal=0.001 (1000x), SOL-USDT-SWAP has ctVal=1 (no inflation), and DOGE-USDT-SWAP has ctVal=1000 (0.001x). A regression that hard-codes ETH-style scaling would pass the ETH test but break BTC silently. Given the CHANGELOG explicitly mentions 'BTC-USDT-SWAP, etc.' as affected, BTC coverage is missing.
- **Evidence**: grep -n 'contract_size=' analytics-service/tests/test_equity_reconstruction.py → 1 hit (default arg), grep -n '0.001\|BTC.*perp.*contractSize\|BTC.*swap.*contract' → 0 matches in the contract-size regression block (lines 2329-2437); equity_reconstruction.py comment at line 1086-1095 explicitly lists BTC-USDT-SWAP with ctVal=0.001 as affected.
- **Fix**: Add test_okx_contract_size_btc_perp_ctval_0_001_no_inflation: same shape as the ETH test, but use _mk_okx_perp_trade(symbol='BTC/USDT:USDT', contract_size=0.001, base_amount=0.5, price=70000.0). Add test_okx_contract_size_sol_ctval_1_no_distortion: contract_size=1 (where amount=base_amount), assert no spurious scaling. Parameterise via pytest.mark.parametrize over (symbol, ctVal, base_amount, price) tuples.

#### G17-057 · Migration 077 self-verify DO block tests function body string but won't catch logic regressions
- **File**: `supabase/migrations/077_delete_api_key_cascade_equity.sql:167`
- **Specialist**: `pr-test-analyzer` (confidence 8)
- **Summary**: Migration 077 ships a self-verify DO block (lines 167-202) that checks: (a) prosrc text mentions 'allocator_equity_snapshots', (b) prosrc mentions 'v_remaining_keys', (c) authenticated has EXECUTE grant, (d) anon does not. These are syntactic string-presence checks — they pass even if the cascade branch is inverted (e.g. deletes snapshots when v_remaining_keys > 0 instead of = 0), or if the user_id filter is wrong (cross-allocator wipe). They do not exercise the function end-to-end. The actual behavioral correctness has no pytest/vitest coverage either (see finding 1).
- **Evidence**: supabase/migrations/077_delete_api_key_cascade_equity.sql:179-185 prosrc LIKE checks only; no equivalent behavioral integration test exists in src/__tests__/delete-allocator-api-key-rpc.test.ts.
- **Fix**: Strengthen the DO block to actually invoke delete_allocator_api_key in a transaction-rollback wrapper (BEGIN; CALL …; ROLLBACK;) against a seeded test row pair to prove cascade behavior, OR (preferred, also addresses finding 1) add behavioral coverage in the TypeScript live-DB test file.

#### G17-058 · Migration 078 healing assumes idempotent re-run safety but isn't tested for re-application
- **File**: `supabase/migrations/078_equity_contract_size_healing.sql:1493`
- **Specialist**: `pr-test-analyzer` (confidence 8)
- **Summary**: Migration 078 is a destructive one-shot. If it gets re-applied (e.g. someone restores from a backup, runs migration list rebuild, or it lands twice via a deploy retry), STEP 3 INSERT enqueues a duplicate reconstruct job for every key — the partial unique index compute_jobs_one_inflight_reconstruct_per_api_key (migration 076) should catch this, but the migration comment claims the NOT EXISTS guard gives 'a clearer conflict-on-insert message than a 23505 if it ever fires.' This is an explicit guard against a known concurrency hazard that has no test. A regression that drops the NOT EXISTS clause (or the partial unique index) would silently let duplicate pending jobs through and the workers would race.
- **Evidence**: supabase/migrations/078_equity_contract_size_healing.sql:1518-1528 the NOT EXISTS guard with explicit anti-race rationale; no test covers re-application or concurrent enqueue.
- **Fix**: Add migration re-application test: apply 078 against test DB, then apply 078 again (or call it via raw SQL) — assert no duplicate compute_jobs rows are created, no 23505 surfaces uncaught. Or apply 078 once, then manually INSERT a pending reconstruct job for one of the keys, then call 078's STEP 3 INSERT … SELECT … NOT EXISTS query — assert that key's row count remains 1, not 2.

#### G17-059 · Migration 078 healing wipe runs without a pre-flight count or recoverable backup — destructive operation with no audit trail
- **File**: `supabase/migrations/078_equity_contract_size_healing.sql:1493`
- **Specialist**: `silent-failure-hunter` (confidence 8)
- **Summary**: `DELETE FROM public.allocator_equity_snapshots` (line 47 in the new file in batch G17, originally line 1493 of the diff) wipes every row in the table with NO row-count capture, NO RAISE NOTICE summary, NO insertion into an audit log table, and NO `RETURNING` clause that could be captured for forensics. The migration comment claims '3 allocators, ~13 snapshot rows on production as of 2026-04-24', but if the migration ever runs against a database with the wrong scope (test pointed at prod, or a future re-execution after months of growth) the destructive scope is invisible until someone notices the dashboard is empty. Migration self-verification blocks earlier in this batch (077 DO $$ block lines 121-148) raise on missing branches, but there is NO equivalent post-condition check here: the migration cannot tell you whether it wiped 13 rows or 130000.
- **Evidence**: supabase/migrations/078_equity_contract_size_healing.sql:46-49 -- STEP 1: purge every allocator_equity_snapshots row. DELETE FROM public.allocator_equity_snapshots; -- (no RAISE NOTICE, no row count capture, no audit trail)
- **Fix**: Wrap STEP 1 in: `WITH deleted AS (DELETE FROM public.allocator_equity_snapshots RETURNING 1) SELECT count(*) INTO v_deleted FROM deleted; RAISE NOTICE 'Migration 078: purged % equity snapshots', v_deleted;`. Add an explicit assertion `IF v_deleted > 1000 THEN RAISE EXCEPTION 'Migration 078: refusing to wipe % rows (>1000 sanity ceiling)', v_deleted; END IF;`. This converts a silent destructive operation into a self-narrating one and gives operators an explicit safety hatch.

#### G17-060 · PR #67 lock_timeout '3s' applies only to migration transaction, not to function callers
- **File**: `supabase/migrations/20260422182451_delete_api_key_cascade_equity.sql:45`
- **Specialist**: `code-reviewer` (confidence 8)
- **Summary**: `SET lock_timeout = '3s'` is set at the top of the migration transaction, outside the CREATE OR REPLACE FUNCTION body. It bounds the lock waits of the migration itself (mostly catalog locks for CREATE FUNCTION and grants) but does NOT propagate to future invocations of delete_allocator_api_key by user sessions. The function's runtime lock-wait behavior is whatever the calling session/role default is, typically unbounded. Comment-vs-behavior mismatch that may mislead a reader into thinking the function has a 3s lock guard.
- **Evidence**: supabase/migrations/20260422182451_delete_api_key_cascade_equity.sql:45 `SET lock_timeout = '3s';` at file scope; function body at lines 47-100 contains no `SET LOCAL lock_timeout` and no `SET lock_timeout` inside the function.
- **Fix**: Either move `SET LOCAL lock_timeout = '3s'` inside the function body so it bounds runtime calls, or remove the top-level SET and add a comment clarifying it only protects the migration transaction. Without one of these, the file pattern misleads.

#### G17-061 · Migration 077 RPC executes destructive cross-table DELETE under SECURITY DEFINER without per-statement search_path guard for `allocator_equity_snapshots`
- **File**: `supabase/migrations/20260422182451_delete_api_key_cascade_equity.sql:93`
- **Specialist**: `data-migration` (confidence 8)
- **Summary**: `delete_allocator_api_key` is SECURITY DEFINER with `SET search_path = public, pg_temp`. The DELETE statement reads `DELETE FROM allocator_equity_snapshots WHERE allocator_id = auth.uid()` without `public.` qualifier. The search_path GUC blocks pg_temp-shadowing attacks, but a future migration that creates a SECURITY DEFINER helper using the same pattern (without the `public.` qualifier) inherits this implicit-resolution pattern. Worse, `auth.uid()` is referenced as `auth.uid()` (qualified) only at lines 65,76,81,88,93 — at line 93's DELETE it IS qualified, so this isn't a current vulnerability, but mixing qualified/unqualified table references in a single SECURITY DEFINER function is fragile. The function references `api_keys`, `allocator_holdings`, `allocator_equity_snapshots` all unqualified; only `auth.uid()` is qualified.
- **Evidence**: 20260422182451_delete_api_key_cascade_equity.sql:63,74,81,88,93 — 'api_keys', 'allocator_holdings', 'allocator_equity_snapshots' all unqualified. Compare with migration 075's `request_allocator_holdings_sync` which uses the same `SET search_path = public, pg_catalog` and same unqualified style — established codebase convention. So this is a convention concern not a vulnerability.
- **Fix**: Optional / consistency: schema-qualify all table references inside SECURITY DEFINER bodies (`public.api_keys`, `public.allocator_holdings`, `public.allocator_equity_snapshots`). Or add a `SET search_path = pg_catalog` to be defensive. Document the convention in AGENTS.md.

#### G17-062 · Migration 077 last-key cascade query has a TOCTOU race — concurrent key insert between count check and snapshot DELETE can wipe legitimate multi-key data
- **File**: `supabase/migrations/20260422182451_delete_api_key_cascade_equity.sql:88`
- **Specialist**: `silent-failure-hunter` (confidence 8)
- **Summary**: Step 4 of delete_allocator_api_key runs `SELECT count(*) INTO v_remaining_keys FROM api_keys WHERE user_id = auth.uid()` (line 88-90) and then conditionally DELETEs from allocator_equity_snapshots. If another transaction inserts a new api_keys row between the SELECT and DELETE (the user runs Add Key + Delete Key in parallel browser tabs), the count is 0 but a sibling key exists by the time the DELETE fires — and the sibling's snapshots are silently wiped. The function is SECURITY DEFINER without SERIALIZABLE isolation, so the race window is real. There is no FOR UPDATE lock on api_keys, no INSERT trigger advisory lock, no row-versioning check.
- **Evidence**: supabase/migrations/20260422182451_delete_api_key_cascade_equity.sql:87-96   IF p_cascade_holdings THEN     SELECT count(*) INTO v_remaining_keys       FROM api_keys       WHERE user_id = auth.uid();     IF v_remaining_keys = 0 THEN       DELETE FROM allocator_equity_snapshots         WHERE allocator_id = auth.uid();     END IF;   END IF;
- **Fix**: Take an advisory lock on the allocator_id at function entry (pg_advisory_xact_lock(hashtext(auth.uid()::text))), or use SELECT ... FOR UPDATE on a representative row, or change isolation to SERIALIZABLE for this RPC. The current shape is a low-probability but high-impact silent data loss path — and unlike app-level races, it leaves no log trail.

#### G17-063 · Migration 078 healing INSERT lacks sync_status revoked filter, queues doomed jobs
- **File**: `supabase/migrations/20260424012820_equity_contract_size_healing.sql:86`
- **Specialist**: `code-reviewer` (confidence 9)
- **Summary**: The healing migration's STEP 3 enqueues a reconstruct for every api_key where `disconnected_at IS NULL AND is_active = true`. The poll/refresh cron filters (migration 075 line 195) ADD `sync_status IS DISTINCT FROM 'revoked'`. Revoked api_keys are kept in the table for audit continuity but the worker preflight rejects them. The healing migration therefore queues doomed jobs that will fail at preflight, leaving misleading error rows in compute_jobs and audit log noise.
- **Evidence**: supabase/migrations/20260424012820_equity_contract_size_healing.sql:84-99 — `INSERT INTO public.compute_jobs ... FROM public.api_keys k WHERE k.disconnected_at IS NULL AND k.is_active = true AND NOT EXISTS (...)`. No `AND k.sync_status IS DISTINCT FROM 'revoked'` predicate.
- **Fix**: Add `AND k.sync_status IS DISTINCT FROM 'revoked'` to mirror the cron enqueue filter exactly.

#### G17-064 · Migration 078 healing has no jitter/scheduling for enqueued reconstruct jobs
- **File**: `supabase/migrations/20260424012820_equity_contract_size_healing.sql:84`
- **Specialist**: `code-reviewer` (confidence 9)
- **Summary**: STEP 3 inserts reconstruct jobs without `run_at` jitter. The cron's enqueue_poll_allocator_positions_for_all_keys (migration 075 line 199) and enqueue_refresh_allocator_equity_for_all add `random() * interval '600 seconds'` jitter to spread ccxt API load. After the healing deploy, every affected api_key gets a reconstruct queued at the same instant and the worker claim-cycle (30s) will pick them up in a tight burst. The migration's own comment says scope is '3 allocators, ~13 snapshot rows', which is fine — but if the healing pattern is ever re-used at higher volume, the lack of jitter will hit exchange rate limits.
- **Evidence**: supabase/migrations/20260424012820_equity_contract_size_healing.sql:84 `INSERT INTO public.compute_jobs (kind, api_key_id, exchange) SELECT 'reconstruct_allocator_history', k.id, k.exchange FROM public.api_keys k` — no run_at column, defaults to now().
- **Fix**: Either (a) include a run_at column with `now() + (random() * interval '600 seconds')` to mirror the cron, or (b) add a comment explicitly acknowledging the small-scope assumption and pointing future authors at the jittered cron pattern for larger healing migrations.

#### G17-065 · Migration 078 healing leaves refresh cron unable to enqueue until reconstruct succeeds
- **File**: `supabase/migrations/20260424012820_equity_contract_size_healing.sql:64`
- **Specialist**: `code-reviewer` (confidence 8)
- **Summary**: STEP 1 wipes allocator_equity_snapshots wholesale. The daily refresh cron (enqueue_refresh_allocator_equity_for_all, migration 075 line 249) filters api_keys WHERE EXISTS (SELECT 1 FROM allocator_equity_snapshots aes WHERE aes.allocator_id = ak.user_id). After the wipe, that EXISTS predicate is false for every affected user, so the refresh cron stops enqueueing daily rows for them. The healing migration's STEP 3 reconstruct re-populates the table — IF it succeeds. If reconstruct fails (ccxt down, exchange revoked, transient API error not classified as retryable), the user's refresh cron is broken silently and they fall further behind every day until a manual intervention.
- **Evidence**: supabase/migrations/20260422101911_api_keys_disconnected_at.sql:249-253 enqueue_refresh_allocator_equity_for_all requires `EXISTS (SELECT 1 FROM allocator_equity_snapshots aes WHERE aes.allocator_id = ak.user_id LIMIT 1)`. supabase/migrations/20260424012820_equity_contract_size_healing.sql:64 wipes the entire table.
- **Fix**: Either (a) gate the wipe to only rows reconstructed under affected versions (e.g., where `reconstructed_at < '2026-04-24'`), preserving at least skeletal data so refresh keeps running, or (b) add an alerting/monitoring hook that fires if the post-wipe reconstruct doesn't repopulate the table within the worker SLO.

#### G17-066 · Migration 078 INSERT does not set required fields and depends on column defaults for `status`/`next_attempt_at`/`max_attempts` — implicit drift risk
- **File**: `supabase/migrations/20260424012820_equity_contract_size_healing.sql:84`
- **Specialist**: `data-migration` (confidence 8)
- **Summary**: Migration 078's STEP 3 inserts directly into `public.compute_jobs (kind, api_key_id, exchange)` without going through `enqueue_compute_job()` / `_enqueue_compute_job_internal()`. The RPCs perform pre-check + RAISE-on-XOR-violation + log-audit-event for trace continuity. The direct INSERT relies on the table's column defaults (`status='pending'`, `next_attempt_at=now()`, `max_attempts=3`, `attempts=0`, `parent_job_ids='{}'`) and on the `compute_jobs_target_xor` 4-way CHECK happening to pass when only `api_key_id` is non-null. If any future migration adds a new NOT NULL column to compute_jobs without a default, this INSERT silently breaks; if any future migration adds a required `metadata` field for reconstruct enqueues, the worker reads NULL and may crash. The audit log loses the 'compute_job.enqueued' trail entirely.
- **Evidence**: 20260424012820_equity_contract_size_healing.sql:84-99 inserts only 3 columns. The standard enqueue path lives in scoring_weight_overrides.sql:175+ (`_enqueue_compute_job_internal`) and emits structured logs. Migration 079 (20260424031238_equity_defensive_heal.sql:78) repeats the same pattern verbatim — a direct INSERT bypassing the RPC.
- **Fix**: Replace the direct INSERT with `PERFORM enqueue_compute_job(p_strategy_id := NULL, p_kind := 'reconstruct_allocator_history', p_idempotency_key := 'heal-078-' || k.id::text, p_api_key_id := k.id)` inside the SELECT loop. Or at minimum, EXPLICITLY include `status, next_attempt_at, max_attempts, attempts, parent_job_ids` so the migration is robust to future schema additions and is grep-able for 'how do reconstruct jobs get enqueued'.

#### G17-067 · Migration 078 STEP 2 deletes only `status='done'` reconstruct rows — leaves `failed_final`/`failed_retry` rows that block re-enqueue
- **File**: `supabase/migrations/20260424012820_equity_contract_size_healing.sql:70`
- **Specialist**: `data-migration` (confidence 8)
- **Summary**: `DELETE FROM public.compute_jobs WHERE kind='reconstruct_allocator_history' AND status='done'` filters on `status='done'` only. If a per-api_key reconstruct was previously in `failed_retry` or `failed_final` state (e.g. the user's account had an expired API key earlier, or the worker crashed mid-job), those rows survive. The partial unique index `compute_jobs_one_inflight_reconstruct_per_api_key` is over `status IN ('pending','running','done_pending_children')` and does NOT cover `failed_*`, so the subsequent INSERT in STEP 3 would not be blocked — but the existence of the failed row leaves a misleading audit trail, and the `_api_key_already_reconstructed` gate in migration 076 must also be re-checked: if that helper inspects 'any reconstruct row exists' rather than 'a successful one', the re-enqueue still short-circuits and the heal silently fails for those allocators.
- **Evidence**: 20260424012820_equity_contract_size_healing.sql:70-72 only deletes `status='done'`. Recommended check: migration 076 (`20260422122720_reconstruct_per_api_key_gate.sql`) — if `_api_key_already_reconstructed` checks any non-`failed_*` row, the heal works; if it checks 'any row exists', this is a latent bug. Recommend re-reading 076 to confirm.
- **Fix**: Either (a) delete `status IN ('done', 'failed_final')` to clean up clearly-terminal rows; or (b) verify migration 076's gate explicitly excludes `failed_*` and document the contract in 078's comment block. Add an `RAISE NOTICE` showing how many rows were deleted vs how many api_keys were enqueued, so a mismatch surfaces in the apply log.

#### G17-068 · Migration 078 DELETE of compute_jobs status='done' bypasses migration 076 gate semantics — leaves failed_final rows blocking re-enqueue under certain code paths · _chain_ · refs: data-migration-6, code-reviewer-13
- **File**: `supabase/migrations/20260424012820_equity_contract_size_healing.sql:70`
- **Specialist**: `red-team` (confidence 8)
- **Summary**: STEP 2 deletes only `WHERE kind='reconstruct_allocator_history' AND status='done'`. Migration 076's _api_key_already_reconstructed gate at line 1037 checks specifically `.eq('status', 'done')`, so the gate is correctly bypassed for re-enqueue. BUT migration 076's partial UNIQUE index `compute_jobs_one_inflight_reconstruct_per_api_key` covers `status IN ('pending', 'running', 'done_pending_children')` — NOT failed_*. So failed_final rows for the same api_key persist after 078 → 079 chain → audit trail shows a sequence of dead jobs the operator can't easily distinguish from active healing. Worse: if a per-key gate regression is ever introduced (a future migration that adds `.in_('status', ['done', 'failed_final'])` to the gate), the failed rows reactivate the short-circuit and the heal silently fails for the affected allocator. The 4-PR heal chain (077 → 078 → 079) already PROVES the gate is fragile — and the next failure mode is sitting one schema-tweak away.
- **Evidence**: supabase/migrations/20260424012820_equity_contract_size_healing.sql:70-72 deletes only `status='done'`. supabase/migrations/20260424031238_equity_defensive_heal.sql:68-70 has the same incomplete DELETE. analytics-service/services/equity_reconstruction.py:1037 gate is `status='done'` only — currently correct but undocumented as an invariant.
- **Fix**: Add `OR status = 'failed_final'` to BOTH 078 and 079 STEP 2 — kills clearly-terminal failure rows so the audit trail tells a clean before/after story. Add RAISE NOTICE 'deleted N done + M failed_final rows' for observability. Document in equity_reconstruction.py module docstring that the gate is intentionally `status='done'` only and must NOT be widened without re-auditing healing migrations.

#### G17-069 · Systemic pattern — direct INSERT into compute_jobs in healing migrations bypasses every enqueue invariant, sets precedent for future drift · _new_ · refs: data-migration-5, code-reviewer-5
- **File**: `supabase/migrations/20260424012820_equity_contract_size_healing.sql:84`
- **Specialist**: `red-team` (confidence 8)
- **Summary**: SYSTEMIC: 078 and 079 BOTH do `INSERT INTO compute_jobs (kind, api_key_id, exchange) SELECT ... FROM api_keys` directly. The codebase has a SECURITY DEFINER RPC `enqueue_compute_job` (scoring_weight_overrides + 075) that emits structured logs, performs XOR-validation of target fields, and audit-logs the enqueue event. Every other enqueue path in the system uses it. The healing pattern bypasses that contract WITHOUT explanation. The convention drift means: (a) audit trail loses the 'compute_job.enqueued' breadcrumb for healing jobs, (b) future schema additions to compute_jobs that add NOT NULL columns to the table (with defaults) work but lose any default-routing logic the RPC encodes, (c) the pattern teaches future contributors that 'just INSERT into compute_jobs' is OK — encouraging more bypasses. Both 078 and 079 are immutable migrations; the next heal (will there be one? probabilistically yes given 4-PR chain) will copy the pattern.
- **Evidence**: supabase/migrations/20260424012820_equity_contract_size_healing.sql:84 + 079:78 — direct INSERT. supabase/migrations/20260422101911_api_keys_disconnected_at.sql:204 uses `PERFORM enqueue_compute_job(...)` in the cron RPC.
- **Fix**: For the NEXT healing migration: use `PERFORM public.enqueue_compute_job(p_strategy_id := NULL, p_kind := 'reconstruct_allocator_history', p_api_key_id := k.id, p_idempotency_key := 'heal-080-' || k.id::text)`. Add a project convention doc (AGENTS.md addendum) banning direct INSERT INTO compute_jobs outside of the RPC. Add a SECURITY DEFINER helper `enqueue_reconstruct_for_all_eligible(p_idempotency_prefix TEXT)` so future heals call ONE function and inherit the worker-dispatch filter byte-for-byte.

### LOW (4)

#### G17-070 · _purge_allocator_equity_snapshots returns len(data) which may not reflect actual deletes on minimal returning
- **File**: `analytics-service/services/equity_reconstruction.py:1005`
- **Specialist**: `code-reviewer` (confidence 9)
- **Summary**: _purge_allocator_equity_snapshots reads `len(getattr(res, 'data', None) or [])` to surface the deletion count for audit log (`stale_snapshots_purged`). Supabase-py's delete() defaults to returning='representation' so res.data is populated, but the contract is the same fragile one as persist_equity_snapshots — if a future call site or version reduces to return=minimal, the audit count silently becomes 0 even when rows were wiped, hiding the wipe in the trail.
- **Evidence**: analytics-service/services/equity_reconstruction.py:997-1007 — `supabase.table(...).delete().eq(...).execute()` with no explicit returning parameter; relies on supabase-py default.
- **Fix**: Use `count='exact'` on the delete call and read `res.count` for the audit log, OR explicitly assert returning='representation' in the call so the contract is documented locally.

#### G17-071 · persist_equity_snapshots round-trips full upsert payload only to count rows
- **File**: `analytics-service/services/equity_reconstruction.py:924`
- **Specialist**: `performance` (confidence 9)
- **Summary**: The v0.15.3.3 fix replaced `return len(stamped)` with `return len(getattr(res, 'data', None) or [])` so the audit log reports the count Postgres actually wrote. But supabase-py's default `Prefer: return=representation` makes PostgREST send the full inserted-row representation back over the wire (each row including the JSONB breakdown) only for the function to discard it and return `len(...)`. For a 730-day full backfill that's up to 730 × ~150B = ~110KB per reconstruct of network + JSON-decode overhead per allocator. Migration 078 batch-enqueues a reconstruct for every connected api_key on deploy, so the over-fetch fan-outs once per key. Same pattern applies in `_purge_allocator_equity_snapshots` (line 1005): it issues `.delete().eq(...).execute()` and reads `len(res.data)` for the audit `stale_snapshots_purged` count, materialising every deleted row back to the worker.
- **Evidence**: analytics-service/services/equity_reconstruction.py:910-925,997-1007
- **Fix**: Switch both call sites to PostgREST's `count='exact'` + `returning='minimal'`: `supabase.table('allocator_equity_snapshots').upsert(stamped, on_conflict='allocator_id,asof', ignore_duplicates=True, count='exact').execute()` (then `int(getattr(res, 'count', None) or 0)`), and `.delete(count='exact').eq('allocator_id', X).execute()`. Audit-log semantics are preserved (real Postgres-write count, not `len(stamped)`) without paying for the row payload round-trip.

#### G17-072 · _cap_breakdown runs json.dumps for every row on every reconstruct even on tiny dicts
- **File**: `analytics-service/services/equity_reconstruction.py:219`
- **Specialist**: `performance` (confidence 9)
- **Summary**: `_cap_breakdown` unconditionally serialises the breakdown dict with `json.dumps(breakdown, default=str)` to measure its encoded byte length, then only enters the top-N truncation branch when the encoded length exceeds `RAW_PAYLOAD_CAP_BYTES`. The function is called once per output row in `_compute_daily_equity` (line 855) — i.e. up to 730 times per reconstruct — and once per refresh-job snapshot (line 1499), and once per anchor-adjusted row (line 1212). The cap-check dominant case is 1-3 symbols (USDT + one perp + maybe one spot) where the encoded length can never exceed the cap; `json.dumps` is still executed every time. For 730 rows the cumulative json.dumps cost is non-trivial on the equity-reconstruct hot path that migration 078 will fan-out across every connected api_key on deploy.
- **Evidence**: analytics-service/services/equity_reconstruction.py:219-229,855,1212,1499
- **Fix**: Short-circuit on cardinality before serialising: `if len(breakdown) <= 20: return breakdown`. The truncation branch only ever fires when there are MORE than the 20-symbol cap, so small breakdowns can skip the json.dumps entirely. Preserves identical output semantics on the cap path.

#### G17-073 · Systemic pattern — 4 stacked V-shape fixes in <1 week indicate symptom-chasing over root cause across the analytics worker · _new_ · refs: code-reviewer-11, data-migration-15, pr-test-analyzer-6, silent-failure-hunter-3
- **File**: `analytics-service/services/equity_reconstruction.py:1`
- **Specialist**: `red-team` (confidence 9)
- **Summary**: SYSTEMIC: this batch's PR #67 → #68 → #69 → #70 ships 4 'fix the equity curve' patches in 48 hours (2026-04-22 to 2026-04-24), each layering on the prior. v0.15.4.0's own CHANGELOG admits: 'The previous four fixes (v0.15.3.1 – v0.15.3.4) all targeted "stale rows block fresh reconstruct" — but the *fresh* reconstruct was producing garbage too.' Then v0.15.4.2 (migration 079) further admits v0.15.4.0's fix was insufficient. The diff trail is 6 fixes for one bug. The pattern points to a missing FOUNDATIONAL test: there is no end-to-end equity-replay regression that consumes real OKX trade payloads (with venue+instType+ctVal metadata) and asserts the final value_usd against an externally-computed ground truth. Each layer in the chain (PR #67 cascade, #68 sole-source purge, #69 disconnected exclusion, #70 cost/price, #71 ctVal table) is unit-tested IN ISOLATION — there is no test that simulates the 'fresh user uploads OKX perp key for the first time, reconstruct runs, dashboard shows correct curve' user story end-to-end with the realistic ccxt response shape. Until that test exists, the next quirk (FUTURES, inverse, Bybit V5, OKX new listing) will produce a 7th patch in the same shape.
- **Evidence**: CHANGELOG.md PR #70 entry ('previous four fixes ... were chasing a downstream symptom'). Migration 079 docstring: 'v0.15.4.0 fix relied on ccxt's safe_trade ... which only fires when the market resolved inside safe_market carries a non-None contractSize. On production that path silently failed and cost = amount × price collapsed to cost/price = amount = raw CONTRACT COUNT'. 6 PRs (#67-#71 + later 079) for one bug class.
- **Fix**: Build a `tests/integration/test_equity_replay_real_okx_perps.py` that:   1. Loads a cassette of REAL OKX fills-history payloads (sanitized) including SPOT, SWAP (linear), FUTURES (linear), and inverse SWAP cases   2. Runs the full reconstruct + persist pipeline against a fake supabase   3. Asserts final value_usd within $1 of an externally-computed ground truth (computed via independent script using exchange.fetch_balance equivalent)   4. Parametrize over (venue, instType, ctVal, position_direction) combinations Until this test exists, the audit-trail will keep accumulating heal migrations.

## G18 — PRs #73-#76 — Big-fix-A + V1 dashboard retire + dashboard-parity PR1 + bridge empty-state

### CRITICAL (5)

#### G18-001 · AllocationsTabs loadUiV2Flag swallows localStorage error and silently rolls back V2
- **File**: `src/app/(dashboard)/allocations/AllocationsTabs.tsx:119`
- **Specialist**: `silent-failure-hunter` (confidence 10)
- **Summary**: `loadUiV2Flag` returns `true` on any localStorage failure. The comment claims this is safe, but: (a) if a user has set 'allocations.ui_v2=false' as a rollback escape hatch and their localStorage read fails (private mode, quota, security policy), they get V2 anyway — defeating the rollback. (b) Conversely, if a user expected V1 and ends up on V2 unexpectedly, they have no explanation. The default-to-true is documented as deliberate for SSR, but the catch in the post-hydration effect at line 241 (`if (loadUiV2Flag() === false) setUiV2Flag(false)`) is the actually-runtime version and IT ALSO swallows the failure with no telemetry. A storage failure is a state we should know about.
- **Evidence**: src/app/(dashboard)/allocations/AllocationsTabs.tsx:119-127, 235-243
- **Fix**: Add `logError(err, 'AllocationsTabs.loadUiV2Flag_failed')` inside the catch. The default-true behavior can stay; we just need to know when it happened so a P1 'V1 users seeing V2' issue is debuggable.

#### G18-002 · loadV2Config empty catch on corrupt JSON silently resets user's dashboard
- **File**: `src/app/(dashboard)/allocations/hooks/useDashboardConfig.ts:312`
- **Specialist**: `silent-failure-hunter` (confidence 10)
- **Summary**: `loadV2Config` wraps localStorage read + JSON.parse in `try { ... } catch { /* Corrupted JSON — fall through to defaults. */ }` with an empty catch. When a user's persisted dashboard config is corrupt (truncated quota write, sync conflict from another tab, hand-edit, or schema drift), the user's entire customized layout is silently discarded and replaced with v4 defaults. No log, no Sentry, no UI banner — the user just opens the dashboard and their picker tiles + resize choices are gone with no explanation. This is the single most painful silent failure in the batch: it actively destroys user state without trace. Combined with the persist effect (line 351) that immediately overwrites the corrupt blob with the default, recovery is impossible.
- **Evidence**: src/app/(dashboard)/allocations/hooks/useDashboardConfig.ts:291-316
- **Fix**: Replace empty catch with `logError(err, 'useDashboardConfigV2.load.parse_failed', { rawLength: raw?.length })` (Sentry trail) AND set a sessionStorage flag `dashboard.config.recoveredFromCorruption=true` that AllocationDashboardV2 reads to render a one-time toast: 'We could not read your saved dashboard layout — restored to defaults. If this repeats, please contact support.' Optionally back up the corrupt blob to `quantalyze-dashboard-config.backup` before overwriting so a support agent can recover.

#### G18-003 · loadLegacyConfig empty catch (same corruption-destroys-state bug for legacy hook)
- **File**: `src/app/(dashboard)/allocations/hooks/useDashboardConfig.ts:93`
- **Specialist**: `silent-failure-hunter` (confidence 10)
- **Summary**: `loadLegacyConfig` has the identical empty-catch corruption-eating pattern as the V2 hook: `try { ... } catch { /* Corrupted data — fall back to defaults. */ }`. The legacy hook is documented as 'dormant' but the persist effect at line 149 (legacy) and the load function still run on mount via `useState(loadLegacyConfig)`. Any user who still loads through a legacy code path eats the same silent destruction.
- **Evidence**: src/app/(dashboard)/allocations/hooks/useDashboardConfig.ts:82-97
- **Fix**: Apply the same fix as the V2 hook — `logError` with operation context, sessionStorage flag, optional backup write. If the hook is truly dormant, remove it entirely rather than leaving a landmine.

#### G18-004 · persistV2 swallows localStorage write failures silently (data-loss without trace)
- **File**: `src/app/(dashboard)/allocations/hooks/useDashboardConfig.ts:321`
- **Specialist**: `silent-failure-hunter` (confidence 10)
- **Summary**: `persistV2` wraps `localStorage.setItem` in `try { ... } catch { /* Silent — private-mode / quota-exceeded are non-fatal. */ }`. A user in private mode, with full quota, or with a sync conflict from another tab will see their picker tiles + resize choices APPEAR TO WORK in-memory but never persist. Next page navigation reverts everything with no warning. Quota exceeded is also a real production hazard with large widget layouts. Categorizing this as 'non-fatal' is a UX call masquerading as an error-handling decision: the user EXPECTS their changes to persist when they click 'Add widget'. We're hiding the fact that we silently dropped the write.
- **Evidence**: src/app/(dashboard)/allocations/hooks/useDashboardConfig.ts:318-324
- **Fix**: Distinguish quota-exceeded (DOMException name='QuotaExceededError') from private-mode (no localStorage); for the former, fire a toast 'Your dashboard layout could not be saved — please remove an existing widget'. Add `logError(err, 'useDashboardConfigV2.persist_failed', { tileCount: config.tiles.length, configSize: JSON.stringify(config).length })` so Sentry sees these. Return a boolean from persistV2 so the hook can surface state in addWidget/resizeWidget callers.

#### G18-005 · persistLegacy localStorage failure swallowed (legacy hook same pattern)
- **File**: `src/app/(dashboard)/allocations/hooks/useDashboardConfig.ts:102`

### HIGH (36)

#### G18-006 · Big-fix-A weight column unsigned-format contract is untested — formatPercent contract test only catches local re-declarations, not signed-flag drift
- **File**: `src/__tests__/format-percent-contract.test.ts:51`

The contract test at format-percent-contract.test.ts is an AST scan that fails if ANY file outside lib/utils.ts redeclares formatPercent — that's good for one regression class. But it does NOT catch a regression where a future contributor strips `{ signed: false }` from a Weight cell in HoldingsTable / HoldingDetail / MandateSnapshotWidget / mandate-gates.ts — every weight cell would silently start rendering '+18.50%' instead of '18.50%'. The contract test also does NOT verify that the rendered HoldingsTable/HoldingDetail actually emit unsigned weights.
