Plus HoldingDetail equivalent. This pins the signed-flag contract at the call site without depending on the AST contract.

#### G18-007 · AllocationDashboardV2 renderWidget useCallback depends on `props` — every widget re-renders on any payload change
- **File**: `src/app/(dashboard)/allocations/AllocationDashboardV2.tsx:229`
- **Specialist**: `performance` (confidence 9)
- **Summary**: `renderWidget` is wrapped in useCallback with `[props, config.timeframe]` deps, but `props` is the ENTIRE MyAllocationDashboardPayload object — its reference flips on every Server Component re-render, every 30s router.refresh, and on every parent re-render that doesn't memoize. Combined with the inline `<Component data={props as any} ... />` rendering, EVERY widget tree re-renders unconditionally. Since widgets like HoldingsTableWidget, MandateSnapshotWidget, AllocationByStyleWidget, KpiStripWidget pull from the same payload, ALL of them re-render in lockstep, defeating the purpose of dynamic chunk splitting. There's no React.memo on the lazy widget barrel either.
- **Evidence**: src/app/(dashboard)/allocations/AllocationDashboardV2.tsx:229-259
- **Fix**: Either (a) split `props` into the specific fields each widget consumes and pass those as stable props through a useMemo of {analytics, strategies, holdingsSummary, ...} or (b) wrap each WIDGET_COMPONENT in React.memo with a custom comparator that compares only the fields each widget reads. The cheap fix: stabilize the widget data object via useMemo with the actual primitive deps the widgets need, instead of `data={props as any}`.

#### G18-009 · AllocationDashboardV2 IntersectionObserver effect runs once and is bypassed entirely when first render is empty-state · _new_ · refs: silent-failure-hunter:#26
- **File**: `src/app/(dashboard)/allocations/AllocationDashboardV2.tsx:188`
- **Specialist**: `red-team` (confidence 9)
- **Summary**: The widget_viewed analytics IntersectionObserver useEffect has empty deps `[]` (line 188) and runs once on mount. The early-return at line 263 (`holdingsEmpty && !hasSyncing → <EmptyState />`) returns BEFORE the inner `<div ref={dashboardContainerRef}>` is rendered. When the first paint is the empty-state path, `dashboardContainerRef.current` is null AND the effect's early-return at line 154 (`if (!root) return;`) bails out. Subsequent renders that flip holdingsEmpty=false (e.g. after a 30s router.refresh once sync completes) cause the inner div to mount BUT the useEffect has already run (empty deps) and will not re-fire. The MutationObserver is also never attached. Result: a user who lands on /allocations with zero holdings and then syncs gets ZERO widget_viewed analytics for the entire session, silently breaking the funnel that PR1 specifically wired in. Same effect's MutationObserver-for-picker-tiles path is broken in the same way.
- **Evidence**: src/app/(dashboard)/allocations/AllocationDashboardV2.tsx:151-188 (useEffect with [] deps) + 263-269 (early-return before ref div mounts)
- **Fix**: Add `holdingsEmpty, hasSyncing` to the useEffect deps (or use a ref + sentinel). Better: hoist the observer attachment behind a `useEffect(() => { ... }, [holdingsEmpty, hasSyncing])` so it re-runs when the dashboard transitions from empty → populated. Same fix unblocks the picker-tile MutationObserver path. Add a guard that throws-once if `dashboardContainerRef.current` is null when the dashboard has rendered (data-integrity assertion).

#### G18-010 · AllocationDashboardV2 unconditionally mounts InsightStrip + AlertBanner before WidgetGrid — empty mandate/empty insights creates layout flash · _new_ · refs: silent-failure-hunter:#14

#### G18-011 · renderWidget falls back to 'Unknown widget' placeholder with no telemetry

#### G18-012 · AllocationDashboardV2 holdingsEmpty short-circuit conflates real-empty with payload failure
- **File**: `src/app/(dashboard)/allocations/AllocationDashboardV2.tsx:263`

The page.tsx loader awaits getMyAllocationDashboard which can return a partial payload (e.g. holdingsSummary missing on the empty-portfolio branch at queries.ts:1026). If the upstream query throws a recoverable error and returns the empty branch, the dashboard renders 'Connect an exchange' empty-state even though the user has holdings — they just couldn't be fetched this load. The hasSyncing escape hatch doesn't help: if the network failed, hasSyncing is also false. There's no observable indicator of the difference.

#### G18-013 · Widget chip → AllocationDashboardV2 picker race (microtask after async router.replace)
- **File**: `src/app/(dashboard)/allocations/AllocationsTabs.tsx:449`
- **Specialist**: `code-reviewer` (confidence 8)
- **Summary**: From a non-Overview tab the Widget chip calls changeTab('overview') (router.replace) and then queueMicrotask(dispatch) to fire 'allocations:open-widget-picker'. AllocationDashboardV2 only mounts after the tab becomes Overview, and the listener for that event only attaches after the mount-commit useEffect. router.replace in Next.js 16 starts an async transition — the URL change → re-render → mount is NOT guaranteed to complete inside a single microtask. The microtask flushes before the dashboard mounts, the dispatch is dropped, and the picker never opens. The inline comment claims 'one microtask is sufficient' but this depends on synchronous router behavior the App Router does not promise.
- **Evidence**: AllocationsTabs.tsx:437-450 — `const wasAlreadyOnOverview = activeTab === 'overview'; changeTab('overview'); ... if (wasAlreadyOnOverview) { dispatch(); } else { queueMicrotask(dispatch); }`. AllocationDashboardV2.tsx:86-92 registers the 'allocations:open-widget-picker' listener in useEffect (runs after mount commit, after the URL transition flushes).
- **Fix**: Replace queueMicrotask with a deterministic ready signal: (a) hoist pickerOpen state into AllocationsTabs and pass it as a prop to AllocationDashboardV2 (no event bus, no race); (b) keep the event bus but have AllocationDashboardV2 read a pending-open sentinel (sessionStorage / context) on mount and trigger setPickerOpen(true) from useEffect; (c) retry the dispatch on rAF with a short fallback timeout. Option (a) is the simplest — removes the latent race and the event bus entirely.

#### G18-014 · PR3 tab count badges ('Holdings 8', 'Outcomes 4') in AllocationsTabs have no test coverage
- **File**: `src/app/(dashboard)/allocations/AllocationsTabs.tsx:311`

Logic at AllocationsTabs.tsx:315-320 reads `props.holdingsSummary?.length` and `props.outcomes?.length`, builds tabCount map, then renders the chip only when count > 0. None of this is tested — grep `tabCount|holdingsCount|outcomesCount` finds only the production file. #### G18-015 · PR3 dashboard parity: V2 dashboard has NO rollback path — only Scenario tab has the V1/V2 flag · _new_
- **File**: `src/app/(dashboard)/allocations/AllocationsTabs.tsx:549`
- **Specialist**: `red-team` (confidence 8)
- **Summary**: The `isUiV2` flag is read at line 234, but its only consumer is the SCENARIO panel (line 549-564) where it picks between ScenarioComposer and ScenarioStub. The Overview body (AllocationDashboardV2) is rendered unconditionally at line 509 — there is NO flag-driven branch for the V1 vs V2 dashboard. The PR3 description retired the V1 dashboard and removed the V1 file (AllocationDashboard.tsx is gone from main per `ls`), so even if a user sets `allocations.ui_v2=false` in localStorage as a rollback, they STILL see the V2 dashboard on Overview. The localStorage flag is misnamed (it controls Scenario, not the broader UI) and the comment at line 111 calling it the 'allocations.ui_v2 flag handler' for general rollback is misleading. If V2 dashboard breaks, allocators cannot escape — they must wait for a hotfix.
- **Evidence**: AllocationsTabs.tsx:111-128 (loadUiV2Flag) + 234 (isUiV2) + 509 (unconditional V2 mount) + 549-564 (isUiV2 only used on scenario)
- **Fix**: Either (a) rename the flag to `allocations.scenario_v2` so its scope is honest; or (b) add a V1 minimum-viable dashboard the `isUiV2=false` path renders (an EmptyState with a 'V2 rollback in progress, see runbook' banner is acceptable). The current state silently misadvertises a rollback escape hatch that doesn't exist for the largest surface (Overview).

#### G18-016 · AllocationsTabs Widget chip queueMicrotask race is unrecoverable when AllocationDashboardV2 useEffect listener attaches AFTER commit · _chain_ · refs: code-reviewer:#1, silent-failure-hunter:#15
- **File**: `src/app/(dashboard)/allocations/AllocationsTabs.tsx:449`
- **Specialist**: `red-team` (confidence 8)
- **Summary**: Chain with code-reviewer #1. Verified that AllocationDashboardV2 is imported as a direct module (not next/dynamic), but `useEffect(() => { window.addEventListener(...) }, [])` (line 86-92 of AllocationDashboardV2.tsx) runs AFTER React's commit phase, not in the microtask queue. The Widget chip's `queueMicrotask(dispatch)` dispatches BEFORE React.useEffect runs. Even with the synchronous router.replace + commit flush, React's effect phase is scheduled via the rendering pipeline (microtask + paint + post-paint). Browser micro/macrotask interleaving with React 19's concurrent rendering means the dispatch happens before listener registration in ~all cases except when the user is already on Overview (the `wasAlreadyOnOverview` path correctly fires synchronously). The fallback retry on a 100ms setTimeout would partially mitigate but the current code has NO retry. Combined with no error log (silent-failure-hunter #15), a user clicking Widget from Holdings/Mandate/Risk gets a tab change with NO picker opening, no error, no explanation. The comment at line 436 ('one microtask is sufficient') is wrong.
- **Evidence**: AllocationsTabs.tsx:419-451 + AllocationDashboardV2.tsx:86-92
- **Fix**: Lift `pickerOpen` state into AllocationsTabs and pass it as a prop to AllocationDashboardV2. Remove the CustomEvent bridge entirely. Alternative: store a pending-open sentinel in sessionStorage that AllocationDashboardV2 reads on mount (`useEffect(() => { if (sessionStorage.getItem('pendingPickerOpen') === '1') { sessionStorage.removeItem('pendingPickerOpen'); setPickerOpen(true); } }, [])`). Either fix removes the timing race.

#### G18-017 · Custom event bridge dispatches widget-picker open even when listener mounting may have failed
- **File**: `src/app/(dashboard)/allocations/AllocationsTabs.tsx:439`
- **Specialist**: `silent-failure-hunter` (confidence 7)
- **Summary**: The Widget chip click handler uses queueMicrotask to dispatch 'allocations:open-widget-picker' AFTER changeTab routes to Overview. The comment acknowledges the AllocationDashboardV2 listener may not yet exist if AllocationDashboardV2 hasn't hydrated. queueMicrotask is best-effort: if AllocationDashboardV2 throws during mount, the listener never registers and the event dispatch is dropped silently. The user clicks Widget, sees the tab change happen, and... nothing else. There's no fallback or retry, no telemetry on dropped events.
- **Evidence**: src/app/(dashboard)/allocations/AllocationsTabs.tsx:419-451
- **Fix**: Replace the event bridge with a lifted-state pattern (pickerOpen in TweaksProvider context or AllocationsTabs state passed as a prop). Event-based cross-component coordination is a known anti-pattern when the listener can be conditionally mounted. If the event approach must stay, log a dispatch-result via PostHog and have a 100ms retry.

#### G18-018 · BridgeWidget empty-state CTA hard-reloads inside same-route navigation, drops drawer + picker + tweaks state · _chain_ · refs: code-reviewer:#2
- **File**: `src/app/(dashboard)/allocations/components/BridgeWidget.tsx:156`
- **Specialist**: `red-team` (confidence 8)
- **Summary**: Chain with code-reviewer #2 — verified live. Worse than the specialist noted: when the BridgeWidget is rendered as the BridgeHero tile inside AllocationDashboardV2 on the Overview tab, the empty-state `<a href='/allocations?tab=outcomes'>` triggers a FULL document reload to the SAME pathname `/allocations` with just a query param flip. The reload destroys: (a) the dashboard's persisted widget-picker state, (b) ALL Tweaks panel state (TweaksProvider mounted at AllocationsTabs root), (c) the user's scroll position, (d) any in-flight ScenarioComposer drafts, (e) IntersectionObserver widget_viewed analytics events for this session (the firedRef resets). Plus a network round-trip for a same-route nav. The InsightStrip at the same level uses next/link properly (`<Link href='/allocations?tab=scenario'>`), so this is anomalous within the SAME render tree.
- **Evidence**: BridgeWidget.tsx:156-161 (raw <a>) + InsightStrip.tsx:118 (sibling Link) + same dashboard tree
- **Fix**: Replace `<a href='/allocations?tab=outcomes'>` with `<Link href='/allocations?tab=outcomes'>` AND prefer accepting an `onViewOutcomes` callback prop so BridgeHeroWidget can fire `router.replace('/allocations?tab=outcomes', { scroll: false })` — matching the tab-chip routing idiom. The simplest fix is the Link swap; the callback path is the principled fix.

#### G18-019 · BridgeWidget empty state ambiguous: 'All clear' shown for missing flaggedHoldings vs genuinely-empty
- **File**: `src/app/(dashboard)/allocations/components/BridgeWidget.tsx:89`
- **Specialist**: `silent-failure-hunter` (confidence 9)
- **Summary**: `BridgeWidget` displays 'All clear · Your allocations are within mandate' whenever `flaggedHoldings.length === 0`. The data flows in from `BridgeHeroWidget.tsx:56-57` where flaggedHoldings is read with `?? []` and matchDecisionsByHoldingRef with `?? {}`. If the dashboard payload silently fails (network blip, an upstream `__error` only handled by OutcomesWidget but not Bridge), the user sees 'All clear' — the most reassuring possible message — when in reality we don't know the state of their portfolio. This is the canonical 'fallback empty-state confused with real-empty' bug for a SAFETY-RELEVANT widget. An allocator deciding not to rebalance because Bridge says 'All clear' has been silently misinformed.
- **Evidence**: src/app/(dashboard)/allocations/widgets/bridge/BridgeHeroWidget.tsx:55-72, src/app/(dashboard)/allocations/components/BridgeWidget.tsx:89-164
- **Fix**: BridgeHeroWidget already checks `__error` on `data` (line 30); extend that signal upstream so any partial-load on the dashboard payload (e.g. flaggedHoldings undefined because the query threw) marks `payload.flaggedHoldings = null` (not `[]`), then BridgeWidget needs `flaggedHoldings === null → render 'Bridge status unavailable, retry' state` vs `flaggedHoldings.length === 0 → 'All clear'`. Critically, never collapse 'unknown' and 'safe' into the same UI for risk-relevant widgets.

#### G18-020 · HoldingDetail notes fetch failure conflated with 404 — silently degrades into edit mode
- **File**: `src/app/(dashboard)/allocations/components/HoldingDetail.tsx:105`
- **Specialist**: `silent-failure-hunter` (confidence 9)
- **Summary**: The note-load effect catches ALL exceptions from fetch + json parse and silently transitions to edit mode: `} catch { if (!cancelled) setNoteEditing(true); }`. The else branch at line 102 ALSO catches non-OK responses (anything that isn't `res.ok`) into the same 'start in edit mode' path. This means: (a) auth/RLS failures (401/403), (b) server errors (500), (c) network drops, and (d) actual 'no note exists' (404) all funnel into the SAME 'show empty textarea' UX. A user with a saved note may see an empty editor, type a new note, and on save trigger a silent overwrite — or worse, see the apparent absence of their note as data loss. The user has zero way to distinguish 'no note recorded yet' from 'we cannot reach the notes API'.
- **Evidence**: src/app/(dashboard)/allocations/components/HoldingDetail.tsx:79-114
- **Fix**: Discriminate on res.status: 404 → empty state (edit mode), 401/403 → 'You don\'t have access to notes' error chrome, 5xx + network → 'Notes are temporarily unavailable, try again' with retry button. Catch block should `logError(err, 'HoldingDetail.note_fetch_failed', { scopeRef })`. Never auto-route a transport failure into the same UI as legitimately-empty content — that's the textbook 'real-empty vs fallback-empty' confusion.

#### G18-021 · HoldingsTable BridgeOutcomeBanner dismissal swallows banner state on router.refresh failure
- **File**: `src/app/(dashboard)/allocations/components/HoldingsTable.tsx:586`
- **Specialist**: `silent-failure-hunter` (confidence 8)
- **Summary**: The HoldingsTable design mode renders BridgeOutcomeBanner with onDismiss firing `router.refresh()`. The banner's actual dismissal is server-side (POST decided before onDismiss fires), but if router.refresh() throws (auth failure, network blip), the banner never unmounts, the server thinks the decision is recorded, and the user sees a 'dismissed' banner still on screen with no feedback that anything is wrong. The comment correctly notes: 'Without this the banner re-renders from the memoized prop and the user sees no feedback until full page reload.' But the fix relies on router.refresh succeeding — if it fails, the same confusion returns.
- **Evidence**: src/app/(dashboard)/allocations/components/HoldingsTable.tsx:577-588
- **Fix**: Wrap `router.refresh()` in a try/catch and on failure call setExpandedRowId(null) AND surface a toast 'Dismissed. Refresh to see updated list.' Add logError telemetry on router.refresh failure.

#### G18-022 · HoldingsTableProps is a mode-switched union (legacy/new) without a discriminant — fields silently overlap
- **File**: `src/app/(dashboard)/allocations/components/HoldingsTable.tsx:127`
- **Specialist**: `type-design-analyzer` (confidence 9)
- **Summary**: HoldingsTableProps fuses two distinct call shapes (legacy Phase 08 mode vs new Plan 08 design mode) into one optional-everywhere interface. The component dispatches on `props.rows ? Design : Legacy` (L150-170). Nothing prevents a caller from passing both `holdings` AND `rows`, both `notesByHoldingScopeRef` AND `flaggedHoldingsByRef`, or `rows: []` (truthy empty array — silently routes to Design path that renders a table with no data instead of legacy with empty state). The legacy/design split is exactly what TS discriminated unions exist to express.
- **Evidence**: src/app/(dashboard)/allocations/components/HoldingsTable.tsx:127-170
- **Fix**: Convert to discriminated union: `type HoldingsTableProps = { mode: 'legacy'; holdings: HoldingRow[]; ...legacyFields } | { mode: 'design'; rows: DesignHoldingRow[]; ...designFields }`. Callers must pick a mode explicitly; the compiler then refuses to mix fields. If the long-term plan is to retire legacy mode, mark `mode: 'legacy'` as @deprecated.

#### G18-023 · WidgetGrid resize handler provides ZERO live visual feedback — width updates only at pointerup · _new_ · refs: performance:#8
- **File**: `src/app/(dashboard)/allocations/components/WidgetGrid.tsx:150`
- **Specialist**: `red-team` (confidence 8)
- **Summary**: The `move` handler at lines 150-158 only writes `handleEl.dataset.pendingW = String(target)` — it never calls onResize during drag. The cell stays at startW for the entire drag duration. The user drags 200px right, sees no preview, releases, and the widget SNAPS to the new column count. No ghost overlay, no preview line, no live-snap. Users dragging incrementally have no way to know whether they've crossed the snap threshold for w=3 vs w=4. Combined with the per-render bug (a 4-column animation in a 4-column grid means the snap is jarring), the resize UX is broken. The designer source referenced at line 126 explicitly shows live snap with a per-frame preview. This is a regression vs the prototype that no test catches.
- **Evidence**: WidgetGrid.tsx:130-180 (handleResizePointerDown) — no setState or callback during move
- **Fix**: During `move`, set local pending-w state via setState (or write to a CSS variable on handleEl) so the rendered grid-column-span visibly previews the resize target. The current data-pendingW dataset write happens but no consumer reads it during drag. Wire a `data-pending-w={String(target)}` on the widget-cell AND a CSS rule that visually narrows/widens the cell during drag (with `grid-column: span var(--pending-w)` or a similar approach).

#### G18-024 · WidgetGrid drop handler uses ?? fallback to closure state — silent no-op on missing dataTransfer
- **File**: `src/app/(dashboard)/allocations/components/WidgetGrid.tsx:217`
- **Specialist**: `silent-failure-hunter` (confidence 8)
- **Summary**: `const fromTransfer = e.dataTransfer?.getData?.('text/plain') ?? ''; const fromK = fromTransfer || draggingK; if (fromK && fromK !== k) onMove(fromK, k);` — when both dataTransfer and draggingK are falsy (e.g. cross-frame drag, synthetic event, browser security restriction), the drop is silently dropped. The user sees the drop animation complete with no resulting move and no feedback. No telemetry.
- **Evidence**: src/app/(dashboard)/allocations/components/WidgetGrid.tsx:208-222
- **Fix**: When fromK is empty after the fallback, log `logError(new Error('WidgetGrid drop: no source key'), 'WidgetGrid.drop_no_source')` so we know how often this happens. Surface a brief visual cue (e.g., shake the source cell) to tell the user the move didn't take.

#### G18-025 · WidgetStateProps mode discriminator is decoupled from its variant payload
- **File**: `src/app/(dashboard)/allocations/components/WidgetState.tsx:44`
- **Specialist**: `type-design-analyzer` (confidence 9)
- **Summary**: WidgetStateProps has `mode: WidgetStateMode` plus four independently-optional payloads (`partial`, `error`, `empty`, `children`). Nothing in the type forbids `<WidgetState mode='error' empty={{title:'foo'}} />` (mode+payload mismatch — empty is ignored, error?.message falls back to 'Something went wrong'). Conversely `<WidgetState mode='error' />` silently renders fallback copy when the call site forgot the error prop. The component-internal `props.empty?.title` / `props.error?.message ?? 'Something went wrong'` (L67-90, L113-135) all use optional chaining because the type can't promise the right payload is present.
- **Evidence**: src/app/(dashboard)/allocations/components/WidgetState.tsx:42-55
- **Fix**: Make WidgetStateProps a discriminated union: `type WidgetStateProps = { mode: 'loading' } | { mode: 'empty'; empty: {...} } | { mode: 'partial'; partial: {...} } | { mode: 'error'; error: {...} } | { mode: 'success'; children: ReactNode }`. The renderer then narrows once on `props.mode` and TS guarantees the matching payload is present — removes every `?.` and the silent 'Something went wrong' fallback.

#### G18-026 · useDashboardConfigV2 hasMutated.current sets to true on first effect run, then any subsequent layoutVersion bump silently wipes mutations · _chain_ · refs: silent-failure-hunter:#1
- **File**: `src/app/(dashboard)/allocations/hooks/useDashboardConfig.ts:352`
- **Specialist**: `red-team` (confidence 7)
- **Summary**: The first-mount persist guard (lines 345-351) flips hasMutated.current → true on the first effect run. This works for the initial 'observe-without-write' goal. But: in a future LAYOUT_VERSION bump scenario, the load path resets to defaults at line 296-298 INSIDE loadV2Config. setState fires (via the useState lazy initializer), the first effect runs and writes the reset-to-defaults blob to localStorage. The user's ENTIRE previous layout (their picker tiles, resize choices) is OVERWRITTEN with v(LAYOUT_VERSION)-defaults on first mount post-bump — silently, no banner, no Sentry event. The Voice-D8 'reset on mismatch precedent' is documented but the consequence (silent layout destruction) is not communicated to the user. A user who personalized 6 tiles over 3 months sees them all gone on next visit after a release.
- **Evidence**: useDashboardConfig.ts:287-316 (loadV2Config reset) + 345-352 (first persist always writes loaded state) + 296-298 (layoutVersion mismatch → defaults)
- **Fix**: Inside loadV2Config when layoutVersion !== LAYOUT_VERSION: (a) backup the corrupt blob to `quantalyze-dashboard-config.preReset.<oldVersion>` in localStorage so a support agent can recover; (b) set sessionStorage flag `dashboard.layout.reset_from_version=<oldVersion>` so AllocationDashboardV2 surfaces a one-time toast on mount; (c) emit a usage event `dashboard_layout_reset` with from/to versions. Chain with silent-failure-hunter:#1 — the same anti-pattern (silent reset) is the documented v0.15.7.0 path.

#### G18-027 · useDashboardConfigV2 moveWidget silently no-ops when 'from' or 'to' tile not found
- **File**: `src/app/(dashboard)/allocations/hooks/useDashboardConfig.ts:389`
- **Specialist**: `silent-failure-hunter` (confidence 8)
- **Summary**: `moveWidget` does `if (fromIdx < 0 || toIdx < 0) return prev;` — a perfectly silent no-op when the keyboard-reorder or DnD passes a key not in tiles. AllocationDashboardV2's onMoveWrapper relies on this code to resolve sentinels, and any mismatch (race after a removal, a stale closure) results in the user pressing ArrowDown / dragging a widget and seeing NOTHING happen, with no console warning. The aria-live announcement in WidgetChrome (line 130) fires 'Moved X down' regardless, so screen-reader users are told the reorder succeeded when it didn't.
- **Evidence**: src/app/(dashboard)/allocations/hooks/useDashboardConfig.ts:384-395, src/app/(dashboard)/allocations/components/WidgetChrome.tsx:122-135
- **Fix**: Return a boolean from moveWidget; have AllocationDashboardV2.onMoveWrapper await that result and only call `announce('Moved ...')` on success. Log `logError(new Error('moveWidget tile not found'), 'useDashboardConfigV2.move_noop', { fromK, toK })` so the race condition surfaces in Sentry.

#### G18-028 · WidgetProps.data typed as `any` defeats every downstream widget's type system
- **File**: `src/app/(dashboard)/allocations/lib/types.ts:78`
- **Specialist**: `type-design-analyzer` (confidence 10)
- **Summary**: WidgetProps declares `data: any` (with explicit eslint-disable). Every widget receives the full MyAllocationDashboardPayload through this prop, but the contract is erased at the boundary so each widget hand-narrows via `(data ?? {}) as Partial<MyAllocationDashboardPayload>` (KpiStripWidget L51, HoldingsTableWidget L39, MandateSnapshotWidget L41), or `(data ?? {}) as EquityChartWidgetData` (EquityChart L1248), or `data as MyAllocationDashboardPayload | undefined` (OutcomesWidget L733, BridgeHeroWidget L55), or `(data?.strategies ?? []) as StrategyRow[]` (AllocationByStyleWidget L40). Twelve+ widgets repeat the same unsafe cast; renaming a payload field can never produce a compile error. Designer-key resolution + STRATEGY_COMPOSITE_WIDGETS gating already constrains which widget receives which payload, so the actual type IS knowable.
- **Evidence**: src/app/(dashboard)/allocations/lib/types.ts:78-84
- **Fix**: Replace `data: any` with `data: MyAllocationDashboardPayload` (the only real producer is AllocationDashboardV2.renderWidget). Drop the per-widget `as Partial<...>` rewraps. Width/height props are unused — delete them. Result: payload field renames flow into widgets as compile errors instead of silent runtime nulls.

#### G18-029 · widget-registry.ts comment lies: persisted 'bridge-outcome-banner' tiles render 'Unknown widget', not the legacy banner · _new_
- **File**: `src/app/(dashboard)/allocations/lib/widget-registry.ts:600`
- **Specialist**: `red-team` (confidence 10)

Verified against the live code: (a) `bridge-outcome-banner` has NO entry in WIDGET_REGISTRY (registry only carries `bridge-hero` at line 533), (b) WIDGET_COMPONENTS does NOT have a `bridge-outcome-banner` key (widgets/index.ts only has `bridge-hero` at line 120), (c) `resolveWidgetId('bridge-outcome-banner')` returns the unchanged id (lines 632-633 in widget-registry.ts), (d) renderWidget then hits the `WIDGET_COMPONENTS[k]` undefined fallback at AllocationDashboardV2.tsx:232-241 and renders 'Unknown widget: bridge-outcome-banner'. The same misclaim covers `allocation-donut` rollbacks — but that one IS registered (line 238), so only `bridge-outcome-banner` is broken. - **Fix**: Either (a) add a `bridge-outcome-banner` entry to WIDGET_REGISTRY + WIDGET_COMPONENTS pointing at components/BridgeOutcomeBanner so the comment becomes true; or (b) add `bridge-outcome-banner: 'bridge-hero'` to DESIGNER_KEY_TO_WIDGET_ID so resolveWidgetId migrates the legacy id at read time; or (c) update the comment to admit the rollback path is broken. Option (b) preserves user state with one-line of migration code and matches the pattern used for `allocation-donut`.

#### G18-030 · BridgeHeroWidget happy path (variant pass-through, outcomes forwarding, flagged data wiring) is not tested — only the error branch is
- **File**: `src/app/(dashboard)/allocations/widgets/bridge/BridgeHeroWidget.test.tsx:44`
- **Specialist**: `pr-test-analyzer` (confidence 8)
- **Summary**: BridgeHeroWidget.test.tsx only covers the error-branch routing through WidgetState v2 (2 tests, both seed `data={{__error: true}}`). The actual production path — reading `payload.flaggedHoldings`, `payload.matchDecisionsByHoldingRef`, `payload.outcomes`, and forwarding `variant` from TweaksContext — has no test. PR2's whole point was the rich empty-state surfacing 'Last reviewed N days ago' + outcomes count, which flows through this adapter into BridgeWidget. The BridgeWidget tests verify the rendering with direct props but the adapter (the one registered in WIDGET_COMPONENTS) is what production actually mounts. A regression where the adapter drops `outcomes={outcomes}` (or forwards `payload.outcomes ?? null` instead of `?? []`) would silently regress PR2's empty-state polish without any test failing.
- **Evidence**: BridgeHeroWidget.test.tsx lines 1-80 — only 2 tests, both error-branch. Grep `useTweakValue|bridgeVariant|TweaksProvider` in widgets/bridge/*.test.tsx → no matches. BridgeHeroWidget.tsx:24,28,62 reads variant + outcomes + flaggedHoldings from payload and forwards to BridgeWidget; none of these forwardings are asserted at the adapter level.

#### G18-031 · `__error: true` is a magic in-band signal on `data: any`, not a tagged variant
- **File**: `src/app/(dashboard)/allocations/widgets/bridge/BridgeHeroWidget.tsx:30`
- **Specialist**: `type-design-analyzer` (confidence 9)
- **Summary**: BridgeHeroWidget (L30-32) and OutcomesWidget (L729-731) both check `data && typeof data === 'object' && (data as { __error?: unknown }).__error` to render an error state. This sentinel is not part of MyAllocationDashboardPayload and not part of WidgetProps; it exists only in test cassettes (BridgeHeroWidget.test.tsx L49,L69; OutcomesWidget.v2.test.tsx L85,L105). Production code never sets `__error: true` on the payload — meaning the error branch can fire ONLY in tests. The 'error state' is therefore unreachable in production yet appears to handle errors. If a real upstream failure occurs, the widget will silently treat `analytics: null` as 'empty' rather than 'error'.
- **Evidence**: src/app/(dashboard)/allocations/widgets/bridge/BridgeHeroWidget.tsx:30-32; src/app/(dashboard)/allocations/widgets/outcomes/OutcomesWidget.tsx:729-731
- **Fix**: Promote error handling to a real discriminated variant on WidgetProps: `data: { kind: 'ok'; payload: MyAllocationDashboardPayload } | { kind: 'error'; message: string }`. Renderer in AllocationDashboardV2.renderWidget produces the tagged value; widgets narrow on `data.kind`. Either delete the dead `__error` path or make the parent renderer actually emit it on upstream fetch failure.

#### G18-032 · KpiStripWidget embeds <style> block inside render output — media-query CSS re-parsed on every render
- **File**: `src/app/(dashboard)/allocations/widgets/meta/KpiStripWidget.tsx:158`
- **Specialist**: `performance` (confidence 8)
- **Summary**: The component returns inline `<style>{...}</style>` containing 3 @media rules + 4 nested selectors per render. Each render of the KPI strip re-injects this stylesheet into the document head (React inlines <style> into a stylesheet token); React 19 dedupes via the precedence attribute when present, but no `precedence` attribute is set here so the stylesheet is treated as a regular DOM <style> that gets recreated/re-parsed each commit. Combined with the parent rerendering on every router.refresh (Overview polls every 30s) this creates layout/style recalculation churn. The same pattern lives in WidgetGrid.tsx (line 78).
- **Evidence**: src/app/(dashboard)/allocations/widgets/meta/KpiStripWidget.tsx:158-170
- **Fix**: Move the @media rules into globals.css scoped on `.kpi-grid` (the same class name is already used). The selectors are static — they don't need to live inline. Same fix applies to WidgetGrid.tsx:78-93. If inline must remain, add `precedence="default"` so React 19 hoists+dedupes.

#### G18-033 · KpiStripWidget renders em-dashes for missing analytics indistinguishable from genuine zero/null
- **File**: `src/app/(dashboard)/allocations/widgets/meta/KpiStripWidget.tsx:214`
- **Specialist**: `silent-failure-hunter` (confidence 8)
- **Summary**: All 5 KPI cells fall back to em-dash on null. Per the comment at lines 53-63, this is intentional — 'The widget already renders em-dashes for missing values, which is its way of expressing the empty/warmup state'. But: (a) for AUM the code falls back to summing holdingsSummary[].value_usd, which silently emits a misleading number if holdings exist but analytics fetch failed (the user sees a real AUM with em-dashes elsewhere, suggesting partial data is normal). (b) Sharpe, MaxDD, Vol, AvgRho all default to em-dash both when analytics is null AND when the individual field is null. There's no way for the user to tell 'analytics service down' from 'we don't have enough history to compute Sharpe yet'. The widget has explicit comments embracing this — 'we do NOT manufacture a new state branch' — but ambiguity here drives a user to assume the warmup case in production incidents.
- **Evidence**: src/app/(dashboard)/allocations/widgets/meta/KpiStripWidget.tsx:191-228, comments at 53-63
- **Fix**: At minimum: when payload.analytics === null entirely (not just one field), render a small inline 'Analytics warming up' or 'Analytics unavailable' banner above the strip. Discriminate fetch-failure vs not-yet-computed via a payload flag (similar to mandate fix above). Without this, KPIs silently lie about what the platform knows.

#### G18-034 · OutcomesWidget curves fetch error is generic and never logged
- **File**: `src/app/(dashboard)/allocations/widgets/outcomes/OutcomesWidget.tsx:370`
- **Specialist**: `silent-failure-hunter` (confidence 9)
- **Summary**: The curves-fetch effect catches all errors and sets a single string state: `if (!cancelled) setError('Failed to load curves');`. The error is not logged to Sentry (no logError call), so we have zero observability into how often it fires, what HTTP status drove it, or which outcomes are affected. The user sees a generic 'Failed to load curves' (and actually they DON'T — looking at the render at line 446, when `error` is non-null the code path `isPending || isLoading || error ? null : <Sparkline>` just hides the sparkline silently — the error message is never rendered anywhere visible to the user). This is a TRIPLE failure: error not logged, error message stored but never surfaced, and the empty result reads as 'no chart data' instead of 'we couldn't load it'.
- **Evidence**: src/app/(dashboard)/allocations/widgets/outcomes/OutcomesWidget.tsx:358-380, 446
- **Fix**: Inside the catch, `logError(err, 'OutcomesWidget.curves_fetch_failed', { outcomeId: outcome.id })`. Surface the error state in the UI: replace the silent `null` with `<div className='text-xs text-text-muted'>Could not load chart · <button onClick={retry}>Retry</button></div>`. Include the outcomeId in the error message for support.

#### G18-035 · HoldingsTableWidget revoked-status assertion is a false-confidence smoke test (title claims propagation; body only proves no crash)
- **File**: `src/app/(dashboard)/allocations/widgets/positions/HoldingsTableWidget.test.tsx:159`
- **Specialist**: `pr-test-analyzer` (confidence 9)
- **Summary**: The test 'propagates sync_status=revoked through revokedStatusByHoldingId' renders the widget with a revoked api_key and asserts only `screen.getByText(/SOL/i)` — i.e. the row is in the DOM. It does NOT assert the holding gets the revoked status. The matching T12b regression in HoldingsTabPanel.test.tsx (lines 109-127) extracts the map from a HoldingsTable stub and asserts map[ref] === 'revoked'. HoldingsTableWidget is the V2 dashboard surface (a distinct widget, not the Holdings tab body), so its revoked join is independent code. A bug where api_key_id lookup returns 'unknown' instead of 'revoked' (e.g. someone refactors keyStatusById to drop the FK match) would silently pass this test while breaking the strikethrough + amber chip rendering on the Overview holdings tile.
- **Evidence**: HoldingsTableWidget.test.tsx:159-172 — describe block title says 'propagates sync_status=revoked through revokedStatusByHoldingId' but the only assertion is `expect(screen.getByText(/SOL/i)).toBeInTheDocument()`. Compare HoldingsTabPanel.test.tsx:109-127 which uses a HoldingsTable stub and asserts `expect(map[ref]).toBe('revoked')`.
- **Fix**: Mock HoldingsTable (same idiom as HoldingsTabPanel.test.tsx) so it surfaces the revokedStatusByHoldingId prop verbatim (e.g. as a data-revoked-map JSON attribute). Then assert: render with revoked apiKey → map[buildHoldingRef({venue,symbol,holding_type})] === 'revoked'. Add a complete-apiKey case and a null-api_key_id case for parity with the HoldingsTabPanel T12b coverage.

#### G18-036 · HoldingsTableWidget defensive '?? unknown' on missing api_key FK masks revoked-key UI
- **File**: `src/app/(dashboard)/allocations/widgets/positions/HoldingsTableWidget.tsx:66`
- **Specialist**: `silent-failure-hunter` (confidence 8)
- **Summary**: When holding.api_key_id resolves into the apiKeys array but the corresponding key is missing (FK should prevent this but the code comment admits 'RESTRICT FK should prevent this in practice'), the status defaults to 'unknown' — NOT 'revoked'. The downstream HoldingsTable check at HoldingsTable.tsx:502 is `isRevoked = revokedStatusByHoldingId[row.id] === 'revoked'`, so an 'unknown' status fails the revoked check and the amber 'Key revoked' chip never renders. Result: a user whose api_key was deleted (or whose data join broke) sees a healthy-looking holding row when in reality we have NO IDEA if the key is alive. This silently hides the very 'revoked-key' UI that the chip exists to surface.
- **Evidence**: src/app/(dashboard)/allocations/widgets/positions/HoldingsTableWidget.tsx:49-70, src/app/(dashboard)/allocations/HoldingsTabPanel.tsx:64-67
- **Fix**: When the api_key lookup misses, log a warning to Sentry with the holding ref and api_key_id, and surface a separate 'Key unknown — check exchange connection' chip (not the green-light default). The FK should prevent this, so when it happens it's a real data-integrity event worth flagging.

#### G18-037 · MandateSnapshotWidget recomputes 5 gates over strategies+holdings on every render with no memoization
- **File**: `src/app/(dashboard)/allocations/widgets/risk/MandateSnapshotWidget.tsx:42`
- **Specialist**: `performance` (confidence 9)
- **Summary**: deriveMandateGates iterates strategies (maxStrategyWeight loop + groupedByStyle Map build) and holdings (reduce for totalAum) on EVERY render. The widget receives `data` as the whole MyAllocationDashboardPayload from AllocationDashboardV2 — and the dashboard polls router.refresh() every 30s while Overview is visible, so referential identity of strategies/holdingsSummary changes on every refresh AND on every parent state change (pickerOpen, kbdMode toggles in WidgetChrome, etc.). 5× per-gate compute × N strategies + N holdings runs unconditionally. Fix is one useMemo with [payload.mandate, payload.analytics, payload.holdingsSummary, payload.strategies] deps.
- **Evidence**: src/app/(dashboard)/allocations/widgets/risk/MandateSnapshotWidget.tsx:42-49
- **Fix**: Wrap `deriveMandateGates(...)` and `countPassingGates(gates)` in useMemo keyed on payload.mandate/analytics/holdingsSummary/strategies — matches the pattern HoldingsTableWidget already uses for its maps. Also wrap MandateGateLine in React.memo since the row inputs are stable per gate.key.

#### G18-038 · MandateSnapshotWidget surfaces 'No mandate set yet' for both genuinely-unset AND fetch failures
- **File**: `src/app/(dashboard)/allocations/widgets/risk/MandateSnapshotWidget.tsx:94`

Three legitimately-different states get one indistinguishable UI message. A user who has carefully configured their mandate but whose data fetch swallowed a permission error sees 'No mandate set yet' — false statement that drives action (open the mandate form, see fields already populated, get confused). The 5-gate display also defaults every threshold to em-dash, suggesting nothing is configured.

Add logError telemetry so swallowed PGRST205 events surface in Sentry.

#### G18-039 · InsightStrip runs full computeAllInsights on every dashboard render with no memoization
- **File**: `src/components/portfolio/InsightStrip.tsx:82`
- **Specialist**: `performance` (confidence 9)
- **Summary**: `const insights = computeAllInsights(analytics, portfolioStrategies, portfolioAgeDays).slice(0, max);` runs at top level of the function component with no useMemo. PR1 wires this into AllocationDashboardV2 as a sibling to WidgetGrid, so every parent re-render (and every 30s router.refresh on Overview) re-runs all 7 insight rules over analytics + strategies. The function is documented as having 7 rules and produces a sliced array — non-trivial cost, especially since `analytics` is a payload-derived object reference that flips on every router.refresh. Also `flaggedCount !== undefined && flaggedCount > 0` short-circuits the early-return, but insights[] is computed BEFORE the empty-check, so we pay the compute cost even when we return null.
- **Evidence**: src/components/portfolio/InsightStrip.tsx:82-86
- **Fix**: Wrap in useMemo: `const insights = useMemo(() => computeAllInsights(analytics, portfolioStrategies, portfolioAgeDays).slice(0, max), [analytics, portfolioStrategies, portfolioAgeDays, max])`. Move it AFTER the empty-state short-circuit so we don't compute when returning null (currently insights.length === 0 && !flaggedCount returns null AFTER computing — flip order).

#### G18-040 · InsightStrip dead-code branch `{false ? ... :}` and dead `flaggedCount === 0` branch never trigger the empty-state copy · _new_
- **File**: `src/components/portfolio/InsightStrip.tsx:106`
- **Specialist**: `red-team` (confidence 9)
- **Summary**: PR3's modification to InsightStrip now returns null when `insights.length === 0 && !flaggedCount` (lines 94-96). The body at line 106 then renders `{false ? <empty-copy/> : <ul>...</ul>}` — a literal `false ?` ternary with one branch unreachable. The 'No unusual activity in the trailing window' fallback at lines 106-109 is documented but cannot execute. Two latent issues: (1) the dead branch hides the original intent so a future contributor reading the file cannot tell whether the empty-state copy was deliberately removed or accidentally short-circuited; (2) the early-return path also kills the 'What we noticed' header even when flaggedCount is 0 but the user might benefit from an explicit 'no flags' state. The combined effect: a user whose insights computation degrades to empty results and whose flag count is undefined (older payload shape, payload error) sees the section vanish silently — no error, no fallback copy.
- **Evidence**: src/components/portfolio/InsightStrip.tsx:94-96 + 106-109
- **Fix**: Remove the `{false ? ... : ...}` literal and inline the truthy branch. Delete the unreachable empty-state copy or replace the early-return with an explicit reachable branch that surfaces 'No unusual activity' alongside an aria-live region so screen-readers know the insight surface is intentionally empty. Add a test pinning the rendering for `insights=[], flaggedCount=0` and `insights=[], flaggedCount=undefined`.

#### G18-041 · InsightStrip computes computeAllInsights BEFORE early-return — pays cost for null render path · _chain_ · refs: performance:#2
- **File**: `src/components/portfolio/InsightStrip.tsx:82`
- **Specialist**: `red-team` (confidence 8)
- **Summary**: Chain with performance #2 — verified live AND added regression: lines 82-86 unconditionally call `computeAllInsights(analytics, portfolioStrategies, portfolioAgeDays).slice(0, max)`. The early-return at line 94 only checks `if (insights.length === 0 && !flaggedCount) return null;` — meaning we ALREADY paid the compute cost when we return null. This widget is mounted in AllocationDashboardV2.tsx:282 above WidgetGrid and re-renders on every 30s router.refresh PLUS every payload change. computeAllInsights iterates all 7 portfolio rules; for portfolios that genuinely have no insights (most onboarding cases), this is pure waste. Also no useMemo: same identity-flipping analytics object re-runs the function on every parent render.
- **Evidence**: src/components/portfolio/InsightStrip.tsx:82-96
- **Fix**: Swap order: check the early-return predicate FIRST (without computing insights). The current logic needs `insights.length === 0` AFTER computing — but we could short-circuit on `analytics === null` (which most early-return paths trigger). Better: wrap in useMemo `const insights = useMemo(() => analytics === null ? [] : computeAllInsights(...).slice(0, max), [analytics, ...])` AND move the empty-check after the memo. Together: zero compute when no analytics, one compute per analytics-identity flip otherwise.

#### G18-043 · AllocationDashboardV2 Suspense fallback for unknown widget components has no error-state distinguishability
- **File**: `src/app/(dashboard)/allocations/AllocationDashboardV2.tsx:243`
- **Specialist**: `silent-failure-hunter` (confidence 8)
- **Summary**: The Suspense wrapper around lazy-loaded widgets renders a pulsing animation as fallback. If the lazy import throws (network error, bundle deletion, chunk hash mismatch after deploy), the Suspense fallback shows the same pulsing state forever — no error boundary above it, no error handler. The user sees 'loading' indefinitely with no path to recovery. Suspense + lazy without ErrorBoundary is a classic silent-failure mode in Next.js.
- **Evidence**: src/app/(dashboard)/allocations/AllocationDashboardV2.tsx:242-256
- **Fix**: Wrap the Suspense in a React ErrorBoundary that renders 'Widget failed to load — <button>Retry</button>'. Log to Sentry. This is critical for chunk-hash mismatches after a deploy when users have a stale tab open.

#### G18-044 · AllocationDashboardV2 keeps inactive tabpanels mounted via `hidden=` BUT lazy-mounts via `&&` — DOM tabpanels are always present with role=tabpanel
- **File**: `src/app/(dashboard)/allocations/AllocationsTabs.tsx:503`
- **Specialist**: `performance` (confidence 8)
- **Summary**: The tabpanel pattern combines `hidden={activeTab !== X}` + `{activeTab === X && <Panel/>}`. The DESIRED state (per the comment at line 495-502) is: hidden divs stay in DOM as empty tabpanel shells, content lazy-mounts. That's correct — but six divs each with role=tabpanel, id, and aria-labelledby get measured/painted on every render (~6 React reconciler diff passes on the empty case). More importantly, `<AllocationDashboardV2 {...props} />` at line 509 receives the spread of the whole payload every render — props identity flips on every router.refresh, blowing through V2's render dispatcher. Combined with the 30s poll, the entire dashboard tree reconciles every 30s.
- **Evidence**: src/app/(dashboard)/allocations/AllocationsTabs.tsx:503-565
- **Fix**: Memoize the dashboard payload at the AllocationsTabs root before spreading: `const stablePayload = useMemo(() => props, [/* a stable identity proxy or specific deep deps */])` — better, wrap AllocationDashboardV2 (and HoldingsTabPanel etc.) in React.memo so identity-equal payloads short-circuit. Also consider reducing the 30s polling interval to use SWR-style stale-while-revalidate via a hash check on the payload before forcing a tree re-render.

#### G18-045 · AllocationsTabs polling re-runs router.refresh on Overview but pauses cleanup race on tab change · _new_ · refs: silent-failure-hunter:#22
- **File**: `src/app/(dashboard)/allocations/AllocationsTabs.tsx:263`
- **Specialist**: `red-team` (confidence 8)
- **Summary**: The polling useEffect at lines 263-269 starts a 30s setInterval when activeTab === 'overview'. When the user switches to Holdings, the effect's cleanup (clearInterval) runs — fine. But if the cleanup fires DURING a router.refresh's microtask (the 30s tick races with a user tab click), the in-flight router.refresh continues to mutate route state on Holdings. There's no AbortController; router.refresh doesn't accept one. A user can click Holdings during a refresh and see the URL flip back to /allocations briefly before settling. Minor UX hiccup but observable.
- **Evidence**: AllocationsTabs.tsx:263-269
- **Fix**: Track an inflightRefreshCount via useRef; only start a new interval when 0. On effect cleanup, if a refresh is mid-flight, defer the next tick. Or: track the abort-flag in a ref and check it inside the interval callback before calling router.refresh. The simplest mitigation is to wrap router.refresh in a try/catch and add telemetry.

#### G18-046 · AllocationsTabs parseTab silent fallback hides bookmark / external-link breakage

Acknowledged as 'D-04 silent fallback' in the code comment, but the rationale doesn't address debuggability: support cannot tell 'user typoed a URL' from 'we have a broken outbound link in marketing'. No logging of unknown values.

- **Fix**: Inside the default branch, if `raw` is non-null and non-empty and not in the legacy aliases set ('performance'), call `logEvent('allocations_invalid_tab', { raw })`. That at least catches systemic typos in marketing URLs or stale docs.

#### G18-048 · WidgetGrid creates closure-heavy inline onDragStart/onDragOver/onDrop per cell every render
- **File**: `src/app/(dashboard)/allocations/components/WidgetGrid.tsx:186`
- **Specialist**: `performance` (confidence 8)
- **Summary**: WidgetCell takes 5 setter functions + onMove/onResize/onRemove as props, and creates 4 inline handlers (onDragStart, onDragEnd, onDragOver, onDrop) per cell. There's no useCallback on these in WidgetGrid (line 186-222), and no React.memo on WidgetCell, so every render of the parent (WidgetGrid receives new onMove/onResize/onRemove on every parent render) cascades through all N cells. With 7 default tiles, that's 7 × 4 = 28 closure allocations per render, plus full WidgetChrome re-render per cell.
- **Evidence**: src/app/(dashboard)/allocations/components/WidgetGrid.tsx:113-264
- **Fix**: (1) Wrap WidgetCell in React.memo with a custom comparator on [k, w, draggingK===k, dragOverK===k, identity-equal callbacks]. (2) Lift the inline handlers in WidgetCell to useCallback. (3) In the parent AllocationDashboardV2, the onResize/onRemove/onMove callbacks come from useDashboardConfigV2 — verify those are useCallback-wrapped (renderWidget is the same problem). Currently every dashboard rerender allocates new handlers for each cell.

#### G18-049 · TweakState parsed from localStorage via raw cast — no validation against allowed string literals
- **File**: `src/app/(dashboard)/allocations/context/TweaksContext.tsx:55`
- **Specialist**: `type-design-analyzer` (confidence 9)
- **Summary**: `loadTweaks` (L55-65) does `JSON.parse(raw) as Partial<TweakState>` and spreads it on top of TWEAK_DEFAULTS. The TweakState literal-union members (`density: 'tight'|'comfortable'|'loose'`, `bridgeVariant: 'subtle'|'card'|'full'`, etc.) are not validated. A user-pasted or corrupted localStorage entry like `{ bridgeVariant: 'gigantic' }` flows into useTweakValue('bridgeVariant') and is passed to BridgeWidget which falls to the default 'full' variant render path only because all three variant ifs miss — but the type system declares the value is one of three. Worse, `chartStyle: 'spiral'` would silently disable the area-fill branch in EquityChart L990.
- **Evidence**: src/app/(dashboard)/allocations/context/TweaksContext.tsx:55-65
- **Fix**: Replace the raw cast with field-by-field validation: `bridgeVariant: ['subtle','card','full'].includes(parsed.bridgeVariant) ? parsed.bridgeVariant : TWEAK_DEFAULTS.bridgeVariant`. Or pull a tiny `safeUnion(allowed, value, fallback)` helper to share the pattern. Same fix applies to DashboardConfig.tiles[*].k validation.

#### G18-050 · TileConfig.w invariant `1|2|3|4` not enforced when reading persisted layout
- **File**: `src/app/(dashboard)/allocations/hooks/useDashboardConfig.ts:287`
- **Specialist**: `type-design-analyzer` (confidence 9)
- **Summary**: TileConfig declares `w: 1 | 2 | 3 | 4` (types.ts L9) but `loadV2Config` only validates `layoutVersion`, `Array.isArray(tiles)`, and `looksLikeLegacyTile` shape — it never validates the `w` value of each tile. A hand-edited localStorage blob (or a corrupted write from a future code path) carrying `{k:'kpi-strip', w: 7}` or `{k:'kpi-strip', w: 'wide'}` will deserialize, pass through `normalizeTilesToRegistryIds`, reach WidgetGrid as `gridColumn: span 7` (cell occupies more columns than the 4-col grid) or `span wide` (invalid CSS). The `1|2|3|4` literal type is enforced only at hook-write time via clampWidth.
- **Evidence**: src/app/(dashboard)/allocations/hooks/useDashboardConfig.ts:287-316 (no w validation between L294 parse and L310 return)
- **Fix**: Add a `clampTile` helper that runs every tile through `{ k: resolveWidgetId(t.k), w: clampWidth(t.w), config: t.config }` inside loadV2Config (or fold into normalizeTilesToRegistryIds). The cast `parsed as DashboardConfig` (L294) is currently load-bearing for an invariant the data doesn't actually carry.

#### G18-051 · FlaggedHolding shape duplicated in holdings-adapter — two competing source-of-truth types
- **File**: `src/app/(dashboard)/allocations/lib/holdings-adapter.ts:56`
- **Specialist**: `type-design-analyzer` (confidence 8)
- **Summary**: HoldingsAdapterInputs.flaggedHoldings (L56-62) declares a local `composite_score: number` field while the live `FlaggedHolding` (holding-outcome-adapter.ts L16) exposes `top_candidate_composite: number`. The comment at L49-55 admits the duplication and says call sites must remap one to the other. HoldingsTableWidget.tsx L114-124 then performs that exact remap (`composite_score: f.top_candidate_composite`). The 'narrow boundary' justification is real, but the type design forces every call site to manually translate names — a single rename in either type will break in five places (HoldingsTableWidget L114-124, plus HoldingsTabPanel) with no compile error if both rename at once.
- **Evidence**: src/app/(dashboard)/allocations/lib/holdings-adapter.ts:48-62
- **Fix**: Make HoldingsAdapterInputs.flaggedHoldings extend `Pick<FlaggedHolding, 'venue'|'symbol'|'holding_type'|'top_candidate_strategy_id'> & { composite_score: number }` so when the live type gains/loses fields, the adapter sees them. Or, better, accept the live FlaggedHolding shape directly and read `top_candidate_composite` inside the adapter — no remap layer.

#### G18-052 · LegacyTileConfig and TileConfig share filename but no structural marker — write-time confusion possible
- **File**: `src/app/(dashboard)/allocations/lib/types.ts:26`
- **Specialist**: `type-design-analyzer` (confidence 9)
- **Summary**: TileConfig (`{k, w, config?}`) and LegacyTileConfig (`{i, widgetId, x, y, w, h, config?}`) both export from `lib/types.ts` and both ship under tiles[]. The legacy hook (useDashboardConfig L134) reads/writes the SAME localStorage key as V2 (L41 STORAGE_KEY = 'quantalyze-dashboard-config'). The only thing keeping them from clobbering each other is run-time inspection (`looksLikeLegacyTile`, `layoutVersion` mismatch). Both shapes accept `config?: Record<string, unknown>` so a malformed write would not even violate either schema. Nothing in the type prevents a legacy `addTile` from producing a `{ i, widgetId, x, y, w: 12, h: 4 }` blob that fails V2's `looksLikeLegacyTile` check only because the comment says it has those fields — refactor risk is high.
- **Evidence**: src/app/(dashboard)/allocations/lib/types.ts:7-40; src/app/(dashboard)/allocations/hooks/useDashboardConfig.ts:40-49
- **Fix**: Tag both unions: `interface TileConfig { __v: 4; k: string; w: 1|2|3|4 }` and `interface LegacyTileConfig { __v: 3; i: string; widgetId: string; ... }`. The runtime check becomes `tile.__v === 4` instead of structural field probing. Alternatively, delete LegacyTileConfig now that the legacy hook is dormant (per the comment at L24 the V1 root was removed in v0.15.7.0).

#### G18-053 · WidgetMeta.defaultW is `number` not `1|2|3|4` despite registry-level invariant
- **File**: `src/app/(dashboard)/allocations/lib/types.ts:66`
- **Specialist**: `type-design-analyzer` (confidence 8)
- **Summary**: WidgetMeta.defaultW is typed `number` (L66) but the registry has TWO overlapping populations: legacy 12-col values (3/4/6/12 for the 6-col `LegacyTileConfig.w`) and the new 4-col values that must clamp into `1|2|3|4` for TileConfig.w. The V2 hook applies `clampWidth(meta?.defaultW)` at addWidget time — but the registry itself does not encode WHICH grid the value targets. New entries like `mandate-snapshot: defaultW: 2` and legacy entries like `equity-curve: defaultW: 12` (widget-registry.ts L31) live side-by-side with no type-level distinction. A future contributor reading `defaultW: 6` cannot tell if it means '6 of 12 cols' or '6 of 4 cols (will clamp)'.
- **Evidence**: src/app/(dashboard)/allocations/lib/types.ts:66-73; src/app/(dashboard)/allocations/lib/widget-registry.ts:31-50
- **Fix**: Split into `defaultW12: 1..12` (legacy hook) and `defaultW4: 1|2|3|4` (V2 hook). Or, since the comment at L73 says defaultH is being phased out, rewrite the registry to carry only `defaultW: 1|2|3|4` and delete the legacy fallback path. Either approach prevents the silent 'value too big' clamp.

#### G18-054 · DashboardConfig.timeframe is unconstrained `string` but only 'YTD' is ever produced
- **File**: `src/app/(dashboard)/allocations/lib/types.ts:13`
- **Specialist**: `type-design-analyzer` (confidence 9)
- **Summary**: DashboardConfig.timeframe is `string` (types.ts L15). Every concrete value in the codebase is the literal 'YTD' (useDashboardConfig.ts L80, L96, L219, L283; AllocationDashboardV2.tsx L251 falls back to 'YTD'). The V2 hook also exposes `setTimeframe(tf: string)` (L397) so a caller could store an arbitrary string in localStorage and have it flow into Component props that probably won't recognize anything except 'YTD'. The Period union (EquityChart.tsx L32 `'1M'|'3M'|'6M'|'YTD'|'1Y'|'ALL'|'CUSTOM'`) is the actual intended timeframe vocabulary; it lives only inside EquityChart.
- **Evidence**: src/app/(dashboard)/allocations/lib/types.ts:13-18; src/app/(dashboard)/allocations/hooks/useDashboardConfig.ts:397-399
- **Fix**: Either narrow to the union actually used: `timeframe: Period` (move Period into lib/types.ts and import in EquityChart). Or, if the field is truly dead/aspirational, delete it from DashboardConfig and from the JSON shape — preserving it as `string` advertises a flexibility that's never realized.

#### G18-055 · DESIGNER_KEY_TO_WIDGET_ID values are unconstrained strings, not registry ids
- **File**: `src/app/(dashboard)/allocations/lib/widget-registry.ts:595`
- **Specialist**: `type-design-analyzer` (confidence 9)
- **Summary**: `DESIGNER_KEY_TO_WIDGET_ID: Record<string, string>` (L595) maps short keys → registry ids. The codebase relies on a comment-level invariant ('every value must be a WIDGET_REGISTRY key') that the type system does not enforce. The historic bug noted at L583-589 ('mandate routes to mandate-compliance — there is no widget for it yet') was exactly this drift: the map shipped pointing at an unregistered id, and the renderer's fallback path was the only thing keeping the UI from crashing. The PR1 comment at L614-620 confirms this routing problem cost the team a regression.
- **Evidence**: src/app/(dashboard)/allocations/lib/widget-registry.ts:595-622
- **Fix**: Tighten to `const DESIGNER_KEY_TO_WIDGET_ID: Record<string, WidgetId>` (WidgetId = keyof typeof WIDGET_REGISTRY, see neighboring finding). The mandate-snapshot regression would have failed to compile when the map said `mandate: 'mandate-compliance'` because mandate-compliance isn't in WIDGET_REGISTRY.

#### G18-056 · AllocationByStyleWidget legend re-iterates entries twice in DOM (stacked-bar + legend list) with no row-level memoization
- **File**: `src/app/(dashboard)/allocations/widgets/allocation/AllocationByStyleWidget.tsx:132`
- **Specialist**: `performance` (confidence 8)
- **Summary**: The widget renders `entries.map(...)` TWICE — once for stacked-bar segments (line 132) and once for the legend list (line 145). For each iteration, every row holds inline-style objects (a new object each render) which defeats React.memo at the child level. Each row also calls `colorByTag.get(tag) ?? "#64748B"` twice. Not catastrophic for the typical 3-5 styles but the inline-style allocations + double iteration are wasteful when the parent re-renders 2× per minute (30s poll) AND on every parent state change.
- **Evidence**: src/app/(dashboard)/allocations/widgets/allocation/AllocationByStyleWidget.tsx:132-178
- **Fix**: Pre-build the per-row data (with color resolved once) inside the same useMemo that builds entries, then map ONCE to derive a combined render structure. Or split row into a memoized component that takes [tag, weight, color] primitives and uses stable inline styles.

#### G18-057 · BridgeHeroWidget exposes the entire payload through TweaksContext-read variant but never null-checks variant · _chain_ · refs: type-design-analyzer:#6
- **File**: `src/app/(dashboard)/allocations/widgets/bridge/BridgeHeroWidget.tsx:28`
- **Specialist**: `red-team` (confidence 8)
- **Summary**: `const variant = useTweakValue('bridgeVariant');` at line 28 returns the TWEAK_DEFAULTS.bridgeVariant when outside TweaksProvider. But: if the user's tweaks-localStorage blob carries an invalid bridgeVariant value (the type-design-analyzer #6 finding), it propagates here as the typed string 'card'/'subtle'/'full' but might be any literal at runtime. BridgeWidget at line 169 / 196 / 235 falls through to 'full' if neither 'subtle' nor 'card' match. A malformed value silently picks 'full' — silently overriding the user's explicit choice. The widget has no error state and no telemetry for invalid variant. This is the chain partner of type-design-analyzer:#6.
- **Evidence**: BridgeHeroWidget.tsx:28 + BridgeWidget.tsx:80-85 (variant default 'full') + 169/196/235 (variant branch)
- **Fix**: In useTweakValue or the TweaksProvider's load path, validate enum membership at the boundary (type-design-analyzer:#6 fix). Plus: BridgeWidget should narrow `variant` via a discriminated union or explicit fallback log when an unknown variant value lands.

#### G18-058 · BridgeHeroWidget __error sentinel only triggers from tests — production payload-load failures bypass the error branch · _chain_ · refs: type-design-analyzer:#2, silent-failure-hunter:#9
- **File**: `src/app/(dashboard)/allocations/widgets/bridge/BridgeHeroWidget.tsx:30`
- **Specialist**: `red-team` (confidence 8)
- **Summary**: Chain with type-design-analyzer:#2. Verified: the `__error: true` check at line 30-32 is the ONLY production code path that can render <WidgetState mode='error'>. But queries.ts getMyAllocationDashboard NEVER sets `__error` on the payload — it returns the empty-portfolio shape (`portfolio: null, holdingsSummary: [], flaggedHoldings: []`) on the early-return branch when no portfolio exists. A real upstream RLS failure now throws (per audit-2026-05-07 G8.A.9), which crashes the page to error.tsx — bypassing this widget's error branch entirely. The error path is unreachable in production. Net result: BridgeHeroWidget can never display 'Bridge unavailable' in a real session; only in tests with explicit `__error: true` seeding.
- **Evidence**: BridgeHeroWidget.tsx:30-53 + queries.ts:1940-1972 (no __error injection)
- **Fix**: Either (a) delete the error branch — it's dead code in production; or (b) wire upstream payload errors to set `__error: true` AND propagate the actual error message. Option (b) requires queries.ts to catch transient failures gracefully and stamp the payload; today it throws. The simplest fix is (a): delete dead code and update tests to assert the error path is reached via error.tsx, not the widget chrome.

#### G18-059 · WIDGET_REGISTRY and WIDGET_COMPONENTS keys are not enforced to align — drift is a runtime miss
- **File**: `src/app/(dashboard)/allocations/widgets/index.ts:14`
- **Specialist**: `type-design-analyzer` (confidence 8)
- **Summary**: `WIDGET_REGISTRY: Record<string, WidgetMeta>` (widget-registry.ts L24) and `WIDGET_COMPONENTS: Record<string, LazyWidget>` (widgets/index.ts L14) are two parallel string-keyed maps. The comment at widgets/index.ts L7 says 'Every key must match a key in WIDGET_REGISTRY' but the type system permits any of: (a) a registry id with no component (renders fallback 'Unknown widget' — silent), (b) a component id with no registry entry (picker never shows it, but addWidget('foo') still inserts a tile), (c) typos like `holdings-table` vs `holdings_table`. AllocationDashboardV2 L232-241 has fallback rendering for case (a), but the right design is to refuse mismatched keys at compile time.
- **Evidence**: src/app/(dashboard)/allocations/widgets/index.ts:12-14; src/app/(dashboard)/allocations/lib/widget-registry.ts:24-543
- **Fix**: Define `type WidgetId = keyof typeof WIDGET_REGISTRY` and re-type `WIDGET_COMPONENTS: Record<WidgetId, LazyWidget>`. TS will then complain when (a) a new registry entry has no component, or (b) a component map gains a key not in the registry. The string-key fallback path in renderWidget can then warn in dev rather than silently swallow.

#### G18-060 · OutcomesWidget loading state triggers when outcomes is undefined — never distinguished from fetch failure
- **File**: `src/app/(dashboard)/allocations/widgets/outcomes/OutcomesWidget.tsx:811`
- **Specialist**: `silent-failure-hunter` (confidence 8)
- **Summary**: `if (outcomes === undefined) { return <LoadingState />; }` shows the 5-row skeleton indefinitely when payload.outcomes is undefined. The dashboard payload's empty-portfolio branch (queries.ts:1026) sets `outcomes: []`, but partial failures or older API responses may emit undefined. The user sees a loading skeleton forever, with no error escape and no logged event. Combined with the hasError branch only triggering on an explicit `__error` field, real fetch failures that fail to set that field are misclassified as 'still loading'.
- **Evidence**: src/app/(dashboard)/allocations/widgets/outcomes/OutcomesWidget.tsx:725-813
- **Fix**: After 10 seconds of `outcomes === undefined`, transition to error state with 'Could not load outcomes — refresh'. Add a watchdog timer that logErrors the stuck-loading state. Ensure all upstream payload constructors set `outcomes: []` rather than leaving the field undefined.

#### G18-061 · EquityChart anchorFromFirstPositive returns empty array on all-non-positive input — empty state masks data quality
- **File**: `src/app/(dashboard)/allocations/widgets/performance/EquityChart.tsx:147`
- **Specialist**: `silent-failure-hunter` (confidence 8)
- **Summary**: `anchorFromFirstPositive` returns `[]` when no positive value exists in the equity series, and the empty-state render at line 366 surfaces 'Equity data warming up'. If a user's portfolio is entirely flat or negative (real edge case: 100% short, 100% loss), or if the equity_snapshots data is corrupt with all-zero rows, they see 'warming up' indefinitely. There's no escape hatch — no log, no 'we couldn't anchor this series' affordance, no toggle to view raw values.
- **Evidence**: src/app/(dashboard)/allocations/widgets/performance/EquityChart.tsx:147-157, 366-377
- **Fix**: When equityDailyPoints.length > 0 but composite.length === 0, render a distinct state: 'Equity series anchored failed (no positive base). View raw values?' Log the case to Sentry with the count of non-positive points so we know whether this happens in production.

#### G18-062 · HoldingsTableWidget useMemo for `rows` rebuilds a fresh holdingsSummary array inside the memo, defeating its own dep gating
- **File**: `src/app/(dashboard)/allocations/widgets/positions/HoldingsTableWidget.tsx:126`
- **Specialist**: `performance` (confidence 8)
- **Summary**: Inside the rows useMemo, `holdingsSummary.map((h) => ({venue, symbol, ..., allocated_at: null}))` allocates a fresh array of fresh objects on every memo execution. The memo deps are correct (holdingsSummary identity-equal between runs short-circuits), but the inner toDesignHoldings receives a NEW array each compute pass, causing downstream HoldingsTable to potentially re-derive too. The map step could either move to its own useMemo or simply pass the original holdingsSummary array since it has the same shape (the map only drops fields and adds `allocated_at: null` — could be derived in adapter).
- **Evidence**: src/app/(dashboard)/allocations/widgets/positions/HoldingsTableWidget.tsx:126-153
- **Fix**: Either (a) lift the holdingsSummary mapping to a separate useMemo keyed only on holdingsSummary, OR (b) refactor toDesignHoldings to accept the raw payload field directly and supply allocated_at internally. Same critique applies to the adapterStrategies useMemo at line 90 which maps over strategies inside the memo.

#### G18-063 · PreferencesPanel (admin) Minimum-AUM rename + tier dollar-label change has no test coverage

### LOW (5)

#### G18-064 · BridgeWidget formatRelativeDate constructs new Date() on every render of the empty state
- **File**: `src/app/(dashboard)/allocations/components/BridgeWidget.tsx:60`
- **Specialist**: `performance` (confidence 9)
- **Summary**: `formatRelativeDate(iso, now = new Date())` defaults `now` to a fresh Date allocation per invocation. The empty-state branch (line 145) calls this inline during render. Each parent re-render of BridgeWidget allocates a fresh Date. Not expensive in isolation, but the BridgeHeroWidget is mounted as the top tile on Overview and re-renders with every payload refresh (every 30s from the router.refresh). The locale-aware toLocaleDateString fallback branch (line 73) is also more expensive than the equivalent template string format. Calls to `Date.parse(iso)` per render also re-parse the same ISO string every paint.
- **Evidence**: src/app/(dashboard)/allocations/components/BridgeWidget.tsx:60-78,144
- **Fix**: Wrap the relative-date computation in useMemo keyed on lastOutcome?.created_at. Since the value only depends on the outcome's created_at and changes once a day for most outcomes, memoize aggressively. Bonus: extract the formatRelativeDate computation to lib (it duplicates the BridgeWidget-internal version vs. lib/utils formatRelativeTime).

#### G18-065 · Bridge 'No active breaches' empty-state — formatRelativeDate boundary at 7-day mark is partially tested
- **File**: `src/app/(dashboard)/allocations/components/BridgeWidget.tsx:68`
- **Specialist**: `pr-test-analyzer` (confidence 9)
- **Summary**: PR2's BridgeWidget formatRelativeDate has 6 boundary buckets: 0-day → 'today', 1-day → 'yesterday', 2..6-day → 'N days ago', 7..13 → 'a week ago', 14..59 → 'N weeks ago', 60..364 → 'N months ago', >=365 → absolute date. BridgeWidget.test.tsx covers days 0, 1, 3 (and a plural multi-outcome case at 2 days) — but the boundary transitions at exactly day 7 ('a week ago'), 14 ('2 weeks ago'), 60 ('2 months ago'), 365 (absolute date), and negative (future timestamps → 'today') are not pinned. A future contributor who refactors the if-chain (e.g. uses Math.round instead of Math.floor) would silently mis-bucket day-7 from 'a week ago' to '1 weeks ago'.
- **Evidence**: BridgeWidget.tsx:68-78 — 6 if-branches in formatRelativeDate. BridgeWidget.test.tsx:79-113 covers 3-day + 1-day + 0-day; no boundary-day test at 7/14/60/365 or negative.
- **Fix**: In BridgeWidget.test.tsx, add boundary tests: (1) outcome 7 days old → 'a week ago'; (2) 14 days → '2 weeks ago'; (3) 60 days → '2 months ago'; (4) 366 days → absolute 'Apr 25, 2025' (or whatever the FIXED_NOW-365 resolves to via toLocaleDateString); (5) 1 day in the future (negative elapsedMs) → 'today'.

#### G18-066 · WidgetGrid <style> tag injected inline on every render — same React 19 stylesheet hoisting issue as KpiStripWidget
- **File**: `src/app/(dashboard)/allocations/components/WidgetGrid.tsx:78`
- **Specialist**: `performance` (confidence 9)
- **Summary**: WidgetGrid returns `<style>{...}</style>` inline at the end of its render output (3 @media rules + 4 selectors). React 19 will dedupe stylesheets via precedence attribute when present; this <style> has no precedence so each commit potentially re-parses the rules. The grid re-renders on every drag/resize state change (draggingK, dragOverK), so the inline style block re-evaluates as a string literal multiple times per second during drag.
- **Evidence**: src/app/(dashboard)/allocations/components/WidgetGrid.tsx:78-93
- **Fix**: Move the .widget-grid/.widget-cell @media rules into globals.css. The selectors are already scoped by class; static CSS is the right home. Same fix as KpiStripWidget recommendation.

#### G18-067 · DesignHoldingRow.status string union should pair with its threshold constants
- **File**: `src/app/(dashboard)/allocations/lib/holdings-adapter.ts:120`
- **Specialist**: `type-design-analyzer` (confidence 9)
- **Summary**: DesignHoldingRow.status is `'underperform' | 'watch' | 'ok'` (L120). The mapping from composite_score → status is hand-written ladder at L190-199 against FLAG_COMPOSITE_THRESHOLD (50) and WATCH_COMPOSITE_THRESHOLD (40). The type allows status to be any of the three literals but nothing connects them to the thresholds. If a future contributor adds a new tier (e.g. 'critical' >= 80), they must edit both the union AND the ladder — neither generates an error if the other is skipped.
- **Evidence**: src/app/(dashboard)/allocations/lib/holdings-adapter.ts:118-122,189-199
- **Fix**: Centralize: `const STATUS_TIERS = [{name:'ok', min:0}, {name:'watch', min:40}, {name:'underperform', min:50}] as const; type Status = typeof STATUS_TIERS[number]['name'];` and compute status by `for (...) { if (score >= tier.min) status = tier.name }`. New tiers added in one place propagate to the union and the ladder simultaneously.

#### G18-068 · GateRow.ok = boolean | null encodes three states that should be a tagged union
- **File**: `src/app/(dashboard)/allocations/lib/mandate-gates.ts:78`
- **Specialist**: `type-design-analyzer` (confidence 9)
- **Summary**: GateRow.ok is `boolean | null` where null means 'indeterminate' (threshold unset OR current value missing). Three distinct gates conflate: pass / fail / no-data. countPassingGates (L111-118) filters `ok !== null` to compute `decided.length` — but the same null is used by MandateSnapshotWidget's MandateGateLine (L139-147) to paint a muted dot. The widget can't distinguish 'threshold not set' from 'data not yet loaded', and the type can't express that distinction either; a future stale/loading state would need a fourth meaning crammed into the same null.
- **Evidence**: src/app/(dashboard)/allocations/lib/mandate-gates.ts:63-79
- **Fix**: Replace with `ok: 'pass' | 'fail' | 'no-threshold' | 'no-data'`. The widget then renders distinct dot states; countPassingGates computes only `pass`/`fail` totals. Display copy ('Auto-saved · N/M gates pass') becomes more honest about which gates are unknown vs muted.
