## G19 — PR #77 — Dashboard-parity PR3 (dual-month picker, empty-grid fallback)

### HIGH (13)

#### G19-001 · Empty-grid callout (HANDOFF G9) ships with zero direct tests
- **File**: `src/app/(dashboard)/allocations/AllocationDashboardV2.tsx:326`
- **Specialist**: `pr-test-analyzer` (confidence 10)
- **Summary**: The new conditional `filteredStrategyTileCount > 0` callout (`data-testid="empty-grid-callout"`) is a user-facing dashboard render path introduced by PR3. No test renders AllocationDashboardV2 with strategies=[] AND config.tiles containing a strategy-composite key to verify the callout appears, no test verifies the singular/plural copy switch (`widget` vs `widgets`), and no test verifies the `Browse strategies` Link points at `/discovery`. AllocationDashboardV2.widget-gating.test.tsx only covers the f2 filter list — not the callout. Future copy/href regressions ship silently.
- **Evidence**: grep 'empty-grid-callout' src/**/*.test.tsx → only AllocationDashboardV2.tsx:334; grep 'Connect a strategy' src/**/*.test.tsx → zero hits; grep 'filteredStrategyTileCount' src/**/*.test.tsx → zero hits
- **Fix**: Add `AllocationDashboardV2.empty-grid-callout.test.tsx` with 3 cases: (1) strategies=[] + config.tiles with single strategy-composite key → callout renders with 'unlock 1 widget' (singular); (2) strategies=[] + 3 strategy-composite tiles → 'unlock 3 widgets' (plural); (3) Link[href='/discovery'] is present with text 'Browse strategies →'; (4) strategies=[s1] → callout is absent even with strategy-composite tiles in config (filteredStrategyTileCount=0).

#### G19-002 · `tweaks.showOutcomes === false` outcomes-tile filter has no test
- **File**: `src/app/(dashboard)/allocations/AllocationDashboardV2.tsx:131`
- **Specialist**: `pr-test-analyzer` (confidence 10)
- **Summary**: PR3 added a second filter pass in `visibleTiles` useMemo that strips tiles with `k === "outcomes" || k === "outcomes-timeline"` when `tweaks.showOutcomes` is false (lines 131-138). This is consumer-facing: toggling the Outcomes widget Hide chip should remove the tile from the grid. The Tweaks suite verifies the localStorage write but NOT that the dashboard actually omits the tile when the knob flips. The dual-key handling (`"outcomes"` AND `"outcomes-timeline"`) is the kind of branch where copy/key changes silently regress.
- **Evidence**: grep 'showOutcomes' src/app/(dashboard)/allocations/AllocationDashboardV2.widget-gating.test.tsx → zero hits; grep 'outcomes-timeline' across allocations tests → only registry-barrel test (outcomes.test.tsx:774). No render of AllocationDashboardV2 inside a TweaksProvider that sets showOutcomes=false.
- **Fix**: Extend AllocationDashboardV2.widget-gating.test.tsx with a `showOutcomes filter` describe: render `<TweaksProvider><AllocationDashboardV2 ... config.tiles=[{k:'outcomes'}, {k:'outcomes-timeline'}, {k:'kpi-strip'}] /></TweaksProvider>`; toggle the panel (or seed localStorage with `showOutcomes:false`); assert WidgetGrid receives `tiles` containing only `kpi-strip`. Also assert the inverse: showOutcomes=true keeps both `outcomes` and `outcomes-timeline` tiles in the rendered grid.

#### G19-003 · Empty-grid fallback callout masks fetch failures for the strategies list
- **File**: `src/app/(dashboard)/allocations/AllocationDashboardV2.tsx:117`
- **Specialist**: `silent-failure-hunter` (confidence 8)
- **Summary**: `filteredStrategyTileCount` trips solely on `strategies.length === 0`. The new 'Connect a strategy to unlock N widgets' callout (the explicit HANDOFF G9 deliverable) treats two different states as identical: (a) the user genuinely has no strategies connected, or (b) the strategies query failed/returned an error payload and was coerced to an empty array somewhere upstream. The friendly callout 'helpfully' tells users to /discovery — which sends them on a goose chase if the real problem is a server error. There is no inspection of an error sentinel on `strategies`, no logError, and no telemetry for the empty-callout being shown. This is the canonical 'fallback to a friendly empty state' anti-pattern called out in the audit prompt.
- **Evidence**: src/app/(dashboard)/allocations/AllocationDashboardV2.tsx:117-121
- **Fix**: Widen `MyAllocationDashboardPayload.strategies` to carry an explicit error sentinel (e.g., `{ data: Strategy[] | null; error?: string }`). When `strategies.error` is set, render a distinct 'Failed to load strategies — Retry' affordance, not the friendly /discovery callout, and call `logError('strategies_load_failed', { portfolioId })`. At a minimum, when the callout would be rendered, fire a `trackUsageEventClient('empty_grid_callout_shown', { ... })` so an unexpected spike (suggesting an upstream regression instead of natural emptiness) is detectable.

#### G19-004 · CustomRangePicker dual-month picker silently swallows invalid date input from manual typing
- **File**: `src/app/(dashboard)/allocations/components/CustomRangePicker.tsx:284`
- **Specialist**: `silent-failure-hunter` (confidence 8)
- **Summary**: Both DateInput onChange handlers wrap parseISODate in a silent guard: `const d = parseISODate(v); if (d) { ... }`. When the user types something parseISODate rejects (e.g., partial '2024-' while still typing, paste of '2024/03/01' with slashes, or empty string after clear), the handler silently does nothing — no feedback, no aria-invalid, no validation message. The date input stays out of sync with React state, the user sees their typed value but `start`/`end` Date state is stale, and clicking Apply commits the OLD range silently. This is the exact 'dual-month picker try/catch that swallows invalid date input' pattern called out in the audit brief, just implemented as an `if (d)` guard instead of try/catch.
- **Evidence**: src/app/(dashboard)/allocations/components/CustomRangePicker.tsx:284-291, 305-307
- **Fix**: Track parse failures explicitly: when parseISODate returns null AND v is non-empty, set an `inputError` state and render aria-invalid + an inline 'Invalid date — use YYYY-MM-DD' helper text. Disable Apply until inputs round-trip cleanly. Also surface the silent clamp at line 287 (`clampDate(d, min, max)`) with a tooltip 'Clamped to available range' so users know why their typed date jumped — right now, typing 2020-01-01 with min=2024-01-01 silently substitutes 2024-01-01.

#### G19-005 · parseISODate accepts semantically invalid dates (month 13, day 99) and silently rolls over
- **File**: `src/app/(dashboard)/allocations/components/CustomRangePicker.tsx:54`
- **Specialist**: `silent-failure-hunter` (confidence 7)
- **Summary**: `parseISODate` only checks `Number.isFinite` on the three components, then constructs `new Date(y, m - 1, d)`. JavaScript's Date constructor silently rolls invalid components over: `new Date(2024, 12, 1)` becomes Jan 2025, `new Date(2024, 0, 99)` becomes Apr 8 2024. Users typing or pasting a malformed date like '2024-13-01' (or a typo '2024-02-31') get a silently coerced different date with no signal that their input was wrong. The user thinks they picked Jan 2025; the picker thinks they picked Jan 2025; nobody knows they typed '2024-13-01'. This compounds with the silent-clamp issue above to produce a date wildly different from what the user typed, with no log or visual feedback.
- **Evidence**: src/app/(dashboard)/allocations/components/CustomRangePicker.tsx:54-58
- **Fix**: Reject out-of-range components explicitly: `if (m < 1 || m > 12 || d < 1 || d > 31) return null;`. Stronger: after constructing the Date, verify round-trip: `if (parsed.getFullYear() !== y || parsed.getMonth() !== m-1 || parsed.getDate() !== d) return null;`. This catches Feb 31 etc. Combine with the inputError signaling from finding above so the user sees what's wrong.

#### G19-006 · CustomRangePicker's `min` Date and `max` Date have no compile-time guarantee min <= max
- **File**: `src/app/(dashboard)/allocations/components/CustomRangePicker.tsx:36`
- **Specialist**: `type-design-analyzer` (confidence 9)
- **Summary**: `Props.min: Date` and `Props.max: Date` are two independent Date parameters. The component uses both as bounds and invokes `clampDate(d, min, max)` everywhere, but if a caller passes `min > max` (a real possibility when `equityDailyPoints` is empty and `firstDate` returns `new Date()` while `max` is set to a historical 'today'), the clamp degenerates: `applyMax()` sets `start = min, end = max` producing `start > end` which makes the Apply guard permanently disable the button with no UI signal. This is the textbook 'invariant lives in documentation' case.
- **Evidence**: src/app/(dashboard)/allocations/components/CustomRangePicker.tsx:36-43 (Props), :79-83 (clampDate is broken when min > max), :145 (`invalid = start > end`), :201-206 (applyMax)
- **Fix**: Replace `min: Date; max: Date` with a `DateRange` value object: `class DateRange { constructor(public readonly start: Date, public readonly end: Date) { if (start > end) throw new Error('start must be <= end'); } }` (or branded type via factory). Callers like EquityChart construct it once at the boundary; the picker then accepts a single `DateRange` prop and the inversion bug is unrepresentable.

#### G19-007 · CustomRangePicker.onApply emits raw `{ start: string; end: string }` strings — no validity guarantee
- **File**: `src/app/(dashboard)/allocations/components/CustomRangePicker.tsx:39`
- **Specialist**: `type-design-analyzer` (confidence 9)
- **Summary**: `onApply` is typed as `(range: { start: string; end: string }) => void`. There is no compile-time guarantee that start/end are ISO-8601 dates, that start <= end, or that they fall within [min, max]. The component's internal `invalid` guard catches start>end at click-time, but on the consumer side (EquityChart) the strings flow into `parseISO` and missing/malformed dates result in NaN epochs silently dropping points. Identical shape used at `initialRange?: { start: string; end: string } | null` so the same untyped strings flow in.
- **Evidence**: src/app/(dashboard)/allocations/components/CustomRangePicker.tsx:39 (onApply signature), :42 (initialRange shape), :208-211 (apply emits raw startIso/endIso); EquityChart parseISO at src/app/(dashboard)/allocations/widgets/performance/EquityChart.tsx:135-143 (NaN-fallback path)
- **Fix**: Define a branded ISODate type (`type ISODate = string & { readonly __brand: 'ISODate' }`) and a `ValidDateRange` value object with private constructor validated via `DateRange.tryParse(start, end, { min, max }): Result<DateRange, string>`. onApply emits `DateRange`, initialRange takes `DateRange | null`. Consumers like EquityChart never see raw strings.

#### G19-008 · CustomRangePicker uses dual independent Date state (start, end) — illegal start > end state representable
- **File**: `src/app/(dashboard)/allocations/components/CustomRangePicker.tsx:95`
- **Specialist**: `type-design-analyzer` (confidence 8)
- **Summary**: Internal state is `const [start, setStart] = useState<Date>(...)` and `const [end, setEnd] = useState<Date>(...)` — two independent useState calls. Every mutation path (`pickDay`, `applyPreset`, manual DateInput onChange) has to maintain the invariant `start <= end` by hand. `DateInput` for End simply calls `setEnd(clampDate(d, min, max))` with no check that the new `end >= start` — so typing an End date earlier than Start puts the component into the `invalid = start > end` state, which only disables Apply (no in-grid feedback). This is the 'dual-month picker range types' issue called out in the audit brief.
- **Evidence**: src/app/(dashboard)/allocations/components/CustomRangePicker.tsx:95-108 (two separate useState calls), :145 (`invalid = start > end`), :304-307 (End DateInput onChange has no start-side guard), :155-170 (pickDay handles ordering manually)
- **Fix**: Collapse to a single reducer over a `DateRange` value object: `const [range, dispatch] = useReducer(rangeReducer, initial)`. Actions like `{ type: 'pickStart', d }` validate ordering inside the reducer; illegal states can't be set. Eliminates the `invalid` flag and all the by-hand reordering in pickDay.

#### G19-009 · WidgetProps.data typed as `any` defeats type system at every widget boundary
- **File**: `src/app/(dashboard)/allocations/lib/types.ts:80`
- **Specialist**: `type-design-analyzer` (confidence 9)
- **Summary**: `WidgetProps.data: any` is the contract every widget renders through. BridgeHeroWidget reaches into it with `data as { __error?: unknown }` and `data as MyAllocationDashboardPayload | undefined`. Any payload shape change goes uncaught — including breaking `data.flaggedHoldings`, `data.matchDecisionsByHoldingRef`, `data.outcomes` renames. This is exactly the `Data | null` anti-pattern called out in the audit brief: a discriminated union over { kind: 'ok', payload: T } | { kind: 'error', message: string } | { kind: 'loading' } would make illegal states unrepresentable and force every widget to handle each branch.
- **Evidence**: src/app/(dashboard)/allocations/lib/types.ts:78-84; src/app/(dashboard)/allocations/widgets/bridge/BridgeHeroWidget.tsx:30-32 (`data as { __error?: unknown }`), :55 (`data as MyAllocationDashboardPayload | undefined`)
- **Fix**: Make `WidgetProps` generic: `interface WidgetProps<T = unknown> { data: WidgetData<T>; ... }` where `type WidgetData<T> = { kind: 'ok'; value: T } | { kind: 'error'; message: string } | { kind: 'loading' }`. Each widget then narrows on `data.kind` and gets compile-time enforcement that it handles error/loading branches. At minimum, change `any` to `unknown` so callers are forced to narrow.

#### G19-010 · BridgeHeroWidget encodes 3-state (ok / error / loading) via truthiness checks on `any`
- **File**: `src/app/(dashboard)/allocations/widgets/bridge/BridgeHeroWidget.tsx:30`
- **Specialist**: `type-design-analyzer` (confidence 9)
- **Summary**: The widget detects error state via `data && typeof data === 'object' && (data as { __error?: unknown }).__error` — a magic `__error` sentinel injected on `any`. Loading is never represented (just empty arrays). This is precisely the `Data | null` / truthiness-instead-of-tagged-union anti-pattern. A typo like `__erorr` would silently render the empty payload, and there's no way for TS to verify the producer and consumer agree on the sentinel name. The same pattern recurs across widgets.
- **Evidence**: src/app/(dashboard)/allocations/widgets/bridge/BridgeHeroWidget.tsx:30-32 (sentinel detection), :42 (`hasError` branch), :55-62 (silently coalesces `payload?.flaggedHoldings ?? []` so 'data missing' and 'data is empty' are indistinguishable)
- **Fix**: Replace the `__error` sentinel with a tagged union at the WidgetProps boundary (see prior finding). Producers (loader / fetcher) emit `{ kind: 'error', message }` instead of mutating an `__error` property onto a record. The hero adapter then narrows via `switch (data.kind)` and TS guarantees all three branches are handled.

#### G19-011 · CustomRangePicker `min` bound is off-by-one for non-UTC users (parseISO returns UTC-midnight)
- **File**: `src/app/(dashboard)/allocations/widgets/performance/EquityChart.tsx:207`
- **Specialist**: `code-reviewer` (confidence 9)
- **Summary**: `firstDate()` and `minDate` build a Date from `parseISO()` which returns `Date.UTC(y,m-1,d)`. Wrapping that epoch in `new Date(...)` produces an instant that, when read with local-time methods (`.getFullYear/.getMonth/.getDate`), is the PREVIOUS calendar day for any user west of UTC. CustomRangePicker then compares this UTC-anchored `min` against user-clicked dates built with `new Date(y,m-1,d)` (local midnight) via `<`/`>`, and re-serializes via `toISODate(min)` which uses local methods. Net effect for users in e.g. America/Los_Angeles: the picker's `min` ISO is one day BEFORE the true first-positive day, and the disabled-cell math in MonthGrid is shifted by a day. Tests pass because CI runs in UTC.
- **Evidence**: src/app/(dashboard)/allocations/widgets/performance/EquityChart.tsx:135 `return Date.UTC(y, m - 1, d);` then line 207-210 `function firstDate(points){ return new Date(parseISO(points[0].date)); }` and line 1300-1305 `const minDate = useMemo(() => new Date(parseISO(anchored[0].date)),...)`. Picker call sites pass these to `<CustomRangePicker min={...} max={new Date()} />` (lines 681, 1477). Inside CustomRangePicker.tsx:47-58 `toISODate(d)`/`parseISODate(s)` use local-time methods, mixing timezones with the UTC-anchored `min`.
- **Fix**: Make `parseISO` return a local-midnight Date object (e.g. `new Date(y, m-1, d)`) or change `firstDate`/`minDate` to build a Date via `new Date(y, m-1, d)` from the ISO string rather than from a UTC epoch. Alternatively, keep all comparisons in UTC by reading min/max via `getUTCFullYear/getUTCMonth/getUTCDate` inside CustomRangePicker. Pick one timezone convention and apply consistently across `parseISO`, `firstDate`, `toISODate`, and `parseISODate`.

#### G19-012 · EquityChart `chartStyle === "line"` branch never asserts the area path is absent
- **File**: `src/app/(dashboard)/allocations/widgets/performance/EquityChart.tsx:682`
- **Specialist**: `pr-test-analyzer` (confidence 9)
- **Summary**: PR3 wrapped the gradient-fill `<path d={toArea(...)} fill='url(#eq-grad)'>` in `{chartStyle === 'area' && ...}` (line 682). When the Tweaks knob flips to Line, the area path is removed. No EquityChart test verifies this — the existing test only renames the legacy 'always-visible return summary' case to a 'sync just now' stamp. The `showBench` filter (line 559, 654) is also new but uncovered by tests. A regression that hardcodes `chartStyle='area'` (or inverts the boolean) lands silently and ships a chart that ignores the user's preference.
- **Evidence**: grep 'chartStyle\|showBench\|useTweakValue' src/app/(dashboard)/allocations/widgets/performance/EquityChart.test.tsx → zero hits; EquityChart.tsx:680-687 contains the new conditional area-path branch; EquityChart.tsx:559 contains `{showBench && visibleBenchmarkNormalized && (...)}`
- **Fix**: Add `EquityChart.tweaks.test.tsx` with 4 cases inside a TweaksProvider: (1) chartStyle=area → SVG contains a `<path>` with `fill="url(#eq-grad)"`; (2) chartStyle=line → that path is absent; (3) showBench=true → 'BTC' legend chip + dashed benchmark path present; (4) showBench=false → benchmark legend chip + path both absent. Seed via `localStorage.setItem('allocations.tweaks', JSON.stringify({chartStyle:'line', showBench:false, ...defaults}))` so the provider hydrates to the under-test state.

#### G19-013 · InsightStrip silently disappears when analytics is null — fetch failures indistinguishable from 'no insights fired'
- **File**: `src/components/portfolio/InsightStrip.tsx:94`
- **Specialist**: `silent-failure-hunter` (confidence 9)
- **Summary**: `if (insights.length === 0 && !flaggedCount) return null;` collapses two semantically different states into one render-nothing path: (a) analytics fetched successfully and no rules fired, vs (b) analytics is null because the upstream fetch/computation failed. `computeAllInsights(null, ...)` always returns []. The user has no signal that the 'What we noticed' strip is missing because of an error — it just disappears. With the empty-state fallback explicitly removed in this PR ('No unusual activity in the trailing window'), there is now zero UI evidence that analytics ever failed to load. No logError, no Sentry breadcrumb, no console warning. The new behavior is shipped via the diff at line 94 alongside a dead-code branch at line 106 (`{false ? (` — eslint-bypassed dead conditional that proves the author saw the empty-state path and chose to hide it without preserving an error channel).
- **Evidence**: src/components/portfolio/InsightStrip.tsx:94
- **Fix**: Distinguish failure from absence at the call site: AllocationDashboardV2 should pass a typed `analytics: PortfolioAnalytics | null | { error: true }` (or a separate `analyticsError` prop) so the strip can render a 'Something went wrong loading insights — retry' affordance instead of disappearing. At a minimum: when `analytics === null` AND `portfolioId` is present, call `logError('insight_strip_analytics_null', { portfolioId })` so the silent state at least shows up in Sentry. Also remove the `{false ? (...)` dead branch at line 106 — it's lint-bypassed and confuses future readers.

Future CSS-token or theme-config changes will silently drift the dashboard away from the truth screenshot, and the only signal will be manual review. Given the PR's stated goal is pixel parity, the absence of any pixel-level regression detector is the highest-leverage testing gap.

Commit the baseline PNGs and gate on a 2% threshold. Alternative if Playwright is overkill: jest-image-snapshot against the rendered DOM as PNG via @testing-library + canvas, scoped to the three tab-row states (Overview/Holdings/Risk).

#### G19-015 · Empty-grid fallback misses the case where `tweaks.showOutcomes=false` is the only reason the grid is empty
- **File**: `src/app/(dashboard)/allocations/AllocationDashboardV2.tsx:117`
- **Specialist**: `code-reviewer` (confidence 8)
- **Summary**: `filteredStrategyTileCount` only counts strategy-composite tiles filtered by the f2 gate, not tiles hidden by the `showOutcomes` tweak. `visibleTiles` (line 126-140) additionally filters `outcomes`/`outcomes-timeline` when the user toggles `showOutcomes` off. If the user has e.g. `tiles=[outcomes]` and toggles outcomes off, `visibleTiles=[]` while `filteredStrategyTileCount=0`, so WidgetGrid renders an empty grid with NO callout — the very 'unexpectedly sparse layout' the G9 callout was supposed to prevent. WidgetGrid itself has no empty state.
- **Evidence**: src/app/(dashboard)/allocations/AllocationDashboardV2.tsx:117-121 `const filteredStrategyTileCount = useMemo(() => { if (strategies.length > 0) return 0; return config.tiles.filter((t) => STRATEGY_COMPOSITE_WIDGETS.has(t.k)).length; }, [config.tiles, strategies.length]);` and line 326 `{filteredStrategyTileCount > 0 ? <empty-grid callout> : null}` — no other branch surfaces emptiness.
- **Fix**: Trigger the fallback whenever `visibleTiles.length === 0 && config.tiles.length > 0` (i.e. user has tiles configured but the gate hid them all). Or render a generic 'No widgets visible' note when `visibleTiles.length === 0` and the holdings empty-state short-circuit hasn't fired. The current text ('Connect a strategy to unlock N widgets') is only correct in the strategies-empty case; surface a different copy when the cause is `showOutcomes=false`.

#### G19-016 · renderWidget useCallback depends on full props bag; tile renders thrash on every payload poll
- **File**: `src/app/(dashboard)/allocations/AllocationDashboardV2.tsx:229`
- **Specialist**: `performance` (confidence 8)
- **Summary**: renderWidget = useCallback((k) => <Component data={props as any} … />, [props, config.timeframe]). The `props` object is the entire MyAllocationDashboardPayload, which gets a new reference on every router.refresh() poll (30s interval in AllocationsTabs.tsx:263-269) because the SSR boundary re-creates the payload object on each refresh. So every 30s: renderWidget identity changes → WidgetGrid receives a new prop ref → every tile re-renders with a fresh `data` ref → each widget's useMemo deps that observe `data` (e.g., EquityChartWidget reads d.equityDailyPoints) invalidate even when the underlying array reference is stable. The diff doesn't introduce renderWidget but does introduce the renderWidget consumer set (AllocationsTabs polling already existed; this batch routes more widgets through the same path). Worth flagging because the new Tweaks-context subscriptions in EquityChart + BridgeHeroWidget amplify the cascade — a context invalidation now also forces this whole tree through one more render.
- **Evidence**: src/app/(dashboard)/allocations/AllocationDashboardV2.tsx:229-259
- **Fix**: Either (a) destructure `props` once into the specific slices each widget needs and pass only those slices, with stable references for each, OR (b) split `renderWidget` per-tile using a useMemo'd map keyed on `k` so a payload change only invalidates the widgets that actually depend on the changed slice, OR (c) at minimum, hoist the `props as any` cast out so the destructured fields are referenced individually in the useCallback deps array (props.equityDailyPoints, props.flaggedHoldings, etc.) — keeps the closure but lets React skip the re-create when only an unrelated payload slice mutates.

#### G19-017 · Unknown widget render dispatcher hides production breakage in a quiet inline note
- **File**: `src/app/(dashboard)/allocations/AllocationDashboardV2.tsx:232`
- **Specialist**: `silent-failure-hunter` (confidence 8)
- **Summary**: When `WIDGET_COMPONENTS[k]` is undefined (e.g., a stale localStorage layout still references a widget id that no longer ships), the dispatcher renders an inline 'Unknown widget: <code>' note. There is no logError, no trackUsageEventClient, no Sentry breadcrumb. In production, a widget rename or removal will silently leave allocators staring at a friendly text note instead of their saved widget, and the engineering team has no telemetry that this is happening. This is the 'fallbacks must be explicit and justified' rule violation — the fallback is justified (don't crash the grid) but masks the underlying state-versioning problem.
- **Evidence**: src/app/(dashboard)/allocations/AllocationDashboardV2.tsx:229-241
- **Fix**: Inside the `if (!Component)` branch, before returning the note, call `trackUsageEventClient('unknown_widget_id_rendered', { widget_id: k, tiles: config.tiles.length })` and `logError('unknown_widget_id', { widget_id: k })`. This gives engineering a Sentry signal when a tile id disappears from the registry without a migration step, and lets product see usage so the orphan tile can be pruned from saved layouts.

#### G19-018 · AllocationDashboardV2 outcomes filter compares both 'outcomes' and 'outcomes-timeline' tile keys — registry id ambiguity persists in the type
- **File**: `src/app/(dashboard)/allocations/AllocationDashboardV2.tsx:135`
- **Specialist**: `type-design-analyzer` (confidence 8)
- **Summary**: The new tweaks filter does `t.k !== 'outcomes' && t.k !== 'outcomes-timeline'`. The inline comment admits 'Outcomes-timeline tile registry id can come from either the short key "outcomes" (truth default) or the full id "outcomes-timeline" (post-normalization layouts).' This is a type-design failure: `t.k` is typed as `string` but the domain has two coexisting registry-id conventions that mean the same logical widget. Any new widget with a short/long alias will repeat the bug if a future maintainer forgets to include both branches.
- **Evidence**: src/app/(dashboard)/allocations/AllocationDashboardV2.tsx:131-138 (filter); diff comment at batch-G19.diff:251-256 admits two registry-id conventions
- **Fix**: Define `type WidgetId = 'overview' | 'outcomes-timeline' | 'bridge-hero' | ...` as a string literal union (replace the `Set<string>` of STRATEGY_COMPOSITE_WIDGETS), and a `normalizeWidgetId(raw: string): WidgetId | null` factory used at the write boundary so `TileConfig.k: WidgetId` is enforced. Then `t.k === 'outcomes-timeline'` is a single comparison the compiler can audit.

#### G19-019 · Tab-row count badges (Holdings/Outcomes) ship without tests
- **File**: `src/app/(dashboard)/allocations/AllocationsTabs.tsx:493`
- **Specialist**: `pr-test-analyzer` (confidence 9)
- **Summary**: PR3's new `tabCount` derivation (`holdingsCount = props.holdingsSummary?.length ?? 0; outcomesCount = props.outcomes?.length ?? 0`) and the count-badge render branch (`typeof count === 'number' && count > 0`) are user-facing affordances claimed in the CHANGELOG. AllocationsTabs.test.tsx has no test that passes a populated holdingsSummary/outcomes and asserts the count badge appears, no test that verifies count=0 hides the badge, and no test of the null-coalescing fallback (props.holdingsSummary=undefined → 0). Future schema changes to either array silently break the affordance.
- **Evidence**: grep 'tabCount\|count badge\|holdingsCount\|outcomesCount' src/app/(dashboard)/allocations/AllocationsTabs.test.tsx → zero hits; AllocationsTabs.tsx:493-497 derives counts; AllocationsTabs.tsx:534-545 renders the badge conditionally.
- **Fix**: Extend AllocationsTabs.test.tsx with: (1) props with holdingsSummary=[h1,h2,h3] → Holdings tab contains text '3' within the badge span; (2) outcomes=[] → Outcomes tab has no count badge; (3) props.holdingsSummary=undefined → no crash, no badge. Use `within(screen.getByRole('tab', {name:/Holdings/})).getByText('3')` to anchor on the badge.

#### G19-020 · Export chip stub has no test — silent regression risk for accidental Holdings-route removal
- **File**: `src/app/(dashboard)/allocations/AllocationsTabs.tsx:463`

AllocationsTabs.widget-chip.test.tsx covers the Widget chip but NOT the Export chip — no assertion that clicking Export navigates to Holdings. When the next PR wires up real export logic, the chip will be re-implemented and the routing fallback can silently disappear (the user clicks Export from Risk and nothing happens). Low-cost test that protects the stub contract.

#### G19-021 · AllocationsTabs Export chip silently routes user to Holdings without explaining why
- **File**: `src/app/(dashboard)/allocations/AllocationsTabs.tsx:580`
- **Specialist**: `silent-failure-hunter` (confidence 8)
- **Summary**: The new Export chip's onClick is `changeTab('holdings')` with comment 'Stub: export-CSV / export-PDF flows are owned by the Holdings tab today.' A user clicking 'Export' from the Risk tab is silently teleported to Holdings with zero feedback about why. No toast, no breadcrumb, no aria-live. The chip is labeled 'Export' but performs 'navigate to Holdings'. Users will report 'I clicked Export from Risk and nothing happened (it just navigated me away)'. This is a fallback to a stub that the audit rules explicitly call out — 'Mock/fake implementations belong only in tests'. Production code shipping an Export chip that silently navigates away is exactly the anti-pattern.
- **Evidence**: src/app/(dashboard)/allocations/AllocationsTabs.tsx:578-595
- **Fix**: Either (a) hide the Export chip entirely until the global export surface lands (the cleanest answer per Rule 2 'Simplicity First — no features beyond what was asked'), (b) make the chip a Holdings-tab-only affordance so it doesn't appear when the user can't reach it, or (c) on click, show a small toast 'Export lives in the Holdings tab — taking you there' so the navigation is at least explained. The current behavior surprises the user and looks like the button is broken.

#### G19-022 · CustomEvent dispatch for widget picker has no listener-presence guard or telemetry
- **File**: `src/app/(dashboard)/allocations/AllocationsTabs.tsx:564`
- **Specialist**: `silent-failure-hunter` (confidence 8)
- **Summary**: The Widget chip dispatches `window.dispatchEvent(new CustomEvent('allocations:open-widget-picker'))` and assumes AllocationDashboardV2 is mounted to receive it. If the user clicks the Widget chip on Risk tab and the Overview tab's AllocationDashboardV2 isn't yet mounted (Risk panel is lazy-loaded; Overview isn't, but a future regression could change that), the CustomEvent fires into the void with no error and no fallback. There is no telemetry tracking 'Widget chip clicked but picker never opened', so the silent-failure case is invisible to engineering. The cross-component CustomEvent bridge is a clever workaround for prop-drilling, but it introduces an invisible coupling that fails silently when broken.
- **Evidence**: src/app/(dashboard)/allocations/AllocationsTabs.tsx:556-566
- **Fix**: Track the dispatch: `trackUsageEventClient('open_widget_picker_dispatched', { source: 'tab_row_chip' })` and have the AllocationDashboardV2 listener track `'open_widget_picker_received'`. If the two counts diverge in analytics, you have a silent-dispatch problem. Better: lift picker state to AllocationsTabs (the parent that owns the chip and the dashboard) so the bridge is direct, not event-based — the comment 'event-based bridge avoids hoisting picker state' is choosing convenience over loud failures.

#### G19-023 · CustomRangePicker positioned absolutely with no overflow guard — picker is clipped on small screens / when chart is near the viewport edge
- **File**: `src/app/(dashboard)/allocations/components/CustomRangePicker.tsx:218`
- **Specialist**: `code-reviewer` (confidence 8)
- **Summary**: The popover root uses `position: absolute; top: calc(100% + 6px); right: 0;` and the calendar area declares `minWidth: 520`. There is no viewport-edge collision detection. On screens narrower than ~660px, or when the EquityChart period toggle is rendered near the viewport's right/bottom edge (e.g. half-screen window, narrow tab panel), the picker is clipped off the visible area with no way to scroll to it — making the picker unusable. The earlier single-month range picker fit in ~320px, so the regression is specific to the dual-month layout introduced here.
- **Evidence**: src/app/(dashboard)/allocations/components/CustomRangePicker.tsx:213-230 `<div ref={ref} role='dialog' style={{ position: 'absolute', top: 'calc(100% + 6px)', right: 0, zIndex: 50, ..., display: 'flex', ... }}>` plus presets rail width 130 (line 235) + calendar `minWidth: 520` (line 268) gives a ~650px popover with no edge guard.
- **Fix**: Add a min-width media query or measure the rect and flip `right: 0` to `left: 0` (or use a portal anchored relative to viewport) when the popover would overflow. At minimum, wrap the calendar area in `flex-wrap` so it stacks below the presets rail on narrow viewports, or expose an `align='left'` prop and let EquityChartWidget pick the orientation based on its position.

#### G19-024 · CustomRangePicker setViewMonth on every valid keystroke forces dual MonthGrid recompute
- **File**: `src/app/(dashboard)/allocations/components/CustomRangePicker.tsx:284`
- **Specialist**: `performance` (confidence 8)
- **Summary**: The Start date input's onChange handler (lines 284-291) parses the typed value and, on every successful parse, calls setStart(c) AND setViewMonth(startOfMonth(c)). As the user types '2026-05-15' the picker re-parses each intermediate value; on every valid date the viewMonth state changes, which invalidates the `cells = useMemo([month])` dep in BOTH MonthGrid instances, regenerating 42-element Date arrays × 2 months × N keystrokes. Compounded by the fact that DayCell is not React.memo-wrapped — all 84 DayCells re-render on every state change inside the picker. UX is also poor: the calendar jumps to whatever month the user is partway through typing.
- **Evidence**: src/app/(dashboard)/allocations/components/CustomRangePicker.tsx:284-291
- **Fix**: Either (a) drop the setViewMonth(startOfMonth(c)) call from the Start input's onChange — the user can navigate to the typed month manually if needed, and the Apply path won't move the view anyway, OR (b) only update viewMonth on Enter / blur, not on every onChange. Also wrap DayCell in React.memo with a shallow-equality comparator so the 84-cell rerender storm collapses to only the cells whose state actually changed.

#### G19-025 · CustomRangePicker month-navigation arrows have no test for actual month advance
- **File**: `src/app/(dashboard)/allocations/components/CustomRangePicker.tsx:563`
- **Specialist**: `pr-test-analyzer` (confidence 9)
- **Summary**: PR3 added `aria-label='Previous month'` and `aria-label='Next month'` nav buttons that call `setViewMonth(addMonths(viewMonth, -1))` / `+1`. The only assertion is `expect(getAllByText('‹').length).toBeGreaterThanOrEqual(1)` — that the glyph exists, not that clicking it advances the displayed month label. Off-by-one or wrong-sign regressions in `addMonths` ship silently. Also no test of cross-year boundary (Dec→Jan) or the leap-year February (2024-02-29 is a leap day; current MIN/MAX dates would render it).
- **Evidence**: grep 'Previous month\|Next month\|setViewMonth' src/app/(dashboard)/allocations/components/CustomRangePicker.test.tsx → zero hits; CustomRangePicker.tsx:333 dispatches `setViewMonth(addMonths(viewMonth, -1))`; CustomRangePicker.tsx:64 `addMonths` uses `.setMonth(x.getMonth() + n)` which has known JS quirks at month boundaries (Jan 31 + 1 month = March 3, not Feb 28).
- **Fix**: Add to CustomRangePicker.test.tsx: (1) click 'Previous month' on the left grid, assert leftMonth label flips from e.g. 'April 2024' → 'March 2024' AND rightMonth flips from 'May 2024' → 'April 2024'; (2) navigate across year boundary (min=2023-12-01, max=2024-02-01, initial viewMonth=2024-01) clicking ‹ shows 'December 2023'; (3) initialRange spanning leap day 2024-02-29 renders without throwing and the date cell `29` is clickable in February.

#### G19-026 · CustomRangePicker `pickDay` two-click range selection has no test
- **File**: `src/app/(dashboard)/allocations/components/CustomRangePicker.tsx:155`
- **Specialist**: `pr-test-analyzer` (confidence 9)
- **Summary**: The PR3 grid's primary interaction — clicking two day cells to set start/end — is entirely untested. `pickDay` has a non-trivial state machine: first click sets start=end=d and flips pickMode to 'end'; second click branches on `d < start` (swap into [d, prevStart]) vs `d >= start` (set end=d) and flips pickMode back to 'start'. The clamping guard (`if (d < min || d > max) return`) is also untested. Bugs in this state machine produce wrong ranges silently — the user thinks they picked Apr 10 → Apr 20 but onApply fires with Apr 20 → Apr 20. No existing test clicks any `DayCell`.
- **Evidence**: grep 'DayCell\|pickDay\|onPick' src/app/(dashboard)/allocations/components/CustomRangePicker.test.tsx → zero hits; CustomRangePicker.tsx:155-170 defines the state machine with three branches; CustomRangePicker.tsx:684 wires `onClick={() => !disabled && onPick(d)}`
- **Fix**: Add CustomRangePicker.test.tsx cases: (1) click day cell for Apr 10 then Apr 20 → Apply fires {start:'2024-04-10', end:'2024-04-20'}; (2) click Apr 20 then Apr 10 (reverse order) → range swaps to {start:'2024-04-10', end:'2024-04-20'}; (3) click a day < min → state unchanged (no setStart, no setEnd); (4) click same day twice → start === end and dayCount chip reads '1 day' (singular).

#### G19-027 · Range-picker date-input edits (manual typing) have no test post-PR3
- **File**: `src/app/(dashboard)/allocations/components/CustomRangePicker.tsx:278`
- **Specialist**: `pr-test-analyzer` (confidence 8)
- **Summary**: PR3 refactored the date inputs to parse, clamp, AND sync viewMonth on every change (`setStart(c); setViewMonth(startOfMonth(c));`). The previous test that typed a value into the start input (`fireEvent.change(startInput, {target: {value: '2024-05-01'}})`) survived the refactor, but no test verifies the viewMonth side effect — manual editing should advance the visible calendar so the user sees their typed date highlighted. A regression here strands users typing 2024-12-15 while the calendar stays on April. Also no test verifies the clamp behavior (typing 2025-12-01 with max=2024-06-30 → state stays at 2024-06-30, not the user's input).
- **Evidence**: CustomRangePicker.tsx:284-290 wires the start onChange with clamp+setViewMonth; CustomRangePicker.test.tsx only tests `applyBtn.disabled` after a typed change, not viewMonth advance or clamp.
- **Fix**: Add CustomRangePicker.test.tsx: (1) type Start='2024-05-15' → assert one of the MonthGrid headers reads 'May 2024'; (2) type Start='2099-01-01' (above max) → input value displays clamped maxIso and Apply fires onApply.end (NOT 2099-01-01); (3) type Start with malformed value ('not-a-date') → parseISODate returns null → no state change, no crash.

#### G19-028 · CustomRangePicker silently clamps user-typed dates to min/max boundary without feedback
- **File**: `src/app/(dashboard)/allocations/components/CustomRangePicker.tsx:287`
- **Specialist**: `silent-failure-hunter` (confidence 8)
- **Summary**: `clampDate(d, min, max)` silently rewrites a user's typed date if it falls outside the allowed window. User types '2024-01-01', min is '2024-03-15', the input value becomes '2024-03-15' with no indication that their input was modified. The HTML `min`/`max` attributes prevent the date-picker spinner from crossing, but copy-paste and direct typing bypass that. The user sees their date change without understanding why; no aria-live message, no tooltip, no log. Compounds with the parseISODate finding above: 2024-13-99 silently coerces to Apr 8 2025, then silently clamps to max, giving the user a wildly different date with no breadcrumbs.
- **Evidence**: src/app/(dashboard)/allocations/components/CustomRangePicker.tsx:287, 306
- **Fix**: When `clampDate` modifies the input, render an aria-live='polite' helper text below the input ('Clamped to allowed range: 2024-03-15 to 2024-06-30'). Track the clamp event via `trackUsageEventClient('date_range_clamped', { typed: v, clamped: toISODate(c) })` so product sees how often users hit the boundary.

#### G19-029 · CustomRangePicker apply() silently returns when invalid range, providing only the disabled button as feedback
- **File**: `src/app/(dashboard)/allocations/components/CustomRangePicker.tsx:208`
- **Specialist**: `silent-failure-hunter` (confidence 8)
- **Summary**: `function apply() { if (invalid) return; onApply({ start: startIso, end: endIso }); }` swallows the invalid case silently. The Apply button is disabled in this state, but the function is callable from any code path (e.g., a future Enter-key submit handler), and the silent return means an invariant violation never surfaces. There is no logError, no console.warn. While the user-facing UX is okay because the button is disabled, the underlying function is a silent failure waiting to be re-bound to a keyboard shortcut that bypasses the disabled state.
- **Evidence**: src/app/(dashboard)/allocations/components/CustomRangePicker.tsx:208-211
- **Fix**: Either remove the silent guard and rely entirely on the disabled button (let the caller fail loudly if they bypass it), or surface the failure: `if (invalid) { logError('range_picker_invalid_apply', { start: startIso, end: endIso }); return; }`. The disabled UI is the user-facing affordance; the function-level guard should be a noisy assertion, not a quiet no-op.

#### G19-030 · pickDay silently no-ops on out-of-range click rather than asserting unreachability
- **File**: `src/app/(dashboard)/allocations/components/CustomRangePicker.tsx:156`
- **Specialist**: `silent-failure-hunter` (confidence 8)
- **Summary**: `function pickDay(d: Date) { if (d < min || d > max) return; ... }`. The day cells already disable out-of-range clicks at the button level (`disabled: d < earliest || d > latest`), so a click reaching pickDay with an out-of-range date is a programming error. The silent return swallows that invariant. If a future refactor accidentally drops the `disabled` attribute or the `!disabled && onPick(d)` guard, pickDay will silently swallow the click with no log — turning a visible bug into an invisible one.
- **Evidence**: src/app/(dashboard)/allocations/components/CustomRangePicker.tsx:155-157
- **Fix**: Replace the silent return with a dev-mode assertion: `if (d < min || d > max) { if (process.env.NODE_ENV !== 'production') console.warn('pickDay called with out-of-range date', { d, min, max }); return; }`. Or remove the guard entirely and rely on the disabled-button + onClick guard upstream — duplicate defense is fine, but it should be loud about the upstream having failed.

#### G19-031 · TweaksContext hardcodes accent hex `#0E9F84` instead of referencing DESIGN.md tokens
- **File**: `src/app/(dashboard)/allocations/context/TweaksContext.tsx:129`
- **Specialist**: `code-reviewer` (confidence 8)
- **Summary**: The 'Full' accent intensity branch writes literal hex colors (`#0E9F84`, `#0B8870`) directly onto `documentElement.style`, bypassing the DESIGN.md token system the rest of the codebase uses. Per CLAUDE.md ('All font choices, colors, spacing, and aesthetic direction are defined there. Do not deviate without explicit user approval.'), this is a guardrail violation. If DESIGN.md's accent ever changes, this code stays wrong and the 'Full' tweak drifts away from the rest of the app's palette.
- **Evidence**: src/app/(dashboard)/allocations/context/TweaksContext.tsx:126-138 `if (state.accentIntensity === 'full') { root.style.setProperty('--color-accent', '#0E9F84'); root.style.setProperty('--color-accent-hover', '#0B8870'); root.style.setProperty('--color-chart-strategy', '#0E9F84'); } else { root.style.removeProperty(...); }`
- **Fix**: Source the 'full' accent values from a CSS variable defined in globals.css (e.g. `--color-accent-full`, `--color-accent-hover-full`) and read them via `getComputedStyle(root).getPropertyValue('--color-accent-full')` before applying, or just toggle a body attribute like `data-accent='full'` and let globals.css drive both the default and full variants from DESIGN.md tokens.

#### G19-032 · `data-density` cleanup removes the body attribute when TweaksProvider unmounts, dropping density across the app
- **File**: `src/app/(dashboard)/allocations/context/TweaksContext.tsx:104`
- **Specialist**: `code-reviewer` (confidence 8)
- **Summary**: `useEffect` cleanup for the density side-effect runs `document.body.removeAttribute('data-density')` on every density change AND on provider unmount. The body attribute is global state shared across the whole app — a future caller that mounts another consumer of `--row-h` on a non-allocations route would lose the density token entirely. Same global-attribute pattern for `data-display-font` (line 116-121). The accent-intensity effect (line 126-138) has the inverse asymmetry: it has NO cleanup, so when the provider unmounts the inline `--color-accent` overrides persist forever on `documentElement`.
- **Evidence**: src/app/(dashboard)/allocations/context/TweaksContext.tsx:104-109 `useEffect(() => { document.body.setAttribute('data-density', state.density); return () => { document.body.removeAttribute('data-density'); }; }, [state.density]);` — note the removeAttribute cleanup. Contrast with line 126-138 where no cleanup is returned for the inline-style branch.
- **Fix**: Drop the cleanup that removes the body attribute (let it persist with the latest value); reset by setting to the default instead of removing when accent intensity flips back to `muted`. For the accent effect, add a cleanup that removes the three inline `--color-*` properties on unmount so the dashboard route doesn't leave a stale palette behind.

#### G19-033 · TweaksContext hydration ordering (no-overwrite-before-hydration) is untested
- **File**: `src/app/(dashboard)/allocations/context/TweaksContext.tsx:91`
- **Specialist**: `pr-test-analyzer` (confidence 8)
- **Summary**: TweaksContext.tsx introduces a `hydrated` boolean gate (line 81) so the persist-effect doesn't overwrite stored localStorage with TWEAK_DEFAULTS on the initial render before the hydrate-effect runs. This race is exactly the bug pattern that loses user preferences. The Tweaks.test.tsx 'restores persisted state on mount' test renders WITH localStorage pre-seeded, but no test asserts the inverse — that mounting a Harness with a clean localStorage does NOT write TWEAK_DEFAULTS first (which would clobber a concurrent write from another tab) and only writes after a user actually toggles a knob.
- **Evidence**: TweaksContext.tsx:91-99 has `if (!hydrated) return;` guard with no test pinning the behavior; Tweaks.test.tsx has no assertion on `localStorageMock.setItem.mock.calls.length` after a clean render (the count should be 0 after mount, 1 after first user toggle).
- **Fix**: Add Tweaks.test.tsx 'hydration' case: clear localStorageMock.setItem.mock.calls, render `<Harness />`, await microtasks; assert `localStorageMock.setItem` was NOT called with 'allocations.tweaks' before any user interaction. Then click a Density chip and assert it WAS called exactly once.

#### G19-034 · TweaksContext loadTweaks() silently swallows JSON.parse failures with bare catch
- **File**: `src/app/(dashboard)/allocations/context/TweaksContext.tsx:62`
- **Specialist**: `silent-failure-hunter` (confidence 9)
- **Summary**: `try { ... } catch { return TWEAK_DEFAULTS; }` silently discards every failure mode: corrupt JSON in localStorage, SecurityError (Safari private mode), QuotaExceededError, schema-version mismatch from an old layout, JSON containing non-Partial<TweakState> shape that breaks the spread. The user toggles settings, persists them, then loads the app one day and silently sees defaults — they have no idea their state was corrupted or that the parse failed. No logError, no console.warn, no Sentry. The bare catch hides the difference between 'no value stored' and 'stored value is broken'. The existing v0.15.x persisted state survives the lift per the PR description; if any of those payloads have an unexpected shape (e.g., the old 'compact'/'spacious' density values that this PR renamed to 'tight'/'loose'), this catch will silently coerce to defaults with no migration log.
- **Evidence**: src/app/(dashboard)/allocations/context/TweaksContext.tsx:62-64
- **Fix**: Replace `catch {}` with `catch (err) { logError('tweaks_load_failed', err, { storageKey: STORAGE_KEY }); return TWEAK_DEFAULTS; }`. Also validate parsed values against the union type — `parsed.density` might be the old 'compact' which is no longer valid in the new TweakState union but the spread will happily accept it. Add a normalizeTweaks(parsed) that maps deprecated values ('compact' -> 'tight', 'spacious' -> 'loose') so the v0.15.x state lift actually works as the comment claims, not silently resets to defaults.

#### G19-035 · TweaksContext persistence catch silently drops Safari private mode / quota errors
- **File**: `src/app/(dashboard)/allocations/context/TweaksContext.tsx:96`
- **Specialist**: `silent-failure-hunter` (confidence 9)
- **Summary**: `catch { /* Safari private mode / quota — non-fatal. */ }` is empty (the comment is the entire body). A user in Safari private mode or with full localStorage will toggle tweaks, see the UI update via state, reload, and find every preference reset — with no clue why. Empty catch blocks are explicitly forbidden per the audit rules. The comment 'non-fatal' is technically true for the app but absolutely fatal for the user's expectation that their preferences persist. There is no telemetry, no inline 'preferences not saved' indicator, no logError.
- **Evidence**: src/app/(dashboard)/allocations/context/TweaksContext.tsx:94-98
- **Fix**: At minimum: `catch (err) { logError('tweaks_persist_failed', err, { storageKey: STORAGE_KEY }); }`. Better: surface a small inline 'Settings won't persist in this session' banner in the Tweaks panel when persistence fails, so the user knows their changes are session-scoped only. The current empty catch is exactly the 'silent failure' the audit rules forbid.

#### G19-036 · useTweaks fallback outside provider returns silent no-op setters
- **File**: `src/app/(dashboard)/allocations/context/TweaksContext.tsx:160`
- **Specialist**: `silent-failure-hunter` (confidence 8)
- **Summary**: When `useTweaks()` is called outside a TweaksProvider, it returns a stub with `set: () => {}, reset: () => {}, togglePanel: () => {}`. A developer who forgets to wrap a route in TweaksProvider will see the Tweaks panel render with default state, click 'Tight' or 'Full', and watch nothing happen. No console warning, no dev-mode error, no telemetry. The component appears broken but neither the user nor the developer gets any signal that the provider is missing. The comment 'every widget must function with factory defaults' is fine for read-only callers like `useTweakValue('chartStyle')`, but the panel's mutation surface returning no-op setters silently is a debugging nightmare.
- **Evidence**: src/app/(dashboard)/allocations/context/TweaksContext.tsx:160-172
- **Fix**: In dev mode (`process.env.NODE_ENV !== 'production'`), add `console.warn('useTweaks() called outside TweaksProvider — mutations will no-op')` inside the if-no-context branch. For mutation methods specifically, prefer throwing rather than no-oping when called outside provider — read access can fall back, but a `set()` call outside a provider is always a programming error. Alternatively, split the hook: `useTweakValue(key)` falls back to defaults (read-only), `useTweaks()` requires a provider and throws if missing.

#### G19-037 · Old persisted Tweaks state (compact/spacious/loud/default) silently coerces to invalid TweakState union
- **File**: `src/app/(dashboard)/allocations/context/TweaksContext.tsx:60`
- **Specialist**: `silent-failure-hunter` (confidence 8)
- **Summary**: The PR rename: density { compact, comfortable, spacious } -> { tight, comfortable, loose } and accentIntensity { muted, default, loud } -> { muted, full }. Existing users have `{ density: 'compact' }` or `{ accentIntensity: 'loud' }` in localStorage under the same STORAGE_KEY (the diff says 'same key as the QA-gated v0.15.x panel — stored preferences survive the lift'). `loadTweaks` spreads the parsed partial onto TWEAK_DEFAULTS: `{ ...TWEAK_DEFAULTS, ...parsed }`. There is no validation that parsed.density is one of the new union members. The result: a user with persisted `density: 'compact'` gets state.density === 'compact' at runtime — but the TypeScript union says only 'tight' | 'comfortable' | 'loose'. CSS `body[data-density='compact']` has no matching rule (only `tight`/`loose` are styled). The user sees stale density, the type system is lied to, no log fires.
- **Evidence**: src/app/(dashboard)/allocations/context/TweaksContext.tsx:60-61
- **Fix**: Add a normalization step: `const MIGRATE_DENSITY: Record<string, TweakState['density']> = { compact: 'tight', spacious: 'loose' }; const MIGRATE_ACCENT: Record<string, TweakState['accentIntensity']> = { default: 'muted', loud: 'full' };` then validate-and-migrate each field. Log via `logEvent('tweaks_state_migrated', { from: parsed.density, to: ... })` so the migration is observable. Without this, the v0.15.x lift claim in the changelog is false and users will silently see broken styling.

#### G19-038 · TweakState loaded from localStorage via unchecked `Partial<TweakState>` cast — silent enum drift
- **File**: `src/app/(dashboard)/allocations/context/TweaksContext.tsx:60`
- **Specialist**: `type-design-analyzer` (confidence 9)
- **Summary**: `loadTweaks()` does `JSON.parse(raw) as Partial<TweakState>` and spreads into `TWEAK_DEFAULTS`. There is zero runtime validation that string-union fields (density, accentIntensity, displayFont, bridgeVariant, chartStyle) contain values in the declared union. The diff explicitly states the storage key 'allocations.tweaks' is reused from the v0.15.x panel, but the union shape changed: old density values were 'compact' / 'comfortable' / 'spacious', new values are 'tight' / 'comfortable' / 'loose'. Old accentIntensity was 'muted' / 'default' / 'loud', new is 'muted' / 'full'. Any allocator with a persisted 'compact'/'spacious'/'default'/'loud' value silently lands in a state where no segmented button is `active` (every `state.density === 'tight'` comparison is false) and clicking any button works, but the initial paint is broken.
- **Evidence**: src/app/(dashboard)/allocations/context/TweaksContext.tsx:55-65 (`loadTweaks` cast w/o runtime narrowing); diff CHANGELOG lines 36-39 confirm storage key reuse across schema change; old TweakState diff at batch-G19.diff:1961-1980 shows the renamed unions
- **Fix**: Add a `parseTweakState(raw: unknown): TweakState` function that walks each field with `isDensity(x)` / `isAccentIntensity(x)` typeguards and falls back to TWEAK_DEFAULTS[key] on mismatch. Optionally bump STORAGE_KEY to 'allocations.tweaks.v2' so old values are simply ignored. The current spread-into-defaults pattern lets garbage-in-garbage-out for enum mismatches.

#### G19-039 · useTweaks fallback (outside-provider) silently no-ops mutations — masks integration bugs
- **File**: `src/app/(dashboard)/allocations/context/TweaksContext.tsx:160`
- **Specialist**: `type-design-analyzer` (confidence 8)
- **Summary**: When called outside a `TweaksProvider`, `useTweaks` returns `{ state: TWEAK_DEFAULTS, set: () => {}, reset: () => {}, ... }`. This is intentional per comment, but the type signature is identical to the real value: callers cannot distinguish 'I'm reading from a real provider' vs 'I'm silently writing to /dev/null'. A real bug — forgetting to wrap a tab in TweaksProvider — would manifest as 'segmented control clicks visibly trigger setActive() but nothing persists', i.e., a confusing UX with no error. Same shape used by `useTweakValue`.
- **Evidence**: src/app/(dashboard)/allocations/context/TweaksContext.tsx:158-174 (silent fallback returning identical contract); :180-182 (`useTweakValue` inherits same fallback)
- **Fix**: Either (a) throw `useTweaks must be used inside <TweaksProvider>` when context is null (treat missing provider as a programmer error), or (b) introduce a tagged result `{ source: 'provider' | 'defaults', ... }` so consumers like `Tweaks` can refuse to mount the panel when source==='defaults'. Option (a) is simpler and matches React's idiomatic context-hook pattern.

#### G19-040 · TweaksContext.set discards key/value invariant relationship — booleans and unions share one signature
- **File**: `src/app/(dashboard)/allocations/context/TweaksContext.tsx:69`
- **Specialist**: `type-design-analyzer` (confidence 8)
- **Summary**: `set: <K extends keyof TweakState>(key: K, value: TweakState[K]) => void` IS correctly generic — but the panel calls `set('showBench', true)` and `set('density', 'tight')` with the same shape. While this is type-safe at the call site, the absence of an exhaustive segmented-control invariant means there's no compile-time link between 'this Row label shows density options' and 'these Seg buttons set density values'. A typo like `set('density', 'compact')` (old enum) would be caught, but the wider design (segmented buttons hand-wired from Tweaks.tsx) doesn't enforce 'every union member has a Seg rendered'. Test at row 'Reset' confirms TWEAK_DEFAULTS equality but no test confirms 'every density value is selectable from the UI'.
- **Evidence**: src/app/(dashboard)/allocations/components/Tweaks.tsx:112-209 (Row/Seg pairs hand-wired); src/app/(dashboard)/allocations/context/TweaksContext.tsx:33-41 (TweakState union)
- **Fix**: Define `SegmentedField<K extends keyof TweakState> = { key: K; label: string; options: Array<{ value: TweakState[K]; label: string }> }` and a `SEGMENTED_FIELDS: ReadonlyArray<SegmentedField<...>>` array. The Tweaks panel then maps over this single source of truth, and a `satisfies` clause forces every union member to appear as an option. Adding a new density value to TweakState would fail typecheck until a corresponding option is added.

#### G19-041 · BridgeHeroWidget context coupling re-renders BridgeWidget on every Tweaks panel toggle
- **File**: `src/app/(dashboard)/allocations/widgets/bridge/BridgeHeroWidget.tsx:28`
- **Specialist**: `performance` (confidence 8)
- **Summary**: BridgeHeroWidget calls useTweakValue('bridgeVariant') which subscribes to the full TweaksContext value. Any panelOpen toggle (clicking the floating Tweaks chip) invalidates the context value and re-renders BridgeHeroWidget → which re-renders BridgeWidget with all its derived flagged-holding rows and decision markers. BridgeWidget is not memoized, so the cascade reaches its full render tree on every panel toggle, even though the bridgeVariant value did not change. Combined with the EquityChart finding (same root cause), every panel open/close causes a multi-widget re-render storm on the Overview tab.
- **Evidence**: src/app/(dashboard)/allocations/widgets/bridge/BridgeHeroWidget.tsx:28 + src/app/(dashboard)/allocations/context/TweaksContext.tsx:180-182
- **Fix**: Same as the EquityChart fix — split TweaksContext or migrate useTweakValue to a useSyncExternalStore-backed selector hook. Cheapest local fix: wrap BridgeHeroWidget's returned tree in React.memo with a custom comparator that only re-runs when `variant` actually changes.

#### G19-042 · BridgeHeroWidget `variant` prop wiring via TweaksContext has no test
- **File**: `src/app/(dashboard)/allocations/widgets/bridge/BridgeHeroWidget.tsx:24`
- **Specialist**: `pr-test-analyzer` (confidence 8)
- **Summary**: PR3 added `const variant = useTweakValue('bridgeVariant')` and passes it to `<BridgeWidget variant={variant} />`. This is the consumer side of the Tweaks 'Subtle / Card / Hero' segmented control — the primary user-visible knob per the CHANGELOG. There's no test that verifies BridgeHeroWidget actually reads the context value and forwards it. A future refactor that drops the `useTweakValue` import or passes a stale default would silently break the live design-variation flip.
- **Evidence**: grep 'bridgeVariant' src/app/(dashboard)/allocations/widgets/bridge/*.test.tsx → zero hits; BridgeHeroWidget.tsx:21-24 wires the context read; BridgeWidget.test.tsx exists but tests the leaf with explicit props, not the wrapper.
- **Fix**: Add `BridgeHeroWidget.tweaks.test.tsx`: spy on BridgeWidget render via `vi.mock('../../components/BridgeWidget', ...)`; render BridgeHeroWidget inside `<TweaksProvider>` with localStorage seeded to bridgeVariant='subtle'; assert the BridgeWidget mock received `variant: 'subtle'`. Repeat for 'card' and 'full'.

#### G19-043 · Tweaks context coupling forces EquityChart full re-render on panel open/close
- **File**: `src/app/(dashboard)/allocations/widgets/performance/EquityChart.tsx:263`
- **Specialist**: `performance` (confidence 9)
- **Summary**: EquityChart now subscribes to TweaksContext via useTweakValue('chartStyle') + useTweakValue('showBench'). useTweakValue internally reads useTweaks().state[key], which subscribes to the entire context value object. When any context field changes (notably panelOpen via TweaksToggle click, or any density/font/accent toggle), EquityChart re-renders and re-executes ~100+ lines of un-memoized chart-projection math (visibleNormalized.map, allValues loop, yTicks IIFE, X-axis tick density linear search, toPath/toArea path string concat). For ALL-period charts (potentially thousands of points × ~20 overlays = 50k+ values), every Tweaks panel toggle triggers this cascade across both EquityChart instances (Overview and ScenarioComposer paths). Pre-existing render code; the new context subscription is the introduced regression.
- **Evidence**: src/app/(dashboard)/allocations/widgets/performance/EquityChart.tsx:263-264 + src/app/(dashboard)/allocations/context/TweaksContext.tsx:180-182
- **Fix**: Either (a) wrap EquityChart's expensive projection block (lines 396-491) in useMemo keyed on [visible, visibleBenchmarkNormalized, overlaySeries, width], OR (b) split TweaksContext into two contexts (state + panelOpen) so panel toggles don't invalidate state-only consumers, OR (c) replace useTweakValue with a useSyncExternalStore-based selector hook that only re-renders when the selected slice changes.

#### G19-044 · anchorFromFirstPositive runs three times per render for the same data
- **File**: `src/app/(dashboard)/allocations/widgets/performance/EquityChart.tsx:1300`
- **Specialist**: `performance` (confidence 9)
- **Summary**: EquityChartWidget calls anchorFromFirstPositive(equityDailyPoints) inside the minDate useMemo (line 1300-1305) AND inside the periodReturn useMemo (line 1312-1321). Then EquityChart (the child) calls it AGAIN at line 283-286 for `composite`. Each call performs findIndex + slice + map over the full DailyPoint[] array (O(n)) and allocates a new array. For an ALL-period equity series with several thousand daily points, this is three duplicate O(n) passes per top-level render. The new periodReturn useMemo (introduced by PR3 for the always-visible chip in the card header — see EquityChart.tsx lines 1308-1321) is what makes this triple-duplication new in this batch.
- **Evidence**: src/app/(dashboard)/allocations/widgets/performance/EquityChart.tsx:1301 and 1313 and 284
- **Fix**: Hoist a single `const anchored = useMemo(() => anchorFromFirstPositive(equityDailyPoints), [equityDailyPoints])` in EquityChartWidget, pass that anchored array down via a new prop, and have EquityChart skip its own anchor pass when it receives the pre-anchored input. Alternatively, memoize anchorFromFirstPositive with a WeakMap keyed on the input reference.

#### G19-045 · EquityChartWidget minute-clock re-renders entire chart tree every 60s
- **File**: `src/app/(dashboard)/allocations/widgets/performance/EquityChart.tsx:1280`
- **Specialist**: `performance` (confidence 8)
- **Summary**: EquityChartWidget runs setInterval(() => setNow(Date.now()), 60_000) (line 1280) so the 'last sync Xh ago' string in the card header stays fresh. Each tick re-renders EquityChartWidget, recomputes the minDate / periodReturn useMemos (they don't change so the memos hit), and re-renders the inner EquityChart — which re-runs all the un-memoized projection math (visibleNormalized, allValues loop, yTicks IIFE, X-axis tick density linear search, toPath/toArea). With multiple EquityChart instances on the page (Overview tile + ScenarioComposer baseline + scenario projection) this is hundreds of ms of repeated work every minute that only updates one text node.
- **Evidence**: src/app/(dashboard)/allocations/widgets/performance/EquityChart.tsx:1275-1285
- **Fix**: Hoist the 'last sync ago' string into a tiny dedicated component (e.g. `<RelativeTime iso={lastSyncAt} />`) that holds its own minute clock and renders only the <div>. The parent EquityChartWidget should stop holding the minute clock so the chart tree never re-renders on tick. Alternative: useSharedMinuteClock (the project-canonical hook referenced in the comment on lines 1273-1274) already exists for this exact pattern — adopt it and scope the re-render to one leaf.

#### G19-046 · InsightStrip leaves dead `{false ? ... : ...}` branch in production JSX
- **File**: `src/components/portfolio/InsightStrip.tsx:106`
- **Specialist**: `code-reviewer` (confidence 8)
- **Summary**: After the PR3 'silenced when empty' change the component returns null at line 94 when nothing fires, but the original empty-state branch was left in the render path guarded by `{false ? (...) : (...)}`. The 'No unusual activity in the trailing window' copy is unreachable. This violates Rule 3 (Surgical Changes — clean up only your own mess but ALSO don't leave broken/dead code) and Rule 12 (Fail loud — dead code hides intent). Future maintainers will read this and wonder which branch is the truth.
- **Evidence**: src/components/portfolio/InsightStrip.tsx:106-110 `{false ? ( <p className='text-sm text-text-secondary'>No unusual activity in the trailing window.</p> ) : ( <ul role='list' className='space-y-2'>...</ul> )}`
- **Fix**: Delete the `{false ? ... : ...}` wrapper and render the `<ul>` directly; remove the dead 'No unusual activity' fallback paragraph. If a future empty-state design is needed, restore it deliberately with a real predicate.

#### G19-047 · InsightStrip dead-code branch (`{false ? ... : ...}`) hides removed empty-state from future readers
- **File**: `src/components/portfolio/InsightStrip.tsx:106`
- **Specialist**: `silent-failure-hunter` (confidence 8)
- **Summary**: The PR sets the empty-state condition to a literal `false`: `{false ? <p>No unusual activity...</p> : <ul>...</ul>}`. This is dead code masquerading as a conditional. Future readers will assume there's a runtime case where the empty-state fires; eslint may rightfully flag it; refactors may accidentally restore it. More importantly, it's a silent record of the old empty-state being removed — any audit hunting for 'where does the strip fall back?' will think the branch is reachable. Combined with the early-return-null at line 94, the strip now has zero way to communicate 'analytics fetch failed', and the literal `false` is the smoking gun that the author chose silence over a proper error path.
- **Evidence**: src/components/portfolio/InsightStrip.tsx:106-110
- **Fix**: Delete the dead branch entirely — render the `<ul>` directly. Then audit whether the truly-empty case (insights=0, flaggedCount>0) needs a different shape (the strip currently still shows only the flaggedCount line, which is correct, but the docstring still claims 'the strip stays visible with a fallback' which is now false). Update the docstring (lines 17-22) to match the new behavior.

#### G19-048 · InsightStrip's portfolioId-gated bridge silently degrades when portfolioId is null
- **File**: `src/components/portfolio/InsightStrip.tsx:65`
- **Specialist**: `silent-failure-hunter` (confidence 8)
- **Summary**: `isBridgeable` returns false when `portfolioId` is null, causing the BridgeTrigger to be silently replaced with a plain `<span>`. AllocationDashboardV2 line 284 passes `portfolioId={portfolio?.id ?? null}`. So when `portfolio` is null (e.g., portfolio lookup failed or user has no portfolio yet), the bridge trigger silently disappears from underperformance insights with no signal. The user sees an underperformance sentence with no 'Find Replacement' affordance and has no idea this functionality is missing because the portfolio failed to load. The optional `?.id ?? null` chaining is the precise 'optional chaining that hides errors' pattern called out in the audit rules.
- **Evidence**: src/components/portfolio/InsightStrip.tsx:65-71, src/app/(dashboard)/allocations/AllocationDashboardV2.tsx:284
- **Fix**: If portfolioId is null but analytics is non-null (so insights were computed), that's a bug — analytics implies a portfolio. Add `if (analytics && !portfolioId) logError('insight_strip_orphan_analytics', { ... })`. Better: type the props to refuse this state — `portfolioId: string | null; analytics: PortfolioAnalytics | null` should be a discriminated union: either both null (no portfolio) or both set (portfolio loaded). Right now they're independent and the silent-degrade is invisible.

### LOW (1)

#### G19-049 · CustomRangePicker.pickMode is implicit state machine — encode transitions in type
- **File**: `src/app/(dashboard)/allocations/components/CustomRangePicker.tsx:110`
- **Specialist**: `type-design-analyzer` (confidence 9)
- **Summary**: `const [pickMode, setPickMode] = useState<'start' | 'end'>('start')` plus the convoluted `pickDay` body (`if (pickMode === 'start' || (start && end && d < start))`) implements a hidden state machine: idle (about to pick start) → selecting (start picked, picking end) → idle. The conditions for transitions are spread across all 4 mutation handlers (`pickDay`, `applyPreset`, `applyMTD`, `applyYTD`, `applyMax`). A reducer + tagged state would make the transitions explicit and prevent races (e.g., applyPreset sets pickMode='start' even though it has already chosen both endpoints — fine, but a refactor could easily break it).
- **Evidence**: src/app/(dashboard)/allocations/components/CustomRangePicker.tsx:110 (pickMode state), :155-170 (pickDay branching), :180/189/198/205 (every preset action force-resets pickMode='start')
- **Fix**: `type PickerState = { kind: 'idle'; range: DateRange } | { kind: 'pickingEnd'; pendingStart: Date }` with a `reducer(state, action: { type: 'pickDay'; d: Date } | { type: 'applyPreset'; days: number } | ...)`. Each action's effect on state is one switch case; impossible transitions (e.g., 'pickingEnd' while no pendingStart exists) become unrepresentable.
