## G20 — PRs #79-#80 — UAT cleanup + mandate auto-save limiter + dashboard-parity PR4

### HIGH (6)

#### G20-001 · KpiCell.value: string collapses Maybe<number> into pre-formatted em-dash, making 'missing' vs 'real zero' indistinguishable
- **File**: `src/app/(dashboard)/allocations/widgets/meta/KpiStripWidget.tsx:42`
- **Specialist**: `type-design-analyzer` (confidence 9)
- **Summary**: The KpiCell type pre-formats numeric KPIs into a string (e.g. '—', '$48.73M', '+14.32%'). Once flattened, downstream code cannot tell whether a cell reads '—' because the analytics row hasn't been computed (computation_status='pending'), failed (computation_status='failed'), or is genuinely zero/null. fmtPct(0, true) yields '+0.00%' while fmtPct(null, true) yields '—', but the cell-construction call sites (line 193-198) only coalesce nullable analytics fields with ??null and never distinguish '0 returned' from 'no measurement yet'. This is the exact 'KPI value types that conflate 0 with missing' anti-pattern the audit flagged.
- **Evidence**: src/app/(dashboard)/allocations/widgets/meta/KpiStripWidget.tsx:42-48 (KpiCell), 193-198 (?? null collapse), 262-266 (fmtPct returns '—' for null only, never for unmeasured)
- **Fix**: Introduce a domain-level KpiValue type that preserves the distinction at the contract boundary: type KpiValue = | { kind: 'missing'; reason: 'pending' | 'failed' | 'no_data' } | { kind: 'computed'; value: number } | { kind: 'not_applicable' }. Format only at the leaf render site so test+UI can branch on missingness vs zero. Drives correct copy ('Computing...' vs '—' vs '0.00%').

#### G20-002 · EquityChartWidgetData lacks discriminated stale/fresh tag — allKeysStale:boolean + lastSyncAt:string|null permits 4 states with overlapping semantics
- **File**: `src/app/(dashboard)/allocations/widgets/performance/EquityChart.tsx:1231`
- **Specialist**: `type-design-analyzer` (confidence 9)
- **Summary**: The equity-header data bag has allKeysStale?: boolean and lastSyncAt?: string|null as independent optional fields. This permits 4 combos: (stale=true, lastSync=null), (stale=true, lastSync=string), (stale=false, lastSync=null), (stale=false, lastSync=string). The 'fresh-but-never-synced' state (stale=false + lastSync=null) is renderable and currently shows 'sync just now' — a lie. Conversely 'stale + no lastSync' falls back to 'data stale' which hides whether sync ever happened. The type doesn't encode the invariant that staleness should derive from lastSyncAt (or vice versa).
- **Evidence**: src/app/(dashboard)/allocations/widgets/performance/EquityChart.tsx:1231-1245 (interface EquityChartWidgetData), 1286-1292 (syncStampCopy reconstructs state from two independent fields)
- **Fix**: Replace the two-field shape with a discriminated union: type SyncState = | { kind: 'never_synced' } | { kind: 'fresh'; lastSyncAt: string } | { kind: 'stale'; lastSyncAt: string }. Each combo is named, the impossible 'fresh-but-never-synced' state becomes unrepresentable, and the syncStampCopy switch becomes exhaustive.

#### G20-003 · useMandateAutoSave 429 path silently drops savingFields cleanup mid-retry
- **File**: `src/components/mandate/useMandateAutoSave.ts:134`
- **Specialist**: `silent-failure-hunter` (confidence 9)
- **Summary**: On 429 the hook sets fieldErrors + saveState='error' and then `await wait(retryAfter * 1000); continue;` — but never removes the field from savingFields. The field's slider/chip stays in aria-busy=true while the hook silently sleeps for the Retry-After window (could be 5-60s in production). The user has no visible signal whether the save is in-flight, queued, or stuck, AND if generation changes during the wait the code returns at line 142 without ever cleaning up savingFields either. UI state remains 'saving' indefinitely.
- **Evidence**: src/components/mandate/useMandateAutoSave.ts:134-144
- **Fix**: Always clear the field from savingFields when entering the 429 wait, and add a defensive `setSavingFields((prev) => { const n = new Set(prev); n.delete(fieldName); return n; })` in the generation-mismatch early return at line 142. Or surface a distinct visual state (e.g. 'queued, retrying in 5s') so the user sees the system is alive.

#### G20-004 · mandateAutoSaveLimiter at 30/60s with 4-retry exponential backoff can silently exhaust budget
- **File**: `src/components/mandate/useMandateAutoSave.ts:81`
- **Specialist**: `silent-failure-hunter` (confidence 8)
- **Summary**: Combined with the new 30/min mandateAutoSaveLimiter (route.ts:38, ratelimit.ts:136), the 4-retry loop here means a single 429 burst can chew up to 4 buckets per field. With 8 fields fanning out from one mandate edit (PR's own analysis) plus retries, the limiter resets only via Upstash's sliding window — a user iterating rapidly can hit 30/min while the hook silently retries with backoff. The 429 inline error 'Saving too fast. Will retry in Xs.' is the visible signal, but generation-counter races mean the user can keep editing, bumping gen counters, leaving older saves to silently abandon (per the earlier finding on savingFields).
- **Evidence**: src/components/mandate/useMandateAutoSave.ts:80-83,134-144
- **Fix**: Either lower MAX_ATTEMPTS to 2 on the 429 branch (don't burn budget on retries that just re-429), or have the hook back off WITHOUT counting the wait against MAX_ATTEMPTS. Also surface a 'budget exhausted — saves paused' toast to the user, not just per-field inline errors.

#### G20-005 · SaveState union 'idle|saving|saved|error' mixes throttled-but-retrying with permanent failure; UI cannot distinguish recoverable from terminal errors
- **File**: `src/components/mandate/useMandateAutoSave.ts:5`
- **Specialist**: `type-design-analyzer` (confidence 9)
- **Summary**: export type SaveState = 'idle' | 'saving' | 'saved' | 'error' — the lone 'error' state is reused for: (a) 429 throttling with active in-flight retry (line 140), (b) 400/401 permanent validation failure (line 153), (c) 5xx exhausted retries (line 171), (d) network failure exhausted retries (line 107). The hook then sits in 'error' during the await wait(retryAfter*1000) on line 141 even though it's actively going to retry, conflating 'failed' with 'throttled' — exactly the anti-pattern the audit flagged. Consumers reading saveState='error' cannot tell whether to surface 'Saving too fast, retrying...' (recoverable) vs 'Couldn't save. Try again.' (terminal).
- **Evidence**: src/components/mandate/useMandateAutoSave.ts:5 (SaveState union), 134-144 (429 throttle path sets state='error' before retry), 146-159 (400/401 terminal), 162-179 (5xx exhausted)
- **Fix**: Discriminate the failure modes: type SaveState = | { kind: 'idle' } | { kind: 'saving' } | { kind: 'saved'; at: Date } | { kind: 'throttled'; retryAfter: number; willRetry: true } | { kind: 'failed'; reason: 'validation' | 'auth' | 'network' | 'server' }. The 429 retry-in-flight state becomes its own branch; consumers stop conflating it with terminal failure. Also closes the gap where the hook leaves state='error' set across the retry sleep window.

#### G20-006 · PortfolioAnalytics fields are 'number | null' with no Maybe<number> discriminator; '0' computed result is indistinguishable from 'never computed'
- **File**: `src/lib/types.ts:571`
- **Specialist**: `type-design-analyzer` (confidence 9)
- **Summary**: Every PortfolioAnalytics metric (portfolio_sharpe, portfolio_volatility, portfolio_max_drawdown, avg_pairwise_correlation, return_24h, return_mtd, return_ytd, total_aum, total_return_twr/mwr) is typed as 'number | null'. The PortfolioAnalytics row also carries 'computation_status' (pending/computing/complete/failed) and 'computation_error', but the metric nullability is NOT linked to the status field at the type level. KpiStripWidget reads 'analytics?.return_ytd ?? null' without consulting computation_status, so a row with status='computing' and return_ytd=null renders the same '—' as status='complete' return_ytd=null (real null). And '0.00%' from a computed-and-zero return reads identically to a real return of 0.00% — there is no way to distinguish a freshly-warmed-up portfolio from one with no movement.
- **Evidence**: src/lib/types.ts:571-596 (interface PortfolioAnalytics); src/app/(dashboard)/allocations/widgets/meta/KpiStripWidget.tsx:187-198 (??null coalesce ignores computation_status)
- **Fix**: Make the type a discriminated union on computation_status: type PortfolioAnalytics = | { computation_status: 'pending' | 'computing'; portfolio_sharpe?: never; ... } | { computation_status: 'failed'; computation_error: string } | { computation_status: 'complete'; portfolio_sharpe: number | null; ... }. The complete branch lets metrics be null (genuinely uncomputable, e.g. <30d history) while making it impossible to read a metric before completion.

### MEDIUM (30)

#### G20-007 · E2E bridge-outcome.spec.ts hard-skipped indefinitely — silent regression risk
- **File**: `e2e/bridge-outcome.spec.ts:125`
- **Specialist**: `silent-failure-hunter` (confidence 8)
- **Summary**: `test.skip(true, 'Phase 9.1 superseded — see file-level docstring; fixture rebuild tracked as follow-up');` unconditionally skips the entire Phase 1 Bridge Outcome recording suite. The skip carries no ticket-id reference, no expiry/TODO date, and no `expect(false).toBe(true)` canary to force the rebuild to happen. The Phase 9.1 HoldingsTable banner mounting path is now ONLY covered by unit tests (bridge-outcome-label.test.ts + per-component widget tests), with NO integration coverage of the rendered banner's actual user flow. Code-level review at .gstack/deploy-reports/... is documentation, not enforcement.
- **Evidence**: e2e/bridge-outcome.spec.ts:119-125
- **Fix**: Replace `test.skip(true, ...)` with `test.skip(!process.env.E2E_BRIDGE_REBUILT, 'Rebuild fixture per file-level docstring')`. Or open a GH issue and reference it inline: `test.skip(true, 'TODO #NNN — fixture rebuild after Phase 9.1')`. The hard-skip without a fail-by date silently rots.

#### G20-008 · AllocationDashboardV2 renderWidget callback rebuilds on every parent state change, defeating Suspense memoization across all tiles
- **File**: `src/app/(dashboard)/allocations/AllocationDashboardV2.tsx:229`
- **Specialist**: `performance` (confidence 8)
- **Summary**: `renderWidget` is wrapped in useCallback with deps `[props, config.timeframe]`, but `props` is the FULL `MyAllocationDashboardPayload` object passed from the page (which is fresh-by-reference every server-component boundary crossing) and `config.timeframe` (config object comes from useDashboardConfigV2 hook). Any time AllocationDashboardV2 re-renders for an unrelated reason — pickerOpen toggle, IntersectionObserver MutationObserver callback firing (line 175-182, which can fire on any DOM mutation in the dashboard tree), drag/move state — `renderWidget` gets a fresh identity. That identity is passed to WidgetGrid → renderWidget(k) is called per cell → each call constructs a fresh `<Component data={props as any} />` element. React doesn't memoize across these without React.memo on the leaf components. With ~10 tiles mounted (a realistic dashboard parity layout), one local state change triggers all 10 widgets to re-render their full subtree, including the 1000+ LOC EquityChart with its expensive useMemo chain. Each tile passes the WHOLE props bag (`data={props as any}`) — every payload field becomes a render-trigger surface for every widget, not just the widget that consumes that field.
- **Evidence**: src/app/(dashboard)/allocations/AllocationDashboardV2.tsx:229-259 (renderWidget useCallback deps); :248-254 (Component receives full props bag); :175-182 (MutationObserver triggers re-observe on any subtree mutation, no debounce); :150-188 (no cleanup on widgetViewsFiredRef when widgets unmount → potential leak across drag/move sessions but minor); src/app/(dashboard)/allocations/widgets/performance/EquityChart.tsx (no React.memo).
- **Fix**: (1) Wrap each widget in React.memo with a prop-bag equality check that only re-renders when the widget's specific data slice changes. (2) Replace `data={props as any}` with per-widget data extraction: e.g., EquityChartWidget receives `equityDailyPoints + btcBenchmark + equityOverlays + allKeysStale + lastSyncAt` not the whole payload. (3) MutationObserver in the IntersectionObserver effect should debounce (rAF or 100ms) — currently it re-queries all tiles on every DOM mutation, including the resize-handle pointer drags that mutate inline styles continuously.

#### G20-009 · useTweakValue is not a true selector — toggling any knob re-renders all tweak consumers
- **File**: `src/app/(dashboard)/allocations/context/TweaksContext.tsx:180`
- **Specialist**: `performance` (confidence 8)
- **Summary**: `useTweakValue(key)` is implemented as `useTweaks().state[key]` — it subscribes to the entire context value object, which is rebuilt via useMemo whenever ANY field of `state` changes. As a result, toggling `displayFont` from serif→sans re-renders every consumer that reads any tweak (EquityChartWidget, EquityChart, BridgeHeroWidget, AllocationDashboardV2), not just the ones that care about displayFont. With the new PR4 displayFont body-attribute effect (TweaksContext.tsx:116-121), each click on the Display Font knob now (a) sets React state → re-renders all consumers, (b) writes body[data-display-font], (c) triggers a CSS-driven font swap on every .font-display heading on the page. The fan-out is invisible in test data but with ~10+ widgets mounted (dashboard parity tile set) and the EquityChart's expensive useMemo chain on `visible`/`overlayseries`/`yTicks` running, a knob toggle has visible jank potential. A proper selector (useSyncExternalStoreWithSelector or Object.is comparison on the slice) would make displayFont toggle re-render only the body-attribute effect.
- **Evidence**: src/app/(dashboard)/allocations/context/TweaksContext.tsx:180-182 (selector is a property access on whole context); :148-151 (`value` useMemo depends on full `state`); src/app/(dashboard)/allocations/widgets/performance/EquityChart.tsx:263-264, 1249 (consumers via useTweakValue).
- **Fix**: Replace context-based selectors with a Zustand-style external store using useSyncExternalStoreWithSelector(getSnapshot, () => state[key], Object.is), or split TweaksContext into per-slice contexts. Cheaper interim: wrap each downstream widget in React.memo and pass `chartStyle` / `showBench` as explicit props from a thin container that does the context read.

#### G20-010 · Display-font knob toggle causes layout reflow across every .font-display heading on the page
- **File**: `src/app/(dashboard)/allocations/context/TweaksContext.tsx:116`
- **Specialist**: `performance` (confidence 8)
- **Summary**: The new displayFont effect writes `body[data-display-font=sans|serif]`, which the matching CSS rule in globals.css (body[data-display-font="sans"] .font-display) uses to swap `font-family: var(--font-sans)` and `font-weight: 500` on every `.font-display` element. The Display Font knob switches between Instrument Serif (a serif-stack font) and DM Sans — fundamentally different glyph metrics and weights. Every toggle invalidates layout for every heading using `.font-display` (per the TODOS.md tally: My Allocation H1, KPI cell labels, Bridge "All clear" headline, Equity curve title, Holdings header, Allocation by style header — ~8-15 sites). Browsers must recompute box sizes for each, potentially shifting positions of siblings. The card-header h3 in EquityChartWidget now uses .font-display with fontSize: 14 + fontWeight: 500 (EquityChart.tsx:1382) — flipping to serif may push the legend chips/period toggle/sync stamp to wrap to a new line (flexWrap: 'wrap' on the parent). The cleanup on effect unmount (removeAttribute) compounds the flicker: toggling between dashboard tabs unmounts/remounts the AllocationsTabs → TweaksProvider unmounts → body attr removed → all headings flip to default. There is no will-change / font-display: swap hint to soften the transition.
- **Evidence**: src/app/(dashboard)/allocations/context/TweaksContext.tsx:116-121 (effect writes body attr; cleanup removes it on every state change AND on unmount); src/app/globals.css:144-151 (rule swaps font-family + font-weight); src/app/(dashboard)/allocations/widgets/performance/EquityChart.tsx:1382-1389 (.font-display h3 with flex parent that wraps).
- **Fix**: (a) Drop the effect-cleanup `removeAttribute` so re-entry from another tab doesn't yo-yo back to the default attribute then forward again — set the attribute once and let the next state change overwrite it (the only time the attribute should be removed is on full TweaksProvider unmount, which is page navigation). (b) Use `font-size-adjust` on .font-display so the two stacks share an apparent x-height, minimizing reflow extent. (c) Avoid changing `font-weight` in the swap (current rule changes 500→default), or apply the same weight to both branches.

#### G20-011 · TweaksContext displayFont effect (body[data-display-font]) has no regression test
- **File**: `src/app/(dashboard)/allocations/context/TweaksContext.tsx:117`
- **Specialist**: `pr-test-analyzer` (confidence 9)
- **Summary**: PR4 #3 added a new useEffect that writes document.body.setAttribute('data-display-font', state.displayFont) on every state change. This is paired with a single CSS rule (globals.css:147) that swaps .font-display to var(--font-sans) when the attribute is 'sans'. If the effect is removed or if the attribute name drifts (e.g. data-displayfont, data-display_font), the knob silently becomes a no-op again — which is the exact bug PR4 #3 is fixing. Tweaks.test.tsx never asserts the attribute write, only the in-state value (lines 189, 205).
- **Evidence**: grep -nE 'data-display-font|font-display' src/**/*.test.* — zero matches. TweaksContext.tsx:117 sets the attribute; Tweaks.test.tsx parses persisted JSON for displayFont but never asserts body.getAttribute('data-display-font'). The companion 'data-density' attribute IS asserted at Tweaks.test.tsx:119, 217 — the parallel coverage is missing for displayFont.
- **Fix**: Add 'applies body[data-display-font] when displayFont changes' to Tweaks.test.tsx (mirror the existing 'applies body[data-density]' test at line 113). Click the 'Sans' segmented button, assert document.body.getAttribute('data-display-font') === 'sans'. Click 'Serif', assert it flips back to 'serif'. Add a hydration follow-up asserting that a persisted displayFont='sans' restores the body attribute on mount (currently line 217 only covers data-density).

#### G20-012 · TweaksContext localStorage write empty catch hides quota/private-mode failures
- **File**: `src/app/(dashboard)/allocations/context/TweaksContext.tsx:94`
- **Specialist**: `silent-failure-hunter` (confidence 8)
- **Summary**: `try { window.localStorage.setItem(...) } catch { /* Safari private mode / quota — non-fatal. */ }` swallows ALL storage errors. Comment cites Safari private mode + quota, but the catch also masks (a) corrupted JSON.stringify on cyclic state shape, (b) cross-origin frame storage denials, (c) browser extension storage shims that intermittently throw. Users in private mode silently lose their density/displayFont/accentIntensity preference on every refresh with NO indication. There is no console.warn, no toast, no event dispatch.
- **Evidence**: src/app/(dashboard)/allocations/context/TweaksContext.tsx:92-99
- **Fix**: Replace the empty catch with `catch (err) { console.warn('[TweaksContext] localStorage write failed; preferences will not persist:', err); }`. Optionally dispatch a one-time toast on first failure so private-mode users understand why their settings reset.

#### G20-013 · displayFont value escapes the type system via setAttribute(string), uncoupling the TS enum from globals.css selector
- **File**: `src/app/(dashboard)/allocations/context/TweaksContext.tsx:36`
- **Specialist**: `type-design-analyzer` (confidence 8)
- **Summary**: TweakState.displayFont is typed 'serif | sans' (line 36), but the effect on line 117 writes document.body.setAttribute('data-display-font', state.displayFont) and globals.css has a single matching selector body[data-display-font='sans'] (line 948). The type system can't tell that adding a new variant ('mono', 'rounded', etc.) requires a paired CSS rule — the new enum value would silently no-op because the selector only matches the literal 'sans'. The audit specifically flagged 'displayFont knob type that allows arbitrary string' — while the TS type is constrained, the type contract dissolves at the DOM boundary because the attribute is a free-form string and only one literal value is wired up.
- **Evidence**: src/app/(dashboard)/allocations/context/TweaksContext.tsx:36 ('serif'|'sans'), 117 (setAttribute with any string), src/app/globals.css:948 (rule keyed on 'sans' literal only)
- **Fix**: Either (a) keep the union narrow but add a const PRESENT_VARIANTS: readonly TweakState['displayFont'][] paired with a runtime assertion that globals.css has a rule for each, or (b) move the styling source-of-truth onto the TS side: const DISPLAY_FONT_STYLES: Record<TweakState['displayFont'], CSSProperties> = { serif: {fontFamily:'var(--font-serif)',fontWeight:400}, sans: {fontFamily:'var(--font-sans)',fontWeight:500} }, then apply via root.style.setProperty('--font-display-family', styles.fontFamily) inside the effect. Adding a variant becomes a compile error on the Record.

#### G20-014 · KpiStripWidget separator var(--color-border) fix has no regression test
- **File**: `src/app/(dashboard)/allocations/widgets/meta/KpiStripWidget.tsx:92`
- **Specialist**: `pr-test-analyzer` (confidence 9)
- **Summary**: PR4 #2 swapped four references from 'var(--border)' (undefined in Tailwind v4 @theme inline — invalid CSS, dividers silently absent) to 'var(--color-border)'. This is the literal bug-fix the PR claims to ship. No test asserts the borderLeft style on KPI cells references --color-border. A regex refactor that reverts the variable name (or a copy-paste that re-introduces var(--border) in a sibling widget) ships broken separators with green CI.
- **Evidence**: grep -nE 'color-border|borderLeft|separator|divider' src/app/(dashboard)/allocations/widgets/meta/KpiStripWidget.test.tsx src/app/(dashboard)/allocations/widgets/meta/KpiStripWidget.v2.test.tsx — zero matches. Also walk the inline <style> block textContent and expect.not.toMatch(/var\(--border\)/) and expect.toMatch(/var\(--color-border\)/g) appearing >=4 times (1 base + 4 responsive overrides). Fails against any code path that reverts to undefined var(--border).

#### G20-015 · KpiStripWidget AUM falls through to $0.00 when holdings have non-numeric value_usd
- **File**: `src/app/(dashboard)/allocations/widgets/meta/KpiStripWidget.tsx:237`
- **Specialist**: `silent-failure-hunter` (confidence 8)
- **Summary**: computeAum() falls back to summing holdingsSummary[].value_usd with a silent `typeof h.value_usd === 'number' ? h.value_usd : 0` coercion. When holdings exist but their value_usd is missing/undefined/null (e.g. analytics-service hasn't priced them yet, or a partner-import row never resolved a venue quote), each unpriced holding silently contributes 0 to AUM. User sees a confident `$0.00` or a partial sum rather than the em-dash that would signal 'data not ready'. Same fall-through applies when `analytics.total_aum` is literally 0 — fmtCurrencyCompact(0) returns `$0.00`, indistinguishable from 'no AUM yet'.
- **Evidence**: src/app/(dashboard)/allocations/widgets/meta/KpiStripWidget.tsx:235-241,250
- **Fix**: Count non-numeric holdings as a missing-data signal: if any holdingsSummary row lacks numeric value_usd, treat AUM as null (em-dash) rather than silently zeroing. Or surface a per-cell 'partial' badge so users distinguish 'priced and zero' from 'pricing pending'.

#### G20-016 · EquityChartWidget rebuilds overlay arrays + legend chips on every render — defeats inner-chart memoization
- **File**: `src/app/(dashboard)/allocations/widgets/performance/EquityChart.tsx:1260`
- **Specialist**: `performance` (confidence 8)
- **Summary**: The wrapper widget stabilizes `equityDailyPoints` via useMemo but leaves `benchmark`, `overlays = d.equityOverlays ?? []`, `stale`, `lastSyncAt`, `hasBenchmark` as unmemoized property reads from a new `d` object every render (`const d = (data ?? {}) as EquityChartWidgetData;`). Every render: (a) `overlays` is a new array literal whenever `d.equityOverlays` is null/undefined, breaking the inner `EquityChart`'s `enrichedOverlays` useMemo identity check (line 315) and forcing the heavy `overlaySeries.map(o => …)` pipeline to recompute even when nothing changed; (b) the wrapper renders `overlays.map(o => <HeaderLegendSwatch …/>)` (line 1414) creating fresh element instances on every parent re-render; (c) `setNow(Date.now())` fires every 60s via setInterval, triggering a full widget re-render — which then ripples through the inner EquityChart's memo deps because the unmemoized `benchmark` and `overlays` references are now fresh again from the new `d` object. The IntersectionObserver in AllocationDashboardV2 also fires `setPickerOpen` and other state changes that ripple props down (renderWidget callback re-creates with new `props` reference on every parent state change, which Suspense forwards through the Component prop bag). Net effect: every 60s the entire equity chart pipeline (anchorFromFirstPositive, sliceByPeriod, normalization, yTick walker, path string building) re-runs even when no real input changed.
- **Evidence**: src/app/(dashboard)/allocations/widgets/performance/EquityChart.tsx:1247-1263 (d destructured fresh each render; only equityDailyPoints memoized); :1276-1285 (setInterval setNow every 60s); :283-291, :315-327, :333-361 (inner-chart memos keyed on `overlays`/`benchmark` which churn from wrapper); src/app/(dashboard)/allocations/AllocationDashboardV2.tsx:229-259 (renderWidget callback rebuilt on every parent state change because `[props, config.timeframe]` includes whole props bag).
- **Fix**: Memoize the rest of the destructure in the wrapper: `const benchmark = useMemo(() => d.btcBenchmark, [d.btcBenchmark]);` and `const overlays = useMemo(() => d.equityOverlays ?? EMPTY, [d.equityOverlays]);` with EMPTY as a module-level frozen array. Wrap `EquityChart` and `EquityChartWidget` in React.memo. Memoize `renderWidget`'s child element identities — currently the Suspense wrapper rebuilds every render. The 60s clock should not flush through to inner-chart memos.

Companion test for customRange/onCustomRangeChange via the CUSTOM picker dialog Apply flow.

#### G20-020 · EquityChart basePort=0 produces NaN/Infinity normalization with no surface
- **File**: `src/app/(dashboard)/allocations/widgets/performance/EquityChart.tsx:395`
- **Specialist**: `silent-failure-hunter` (confidence 8)
- **Summary**: `const basePort = visible[0]?.value ?? 1;` — the nullish-coalesce only catches undefined. If visible[0].value is literally 0 (zero-equity row that slipped past the f7 anchor because the period slice landed on a pre-anchor day), `visibleNormalized = visible.map((p) => p.value / basePort)` divides by 0 and emits Infinity/NaN. The Y-axis ticks then compute against NaN yMin/yMax and the SVG path silently renders as a broken line or off-screen, with NO log, NO empty-state copy, and NO 'data invalid' indicator. periodReturn at line 405-407 silently produces NaN too.
- **Evidence**: src/app/(dashboard)/allocations/widgets/performance/EquityChart.tsx:395-407
- **Fix**: Guard basePort: `const basePort = visible[0]?.value && visible[0].value > 0 ? visible[0].value : null; if (basePort == null) return <empty-state />;`. Make the failure visible — emit 'Equity data warming up' or 'Invalid window — try a wider range' rather than rendering a NaN path.

#### G20-021 · EquityChart y-tick walker falls through to smallest candidate (0.001%) on degenerate ranges
- **File**: `src/app/(dashboard)/allocations/widgets/performance/EquityChart.tsx:480`
- **Specialist**: `silent-failure-hunter` (confidence 8)
- **Summary**: The walker `let stepPct = candidates[0];` (line 480) seeds at 0.001%. The loop only updates stepPct when tickCount(c) >= MIN_TICKS. If yMin == yMax (perfectly flat series, no padding kicks in because the `|| 0.002` fallback at line 450 IS the only thing producing a non-zero range), the smallest candidate produces tickCount = 1, which is < MIN_TICKS (5), so the `else break;` fires immediately — leaving stepPct stuck at the SEED value 0.001 (= 0.00001 stepVal). The for-v loops at lines 488-489 then iterate ~80000+ ticks across the padded range, producing a SVG dom flood. No error, no log, no fallback — just a frozen render.
- **Evidence**: src/app/(dashboard)/allocations/widgets/performance/EquityChart.tsx:480-490
- **Fix**: Guard MIN_TICKS unsatisfiable: if no candidate meets tickCount >= MIN_TICKS, fall back to a fixed 3-tick render (yMin, 1, yMax) or pick the LARGEST candidate (densest legal ticks). Add a console.warn breadcrumb when the fallback fires so flat-line allocators surface in logs.

#### G20-022 · Equity card header sync stamp falls back to 'sync just now' when lastSyncAt is null
- **File**: `src/app/(dashboard)/allocations/widgets/performance/EquityChart.tsx:1286`
- **Specialist**: `silent-failure-hunter` (confidence 8)
- **Summary**: `syncStampCopy = (!lastSyncAt || now === null) ? (stale ? 'data stale' : 'sync just now') : ...` — when lastSyncAt is null, the non-stale branch renders 'sync just now' confidently, even if there has NEVER been a successful sync (queries.ts:1525-1590 produces lastSyncAt=null on accounts with no active keys or no sync history). A brand-new allocator sees an authoritative 'sync just now' chip beside an empty equity chart, suggesting data is fresh when in fact NO sync has occurred. This is the canonical 'N/A falls through to a positive-confirmation copy' silent failure.
- **Evidence**: src/app/(dashboard)/allocations/widgets/performance/EquityChart.tsx:1286-1292
- **Fix**: When lastSyncAt is null, render 'awaiting first sync' or hide the stamp entirely — never 'sync just now'. The latter is a TRUTH CLAIM the system has no evidence for.

#### G20-023 · EquityChart controlled-vs-uncontrolled props are not mutually exclusive at the type level — caller can pass period without onPeriodChange and silently lose updates
- **File**: `src/app/(dashboard)/allocations/widgets/performance/EquityChart.tsx:90`
- **Specialist**: `type-design-analyzer` (confidence 8)
- **Summary**: Props declares period?:Period, onPeriodChange?:(p)=>void, customRange?:CustomRange|null, onCustomRangeChange?:(r)=>void all as independent optionals. The component runtime code on lines 240-249 uses 'controlledPeriod ?? internalPeriod' and 'onPeriodChange?.(p)' — so a caller that passes period={p} without onPeriodChange compiles cleanly: the chart will read the controlled period (locking the toggle) but every user click vanishes (the optional-call is a no-op and 'if (controlledPeriod === undefined) setInternalPeriod(p)' falls through because controlledPeriod IS defined). This is a classic controlled-component invariant violation that the React community ships discriminated unions to prevent.
- **Evidence**: src/app/(dashboard)/allocations/widgets/performance/EquityChart.tsx:90-94 (Props), 240-249 (controlled-vs-uncontrolled merge)
- **Fix**: Split Props into a discriminated union: type EquityChartProps = EquityChartBaseProps & (| {period?:never; onPeriodChange?:never; customRange?:never; onCustomRangeChange?:never} | {period:Period; onPeriodChange:(p:Period)=>void; customRange:CustomRange|null; onCustomRangeChange:(r:CustomRange|null)=>void}). Then either ALL controlled props are present or NONE are — the half-controlled silent-no-op state becomes unrepresentable.

#### G20-024 · Test mock widens CheckLimitResult discriminated union into '{success:boolean; retryAfter:number}', erasing the invariant that retryAfter only exists on failure
- **File**: `src/app/api/preferences/route.test.ts:53`
- **Specialist**: `type-design-analyzer` (confidence 9)
- **Summary**: The real CheckLimitResult (src/lib/ratelimit.ts:174-180) is a discriminated union '{success:true} | {success:false; retryAfter:number; reason?:'ratelimit_misconfigured'}'. The test STATE on line 53 declares 'checkLimitResult: {success:true, retryAfter:0} as {success:boolean; retryAfter:number}' — a structural widening that erases the disjoint shape. As a result: (a) the success branch carries a meaningless retryAfter=0 (production never emits that field on success), (b) the 'reason' fail-CLOSED variant is impossible to mock — so the test can't exercise the 503 misconfigured path, (c) the route's runtime narrowing on if(!rl.success) is still type-correct against production but the mock can deliver shapes production never can.
- **Evidence**: src/app/api/preferences/route.test.ts:53 (manual widened type), 112 (beforeEach re-stamps the widened shape); src/lib/ratelimit.ts:174-180 (real discriminated union)
- **Fix**: Import the real CheckLimitResult and type the mock against it: 'checkLimitResult: CheckLimitResult'. Reset with {success:true} on idle, {success:false, retryAfter:30} on the 429 path. The 503 misconfigured path then gets exercisable: STATE.checkLimitResult = {success:false, retryAfter:60, reason:'ratelimit_misconfigured'}. Catches the bug that route.ts:38-44 ignores the 'reason' field and emits 429 even on misconfig.

#### G20-025 · PUT /api/preferences responses missing Cache-Control: private, no-store (NO_STORE_HEADERS)
- **File**: `src/app/api/preferences/route.ts:40`
- **Specialist**: `api-contract` (confidence 8)
- **Summary**: The PUT handler returns user-scoped 200/400/401/429/500 responses without the project's standard NO_STORE_HEADERS ({Cache-Control: private, no-store}) that withAuth-routed handlers attach. The audit-2026-05-07 round-2 Block D / P1947 standard codified in src/lib/api/headers.ts requires every authenticated route to attach NO_STORE_HEADERS to error AND success responses. The 429 path emits Retry-After but no Cache-Control, so a misbehaving intermediary or browser cache could replay the 429 (or stash the 200 success envelope) across users on a shared cache. The diff modifies only the limiter wire-up and leaves these responses naked.
- **Evidence**: src/app/api/preferences/route.ts:40-43 returns 429 with only Retry-After header; lines 16,35,50,57,89,92,94,105 all omit NO_STORE_HEADERS. Compare withAuth's 401 at src/lib/api/withAuth.ts:33-36 which does set the no-store headers.
- **Fix**: Add `import { NO_STORE_HEADERS } from "@/lib/api/headers";` and merge it into every NextResponse.json header bag in this file. Better: migrate PUT to `export const PUT = withAuth(async (req, user) => {...})` so the CSRF + 401 path and NO_STORE_HEADERS come for free, matching e.g. src/app/api/bridge/outcome/dismiss/route.ts.

#### G20-026 · PUT /api/preferences hand-rolls auth + CSRF instead of using withAuth helper
- **File**: `src/app/api/preferences/route.ts:28`
- **Specialist**: `api-contract` (confidence 8)
- **Summary**: The PUT handler open-codes the same CSRF→createClient→getUser→401 chain that withAuth() encapsulates (src/lib/api/withAuth.ts:9-39). The diff touches this exact 5-line preamble (changes the limiter import on line 9) but doesn't migrate to withAuth, leaving the file out of the project's converging auth wrapper convention. Hand-rolled auth means future hardening (e.g., the NO_STORE_HEADERS on 401, the Cookie response-touch guard) has to be re-applied here every time it lands in withAuth, and it's already drifted — the 401 here returns `NextResponse.json({error:'Unauthorized'},{status:401})` without no-store, while withAuth's 401 attaches NO_STORE_HEADERS.
- **Evidence**: src/app/api/preferences/route.ts:28-36 inline CSRF + auth + 401, vs withAuth wrapper at src/lib/api/withAuth.ts:25-37. Diff at batch-G20.diff:223-226 touched line 28 area without converting.
- **Fix**: Convert to `export const PUT = withAuth(async (req, user) => {...})`. The handler body keeps the limiter check, body parse, validation, RPC dispatch, audit emit, and 200 return. CSRF + 401 + NO_STORE_HEADERS are then inherited consistently.

#### G20-027 · PUT /api/preferences passes raw PostgREST error.message to client (envelope leakage on SQLSTATE 22023)
- **File**: `src/app/api/preferences/route.ts:92`
- **Specialist**: `api-contract` (confidence 8)
- **Summary**: On SQLSTATE 22023 the route forwards `error.message` from update_allocator_mandates straight into the 400 response body. That message originates from the RPC's `RAISE EXCEPTION` text — currently human-readable validation ("max_weight must be between 0.05 and 0.50") but the route does not constrain it. Any future RAISE inside the RPC, or a Postgres reformat (e.g., column qualifiers, schema names, type info appended to violation text), would leak DB internals to the client. The TS layer's validateSelfEditableInput() already enforces these bounds; reaching the RPC 22023 branch means TS validation drifted out of sync, which is exactly when the client gets the most information about the gap. The diff doesn't touch this line but the new limiter widens the burst (5/min → 30/min), making this leak path 6× more reachable per minute.
- **Evidence**: src/app/api/preferences/route.ts:90-93 — `if (error.code === '22023') { return NextResponse.json({error: error.message}, {status: 400}); }`
- **Fix**: Either (a) map SQLSTATE 22023 to a generic 'Validation failed' message and log the raw error.message server-side, or (b) keep an explicit allowlist of known RPC error tokens (e.g., 'mandate_archetype too long', 'invalid liquidity_preference') and pass only those through. The current free-form passthrough is the same shape Block C/M209 flagged on /api/admin/preferences/*.

#### G20-028 · PUT /api/preferences does not translate `reason: 'ratelimit_misconfigured'` into 503
- **File**: `src/app/api/preferences/route.ts:38`
- **Specialist**: `api-contract` (confidence 8)
- **Summary**: src/lib/ratelimit.ts:174-194 defines a tagged CheckLimitResult variant `{success:false, retryAfter:60, reason:'ratelimit_misconfigured'}` for the production fail-CLOSED path (Upstash env missing or Redis throw). The helper `isRateLimitMisconfigured()` is exported precisely so route handlers convert that variant to a 503 Service Unavailable — distinguishing 'real throttle' from 'limiter is broken'. The preferences PUT (and every other route grep'd in src/app/api) silently emits 429 with Retry-After=60 for the misconfig variant. useMandateAutoSave honors Retry-After then re-fires, so a production Upstash outage causes infinite client-side retries on every mandate edit, with the user-facing 'Saving too fast. Will retry in 60s.' message hiding the real outage from operators.
- **Evidence**: src/app/api/preferences/route.ts:38-43 — branches on `!rl.success` only; doesn't import or use isRateLimitMisconfigured. src/lib/ratelimit.ts:189-194 + module docstring lines 17-44.
- **Fix**: ```ts import { mandateAutoSaveLimiter, checkLimit, isRateLimitMisconfigured } from '@/lib/ratelimit'; ... const rl = await checkLimit(mandateAutoSaveLimiter, `preferences:${user.id}`); if (!rl.success) {   if (isRateLimitMisconfigured(rl)) {     return NextResponse.json({error: 'Service temporarily unavailable'}, {status: 503, headers: {'Retry-After': String(rl.retryAfter), ...NO_STORE_HEADERS}});   }   return NextResponse.json({error: 'Too many requests'}, {status: 429, headers: {'Retry-After': String(rl.retryAfter), ...NO_STORE_HEADERS}}); } ``` This should be a route-helper (withRateLimit) so the pattern lands once, not 8+ places.

#### G20-029 · PUT /api/preferences uses hand-rolled validation instead of Zod schema
- **File**: `src/app/api/preferences/route.ts:54`
- **Specialist**: `api-contract` (confidence 8)
- **Summary**: The route relies on validateSelfEditableInput() (src/lib/preferences.ts:102-159), a hand-rolled chain of typeof / Number.isFinite / range checks. Multiple sibling routes in src/app/api use Zod (allocator/holdings/sync, allocator/scenario/commit, bridge/outcome/dismiss, admin/deletion-requests/*/reject, admin/users/[id]/roles). The hand-rolled path has two contract gaps: (1) no type coercion guard — a client posting target_ticket_size_usd as the string '50000' is rejected with 'must be a number' but the same value posted as numeric 50000 is accepted; the JSON-Schema-equivalent Zod schema would normalize via z.coerce.number() or explicit fail-fast; (2) no whole-payload rejection of unknown keys (Zod's .strict()) — the route silently drops any key not in SELF_EDITABLE_PREFERENCE_FIELDS, which means an attacker probing the route for admin-only fields (founder_notes, min_sharpe) gets a 200 success envelope and never learns the field is admin-only, but also never knows it was discarded — both confusing for legit clients and a small probing channel for malicious ones. The diff broadens the limit (30/min) without tightening this surface, making both gaps more reachable. The PR also did not propagate this route to the Zod convention while touching it.
- **Evidence**: src/app/api/preferences/route.ts:54-58 + src/lib/preferences.ts:102-159. Contrast with src/app/api/allocator/scenario/commit/route.ts which uses zod.
- **Fix**: Define a `MandateSelfEditPutSchema = z.object({...}).strict()` in src/lib/preferences.ts that mirrors validateSelfEditableInput, parse with `MandateSelfEditPutSchema.safeParse(body)`. On `success === false`, return 400 with `result.error.issues[0].message` (or a flattened map). Keeps null-to-clear semantics via `.nullable()` on each field.

#### G20-030 · checkLimit accepts Ratelimit|null but isRateLimitMisconfigured() is never consulted at /api/preferences, so fail-CLOSED 503 silently degrades to 429
- **File**: `src/app/api/preferences/route.ts:38`
- **Specialist**: `type-design-analyzer` (confidence 9)
- **Summary**: checkLimit returns a CheckLimitResult that can carry reason:'ratelimit_misconfigured' on the fail-CLOSED branch (ratelimit.ts:216, 237). The discriminated union exists specifically so route handlers can convert misconfig → 503 instead of 429. The preferences PUT route imports checkLimit and calls it on line 38, but only checks rl.success and returns 429 with the synthetic 60s retryAfter — never calls isRateLimitMisconfigured(rl). A production deploy with missing UPSTASH env vars will respond 429 ('throttled') instead of 503 ('service misconfigured'), defeating the canary signal the discriminated reason field was added to support. The type made the distinction available; the call site discarded it.
- **Evidence**: src/app/api/preferences/route.ts:38-44 (if(!rl.success) → 429 only); src/lib/ratelimit.ts:189-195 (isRateLimitMisconfigured helper unused here), 216 (reason set on null-limiter fail-closed)
- **Fix**: After the success guard: if(isRateLimitMisconfigured(rl)) return NextResponse.json({error:'Service unavailable'},{status:503,headers:{'Retry-After':String(rl.retryAfter)}}); then the existing 429 fallback. Mirrors the pattern other audit-protected routes use; surfaces misconfig to canaries instead of letting it look like ordinary throttling. Also retire the manual '{success:boolean;retryAfter:number}' test-mock shape and use the real discriminated type so this regression is caught at test time.

#### G20-031 · MandateForm sends full field value on every keystroke/click — chip arrays grow O(n) per save
- **File**: `src/components/mandate/MandateForm.tsx:97`
- **Specialist**: `performance` (confidence 9)
- **Summary**: For multi-select chip fields (preferred_strategy_types, excluded_exchanges, style_exclusions), each toggle PUTs the ENTIRE updated array, not a diff. Picking 5 strategy types in sequence = 5 PUTs with payloads [a], [a,b], [a,b,c], [a,b,c,d], [a,b,c,d,e]. Total wire bytes = O(n^2) over the burst. For SUBTYPES with ~10 items this is small in absolute terms, but the server-side update_allocator_mandates RPC re-validates the entire array each time + the audit log records each full snapshot. The auto-save protocol could send delta operations (add:X, remove:Y) and let the server coalesce, but the current /api/preferences accepts only the full whitelisted field set. Combined with the no-debounce issue above, a 5-chip burst sends ~30KB+ of redundant payload + audit-log volume in <2s.
- **Evidence**: src/components/mandate/MandateForm.tsx:97-119 (onPreferredTypesToggle / onExcludedExchangesToggle / onStyleExclusionsToggle pass full `next` array); src/components/mandate/useMandateAutoSave.ts:93 (body: JSON.stringify({ [fieldName]: value })); src/app/api/preferences/route.ts:46-78 (full RPC re-validation per call).
- **Fix**: Either (a) debounce per-field (preferred low-cost fix — also addresses the burst issue), or (b) add delta endpoints for array fields. Option (a) alone reduces sends from 5 to 1 during a chip-selection flurry and is the higher-leverage fix.

#### G20-032 · MandateForm fires up to 8+ concurrent uncoalesced PUT /api/preferences requests per edit (no debounce)
- **File**: `src/components/mandate/useMandateAutoSave.ts:67`
- **Specialist**: `performance` (confidence 9)
- **Summary**: useMandateAutoSave.save() invokes fetch() synchronously per field-handler call with no debouncing or coalescing. MandateForm's 8 field handlers (3 strategy chip toggles + 2 exchange chips + max_weight slide commit + ticket-size blur + archetype blur) each call `void save(field, value)` immediately, producing 8 distinct in-flight PUT requests rather than one consolidated save. Each request re-runs full RPC update_allocator_mandates + Supabase round-trip + audit log emission. This is precisely the burst behavior that drove the rate-limit bump from 5/min to 30/min — the underlying inefficiency (every keystroke/click = a network round-trip) was widened, not fixed. Repeated slider commits on `max_weight` (drag = many commit events depending on the slider component) can also stack saves on the same field; only the generation counter protects against state corruption, not network/server load. A 200-300ms debounce per field (with last-write-wins semantics already implemented via generationRef) would cut a typical mandate-edit session from 8-15 PUTs down to 1-3.
- **Evidence**: src/components/mandate/useMandateAutoSave.ts:67-96 (save() calls fetch() unconditionally); src/components/mandate/MandateForm.tsx:88-181 (every handler calls `void save(...)` directly); src/lib/ratelimit.ts:129-136 (30/min limiter explicitly justified by the 8+ PUT burst pattern).
- **Fix**: Add a per-field debounce inside useMandateAutoSave (e.g., 250-400ms trailing-edge timer per field) keyed by fieldName so rapid toggles/typing coalesce into one PUT. The existing generationRef already drops stale responses correctly so the debounce only needs to defer the fetch — no race semantics change. Slider drag should additionally swap onCommit for onCommitDebounced to coalesce multi-step drags.

#### G20-033 · useMandateAutoSave 5xx exhaustion produces a generic 'Couldn't save' that hides server reason
- **File**: `src/components/mandate/useMandateAutoSave.ts:170`
- **Specialist**: `silent-failure-hunter` (confidence 8)
- **Summary**: After 3 retries against a 5xx response, the hook sets `fieldErrors[fieldName] = 'Couldn't save.'` — dropping the server-side error code, body message, AND the 500 'Failed to save mandate' string that route.ts:94 emits. User sees the same generic message whether the RPC failed on a Postgres constraint, a Redis ratelimit-misconfig 503, an Upstash outage, or an actual 500. There is no incident-ID, no retry hint, no console.error breadcrumb in the client. Debugging a real user report becomes 'we don't know what failed'.
- **Evidence**: src/components/mandate/useMandateAutoSave.ts:163-179
- **Fix**: Parse res.json() on the 5xx branch and include the server's error string (or a status-code suffix) in the inline error: `'Couldn't save (HTTP ${res.status}). Try again or refresh.'`. Add a console.error breadcrumb so the client log carries the failure even when the user doesn't report it.

#### G20-034 · useMandateAutoSave generation-mismatch early returns silently abandon savingFields cleanup
- **File**: `src/components/mandate/useMandateAutoSave.ts:102`
- **Specialist**: `silent-failure-hunter` (confidence 8)
- **Summary**: Three generation-mismatch early returns (lines 102, 120, 142, 165) all execute `return` after `if (generationRef.current[fieldName] !== gen)` without clearing the field from savingFields. A user who rapidly edits the same field 3x leaves the first 2 attempts in 'saving' state forever — savingFields.has(fieldName) stays true through the chip rerender, fieldErrors is never cleared from a prior 429, and a console-quiet abandoned save state persists. The newest save's success path is the only escape hatch — if THAT one fails or is replaced, the UI is permanently busy.
- **Evidence**: src/components/mandate/useMandateAutoSave.ts:102,120,142,165
- **Fix**: Wrap the generation-mismatch return in a savingFields cleanup helper. Better: refactor the loop so a single finally block guarantees savingFields.delete(fieldName) regardless of which exit path fires. Without this, 'save took 12s' (timeout) + user-keeps-editing turns into a wedged UI.

#### G20-035 · useMandateAutoSave 400/401 body.error swallowed via .catch(() => ({}))
- **File**: `src/components/mandate/useMandateAutoSave.ts:147`
- **Specialist**: `silent-failure-hunter` (confidence 8)
- **Summary**: `const body = await res.json().catch(() => ({}));` — if res.json() throws (malformed body, content-type mismatch, network drop mid-parse), the catch silently returns an empty object, and `msg = body?.error ?? 'Couldn't save'` falls through to the generic copy. The actual JSON parse error is never logged, never surfaced, never reported. A 400 with a corrupted body becomes indistinguishable from a 400 with a missing error field. Debugging requires asking the user to open devtools — there is no client-side breadcrumb.
- **Evidence**: src/components/mandate/useMandateAutoSave.ts:147-148
- **Fix**: `const body = await res.json().catch((parseErr) => { console.error('[useMandateAutoSave] failed to parse error body:', parseErr); return {}; });`. Better — also log `res.status` and `res.headers.get('content-type')` so the parse failure is debuggable.

#### G20-036 · useMandateAutoSave.save() returns Promise<void>, swallowing all error states into hook state and giving callers no way to react
- **File**: `src/components/mandate/useMandateAutoSave.ts:12`
- **Specialist**: `type-design-analyzer` (confidence 9)
- **Summary**: The save function is typed save: (fieldName, value) => Promise<void>. Every failure mode — 400 validation, 401 auth, 429 throttled, 5xx server, network exhausted — resolves the promise to void after stashing the result in saveState/fieldErrors. Callers (MandateForm) cannot await save() and then branch on the outcome; they must subscribe to hook state and reconstruct what happened. This blocks composable patterns like 'await save(); if-success then close-dialog', and makes the hook untestable for the throttle-then-success path because the promise resolution doesn't carry the final outcome.
- **Evidence**: src/components/mandate/useMandateAutoSave.ts:12 (return type Promise<void>), 105-114, 154-160, 167-178 (every error branch returns void)
- **Fix**: Return a discriminated result: type SaveResult = | {ok:true; savedAt:Date} | {ok:false; reason:'validation'|'auth'|'throttled'|'network'|'server'; message:string; retryAfter?:number}. Callers can await save() and branch deterministically; the hook state remains for UI affordance but stops being the only signal.

### LOW (11)

#### G20-037 · TweaksProvider runs three body-attribute effects + cleanups on initial mount, causing post-hydration paint flicker
- **File**: `src/app/(dashboard)/allocations/context/TweaksContext.tsx:78`
- **Specialist**: `performance` (confidence 9)
- **Summary**: On first mount, TweaksProvider initializes state with TWEAK_DEFAULTS (line 79), then the hydrate effect (line 84) calls setState(loadTweaks()) which triggers a second render with the localStorage-persisted values. Each of density / displayFont / accentIntensity has a separate useEffect that writes body attributes (data-density, data-display-font) or root inline styles (--color-accent etc). If localStorage holds non-default values, the initial render paints with TWEAK_DEFAULTS attrs, then the second render's effects fire and rewrite the attrs, triggering a FOUC: serif headings flash to sans, tight density flashes to comfortable, accent colors flash to muted, then snap to user-preferred. The new PR4 displayFont effect adds a third such flicker channel for users with persisted displayFont='sans'. Also, the cleanup function on each effect runs `removeAttribute`/`removeProperty` — so on every state change the attribute is briefly absent between the cleanup and the next effect run (React 18 strict-mode-like behavior is irrelevant here; the cleanup runs synchronously before the new effect in the SAME microtask).
- **Evidence**: src/app/(dashboard)/allocations/context/TweaksContext.tsx:78-89 (default→hydrate state path); :104-121 (effects with `removeAttribute` cleanups); :126-138 (accent effect mutates root inline styles).
- **Fix**: Either (a) read localStorage synchronously in the initial useState callback (`useState(() => loadTweaks())`) — accepted SSR mismatch is preferable to FOUC for an internal dashboard, or (b) initialize body attrs from a server-rendered initial value via a cookie. Drop the `removeAttribute` cleanups from the density/displayFont effects since they only run on full provider unmount (page navigation) and the next page will set its own values.

#### G20-038 · KpiCell.color is independent of the value's numeric sign — 'pos'/'neg' tint hardcoded per-cell regardless of whether the value is actually positive
- **File**: `src/app/(dashboard)/allocations/widgets/meta/KpiStripWidget.tsx:47`
- **Specialist**: `type-design-analyzer` (confidence 9)
- **Summary**: KpiCell.color?: 'pos'|'neg' is set per-cell at construction (line 210 'color:pos' on YTD TWR; line 221 'color:neg' on Max DD 12m). But the value is a pre-formatted string. A negative YTD return ('-3.42%') still tints positive (green) because the color was decided by the LABEL, not the SIGN. The type cannot enforce the invariant that color matches the value's actual sign. The original truth-screenshot intent is 'always green for return-style cells; always red for drawdown-style cells' which is arguably correct, but the type permits the misalignment with no signal.
- **Evidence**: src/app/(dashboard)/allocations/widgets/meta/KpiStripWidget.tsx:47 (color?:'pos'|'neg'), 200-227 (hardcoded color per row), 122-137 (color application ignores value sign)
- **Fix**: Either make color derive from value sign at construction (computed: color = ytd >= 0 ? 'pos' : 'neg'), or rename the field to communicate the policy: 'tint:'profit'|'loss'|'neutral'' so future maintainers don't read it as a sign claim. Even better: pass the numeric KpiValue and let the renderer pick color from sign + cell semantics together.

#### G20-039 · PR4 yTicks walker now allocates and sorts 28 candidates per render instead of 5
- **File**: `src/app/(dashboard)/allocations/widgets/performance/EquityChart.tsx:462`
- **Specialist**: `performance` (confidence 9)
- **Summary**: The PR4 #4 rewrite of the yTicks walker iterates `p = -3..3` (7 values) × `niceMultipliers.length=4` = 28 candidate numbers, pushes them into an array, sorts them in-place, then walks them calling `tickCount` (3 divisions + Math.floor + addition) per candidate. The previous algorithm allocated 5 candidates with no sort. With the EquityChart rendering ~1000ms is unlikely from this alone, but it runs in the chart's render body (not in a useMemo) — every re-render (60s clock tick, parent state change, tweak toggle, hover, etc.) re-allocates the 28-element array, sorts it, and walks it. On the ALL period across many overlays the cost is dwarfed by the path-string builders, but the walker is gratuitously unmemoized — there is no reason to recompute it when `yMin`/`yMax` haven't changed.
- **Evidence**: src/app/(dashboard)/allocations/widgets/performance/EquityChart.tsx:462-491 (walker is an IIFE in render body, not useMemo); the candidate array always sorts the same set of values (1, 2, 2.5, 5 × 7 powers) — invariant of run.
- **Fix**: Hoist `candidates` to module scope as a frozen pre-sorted array (it's invariant across renders). Wrap the surrounding walker IIFE in useMemo keyed on `[yMin, yMax]`. Together, render-time work drops from ~30 ops + a sort to a single forward walk.

#### G20-040 · PERIODS array and Period union are independently declared with no compile-time enforcement they stay in sync
- **File**: `src/app/(dashboard)/allocations/widgets/performance/EquityChart.tsx:32`
- **Specialist**: `type-design-analyzer` (confidence 9)
- **Summary**: Period is a union of 7 string literals on line 32, PERIODS is 'readonly Period[]' on line 40 declared verbatim. Adding a new period to Period (e.g. '5Y') won't break compilation if PERIODS is missing the literal — the runtime toggle just won't render the new token; tests that iterate PERIODS keep passing silently. The 'as const' on the array provides element narrowing but no exhaustiveness check.
- **Evidence**: src/app/(dashboard)/allocations/widgets/performance/EquityChart.tsx:32 (Period union), 40-48 (PERIODS array)
- **Fix**: Make the array the source of truth: const PERIODS = ['1M','3M','6M','YTD','1Y','ALL','CUSTOM'] as const; export type Period = (typeof PERIODS)[number]. Now Period is derived from PERIODS, so additions can only happen in one place. Or keep the union as truth and add a once-evaluated assertion: const _exhaustive: Record<Period,true> = Object.fromEntries(PERIODS.map(p=>[p,true])) as Record<Period,true>.

#### G20-041 · CustomRange = {start:string; end:string} carries no compile-time guarantee of ISO format or start <= end ordering
- **File**: `src/app/(dashboard)/allocations/widgets/performance/EquityChart.tsx:57`
- **Specialist**: `type-design-analyzer` (confidence 9)
- **Summary**: CustomRange is two unbranded strings. There is no type-level distinction between 'YYYY-MM-DD' and arbitrary text; no invariant that start <= end. parseISO returns NaN on bad input and propagates silently through sliceByPeriod (which then filters everything out and renders an empty chart). The picker UI prevents most bad inputs, but the type is the boundary contract — and it lets the rest of the codebase create invalid ranges via direct construction.
- **Evidence**: src/app/(dashboard)/allocations/widgets/performance/EquityChart.tsx:57 (CustomRange type), 195-199 (parseISO of unchecked strings in sliceByPeriod)
- **Fix**: Brand the strings: type ISODate = string & {__brand:'ISODate'}; type CustomRange = {start:ISODate; end:ISODate}. Provide a parseRange(start,end): CustomRange|{error:string} constructor that validates format AND ordering. The type alone won't stop invalid Date objects from being passed into the SVG path math, but it surfaces the missing validation step at every construction site.

#### G20-042 · anchorFromFirstPositive returns DailyPoint[] indistinguishable from the input — anchored-vs-raw is invisible at the type level
- **File**: `src/app/(dashboard)/allocations/widgets/performance/EquityChart.tsx:147`
- **Specialist**: `type-design-analyzer` (confidence 9)
- **Summary**: anchorFromFirstPositive transforms raw DailyPoints into f7-anchored DailyPoints (value/base normalized so index 0 = 1.0), but the return type is the same DailyPoint[] as the input. Downstream code like sliceByPeriod, periodReturn, and the SVG path code all assume anchored points where index-0-value == 1.0. A caller that bypasses the anchor and passes raw points compiles cleanly and renders wrong (the 0% baseline detaches from the line start). The audit found the periodReturn calculation on line 1312 — if the points weren't anchored, the returned ratio is meaningless.
- **Evidence**: src/app/(dashboard)/allocations/widgets/performance/EquityChart.tsx:147-157 (anchorFromFirstPositive), 1312-1321 (periodReturn assumes anchored input)
- **Fix**: Brand the output: type AnchoredPoints = DailyPoint[] & {__brand:'anchored-f7'}; function anchorFromFirstPositive(points:DailyPoint[]): AnchoredPoints. sliceByPeriod and periodReturn then require AnchoredPoints, surfacing missing-anchor bugs at the call site instead of as silent wrong renders.

#### G20-043 · TC11 'WR-02 burst tolerance' test does not actually test bursts
- **File**: `src/app/api/preferences/route.test.ts:321`
- **Specialist**: `api-contract` (confidence 9)
- **Summary**: The new TC11 test added by PR #79 makes ONE PUT call and asserts `STATE.lastCheckLimitArg === MANDATE_AUTO_SAVE_LIMITER_SENTINEL`. That validates the route is wired to the named limiter sentinel — which is correct as far as it goes — but does NOT validate burst tolerance: it never makes the 8+ sequential calls the WR-02 scenario describes, never asserts each returns 200, and never asserts the underlying limiter would actually permit 30 requests in 60s. The test name + comment promise burst tolerance; the assertion only covers limiter identity. A regression where the limit value is fat-fingered (e.g., mandateAutoSaveLimiter = makeLimiter(3, '60 s')) passes this test cleanly. The CHANGELOG entry calls this regression out as 'TC11 — WR-02 burst tolerance', conflating identity-check with burst-tolerance contract.
- **Evidence**: src/app/api/preferences/route.test.ts:321-334 — one PUT, two identity assertions; no loop, no 200-count assertion, no decremented limiter mock.
- **Fix**: Either (a) rename to `TC11 — PUT is wired to mandateAutoSaveLimiter, not userActionLimiter` to match what's actually asserted, or (b) add a second test that mocks checkLimit with a real call counter, makes 8 sequential PUTs simulating the MandateForm field-level burst, and asserts all 8 return 200 + that the mock counted ≥8 successful slot grants. Then mandateAutoSaveLimiter's 30/min value is genuinely under test.

#### G20-044 · TC11 mandate auto-save burst test does not verify the actual 30/min limit absorbs an 8-action burst
- **File**: `src/app/api/preferences/route.test.ts:321`
- **Specialist**: `pr-test-analyzer` (confidence 9)
- **Summary**: TC11 only asserts the sentinel identity of the limiter passed to checkLimit — it does NOT exercise the actual rate-limit math. The PR's premise is 'MandateForm fans a single edit out into 8+ field-level PUTs ... the 6th save was guaranteed to surface Saving too fast'. A future change that wires the route to a real Upstash limiter at, say, 5/60s but with a sentinel `__id: 'mandateAutoSaveLimiter'` would keep the test green while reintroducing the 429-mid-burst bug. The test asserts wiring, not behavior — Rule 9 violation per project CLAUDE.md.
- **Evidence**: src/app/api/preferences/route.test.ts:330-333 — only assertion is `STATE.lastCheckLimitArg === MANDATE_AUTO_SAVE_LIMITER_SENTINEL`. checkLimit mock at lines 75-78 always returns STATE.checkLimitResult which is reset to {success: true} on every test. No test issues 8 sequential PUTs and asserts none return 429. The actual 30/60s configuration in src/lib/ratelimit.ts:136 is also untested.
- **Fix**: Augment TC11 (or add TC11b) to issue 8 sequential PUTs with checkLimit mock returning {success: true} for the first 30 and {success: false, retryAfter: 30} for any 31st+ — assert all 8 return 200. Add a unit test in src/lib/ratelimit.test.ts asserting `mandateAutoSaveLimiter` makeLimiter args are (30, '60 s') via reading the module's exported limiter object's internal config OR via integration test in a beforeAll harness. Mirror the watchlist/[strategyId]/route.test.ts T-13-01-02 pattern which DOES exercise the 429 path.

#### G20-045 · PUT /api/preferences crashes on JSON body `null` (uncovered 500 path)
- **File**: `src/app/api/preferences/route.ts:48`
- **Specialist**: `api-contract` (confidence 9)
- **Summary**: The route handles invalid JSON via try/catch (line 47-51) → 400 'Invalid request body'. But a valid JSON body of literal `null` is accepted by req.json() and assigned to `body`. Then pickSelfEditableFields(null) (src/lib/preferences.ts:80-88) iterates `SELF_EDITABLE_PREFERENCE_FIELDS` and runs `key in input` against null, which throws TypeError 'Cannot use in operator to search for X in null'. That escapes the route's try/catch (the try only wraps req.json()), so Next.js returns a generic 500 with no audit, no operator log line, and no structured error. Pre-existing; PR didn't touch this path but the diff widened the surface from 5/min to 30/min, making the crash 6× more reachable per authenticated user. Same shape for body=`42` (numeric literal) and body=`'foo'` (string literal) since req.json() also accepts those.
- **Evidence**: src/app/api/preferences/route.ts:46-58, vs pickSelfEditableFields signature at src/lib/preferences.ts:80-88. `key in input` on null/non-object input throws.
- **Fix**: After `body = await req.json();` (line 48), add `if (body === null || typeof body !== 'object' || Array.isArray(body)) { return NextResponse.json({error: 'Invalid request body'}, {status: 400}); }`. Or — if migrating to Zod (medium finding above) — `.parse(body)` on a `z.object({}).strict()` rejects non-object input automatically.

#### G20-046 · PUT /api/preferences with empty/no-self-editable body emits RPC + audit with empty fields
- **File**: `src/app/api/preferences/route.ts:67`
- **Specialist**: `api-contract` (confidence 9)
- **Summary**: If the client posts `{}` or only admin-only fields like `{founder_notes: 'x'}`, `pickSelfEditableFields` returns `{}` (whitelist drops everything). Then `rpcArgs` is `{}`, `clearFields` is `[]`, and the route invokes `update_allocator_mandates({})` (a true no-op COALESCE) AND emits an audit event with `metadata: {fields: [], self_edit: true}`. That's two side-effect calls (one DB RPC, one audit) on a request that semantically did nothing. Cost matters now that the limit is 30/min: a script that posts `{}` 30 times/min produces 60 background writes/min/user with no user-facing change, and the audit_log fills with zero-information rows. The PR doesn't introduce this but the new limit makes it cheaper to trigger.
- **Evidence**: src/app/api/preferences/route.ts:64-77 — `clearFields` empty + `rpcArgs` empty; the route still falls through to the RPC dispatch + audit emit at lines 84 and 98.
- **Fix**: After the validation gate (line 58), short-circuit: `if (Object.keys(fields).length === 0) { return NextResponse.json({success: true, fields: []}); }` — no RPC, no audit. Or, looser: skip the audit emit specifically when `Object.keys(fields).length === 0`.

#### G20-047 · PUT /api/preferences response envelope is bare {success:true} — no echoed value, no version, breaks partial-save reconciliation
- **File**: `src/app/api/preferences/route.ts:105`
- **Specialist**: `api-contract` (confidence 9)
- **Summary**: The 200 response is `{success: true}` with no fields, no echoed values, no updated_at timestamp, no version/etag. useMandateAutoSave (src/components/mandate/useMandateAutoSave.ts:122-131) only reads `res.ok` and stamps `setLastSavedAt(new Date())`. Contract gaps: (1) client never learns whether the server actually persisted the value it sent vs coerced/clamped it (e.g., a UI race where two field saves overlap and the COALESCE RPC merges differently than expected); (2) no concurrency token — if two browser tabs auto-save the same field with different values, both 200 cleanly and the second wins silently; (3) lastSavedAt is client-clock derived, not server-derived, so cross-device sync surfaces show wall-clock skew. With the new 30/min limit broadening the legitimate burst, the probability of overlapping in-flight saves goes up — the bare envelope makes those overlaps invisible.
- **Evidence**: src/app/api/preferences/route.ts:105 returns `{success: true}`; src/components/mandate/useMandateAutoSave.ts:122-131 reads only res.ok.
- **Fix**: Return the freshly-persisted row from the RPC. update_allocator_mandates already runs a COALESCE UPSERT; have it RETURN the updated row and surface `{success: true, preferences: row, mandate_edited_at: row.mandate_edited_at}`. Client can then reconcile: setLastSavedAt(new Date(mandate_edited_at)) and optionally diff per-field server value vs local optimistic state to catch coercion. Bonus: closes the dual-tab last-write-wins window if combined with an If-Match header on the next save.

## G21 — PRs #82-#83 — Queue failed_retry re-claim + 4xx classifier + dedupe by partition keys

### CRITICAL (4)

#### G21-001 · No live SQL test for failed_retry → claimable transition (the headline behavioral fix of PR #82)
- **File**: `analytics-service/tests/test_compute_jobs_fencing.py:538`
- **Specialist**: `pr-test-analyzer` (confidence 10)
- **Summary**: Migration 089 widens claim filter to include status='failed_retry' AND next_attempt_at<=now(). The whole PR exists because 21 prod rows sat stuck for up to 9 days. Yet there is no live-DB regression test that (a) inserts a compute_jobs row with status='failed_retry' and next_attempt_at<=now() (b) calls claim_compute_jobs_with_priority (c) asserts the row was claimed. If a future migration silently drops 'failed_retry' from the IN-list, every existing unit/structural test still passes — only production stuck-row count would catch it. test_compute_jobs_fencing.py already has admin client + _seed_user_id + strategy_id fixture (lines 489-525) and a _claim_one helper (line 528), so this test costs ~15 lines.
- **Evidence**: grep 'failed_retry' analytics-service/tests/*.py → only 1 hit in test_compute_jobs_fencing.py:800 (a mark_done parametrize on inflight-states), no test inserts failed_retry and claims it. supabase/migrations/20260428155809_claim_failed_retry.sql line 11: 'so failed_retry rows sat in the queue forever' — the fix is the entire reason the migration exists.
- **Fix**: Add to test_compute_jobs_fencing.py:  def test_claim_includes_failed_retry_when_backoff_elapsed(admin, strategy_id):     """Migration 089: failed_retry rows whose next_attempt_at <= now() are claimable."""     job = admin.table('compute_jobs').insert({         'strategy_id': strategy_id, 'kind': 'sync_trades',         'status': 'failed_retry', 'priority': 'normal', 'exchange': 'okx',         'next_attempt_at': '2020-01-01T00:00:00Z',  # in the past         'attempts': 1,     }).execute().data[0]     try:         claimed = _claim_one(admin, 'g21-failed-retry')         assert claimed is not None, 'failed_retry row with elapsed backoff must be claimable (PR #82 fix)'         assert claimed['id'] == job['id']         assert claimed['status'] == 'running'         assert claimed['attempts'] == 2  # incremented on claim     finally:         admin.table('compute_jobs').delete().eq('id', job['id']).execute()

#### G21-002 · No test for failed_retry backoff gate (next_attempt_at in the future)
- **File**: `analytics-service/tests/test_compute_jobs_fencing.py:538`
- **Specialist**: `pr-test-analyzer` (confidence 9)
- **Summary**: Migration 089 specifically filters `WHERE status IN ('pending','failed_retry') AND next_attempt_at <= now()`. The backoff schedule (30s/2min/8min from mark_compute_job_failed) is enforced ONLY by the next_attempt_at gate. If a future refactor accidentally drops `next_attempt_at <= now()` from the WHERE clause, the queue would claim failed_retry rows immediately on every poll — bypassing the entire backoff mechanic. No test asserts a failed_retry row with future next_attempt_at is NOT claimed. This is the negative counterpart to finding 1 and is just as load-bearing.
- **Evidence**: supabase/migrations/20260428155809_claim_failed_retry.sql:226 'WHERE status IN (pending,failed_retry) AND next_attempt_at <= now()'. grep for 'next_attempt_at' in analytics-service/tests/ → no test inserts a row with future next_attempt_at and asserts NOT claimed.
- **Fix**: Add to test_compute_jobs_fencing.py:  def test_failed_retry_with_future_next_attempt_at_not_claimed(admin, strategy_id):     """Migration 089 backoff gate: failed_retry rows whose next_attempt_at is in     the future must NOT be claimed (the retry schedule is what gates re-claim)."""     job = admin.table('compute_jobs').insert({         'strategy_id': strategy_id, 'kind': 'sync_trades',         'status': 'failed_retry', 'priority': 'normal', 'exchange': 'okx',         'next_attempt_at': '2099-01-01T00:00:00Z',  # far in the future         'attempts': 1,     }).execute().data[0]     try:         claimed = _claim_one(admin, 'g21-future-backoff')         assert claimed is None or claimed['id'] != job['id'], (             'failed_retry row with future next_attempt_at must NOT be claimed '             '(would bypass the 30s/2min/8min backoff schedule)'         )         # And the row must still be failed_retry afterward.         row = admin.table('compute_jobs').select('status').eq('id', job['id']).single().execute().data         assert row['status'] == 'failed_retry'     finally:         admin.table('compute_jobs').delete().eq('id', job['id']).execute()

#### G21-003 · Throttle probe widening (failed_retry counted) untested — could regress to old pending-only count silently
- **File**: `supabase/migrations/20260428155809_claim_failed_retry.sql:292`
- **Specialist**: `pr-test-analyzer` (confidence 9)
- **Summary**: Migration 089 widens the throttle probe (`v_high_pending`) inside claim_compute_jobs_with_priority to count failed_retry rows: `WHERE priority IN ('normal','high') AND status IN ('pending','failed_retry') AND next_attempt_at <= now()` (line 292). This is load-bearing: a normal/high failed_retry row must throttle low-priority work. If a future change silently reverts this to `status = 'pending'`, normal/high failed_retry rows would let low-priority backfill steal slots — and there is no test. The TestClaimDedupe mocks the entire RPC; no live test validates the throttle behavior.
- **Evidence**: supabase/migrations/20260428155809_claim_failed_retry.sql:288-292 'Throttle probe … Includes failed_retry rows whose backoff has elapsed … so a normal/high failed_retry row correctly throttles low-priority work.' grep 'low.*priority' in tests → no tests for low throttling vs failed_retry.
- **Fix**: Add to test_compute_jobs_fencing.py (uses 3 rows + strategy_id fixture):  def test_throttle_probe_counts_failed_retry_normal_priority(admin, strategy_id):     """Migration 089: a normal-priority failed_retry row throttles low-priority     work (probe widened to count failed_retry alongside pending)."""     # 1 normal failed_retry (ready), 1 low pending (ready) — low must NOT be claimed     user_id = _seed_user_id(admin)     normal = admin.table('compute_jobs').insert({         'strategy_id': strategy_id, 'kind': 'sync_trades',         'status': 'failed_retry', 'priority': 'normal', 'exchange': 'okx',         'next_attempt_at': '2020-01-01T00:00:00Z', 'attempts': 1,     }).execute().data[0]     low = admin.table('compute_jobs').insert({         'strategy_id': strategy_id, 'kind': 'compute_analytics',         'status': 'pending', 'priority': 'low',         'next_attempt_at': '2020-01-01T00:00:00Z',     }).execute().data[0]     try:         res = admin.rpc('claim_compute_jobs_with_priority', {             'p_batch_size': 5, 'p_worker_id': 'g21-throttle',         }).execute()         claimed_ids = {r['id'] for r in res.data}         assert low['id'] not in claimed_ids, (             'low-priority row must be throttled when a normal failed_retry is ready (mig 089 widened probe)'         )     finally:         admin.table('compute_jobs').delete().in_('id', [normal['id'], low['id']]).execute()

#### G21-004 · Migration 090 omits live regression test for partition-key dedupe — the documented test scenario
- **File**: `supabase/migrations/20260428190907_claim_dedupe_partition_keys.sql:252`
- **Specialist**: `pr-test-analyzer` (confidence 10)
- **Summary**: Migration 090 comment lines 252-258 explicitly say: 'A live regression test (insert two failed_retry rows sharing a partition, call claim, assert ≤ 1 returned, savepoint-rollback) is omitted here because every queue partition column has a foreign key … A migration cannot fabricate test users without polluting production.' This reasoning is wrong for the Python test layer: analytics-service/tests/test_compute_jobs_fencing.py already seeds real users via _seed_user_id (line 489) and real strategies via strategy_id fixture. The Python test suite *can* insert two failed_retry rows for the same (kind, allocator_id), call claim, and assert ≤1 returned + no 23505. Without this test, the entire production bug (worker spun for 7min on 2026-04-28 17:10 UTC) has zero automated coverage — only the mocked TestClaimDedupe in test_main_worker.py, which tests the *worker* tolerance, NOT the SQL guarantee.
- **Evidence**: supabase/migrations/20260428190907_claim_dedupe_partition_keys.sql:252-258 (explicit omission). analytics-service/tests/test_main_worker.py:438-508 (TestClaimDedupe) is all mocked: claim_chain.execute.return_value = MagicMock(data=[survivor]) — never tests the SQL function itself. PR #83 CHANGELOG entry line 422 even says 'a live regression test … was run as a one-shot during deploy — it could not be embedded in the migration' but Python tests CAN embed it.
- **Fix**: Add to test_compute_jobs_fencing.py:  def test_claim_dedupes_two_failed_retry_sharing_allocator(admin):     """Migration 090: two failed_retry rows for the same (kind, allocator_id) must     not both be claimed in a single batch — the partial unique index would 23505."""     user_id = _seed_user_id(admin)  # acts as allocator_id (FK to auth.users)     rows = []     for _ in range(2):         r = admin.table('compute_jobs').insert({             'kind': 'rescore_allocator', 'allocator_id': user_id,             'status': 'failed_retry', 'priority': 'normal',             'next_attempt_at': '2020-01-01T00:00:00Z', 'attempts': 1,         }).execute().data[0]         rows.append(r['id'])     try:         res = admin.rpc('claim_compute_jobs_with_priority', {             'p_batch_size': 5, 'p_worker_id': 'g21-dedupe',         }).execute()  # MUST NOT raise 23505         assert len(res.data) <= 1, f'dedupe must claim ≤1 row per partition, got {len(res.data)}'     finally:         for rid in rows:             admin.table('compute_jobs').delete().eq('id', rid).execute()

### HIGH (20)

#### G21-005 · HTTPException 4xx classifier swallows transient infrastructure 403/404/422 as permanent
- **File**: `analytics-service/services/job_worker.py:212`
- **Specialist**: `silent-failure-hunter` (confidence 8)
- **Summary**: The new classifier marks ALL 4xx HTTPException (except 408/429) as 'permanent', sending the job straight to failed_final with NO retry. But routers/internal.py raises 403 'Internal API not configured' (depends on env var INTERNAL_API_TOKEN that can be temporarily misconfigured during a deploy), 403 'Forbidden' on transient token mismatch, and 404 'API key not found' which can occur during a key rotation race. analytics_runner.py also wraps any internal Exception into HTTPException(500,'Analytics computation failed') at line 1198 — a 500 falls through to 'unknown' so retries OK, but the inner exception detail string is lost (replaced with generic message). The 4xx classifier blanket-permanent rule means a strategy that ENCOUNTERS a transient 403 once (e.g., during deploy) terminates as failed_final, requiring manual admin intervention to re-enqueue.
