- **Evidence**: analytics-service/services/job_worker.py:212-217 (HTTPException 4xx → permanent); analytics-service/routers/internal.py:114,118,185 (403 not-configured / Forbidden / 404 transient cases)
- **Fix**: Narrow the permanent classification to status codes that are SEMANTICALLY permanent (400 'Insufficient trade history', 422 validation). Allow caller to opt into permanent-for-this-message via HTTPException.detail prefix, OR keep 403/404 as 'unknown' (retried) because deploy-time 403s should self-heal once env is fixed. At minimum, document and add a regression test that 403 'Internal API not configured' is NOT treated as permanent.

#### G21-006 · classify_exception returns bare tuple[str, str] instead of (Literal['transient','permanent','unknown'], str)
- **File**: `analytics-service/services/job_worker.py:164`
- **Specialist**: `type-design-analyzer` (confidence 9)
- **Summary**: The error classifier's return type is annotated `tuple[str, str]`. The first element is a 3-value enum ('transient' | 'permanent' | 'unknown') enforced by a DB CHECK constraint in compute_jobs.error_kind and re-validated by mark_compute_job_failed (which raises if not in ('transient','permanent','unknown')). The Python side has no Literal/Enum representation: a typo such as `return ('permamnent', ...)` would type-check fine, slip past unit tests that only assert specific strings, and explode at the DB boundary as a generic plpgsql exception with no static signal. The PR-Y2/PR-Y1 audit prompt explicitly flagged 'classifier return type that's bool instead of an enum (Retry|Permanent|Unknown)' — the actual codebase ships the moral equivalent (bare str with a comment annotation). This is the central type-design weakness of PR #82.
- **Evidence**: analytics-service/services/job_worker.py:164 `def classify_exception(exc: Exception) -> tuple[str, str]:` with returns at lines 173, 182, 192, 198, 205, 215, 217, 220
- **Fix**: Define `ErrorKind = Literal['transient', 'permanent', 'unknown']` at module scope (next to the existing Side/PositionDirection Literals at lines 78-79), retype to `def classify_exception(exc: Exception) -> tuple[ErrorKind, str]:`, and propagate to DispatchResult.error_kind. mypy/pyright then catches the typo class statically. Zero runtime cost, single-file change.

#### G21-007 · DispatchResult.error_kind: str | None encodes the same 3-value enum as a comment, not a type
- **File**: `analytics-service/services/job_worker.py:132`
- **Specialist**: `type-design-analyzer` (confidence 9)
- **Summary**: DispatchResult is a frozen-feeling dataclass that carries the classifier's output across module boundaries (job_worker → main_worker → DB RPC). error_kind is typed `str | None` with a comment '# transient | permanent | unknown'. Every `return DispatchResult(error_kind='permanent', ...)` callsite (lines 362, 375, 427, 448, 454, 867, 891, 938, 1483, 1505, 1705, 1723, 1792) is a hardcoded literal — but nothing prevents a callsite (current or future) from passing `error_kind='Permanent'` (capitalization drift), `error_kind='retry'` (wrong vocabulary), or `error_kind=str(some_var)`. Main_worker.py:330 then forwards this directly to the RPC via `kind or 'unknown'`. The DB CHECK catches it, but the failure mode is a postgres exception not a static type error.
- **Evidence**: analytics-service/services/job_worker.py:128-133 DispatchResult dataclass; analytics-service/main_worker.py:322,330 propagates result.error_kind verbatim to the RPC
- **Fix**: Once ErrorKind is defined, change DispatchResult to `error_kind: ErrorKind | None = None`. Tighten the dataclass with `@dataclass(frozen=True, slots=True)` so accidental mutation also fails statically. Add a constructor-side assertion in __post_init__ that error_kind is None or matches the Literal — the DB CHECK becomes defense-in-depth instead of the only guard.

#### G21-008 · HTTPException.detail is Any — silently stringifies dicts/lists with no schema guarantee
- **File**: `analytics-service/services/job_worker.py:215`
- **Specialist**: `type-design-analyzer` (confidence 8)
- **Summary**: FastAPI types `HTTPException.detail: Any` because callers may raise `HTTPException(400, detail={'code': 'INSUFFICIENT_TRADES', 'have': 12, 'need': 30})` for structured client errors. The new classifier branch calls `str(exc.detail)[:480]` which renders a dict as `"{'code': 'INSUFFICIENT_TRADES', 'have': 12, ...}"` — readable for humans, but the admin UI surface loses any structural contract. There is no type at the boundary saying 'compute_jobs.last_error is always a flat string scalar; structured detail must be JSON-serialized'. Worse: a non-stringifiable detail (e.g. an object whose __str__ raises) would crash classify_exception itself, propagate out of the dispatch try/except in main_worker.py:352, and trigger the 'unhandled error' fallback path — turning a permanent 4xx into a fallback 'unknown' kind, defeating the entire point of PR #82.
- **Evidence**: analytics-service/services/job_worker.py:215,217 `f"{status}: {str(exc.detail)[:480]}"`; compare with the rest of classify_exception which uses `str(exc)` (always safe because Exception.__str__ is contractually str)
- **Fix**: Guard the stringification: `try: detail_str = str(exc.detail) except Exception: detail_str = '<unstringifiable detail>'`. Or stronger: introduce a `_format_http_detail(detail: Any) -> str` helper that handles dict/list/str/None explicitly and serializes structured detail via json.dumps with a fallback. Add a regression test mirroring test_http_exception_400_is_permanent but with `detail={'code': 'X', 'data': [...]}` to lock the contract.

#### G21-009 · Job status modeled as bare str with no Python Literal mirroring the DB CHECK
- **File**: `analytics-service/services/job_worker.py:1`
- **Specialist**: `type-design-analyzer` (confidence 9)
- **Summary**: compute_jobs.status is a DB-CHECK enum: ('pending', 'running', 'done', 'done_pending_children', 'failed_retry', 'failed_final'). Migration 089 (the headline change of PR #82) widened the claim filter to `status IN ('pending', 'failed_retry')` — the partition between 'claimable' and 'non-claimable' status values is now a load-bearing invariant. The Python worker reads `job['status']` (untyped dict access), references the literal strings in mark_* RPC params, and has no JobStatus enum/Literal anywhere. A future refactor that splits failed_retry into 'failed_retry_transient' / 'failed_retry_unknown' (a reasonable evolution) would need to grep every str literal across the worker codebase. The audit prompt explicitly flagged 'job status enum encoded as string with no Literal' — this is that.
- **Evidence**: analytics-service/services/job_worker.py uses `job: dict` throughout (lines 505, 857, 878, 900, 961, 1000, etc.); supabase/migrations/20260411144407_compute_jobs_queue.sql:112-120 defines the 6-value CHECK
- **Fix**: Add `JobStatus = Literal['pending','running','done','done_pending_children','failed_retry','failed_final']` plus a `CLAIMABLE_STATUSES: tuple[JobStatus, ...] = ('pending', 'failed_retry')` constant next to TIMEOUT_PER_KIND. The migration's widened filter is then mirrored as a single source of truth in code, and any future status added in SQL forces a Python-side update (via a typed TypedDict ComputeJobRow that exhausts JobStatus in match statements).

#### G21-010 · No test for concurrent claim under partition collision (RPC behavior under contention)
- **File**: `analytics-service/tests/test_compute_jobs_fencing.py:528`
- **Specialist**: `pr-test-analyzer` (confidence 9)
- **Summary**: PR #83 migration 090 comment line 53-57 claims 'Two concurrent workers see the same dedupe winners (the inner CTE is deterministic) and SKIP LOCKED partitions the locked subset.' This is a non-trivial concurrency assertion: if two workers race on a single failed_retry row, FOR UPDATE SKIP LOCKED must give it to exactly one (not zero, not two). The existing fencing test_dedupe layer is fully mocked. No test invokes two parallel RPC calls and asserts disjoint result sets. The fencing suite has the admin client + asyncio support to do this.
- **Evidence**: supabase/migrations/20260428190907_claim_dedupe_partition_keys.sql:53-57. analytics-service/tests/test_main_worker.py:438-508 TestClaimDedupe is mocked (MagicMock + AsyncMock). grep 'concurrent.*claim' in tests → no hits. test_compute_jobs_fencing.py uses sync admin client; concurrency would need threading.Thread or two psycopg connections.
- **Fix**: Add to test_compute_jobs_fencing.py using a thread-pool of two admin clients:  import concurrent.futures  def test_concurrent_claim_disjoint_under_skip_locked(admin, strategy_id):     """Mig 090 contract: two concurrent claim_compute_jobs_with_priority calls     return disjoint row sets via FOR UPDATE SKIP LOCKED."""     # Seed 4 pending rows (different strategies/api_keys so dedupe doesn't fire)     job_ids = []     for i in range(4):         r = admin.table('compute_jobs').insert({             'strategy_id': strategy_id, 'kind': 'sync_trades',             'status': 'pending', 'priority': 'normal', 'exchange': 'okx',             'next_attempt_at': '2020-01-01T00:00:00Z',         }).execute().data[0]         job_ids.append(r['id'])     try:         def _claim_batch(worker):             res = admin.rpc('claim_compute_jobs_with_priority', {                 'p_batch_size': 4, 'p_worker_id': worker,             }).execute()             return {row['id'] for row in (res.data or [])}         with concurrent.futures.ThreadPoolExecutor(max_workers=2) as ex:             f1 = ex.submit(_claim_batch, 'g21-conc-A')             f2 = ex.submit(_claim_batch, 'g21-conc-B')             a, b = f1.result(), f2.result()         assert a.isdisjoint(b), f'two workers got overlapping claims: {a & b}'         # Note: dedupe+single strategy means only 1 row survives; full coverage         # needs multiple strategy/api_key partitions seeded.     finally:         admin.table('compute_jobs').delete().in_('id', job_ids).execute()

#### G21-011 · HTTPException 401/403 and 5xx-not-500 codes untested — relies on assumed 4xx/5xx range bracket
- **File**: `analytics-service/tests/test_job_worker.py:131`
- **Specialist**: `pr-test-analyzer` (confidence 9)
- **Summary**: The classifier uses `if 400 <= status < 500` as the catch-all 4xx branch and lets everything else fall to unknown. Tests cover 400/404/422 explicitly but not 401 (auth-flavored — clear permanent) or 403 (forbidden — clear permanent). Both are commonly raised by FastAPI auth deps in this codebase. If a developer later changes the bracket to `400 < status < 500` (off-by-one), 400 → permanent silently disappears but the 400 test still passes. Adding 401/403 increases edge-density of the bracket boundary. Similarly the 500 test passes — but 503 (Bad Gateway) and 504 (Gateway Timeout) are NOT tested; if the developer later adds a 'transient bracket for 5xx network-flavored codes' the regression won't bite.
- **Evidence**: analytics-service/services/job_worker.py:207-216 — uses `400 <= status < 500` bracket; tests cover only 400/404/422 (a contiguous block, no boundary stress). grep for '401\|403' in test_job_worker.py → no hits.
- **Fix**: Add to TestClassifyException:  def test_http_exception_401_is_permanent(self) -> None:     exc = HTTPException(status_code=401, detail='Not authenticated')     kind, msg = classify_exception(exc)     assert kind == 'permanent'     assert '401' in msg  def test_http_exception_403_is_permanent(self) -> None:     exc = HTTPException(status_code=403, detail='Forbidden')     kind, msg = classify_exception(exc)     assert kind == 'permanent'  def test_http_exception_399_falls_through_to_unknown(self) -> None:     """Boundary: 399 is below the 4xx bracket — falls to unknown."""     exc = HTTPException(status_code=399, detail='odd')     kind, _ = classify_exception(exc)     assert kind == 'unknown'  def test_http_exception_503_is_unknown_retry(self) -> None:     """5xx is retried by default — verify 503 (not just 500)."""     exc = HTTPException(status_code=503, detail='upstream unavailable')     kind, _ = classify_exception(exc)     assert kind == 'unknown'

#### G21-012 · HTTPException detail truncation untested — separate 480-char cap from generic 500-char cap
- **File**: `analytics-service/tests/test_job_worker.py:167`
- **Specialist**: `pr-test-analyzer` (confidence 9)
- **Summary**: The HTTPException branch uses `str(exc.detail)[:480]` while the generic catch-all uses `[:500]` (job_worker.py:213 vs 226). This is a DIFFERENT cap with no test. The existing test_message_is_truncated only covers the generic 500-char cap via RuntimeError. If a future refactor unifies the caps to 500 chars, the 480 cap silently disappears with no test failure — and admin UI rows can blow up if the HTTPException detail is huge. The 20-char headroom is reserved for the `{status}: ` prefix (lines 211, 214); needs to be load-bearing.
- **Evidence**: analytics-service/services/job_worker.py:213 `f"{status}: {str(exc.detail)[:480]}"` vs line 226 `str(exc)[:500]`. grep 'truncated' in test_job_worker.py:167 → only 1 test, on RuntimeError, asserting 500-char cap.
- **Fix**: Add to TestClassifyException:  def test_http_exception_long_detail_is_truncated(self) -> None:     """HTTPException detail is truncated to leave room for '{status}: ' prefix     so total message stays ≤ 500 chars."""     long_detail = 'y' * 5000     exc = HTTPException(status_code=400, detail=long_detail)     _, msg = classify_exception(exc)     assert len(msg) <= 500, f'HTTPException message must be ≤500 chars, got {len(msg)}'     assert msg.startswith('400: '), 'HTTPException message must start with status prefix'

#### G21-013 · HTTPException with non-string detail (dict/list/None) untested — str() coercion may explode
- **File**: `analytics-service/tests/test_job_worker.py:131`
- **Specialist**: `pr-test-analyzer` (confidence 8)
- **Summary**: FastAPI HTTPException allows detail to be any JSON-serializable object (dict, list, model). The classifier does `str(exc.detail)[:480]`, which works on strings but produces noisy `{'code': 'X', ...}` reprs for dicts and `None` for None. analytics_runner is shown raising `HTTPException(400, 'Insufficient trade history')` (string) but other call sites in the codebase may raise with dict/list detail. The error_kind branch logic doesn't change, but the sanitized message stored in compute_jobs.last_error_message could end up as the literal string 'None' — confusing admin diagnostics. No test covers these inputs.
- **Evidence**: analytics-service/services/job_worker.py:212-214 `str(exc.detail)[:480]`. FastAPI HTTPException signature accepts `detail: Any`. No test for non-string detail.
- **Fix**: Add to TestClassifyException:  def test_http_exception_dict_detail_is_permanent(self) -> None:     """FastAPI allows detail to be a dict (validation errors). Classifier must     handle it without crashing and produce a serialized message."""     exc = HTTPException(status_code=422, detail={'field': 'symbol', 'error': 'missing'})     kind, msg = classify_exception(exc)     assert kind == 'permanent'     assert '422' in msg     assert 'field' in msg or 'symbol' in msg  def test_http_exception_none_detail_is_permanent(self) -> None:     exc = HTTPException(status_code=404)  # detail defaults to 'Not Found'     kind, msg = classify_exception(exc)     assert kind == 'permanent'     assert '404' in msg

#### G21-014 · Claim partial index `compute_jobs_claim_ready` not used post-089: filter `WHERE status='pending'` is narrower than RPC predicate `status IN ('pending','failed_retry')`
- **File**: `supabase/migrations/20260411144407_compute_jobs_queue.sql:190`
- **Specialist**: `performance` (confidence 9)
- **Summary**: `compute_jobs_claim_ready` was created in migration 032 with partial predicate `WHERE status = 'pending'`. Migration 089 widened the claim RPCs to `status IN ('pending','failed_retry') AND next_attempt_at <= now()` but never widened this index's predicate. Postgres only uses a partial index when the query WHERE clause implies its predicate; `status IN (...)` does not imply `status='pending'` so the planner falls back to a heap scan or the full-table `compute_jobs_status_created (status, created_at DESC)` followed by re-sorting by next_attempt_at. As compute_jobs grows (Phase-12 backfill enqueues thousands of rows), every 30s dispatch tick burns through this scan, defeating the entire purpose of the dedicated claim index.
- **Evidence**: supabase/migrations/20260411144407_compute_jobs_queue.sql:190-192 vs supabase/migrations/20260428155809_claim_failed_retry.sql:86-91 (legacy RPC `WHERE status IN ('pending','failed_retry')`) and the same widened predicate is still live in the latest claim function at supabase/migrations/20260515114555_compute_jobs_claim_token_fencing.sql:175
- **Fix**: Drop+recreate `compute_jobs_claim_ready` with predicate `WHERE status IN ('pending', 'failed_retry')` (mirroring what migration 089 already did for `idx_compute_jobs_priority_pending`). Both partial indexes need the same widening so the legacy claim RPC stays index-only just like the priority RPC.

#### G21-015 · PR #82 (migration 089) shipped first widened claim filter without partition dedupe — caused real 7-minute production outage
- **File**: `supabase/migrations/20260428155809_claim_failed_retry.sql:150`
- **Specialist**: `code-reviewer` (confidence 8)
- **Summary**: Migration 089 widens the claim filter to `status IN ('pending','failed_retry')` but keeps the existing batch UPDATE without per-partition dedupe. The CHANGELOG of v0.17.0.2 (line 414 of the diff) confirms this caused the worker to spin on `compute_jobs_one_inflight_per_kind_allocator` 23505 errors for ~7 minutes on 2026-04-28 17:10 UTC, draining nothing until 6 rows were manually transitioned to failed_final. The two PRs are tightly coupled: PR #82 introduces a latent corruption pathway that PR #83 fixes. If PR #82 is ever re-applied alone (e.g., on a partial deploy / rollback to 0.17.0.1) the same outage will recur. The PR sequence should have been combined into one atomic deploy, or PR #82 should have shipped with the dedupe inline.
- **Evidence**: L150-157 in 089 migration: `WHERE id IN (SELECT id FROM compute_jobs WHERE status IN ('pending','failed_retry') AND next_attempt_at <= now() ... LIMIT p_batch_size FOR UPDATE SKIP LOCKED)`. No partition-key dedupe. CHANGELOG v0.17.0.2 §Fixed §1 documents the production outage that resulted.
- **Fix**: Either: (a) supersede migration 089 with migration 090 in a single PR for retroactive safety, (b) add a comment to migration 089 explicitly warning that this migration MUST be applied in lockstep with 090 and never as a standalone deploy step, or (c) merge 089 into 090 and drop 089. Production verification: confirm no deployment pipeline can apply 089 without 090.

#### G21-016 · Widened claim filter has no covering index for failed_retry scans
- **File**: `supabase/migrations/20260428155809_claim_failed_retry.sql:86`
- **Specialist**: `data-migration` (confidence 9)
- **Summary**: Migration 089 widens both claim RPCs' inner SELECT to `status IN ('pending','failed_retry')`, but only updates `idx_compute_jobs_priority_pending` (priority-aware path). The legacy `compute_jobs_claim_ready` index (compute_jobs_queue.sql:190-192) has predicate `WHERE status = 'pending'` and is therefore NOT a covering partial index for failed_retry rows after this migration. The legacy `claim_compute_jobs` path and the throttle-disabled branch of `claim_compute_jobs_with_priority` (v_high_pending = 0) fall back to a sequential scan or a less efficient index to find failed_retry rows. For a queue with thousands of historical failed_retry rows this is a measurable claim-latency regression.
- **Evidence**: supabase/migrations/20260428155809_claim_failed_retry.sql:86-91 (inner SELECT filter) and supabase/migrations/20260411144407_compute_jobs_queue.sql:190-192 (`compute_jobs_claim_ready` partial index `WHERE status = 'pending'`).
- **Fix**: Add a follow-up migration that drops and recreates `compute_jobs_claim_ready` with predicate `WHERE status IN ('pending','failed_retry')` (or a separate partial index `WHERE status = 'failed_retry'` keyed on next_attempt_at). The DO-block self-verify in migration 089 should assert the partial index predicate includes failed_retry.

#### G21-017 · attempts counter increment on failed_retry re-claim untested
- **File**: `supabase/migrations/20260428155809_claim_failed_retry.sql:237`
- **Specialist**: `pr-test-analyzer` (confidence 8)
- **Summary**: Migration 089 line 37-38 documents 'claim_compute_jobs increments attempts on every claim … mark_compute_job_failed does NOT increment.' The interplay: a failed_retry row at attempts=N gets re-claimed via mig 089 → attempts=N+1 → after max_attempts (default 3), mark_compute_job_failed transitions to failed_final. This counter semantics is load-bearing for the 30s/2min/8min/failed_final terminal — if the attempts increment is skipped on failed_retry re-claim (e.g. via a guarded `WHERE attempts < max`), jobs would loop forever. The current test_failed_retry that I propose verifies attempts becomes 2 (1 → 2) but no test verifies the terminal transition after 3 claims.
- **Evidence**: supabase/migrations/20260428155809_claim_failed_retry.sql:32-44 'attempts counter semantics' section. supabase/migrations/032 mark_compute_job_failed body — backoff schedule 30s/2min/8min. No test exercises: insert failed_retry attempts=2, claim → attempts=3, run mark_compute_job_failed → status should transition to failed_final.
- **Fix**: Add to test_compute_jobs_fencing.py:  def test_failed_retry_third_attempt_transitions_to_failed_final(admin, strategy_id):     """Mig 089 + mig 032 interplay: failed_retry rows re-claimed beyond max_attempts     (default 3) must transition to failed_final on next mark_failed."""     job = admin.table('compute_jobs').insert({         'strategy_id': strategy_id, 'kind': 'sync_trades',         'status': 'failed_retry', 'priority': 'normal', 'exchange': 'okx',         'next_attempt_at': '2020-01-01T00:00:00Z',         'attempts': 2,  # already attempted twice     }).execute().data[0]     try:         claimed = _claim_one(admin, 'g21-max-attempts')         assert claimed is not None         assert claimed['attempts'] == 3, 'claim must increment attempts on failed_retry'         admin.rpc('mark_compute_job_failed', {             'p_job_id': job['id'], 'p_error_kind': 'transient',             'p_error_message': 'final attempt',         }).execute()         row = admin.table('compute_jobs').select('status').eq('id', job['id']).single().execute().data         assert row['status'] == 'failed_final', (             f'After 3rd attempt, mark_failed must transition to failed_final (got {row["status"]})'         )     finally:         admin.table('compute_jobs').delete().eq('id', job['id']).execute()

#### G21-018 · Partition dedupe misses pre-existing `running` rows — residual 23505 risk after watchdog reclaim
- **File**: `supabase/migrations/20260428190907_claim_dedupe_partition_keys.sql:214`
- **Specialist**: `code-reviewer` (confidence 8)
- **Summary**: Migration 090's CTE filters candidates by `status IN ('pending','failed_retry')` then ranks within partition. The partial unique inflight index `compute_jobs_one_inflight_per_kind_*` predicate is `status IN ('pending','running','done_pending_children')` — it includes `running` but the dedupe does NOT see `running` rows. If a row is stuck in `running` for partition (kind=X, allocator_id=A) (e.g., handler crashed before mark_compute_job_failed fired, before the watchdog has reset it) and a `failed_retry` row exists for the same partition, the dedupe will return the failed_retry row as winner and the batch UPDATE will set it to `running` — violating the partial unique index with 23505. PR #83's design only addresses the `failed_retry` ↔ `failed_retry` and `pending` ↔ `failed_retry` collisions, not the `running` ↔ `failed_retry` collision that the watchdog reclaim window creates. This is the same class of bug PR #83 closed for one race window but left open for another.
- **Evidence**: L214-217: `FROM compute_jobs WHERE status IN ('pending','failed_retry') AND next_attempt_at <= now()`. The CTE never inspects `running` rows. The partial unique index (mig 032/079) requires `running` to be unique per partition too.
- **Fix**: Add a NOT EXISTS subquery in the `deduped` CTE that excludes any candidate row whose partition already has a `running` row in compute_jobs (with the same `kind` and same non-null partition_id). Alternatively guard the UPDATE with an ON CONFLICT DO NOTHING semantic, or catch unique_violation inside the RPC and re-raise as a soft signal the worker can ignore. The acid test: insert one `running` row + one `failed_retry` row for the same (kind, allocator_id), call claim, assert zero 23505 and zero claimed rows.

#### G21-019 · Dedupe over-aggressively suppresses compute_intro_snapshot legitimate concurrent rows
- **File**: `supabase/migrations/20260428190907_claim_dedupe_partition_keys.sql:111`
- **Specialist**: `data-migration` (confidence 9)
- **Summary**: Migration 090 PARTITION BY kind, strategy_id deduplicates intro_snapshot jobs even though the partial unique index compute_jobs_one_inflight_per_kind_strategy explicitly excludes kind = 'compute_intro_snapshot' (migration 048 / 20260416125430_contact_request_metadata.sql:159). Intro snapshots are per-(strategy, allocator) — multiple eligible rows with the same strategy_id but different allocator_ids CAN legitimately coexist in pending/failed_retry. The dedupe forces sequential drain (only 1 per claim batch) for that kind, slowing the queue without any partial-unique-violation risk to prevent. No carve-out is present in either claim RPC.
- **Evidence**: supabase/migrations/20260428190907_claim_dedupe_partition_keys.sql:111-124 and supabase/migrations/20260416125430_contact_request_metadata.sql:154-160 (index predicate `kind <> 'compute_intro_snapshot'`)
- **Fix**: Add `AND kind <> 'compute_intro_snapshot'` (and similar carve-outs for any future kind-excluded inflight indices) to the strategy_id rn_s check, e.g. `WHERE (strategy_id IS NULL OR kind = 'compute_intro_snapshot' OR rn_s = 1)`. Long-term: derive the inflight-index predicate map (kind→partition columns covered) from pg_indexes rather than hardcoding.

#### G21-020 · Dedupe CTE scans entire `pending/failed_retry` set with four full row_number() windows before LIMIT push-down
- **File**: `supabase/migrations/20260428190907_claim_dedupe_partition_keys.sql:109`
- **Specialist**: `performance` (confidence 8)
- **Summary**: The `ranked` CTE in `claim_compute_jobs` (and the priority variant) reads every row satisfying `status IN ('pending','failed_retry') AND next_attempt_at <= now()` and computes four `row_number() OVER (PARTITION BY kind, <col>)` window functions over all of them before the outer LIMIT clamps the result. PostgreSQL cannot push the LIMIT into a CTE with window functions (each window must see every row in its partition to compute rank), so claim cost is O(N) in queue depth for both pending AND failed_retry on EVERY 30s tick. With the failed_retry-claimable widening of 089, a long-tail of failed_retry rows that the worker has not yet finished (or that are mid-backoff but eligible later) inflates this scan permanently. The original 032 claim was an index-tip scan limited to p_batch_size — this is a regression in steady-state CPU even when there is nothing to dedupe.
- **Evidence**: supabase/migrations/20260428190907_claim_dedupe_partition_keys.sql:109-124 (legacy) and :190-225 (priority) — four `row_number() OVER (PARTITION BY kind, ...)` windows fan out before the outer `LIMIT p_batch_size`. Same shape preserved in supabase/migrations/20260515114555_compute_jobs_claim_token_fencing.sql:167-198.
- **Fix**: Add a guard predicate to the ranked CTE that limits the dedupe scan to a reasonable upper bound (e.g. `LIMIT p_batch_size * 10` inside a subquery that already orders by `(priority, next_attempt_at)` so the dedupe only ranks the front of the queue). Or split into two passes: first a cheap index-only scan picks p_batch_size candidate IDs, then a second pass dedupes ONLY those by partition key. Verify with EXPLAIN ANALYZE that the inner scan touches O(p_batch_size) rows, not O(queue depth).

#### G21-021 · NULL partition column dedupe branch untested — rows with partition_id IS NULL skip rank check
- **File**: `supabase/migrations/20260428190907_claim_dedupe_partition_keys.sql:121`
- **Specialist**: `pr-test-analyzer` (confidence 8)
- **Summary**: Migration 090 lines 121-124 contain a key branch: `(portfolio_id IS NULL OR rn_p = 1)` etc. The intent: rows where a partition column is NULL skip that column's rank check because NULL is excluded from the partial unique index. If this branch logic is subtly broken (e.g. a future migration changes `IS NULL` to `IS NOT NULL` or drops the OR), rows with NULL partition_id could be wrongly deduped against unrelated rows. The mocked TestClaimDedupe in test_main_worker.py does not cover this. The fencing suite has the FK fixtures to insert a row with allocator_id but no portfolio_id and prove it's claimable alongside a portfolio-keyed row of the same kind.
- **Evidence**: supabase/migrations/20260428190907_claim_dedupe_partition_keys.sql:120-124 dedupe branch. grep 'IS NULL' in analytics-service/tests/test_compute_jobs_fencing.py → 1 hit, unrelated. No test covers the null-partition branch.
- **Fix**: Add to test_compute_jobs_fencing.py:  def test_dedupe_skips_null_partition_columns(admin, strategy_id):     """Mig 090: a row with allocator_id IS NULL skips the allocator partition     rank check. Two such rows with different strategy_ids both survive dedupe."""     # Two sync_trades rows, both with strategy_id set, both with allocator_id NULL     # — they share kind but DIFFER on strategy_id, so dedupe must allow both.     user_id = _seed_user_id(admin)     strat2 = admin.table('strategies').insert({         'user_id': user_id, 'name': f'g21-null-{uuid.uuid4().hex[:8]}',         'status': 'pending_review', 'source': 'okx',         'strategy_types': [], 'subtypes': [], 'markets': [], 'supported_exchanges': [],     }).execute().data[0]['id']     j1 = admin.table('compute_jobs').insert({         'strategy_id': strategy_id, 'kind': 'sync_trades',         'status': 'pending', 'priority': 'normal', 'exchange': 'okx',         'next_attempt_at': '2020-01-01T00:00:00Z',     }).execute().data[0]     j2 = admin.table('compute_jobs').insert({         'strategy_id': strat2, 'kind': 'sync_trades',         'status': 'pending', 'priority': 'normal', 'exchange': 'okx',         'next_attempt_at': '2020-01-01T00:00:00Z',     }).execute().data[0]     try:         res = admin.rpc('claim_compute_jobs_with_priority', {             'p_batch_size': 5, 'p_worker_id': 'g21-null-part',         }).execute()         claimed_ids = {r['id'] for r in res.data}         assert {j1['id'], j2['id']}.issubset(claimed_ids), (             'dedupe must not collapse rows that differ on strategy_id when allocator_id IS NULL'         )     finally:         admin.table('compute_jobs').delete().in_('id', [j1['id'], j2['id']]).execute()         admin.table('strategies').delete().eq('id', strat2).execute()

#### G21-022 · Priority tie-break inside partition untested (high beats normal beats low)
- **File**: `supabase/migrations/20260428190907_claim_dedupe_partition_keys.sql:196`
- **Specialist**: `pr-test-analyzer` (confidence 8)
- **Summary**: Migration 090 RPC orders the row_number() within each partition by `CASE priority WHEN 'high' THEN 0 WHEN 'normal' THEN 1 ELSE 2 END, next_attempt_at` (lines 196-197). This determines which row WINS the dedupe when two rows share a partition: the higher-priority one. If this ORDER BY clause silently reverts to just `next_attempt_at` (drops priority precedence), an older low-priority row could win over a newer high-priority row in the same partition. The TestClaimDedupe mocks the RPC entirely; no test verifies the priority-precedence-within-partition rule.
- **Evidence**: supabase/migrations/20260428190907_claim_dedupe_partition_keys.sql:194-213 — four `row_number() OVER (PARTITION BY ... ORDER BY CASE priority ..., next_attempt_at)`. No test inserts two same-partition rows with different priorities and asserts which wins.
- **Fix**: Add to test_compute_jobs_fencing.py:  def test_dedupe_priority_tiebreak_high_beats_normal(admin):     """Mig 090: when two failed_retry rows share (kind, allocator_id), the     higher-priority one wins the dedupe — even if it's NEWER."""     user_id = _seed_user_id(admin)     older_normal = admin.table('compute_jobs').insert({         'kind': 'rescore_allocator', 'allocator_id': user_id,         'status': 'failed_retry', 'priority': 'normal',         'next_attempt_at': '2020-01-01T00:00:00Z', 'attempts': 1,     }).execute().data[0]     newer_high = admin.table('compute_jobs').insert({         'kind': 'rescore_allocator', 'allocator_id': user_id,         'status': 'failed_retry', 'priority': 'high',         'next_attempt_at': '2020-06-01T00:00:00Z',  # NEWER         'attempts': 1,     }).execute().data[0]     try:         res = admin.rpc('claim_compute_jobs_with_priority', {             'p_batch_size': 5, 'p_worker_id': 'g21-tiebreak',         }).execute()         claimed_ids = {r['id'] for r in res.data}         assert len(claimed_ids) == 1, f'dedupe must return exactly 1 row, got {len(claimed_ids)}'         assert newer_high['id'] in claimed_ids, (             'high-priority row must win the dedupe tie-break over older normal-priority row'         )     finally:         admin.table('compute_jobs').delete().in_('id', [older_normal['id'], newer_high['id']]).execute()

#### G21-023 · Migration 090 structural DO block cannot detect dedupe CTE removal across function replaces — actually got dropped silently by mig 104
- **File**: `supabase/migrations/20260428190907_claim_dedupe_partition_keys.sql:836`
- **Specialist**: `silent-failure-hunter` (confidence 9)
- **Summary**: The self-verifying DO block only matches the literal strings 'row_number() OVER' and 'PARTITION BY kind, portfolio_id' etc. in pg_proc.prosrc. The diff itself acknowledges the regression test 'could not be embedded in the migration' due to FK constraints to auth.users/strategies/api_keys/portfolios. A later CREATE OR REPLACE FUNCTION can silently drop the dedupe CTE without re-running migration 090's DO block — and this is EXACTLY what mig 20260515114555 (claim_token fencing) documents happened: 'mig 104's CREATE OR REPLACE eliminated the migration-090 partition dedupe by mistake'. The structural check fires only at migration-apply time, not on every claim. There is no runtime invariant to catch a 23505 spin recurrence.
- **Evidence**: supabase/migrations/20260428190907_claim_dedupe_partition_keys.sql:806-861 (structural-only DO block); supabase/migrations/20260515114555_compute_jobs_claim_token_fencing.sql:217-228 (admits mig 104 silently dropped the dedupe)
- **Fix**: Add a runtime invariant: an AFTER UPDATE trigger on compute_jobs that fires when more than one row with the same (kind, partition_id) transitions to running inside a single statement, raising an exception that surfaces as 23505 with a CLEAR diagnostic 'BUG: claim RPC failed dedupe — please report'. OR add a daily cron that runs `SELECT prosrc FROM pg_proc WHERE proname IN ('claim_compute_jobs','claim_compute_jobs_with_priority') AND prosrc NOT LIKE '%PARTITION BY kind%'` and alerts.

#### G21-024 · Dedupe tie-break by next_attempt_at alone is non-deterministic when ties — silently picks arbitrary winner
- **File**: `supabase/migrations/20260428190907_claim_dedupe_partition_keys.sql:650`
- **Specialist**: `silent-failure-hunter` (confidence 8)
- **Summary**: The legacy claim_compute_jobs ranks rows ONLY by `next_attempt_at ASC` within each partition. If two failed_retry rows share a partition AND have identical next_attempt_at (entirely possible — both fail in the same tick, both transition via the same backoff schedule, both get next_attempt_at = now()+30s), row_number() picks by physical order, which is non-deterministic across pg restarts/vacuums. The 'loser' is silently dropped this tick. The priority RPC adds CASE priority as a primary key BUT still ties on next_attempt_at if priority is also equal. There is no id-based tie-breaker — when two rows tie completely, which one becomes runnable is implementation-defined.
- **Evidence**: supabase/migrations/20260428190907_claim_dedupe_partition_keys.sql:649-654 (legacy RPC, no id tiebreak); 735-753 (priority RPC, no id tiebreak)
- **Fix**: Append `, id` to every ORDER BY inside the row_number() OVER clause. PG documents row_number() as 'arbitrary' when the ORDER BY has ties; id is a stable secondary sort that makes the dedupe winner deterministic and reproducible across deploys.

### MEDIUM (24)

#### G21-025 · HTTPException 4xx classifier swallows custom `detail` types that are not stringifiable to the truncated 480-char message
- **File**: `analytics-service/services/job_worker.py:215`
- **Specialist**: `code-reviewer` (confidence 8)
- **Summary**: `HTTPException(status_code=400, detail=...)` accepts `detail` as any type (str, dict, list, custom Pydantic model). The classifier does `str(exc.detail)[:480]` which works for str/dict (repr-style output), but if a handler raises `HTTPException(400, detail=SomeDataclass(...))` or `detail={"errors": [...nested...]}`, the truncation yields garbled JSON/repr that can mislead the admin UI. More importantly, the f-string `f"{status}: {str(exc.detail)[:480]}"` is then truncated again downstream by the consumer's UI fields (`mark_compute_job_failed` p_error column has its own cap). The double-truncation can produce corrupted unicode if the slice falls inside a multi-byte character — exception sanitization should slice by code point, not byte, but slicing a str is by code point in Python so this is OK. Real risk: dict/list detail renders as a string with Python repr quoting (single quotes), which is JSON-invalid if downstream parsers expect JSON.
- **Evidence**: L215-217: `if status in (408, 429): return ('transient', f'{status}: {str(exc.detail)[:480]}'); if 400 <= status < 500: return ('permanent', f'{status}: {str(exc.detail)[:480]}')`
- **Fix**: Document the contract that handlers MUST raise HTTPException with a string `detail`, or coerce non-string detail via `json.dumps(exc.detail, default=str)` then truncate. Adding a unit test with `HTTPException(400, detail={'foo': 'bar'})` would lock the contract.

#### G21-026 · HTTPException classifier branch order untested vs CCXT BaseError — overlap risk if FastAPI HTTPException ever subclasses Exception via ccxt path
- **File**: `analytics-service/services/job_worker.py:204`
- **Specialist**: `pr-test-analyzer` (confidence 8)
- **Summary**: classify_exception orders branches: ccxt.BaseError catch-all (line 204) comes BEFORE the HTTPException branch (line 212). This works today because HTTPException doesn't inherit from ccxt.BaseError. But if a future change wraps HTTPException via a CCXT-flavored intermediate (or if a developer raises a custom exception that inherits from both), the ccxt branch would catch it first and classify it as 'unknown' — silently bypassing the 4xx → permanent logic. No test pins the ordering.
- **Evidence**: analytics-service/services/job_worker.py:200-216 — branch order matters; ccxt.BaseError before HTTPException. No test pins this specific order via a multi-inheritance class.
- **Fix**: Add to TestClassifyException (defensive, low cost):  def test_http_exception_with_ccxt_baseerror_parent_still_permanent(self) -> None:     """Defensive: even if a future caller raises a class inheriting from both,     HTTPException 4xx must classify as permanent, not unknown."""     # Today HTTPException doesn't inherit from BaseError; this test pins the     # contract that the classifier should prefer the more-specific (HTTP) branch.     # If/when refactor flips branch order, this test fires.     class HybridError(HTTPException, ccxt.BaseError):         def __init__(self):             HTTPException.__init__(self, status_code=400, detail='hybrid')             ccxt.BaseError.__init__(self, 'hybrid')     kind, _ = classify_exception(HybridError())     # If this test fails today, it's a signal to reorder the branches so     # HTTPException comes before the ccxt.BaseError catch-all.     # (Acceptable to mark xfail with a comment if current order is intentional.)

#### G21-027 · HTTPException detail can be a dict containing internal context; truncated str(dict) may surface as compute_jobs.last_error
- **File**: `analytics-service/services/job_worker.py:215`
- **Specialist**: `security` (confidence 8)
- **Summary**: The new classifier branch builds last_error via `f"{status}: {str(exc.detail)[:480]}"`. FastAPI's HTTPException.detail is typed `Any` — analytics-service/routers/csv.py raises HTTPException(detail={'ok': False, 'code': 'CSV_INVALID_FORMAT', 'debug_context': {'fmt_received': fmt}, ...}). If any present-or-future queue handler raises HTTPException with a dict detail (or imports/calls into csv.py / portfolio.py etc. which do), `str(dict)` produces the raw Python repr including all internal keys (`debug_context`, server-side hints, raw upstream fields). Truncation at 480 chars can also split UTF-8 bytes mid-character on non-ASCII detail content. This is a contained risk today (queue handlers in services/ only use string detail), but the contract `Exception → last_error` now has no schema check.
- **Evidence**: analytics-service/services/job_worker.py:212-217 (new branch); analytics-service/routers/csv.py:44-50, 70-76, 84-90, 93-99 (HTTPException(detail=dict) examples already in repo)
- **Fix**: Coerce non-string detail to a fixed, safe representation. Replace `str(exc.detail)[:480]` with: `detail_str = exc.detail if isinstance(exc.detail, str) else getattr(exc.detail, 'code', '<non-string detail>'); detail_str[:480]`. Also slice on characters (`str.encode('utf-8', 'replace').decode('utf-8', 'replace')[:480]`) to avoid mid-codepoint truncation.

#### G21-028 · Classifier truncates HTTPException.detail via str() without handling non-string detail types
- **File**: `analytics-service/services/job_worker.py:215`
- **Specialist**: `silent-failure-hunter` (confidence 8)
- **Summary**: FastAPI HTTPException.detail can be any type — dict, list, BaseModel — not just str. The classifier does `str(exc.detail)[:480]` which produces opaque '{...}' representations for dicts and meaningless 'pydantic.BaseModel object at 0x...' for models. Operators reading admin UI rows see garbage instead of the actual failure reason. While today's callsites in analytics-service use plain strings, future code or third-party FastAPI deps raising HTTPException with structured detail will silently lose context.
- **Evidence**: analytics-service/services/job_worker.py:213-217 — `str(exc.detail)[:480]` with no type narrowing
- **Fix**: Explicitly handle non-string detail: `detail_str = exc.detail if isinstance(exc.detail, str) else json.dumps(exc.detail, default=str)`. Add a unit test for HTTPException(detail={'field':'x'}) to lock the contract.

#### G21-029 · Classifier ignores ColdStartSymbolDiscoveryError-shaped failures and gives caller no explicit fallback
- **File**: `analytics-service/services/job_worker.py:212`
- **Specialist**: `silent-failure-hunter` (confidence 8)
- **Summary**: The classifier's HTTPException branch comes AFTER the ccxt.BaseError catch-all and BEFORE the final 'unknown' return. That ordering is correct for the common case. However: when analytics_runner.py:1198 wraps an arbitrary inner exception (ValueError, KeyError, DB error) into HTTPException(500,'Analytics computation failed'), the classifier sees status=500, fails the `400 <= status < 500` check, and falls through to 'unknown' — the inner exception's actual message is gone (replaced by 'Analytics computation failed' before the worker ever sees it). Sentry only gets the wrapper's `__cause__` if exc_info=True, which is NOT used by classify_exception. So operators investigating compute_analytics failures see a generic 500 admin-UI row with no actionable signal.
- **Evidence**: analytics-service/services/analytics_runner.py:1184-1198 (catch Exception → re-raise as HTTPException(500,generic)); analytics-service/services/job_worker.py:212-217 (classifier reads only exc.detail, drops __cause__)
- **Fix**: Include `exc.__cause__` repr in the classifier message when present: `f"{status}: {str(exc.detail)[:300]} (cause: {repr(exc.__cause__)[:180]})"`. OR change analytics_runner.py:1198 to include `str(e)[:200]` in the detail. Pick one — silent context loss across the layer boundary is the actual defect.

#### G21-030 · compute_jobs.priority modeled as bare str — no Priority Literal
- **File**: `analytics-service/services/job_worker.py:1`
- **Specialist**: `type-design-analyzer` (confidence 8)
- **Summary**: compute_jobs.priority is a 3-value DB CHECK enum ('low', 'normal', 'high') that drives the priority-aware claim throttle in claim_compute_jobs_with_priority. Migration 090 (the second half of this batch) re-references priority ordering inside the dedupe CTE (`CASE priority WHEN 'high' THEN 0 WHEN 'normal' THEN 1 ELSE 2 END`). The Python worker never types priority — it's a bare `job.get('priority')` (or absent — dispatch_tick doesn't even read it). When the worker eventually grows a priority-aware feature (e.g., longer timeout for 'high' jobs, or per-priority circuit-breaker rules), the lack of a Priority Literal means the SQL → Python boundary is unguarded.
- **Evidence**: supabase/migrations/20260428120836_compute_jobs_priority.sql:54-55 defines the 3-value CHECK; analytics-service/services/job_worker.py has zero references to priority strings
- **Fix**: Add `Priority = Literal['low', 'normal', 'high']` alongside JobStatus. When a future PR adds priority-driven behavior, the boundary type is already in place. Pair with a typed `ComputeJobRow` TypedDict (status: JobStatus, priority: Priority, kind: JobKind, ...) — the dispatch_tick loop then casts the supabase response once and the rest of the worker enjoys static checking.

#### G21-031 · dispatch and run_* handlers accept untyped `job: dict` — compute_jobs row shape lives only in SQL
- **File**: `analytics-service/services/job_worker.py:505`
- **Specialist**: `type-design-analyzer` (confidence 8)
- **Summary**: Every handler signature in job_worker.py is `async def run_<kind>_job(job: dict) -> DispatchResult:` (lines 505, 857, 878, 900, 961, 1000, 1455, 1505, 1655, 1700, 1789, etc., plus dispatch_tick in main_worker.py). The job dict is the raw supabase response of a compute_jobs row — 17+ columns including the load-bearing `status`, `kind`, `priority`, `attempts`, `claim_token`, `next_attempt_at`, the 4 partition columns, plus the new failed_retry semantics from migration 089. Code calls `job['kind']`, `job['id']`, `job.get('claim_token')`, `job.get('allocator_id')` etc. with KeyError as the only signal. Migration 089's contract — 'failed_retry rows are now claimable when their backoff has elapsed' — exists nowhere in Python. The PR-Y2 / G21 batch is exactly when this matters: the SQL got a major semantic upgrade, but the Python boundary did not.
- **Evidence**: analytics-service/services/job_worker.py:505 `async def run_sync_trades_job(job: dict) -> DispatchResult:` and ~10 other run_* handlers with identical signature; analytics-service/main_worker.py:290-300 iterates jobs as dicts
- **Fix**: Add a `ComputeJobRow(TypedDict, total=False)` in services/job_worker.py reflecting compute_jobs columns with proper Literal types for status/kind/priority/error_kind, plus the 4 partition column unions. Retype every `job: dict` to `job: ComputeJobRow`. This is a one-line-per-handler change; zero runtime cost; massively reduces the risk of a future schema change drifting silently from worker code. Cast once in dispatch_tick (`for job in cast(list[ComputeJobRow], jobs):`) and the rest of the pipeline gets static checking.

#### G21-032 · HTTPException branch uses two non-exclusive `if` statements; static checker cannot see they are exhaustive over 4xx
- **File**: `analytics-service/services/job_worker.py:212`
- **Specialist**: `type-design-analyzer` (confidence 9)
- **Summary**: The new HTTPException branch is structured as: `if isinstance(exc, HTTPException): status = exc.status_code; if status in (408, 429): return (transient, ...); if 400 <= status < 500: return (permanent, ...)`. Both inner `if`s use `return`, so control flow is correct. But the first `if` is not `elif`, so a future maintainer who wants to add a third 4xx-specific rule (say, 451 'Unavailable for Legal Reasons' as permanent-no-retry-no-alert) must understand the exhaustiveness implicit in 'first if returned, so second if is the catch-all'. A `match status:` block with `case 408 | 429`, `case s if 400 <= s < 500`, `case _` (the unmodified fallthrough) would express the 'these are the three buckets of HTTP status the classifier knows about' invariant structurally. Currently the invariant is 'reader-must-trace-the-returns'.
- **Evidence**: analytics-service/services/job_worker.py:212-217
- **Fix**: Rewrite as `match exc.status_code: case 408 | 429: return ('transient', ...); case s if 400 <= s < 500: return ('permanent', ...); case _: pass` (then fall through to the unknown branch). Documents the trichotomy structurally and gives mypy a hook for exhaustiveness checking via a reveal_type on the trailing fallthrough.

#### G21-033 · State machine transitions (pending → running → failed_retry → pending) live only in SQL — no Python-side encoding
- **File**: `analytics-service/services/job_worker.py:1`
- **Specialist**: `type-design-analyzer` (confidence 8)
- **Summary**: The compute_jobs queue is a state machine: pending → running, running → done | done_pending_children | failed_retry | failed_final, failed_retry → pending (the new edge added by migration 089). Migration 038 line 106 documented the INTENT of failed_retry → pending years ago, but the implementation only caught up in PR #82. The Python worker has no representation of this state machine — no transition table, no `class JobStateMachine:` with `valid_transitions: dict[JobStatus, set[JobStatus]]`, no assertions that a claim transitions only from {pending, failed_retry} to {running}. Reviewers reading the diff to migration 089 have to mentally reconstruct 'is failed_retry already in some Python-side set somewhere that needs updating' — and the answer is no, because there is no Python-side set anywhere. This is the long-tail risk: every new status transition is one migration + zero Python changes, until one day a worker assumption silently breaks.
- **Evidence**: analytics-service/services/job_worker.py has no class/dict/set encoding compute_jobs status transitions; the state machine is documented only in CHANGELOG.md and migration headers
- **Fix**: Add a `VALID_TRANSITIONS: Final[dict[JobStatus, frozenset[JobStatus]]]` mapping at module scope in job_worker.py, with comments cross-linking to mark_compute_job_done / mark_compute_job_failed / claim_compute_jobs / reset_stalled_compute_jobs. Even if no runtime code consults the map today, having it in source means future state machine evolutions are diff-visible and migrations + Python advance together. Tiny pragmatic version: a `frozenset[JobStatus]` named CLAIMABLE_STATUSES that mirrors the new SQL WHERE clause exactly.

#### G21-034 · Test `test_partial_batch_from_dedupe_dispatches_survivor` does not verify the SQL dedupe — only that worker tolerates a partial batch
- **File**: `analytics-service/tests/test_main_worker.py:456`
- **Specialist**: `code-reviewer` (confidence 8)
- **Summary**: The test's docstring claims it captures the `claim_compute_jobs_with_priority` partition-dedupe contract, but the test mocks the RPC's response with `MagicMock(data=[survivor])` — it never exercises the SQL function or its CTE. This is a unit test of `dispatch_tick`, not of the dedupe RPC. The actual SQL regression for the 23505 collision is only structurally asserted by the migration's DO block (presence of `row_number() OVER` and `PARTITION BY kind, *` literals in `pg_proc.prosrc`) — that's a presence check, not a behavior check. The CHANGELOG even acknowledges this gap and references a one-shot live test that ran during deploy but cannot be embedded in the migration. A repeatable end-to-end regression test that exercises the actual dedupe SQL against the real compute_jobs table is missing. Rule 9 (Tests verify intent, not just behavior): the dedupe's intent (no 23505 for same-partition failed_retry rows) is not encoded as an automated test that will fail if someone reverts migration 090 in the future.
- **Evidence**: L466-469: `mock_supabase = MagicMock(); claim_chain = MagicMock(); claim_chain.execute.return_value = MagicMock(data=[survivor])`. The SQL function is never invoked. L450-453 docstring: 'The actual SQL regression is gated by the migration's structural DO block ... plus the one-shot live test recorded in the v0.17.0.2 deploy report.'
- **Fix**: Add an integration test using a real Postgres test database (Supabase test project or Docker pg) that: (1) inserts two failed_retry rows for the same (kind, allocator_id), (2) calls `claim_compute_jobs_with_priority(5, 'test-worker')`, (3) asserts exactly one row claimed and no 23505 raised. The migration's comment acknowledges this test is needed; without it, a future schema change can silently drop the dedupe without any CI signal.

#### G21-035 · TestClaimDedupe asserts dispatch is awaited 'once' but does not verify the surviving job's id is forwarded
- **File**: `analytics-service/tests/test_main_worker.py:485`
- **Specialist**: `pr-test-analyzer` (confidence 8)
- **Summary**: `test_partial_batch_from_dedupe_dispatches_survivor` (line 456) uses `mock_dispatch.assert_awaited_once()` but never asserts dispatch was called with the SURVIVOR row (the test sets up `survivor = {'id': 'rescore-survivor', ...}` but never reads back what dispatch received). If dispatch_tick has a bug that passes a stale or wrong job dict to dispatch (e.g. iterates over `claim_chain.execute.return_value.data` incorrectly), the assertion still passes. The test should bind the assertion: `mock_dispatch.assert_awaited_once_with(survivor)` or check `call_args[0][0]['id'] == 'rescore-survivor'`.
- **Evidence**: analytics-service/tests/test_main_worker.py:485 `mock_dispatch.assert_awaited_once()` — no positional or keyword arg check. Compare line 202 `mock_handler.assert_awaited_once_with(job)` in test_job_worker.py — the surrounding pattern DOES bind the job arg.
- **Fix**: In test_main_worker.py:485, change:   mock_dispatch.assert_awaited_once() to:   mock_dispatch.assert_awaited_once_with(survivor) # OR equivalent: assert that the first positional arg in call_args has id='rescore-survivor'. # This makes the test fail if dispatch_tick passes the wrong job through after dedupe.

#### G21-036 · Worker observability: claim batch size < requested not surfaced in any metric/log assertion
- **File**: `analytics-service/tests/test_main_worker.py:456`
- **Specialist**: `pr-test-analyzer` (confidence 8)
- **Summary**: After mig 090, a claim batch can return fewer rows than `p_batch_size` due to dedupe — this is benign but operationally noticeable (it changes throughput). TestClaimDedupe asserts dispatch is called once but doesn't assert any log/metric is emitted for the dedupe drop. If silent dedupe is wanted, that's a design choice — but the PR description in CHANGELOG line 426 calls out the contract 'never assumes len(jobs) == p_batch_size'. No test asserts the worker LOGS this for operational diagnostics (helpful for the next stuck-queue debug session).
- **Evidence**: analytics-service/tests/test_main_worker.py:438-508 — no log/metric assertion when claim returns fewer than batch_size. CHANGELOG line 426 'never assumes len(jobs) == p_batch_size' — silent compliance only.
- **Fix**: Optional: add a log-emission test (low priority, nice-to-have):  @pytest.mark.asyncio async def test_partial_batch_logs_dedupe_signal(caplog) -> None:     """When claim returns fewer rows than batch_size, the worker should log     a structured signal (e.g. 'claim_partial_batch') so operators can observe     dedupe activity in production. If no such log exists today, this test     documents the gap; pivot to skip if log silence is intentional."""     # Skeleton — depends on whether main_worker.dispatch_tick currently logs     # claim batch size. If not, this finding becomes a feature request rather     # than a regression test.

#### G21-037 · DROP INDEX + CREATE INDEX inside transaction blocks compute_jobs writes for the recreation window
- **File**: `supabase/migrations/20260428155809_claim_failed_retry.sql:176`
- **Specialist**: `data-migration` (confidence 8)
- **Summary**: Migration 089 STEP 3 drops `idx_compute_jobs_priority_pending` and recreates it inside a BEGIN/COMMIT block. Since the migration is transactional, neither `DROP INDEX CONCURRENTLY` nor `CREATE INDEX CONCURRENTLY` is permitted. DROP INDEX takes an ACCESS EXCLUSIVE lock on compute_jobs; the subsequent CREATE INDEX takes a SHARE lock until the index is built. For an active queue table with concurrent enqueue/claim traffic this is a measurable write-stall window (visible to users as wizard-submit lag, allocator-rescore lag). Production-volume of compute_jobs at deploy time should be checked before merging.
- **Evidence**: supabase/migrations/20260428155809_claim_failed_retry.sql:49 (`BEGIN;`), :176 (DROP INDEX IF EXISTS), :178-180 (CREATE INDEX IF NOT EXISTS, NOT concurrent).
- **Fix**: Split the index DDL into a separate migration that runs OUTSIDE a transaction (Supabase migration runners can be told `-- ATOMIC: false`), use `CREATE INDEX CONCURRENTLY` for the new index FIRST, then `DROP INDEX CONCURRENTLY` for the old one. For the duration both indices coexist (slight write amplification) but no ACCESS EXCLUSIVE lock is taken.

#### G21-038 · failed_retry rows retain stale claimed_by / claimed_at audit until re-claim
- **File**: `supabase/migrations/20260428155809_claim_failed_retry.sql:80`
- **Specialist**: `data-migration` (confidence 8)
- **Summary**: `claim_compute_jobs` (migration 089) sets `claimed_at = now()` and `claimed_by = p_worker_id` on every claim, including re-claims of failed_retry rows. `mark_compute_job_failed` (migration 032 line 754-756) sets `claimed_at = NULL, claimed_by = NULL` on the failure write — so post-failure a failed_retry row has NULL claimed_at/by, which is correct. BUT once mig 089 enables re-claim, the row's last_error / error_kind from the prior attempt is NOT cleared in the UPDATE. The admin/observability UI continues to display the prior failure's last_error against a row that is now status='running' again, which is misleading during the second attempt window. This was masked before 089 because failed_retry was a terminal state in practice.
- **Evidence**: supabase/migrations/20260428155809_claim_failed_retry.sql:79-84 (UPDATE SET clause does not clear last_error / error_kind) and supabase/migrations/20260411144407_compute_jobs_queue.sql:750-757 (mark_compute_job_failed leaves last_error populated on failed_retry).
- **Fix**: In both `claim_compute_jobs` and `claim_compute_jobs_with_priority` UPDATE clauses add `last_error = NULL, error_kind = NULL` when transitioning failed_retry → running. Alternatively keep the audit trail and add a `prior_error / prior_error_kind` column populated on transition. Choose based on observability requirements but be explicit; current behavior conflates 'currently running' with 'last failure detail'.

#### G21-039 · Index predicate widening (idx_compute_jobs_priority_pending) untested — silent index-only-scan regression risk
- **File**: `supabase/migrations/20260428155809_claim_failed_retry.sql:335`
- **Specialist**: `pr-test-analyzer` (confidence 9)
- **Summary**: Migration 089 drops + recreates `idx_compute_jobs_priority_pending` with the widened predicate `WHERE priority IN ('normal','high') AND status IN ('pending','failed_retry')`. The throttle probe SELECT scans against this index for an index-only scan. If a future migration silently restores the old predicate (`status = 'pending'`), the probe would still WORK correctly but would do a heap fetch for every failed_retry row — turning an O(index lookup) into O(table scan) at high failed_retry volume. No test verifies the predicate. The 089 DO block does check it but the apply-time check is one-shot.
- **Evidence**: supabase/migrations/20260428155809_claim_failed_retry.sql:335-337 partial index recreation. grep 'idx_compute_jobs_priority_pending' in tests → no hits.
- **Fix**: Add to test_compute_jobs_fencing.py:  def test_priority_partial_index_predicate_widened(admin):     """Mig 089: the partial index used by the throttle probe must include     failed_retry in its WHERE predicate so the probe stays index-only."""     res = admin.rpc('exec_sql_for_test', {         'q': "SELECT indexdef FROM pg_indexes WHERE indexname = 'idx_compute_jobs_priority_pending'"     }).execute()     assert res.data, 'idx_compute_jobs_priority_pending not found'     indexdef = res.data[0]['indexdef']     assert 'failed_retry' in indexdef, (         f'Partial index predicate must include failed_retry (mig 089), got: {indexdef}'     )

#### G21-040 · last_error persists across failed_retry → running transition; widened claim filter prolongs visibility window of prior error payload
- **File**: `supabase/migrations/20260428155809_claim_failed_retry.sql:80`
- **Specialist**: `security` (confidence 8)
- **Summary**: The claim RPC sets status='running', claimed_at, claimed_by, and increments attempts, but does NOT clear last_error. Migration 089 makes failed_retry rows re-claimable indefinitely (until they succeed, fail_final, or are deleted), so the previous attempt's error text continues to live in the row through every subsequent retry. classify_exception's catch-all branches (RuntimeError/ValueError/ccxt.BaseError) feed str(exc)[:500] verbatim into mark_compute_job_failed's p_error, which becomes last_error. If a future code path ever serialises sensitive content (PII, partial credentials in a ccxt exception, request bodies, etc.) into an exception message, that content remains stored on the row across retries and is visible to anyone with admin compute_jobs read (get_admin_compute_jobs returns un-redacted last_error per migration 033). G21 itself does not introduce a new leak channel but materially extends the lifetime of any pre-existing leak by re-claiming failed_retry rows instead of leaving them in a terminal state.
- **Evidence**: supabase/migrations/20260428155809_claim_failed_retry.sql:80-94 (no SET last_error=NULL in claim_compute_jobs); supabase/migrations/20260411144407_compute_jobs_queue.sql:750-757 (mark_compute_job_failed sets last_error=p_error every failure)
- **Fix**: In both replaced claim RPCs (claim_compute_jobs and claim_compute_jobs_with_priority), add `last_error = NULL, error_kind = NULL` to the UPDATE SET clause so re-claimed failed_retry rows start the next attempt with a clean error column. Alternative: scrub last_error in a dedicated re-arming step before the claim runs.

#### G21-041 · Throttle probe in claim_compute_jobs_with_priority is global, not tenant-scoped; widened to failed_retry amplifies cross-tenant low-priority starvation
- **File**: `supabase/migrations/20260428155809_claim_failed_retry.sql:62`
- **Specialist**: `security` (confidence 8)
- **Summary**: The throttle probe `SELECT count(*) ... WHERE priority IN ('normal','high') AND status IN ('pending','failed_retry') AND next_attempt_at <= now()` is global across all tenants. Pre-089 this only counted true 'pending' rows, which expired quickly. Post-089 a stuck failed_retry row at normal/high priority belonging to tenant A counts in the probe until it transitions to failed_final, which blocks tenant B's low-priority work for the full retry window (up to 8 minutes + retry chain). Combined with migration 090's partition dedupe, a single tenant with many failed_retry rows sharing partition keys can suppress all low-priority claim batches across the deployment until their backoff completes. This is a cross-tenant DoS amplification — not a data-exposure issue but a STRIDE 'Denial of Service' on shared queue infrastructure.
- **Evidence**: supabase/migrations/20260428155809_claim_failed_retry.sql:91-95 (throttle probe widened to failed_retry); supabase/migrations/20260428190907_claim_dedupe_partition_keys.sql:721-723 (same widening preserved); migration 086 documented the throttle as intentional but pre-089 the failure mode was bounded by 'pending' lifetime
- **Fix**: Either (a) keep the throttle probe scoped to 'pending' only so transient failures of one tenant cannot block others' low-priority work indefinitely; or (b) cap how long failed_retry rows count in the throttle probe (e.g. `next_attempt_at <= now() - interval '1 minute'` so a row in active backoff doesn't throttle); or (c) tenant-scope the throttle (probe by api_key_id/user_id so cross-tenant interference is impossible). Document tenancy isolation guarantees of the throttle explicitly.

#### G21-042 · Self-verifying DO block is one-shot, does not prevent silent regressions in subsequent migrations
- **File**: `supabase/migrations/20260428190907_claim_dedupe_partition_keys.sql:267`
- **Specialist**: `data-migration` (confidence 8)
- **Summary**: Migration 090 STEP 3 DO block uses `prosrc LIKE '%row_number() OVER%'` plus 4 PARTITION BY checks to assert the partition dedupe was installed. This only runs ONCE at apply time. A future migration that CREATE OR REPLACE-s either function WITHOUT including the dedupe will deploy silently — exactly what happened with migration 104 (mig 117 STEP 3's preamble explicitly calls this out: 'mig 104's CREATE OR REPLACE eliminated the migration-090 partition dedupe by mistake'). The structural assertion needed to be a permanent constraint (e.g. an EVENT TRIGGER that re-checks the function body whenever it is replaced) or a CI gate, not a one-shot DO block.
- **Evidence**: supabase/migrations/20260428190907_claim_dedupe_partition_keys.sql:267-321 (DO block); supabase/migrations/20260515114555_compute_jobs_claim_token_fencing.sql:221-228 (preamble admits mig 104 silently dropped the dedupe between 090 and 117).
- **Fix**: Add an EVENT TRIGGER on ALTER FUNCTION/CREATE FUNCTION for these two RPCs that re-asserts the structural shape, OR move the assertion to a CI test that diffs pg_proc.prosrc against an expected fingerprint, OR encode the dedupe in a stored-helper function the RPCs MUST call (so a future replace either keeps the call or fails review).

#### G21-043 · Throttle probe count(*) scans full priority-pending partial index every tick
- **File**: `supabase/migrations/20260428190907_claim_dedupe_partition_keys.sql:179`
- **Specialist**: `performance` (confidence 8)
- **Summary**: `SELECT count(*) INTO v_high_pending FROM compute_jobs WHERE priority IN ('normal','high') AND status IN ('pending', 'failed_retry') AND next_attempt_at <= now()` runs on every claim tick (~12 per minute). The widened `idx_compute_jobs_priority_pending` (089) covers `status IN ('pending','failed_retry')`, so the scan is index-bounded — but it still counts ALL eligible rows. The boolean decision only needs `v_high_pending > 0`. Replacing `count(*)` with `EXISTS` (or `LIMIT 1`) lets Postgres short-circuit on the first index tuple and skip the rest of the (potentially large after 089) backlog. At Phase-12 backfill scale (hundreds of pending compute_analytics rows), counting every row 12 times/min is wasted CPU.
- **Evidence**: supabase/migrations/20260428190907_claim_dedupe_partition_keys.sql:179-183 (089 widened version: `count(*)` with widened predicate); same anti-pattern survived into supabase/migrations/20260515114555_compute_jobs_claim_token_fencing.sql:272-276.
- **Fix**: Replace `SELECT count(*) INTO v_high_pending FROM ... WHERE ...` with `SELECT 1 INTO v_high_pending FROM ... WHERE ... LIMIT 1` or use `IF EXISTS(SELECT 1 FROM ...) THEN v_high_pending := 1; ELSE v_high_pending := 0; END IF;` so the throttle probe short-circuits on the first matching row instead of counting the full backlog.

#### G21-044 · Self-verifying DO block prosrc LIKE scans run on every migration apply
- **File**: `supabase/migrations/20260428190907_claim_dedupe_partition_keys.sql:292`
- **Specialist**: `performance` (confidence 8)
- **Summary**: The DO block at the end runs four `prosrc NOT LIKE '%PARTITION BY kind, <col>%'` checks against pg_proc on every migration apply. While migrations apply rarely (deploy time), this is a 4× full-text scan of the function source for two functions (8 LIKE ops total) inside a `RAISE EXCEPTION IF NOT EXISTS` chain. The bigger concern: these LIKE scans are how the structural assertions verify the dedupe survived, but they pass even if the function body has been replaced with a syntactically valid but semantically broken variant (e.g. `PARTITION BY kind, portfolio_id ORDER BY random()`). The structural check is cheap to run but provides false confidence — combined with the migration's explicit decision to NOT run a behavioral assertion (line 251-256: "A live regression test ... is omitted here because every queue partition column has a foreign key"), the production claim path has zero deploy-time validation of correctness, just textual presence.
- **Evidence**: supabase/migrations/20260428190907_claim_dedupe_partition_keys.sql:292-318 — 8 LIKE scans of pg_proc.prosrc as the only verification gate. Migration 117's verification is even thinner (no DO block re-runs the partition LIKE check).
- **Fix**: Add a behavioral assertion that inserts two stub `compute_jobs` rows with all FK-bearing columns NULL (the kind doesn't need a strategy/allocator), calls `claim_compute_jobs_with_priority(5, 'test')`, asserts `count(*) <= 1`, and savepoint-rollbacks. NULL partition columns skip the FK constraints AND the dedupe rank check, so a synthetic test that doesn't trip the actual bug is useless — instead, fabricate the scenario using a fixed `kind='__migration_test__'` that the dedupe must handle by `next_attempt_at` alone.

#### G21-045 · Self-verifying DO block of migrations 089 and 090 not exercised in any test
- **File**: `supabase/migrations/20260428190907_claim_dedupe_partition_keys.sql:267`
- **Specialist**: `pr-test-analyzer` (confidence 8)
- **Summary**: Both migrations include lengthy DO blocks that assert structural properties (function exists with H-B search_path, body contains `row_number() OVER` and `PARTITION BY` literals). These run at apply-time only. There is no CI test that catches drift if e.g. mig 089 was rolled forward incompatibly with mig 090, or if a later migration silently replaces the function body without the dedupe CTE. A standalone Python check that runs `SELECT pg_get_functiondef(...)` and asserts the literals are present — independent of the apply-time check — would catch silent rollouts of replacement functions outside the migration tree.
- **Evidence**: supabase/migrations/20260428190907_claim_dedupe_partition_keys.sql:267-321 (DO block). supabase/migrations/20260428155809_claim_failed_retry.sql:340+ (DO block). No test in analytics-service/tests/ or tests/ exercises pg_proc.prosrc / pg_get_functiondef.
- **Fix**: Add to test_compute_jobs_fencing.py:  def test_claim_rpc_body_includes_partition_dedupe(admin):     """Mig 090 contract guard: the live function body must include the partition     dedupe CTE. Catches silent function replacement outside the migration tree."""     res = admin.rpc('exec_sql_for_test', {  # or raw psycopg if no helper         'q': "SELECT pg_get_functiondef('public.claim_compute_jobs_with_priority'::regprocedure) AS def"     }).execute()     src = res.data[0]['def']     assert 'row_number() OVER' in src, 'mig 090 partition dedupe missing from live function'     for col in ('portfolio_id', 'strategy_id', 'allocator_id', 'api_key_id'):         assert f'PARTITION BY kind, {col}' in src, f'mig 090 partition window missing: {col}'     assert "status IN ('pending', 'failed_retry')" in src, 'mig 089 failed_retry filter missing' # (If exec_sql_for_test isn't available, use a parallel psycopg connection seeded # from SUPABASE_DB_URL — same pattern as the python_psql fixture in conftest.py.)

#### G21-046 · Dedupe silently drops failed_retry losers with no log line or metric — perpetual partition collision invisible to operators
- **File**: `supabase/migrations/20260428190907_claim_dedupe_partition_keys.sql:760`
- **Specialist**: `silent-failure-hunter` (confidence 9)
- **Summary**: When two failed_retry rows share (kind, allocator_id) and both are eligible (next_attempt_at <= now()), the dedupe CTE picks one winner via row_number() — the loser is filtered out of the claim batch with NO log, no metric, no audit-trail row. dispatch_tick logs only 'Claimed N jobs' at INFO. If a strategy generates two distinct compute_analytics jobs (different correlation_ids, different metadata) that both end up failed_retry on the same partition, one is silently delayed N retry cycles behind the other. If both perpetually fail and re-enter failed_retry, the loser is starved for the whole life of the winner — including the 3 attempts × 30s/2min/8min backoff sequence (≈10 min worst-case delay per cycle). Worse, correlation_id telemetry on the dropped row never reaches the dispatcher this tick, so distributed traces show a gap with no explanation.
- **Evidence**: supabase/migrations/20260428190907_claim_dedupe_partition_keys.sql:758-765 (deduped CTE filter); analytics-service/main_worker.py:288 (only logs claimed count, never logs eligible-but-deduped count)
- **Fix**: Either (a) add a SQL-side counter that emits NOTICE when dedupe drops candidates (operator can scan logs), (b) emit a worker-side log line on every tick comparing the throttle-probe count to len(jobs) and warning when the gap is non-zero for >N consecutive ticks, or (c) write a row to a queue_observability table when dedupe filters >0 candidates so admins can see partition collisions.

#### G21-047 · Throttle probe count() is silently de-correlated from inner claim filter — failed_retry rows counted but not claimed
- **File**: `supabase/migrations/20260428190907_claim_dedupe_partition_keys.sql:178`
- **Specialist**: `silent-failure-hunter` (confidence 8)
- **Summary**: The v_high_pending throttle probe counts rows with `status IN ('pending','failed_retry')` (line 180 in the diff's mig 090 STEP 2), but if a future migration narrows the inner WHERE back to `status = 'pending'` only, the probe will OVER-count: low-priority claim is throttled by counting failed_retry rows that the inner WHERE won't claim anyway. This silently starves low-priority pending jobs forever when a normal/high failed_retry backlog exists. Migration 20260515114555 (claim_token fencing) documents this exact regression: 'Counting failed_retry here while the inner WHERE only takes pending would throttle low-priority pending jobs forever without draining a failed_retry backlog'. The mig 090 probe is correct ONLY because mig 090's inner WHERE also accepts failed_retry — but the coupling is not enforced anywhere.
- **Evidence**: supabase/migrations/20260428190907_claim_dedupe_partition_keys.sql:178-183 (probe IN status); 213-215 (inner WHERE IN status); supabase/migrations/20260515114555_compute_jobs_claim_token_fencing.sql:267-276 (explicit drift correction)
- **Fix**: Use a single SQL-array constant or a CTE that defines the eligibility predicate once and is reused by both probe and inner WHERE. OR add a structural assertion that BOTH have identical status-clause text via pg_proc.prosrc check, so a future replace cannot silently desync them.

#### G21-048 · Partition key tuple is implicit — 4 columns (portfolio_id, strategy_id, allocator_id, api_key_id) with no named PartitionKey type
- **File**: `supabase/migrations/20260428190907_claim_dedupe_partition_keys.sql:83`
- **Specialist**: `type-design-analyzer` (confidence 8)
- **Summary**: Migration 090's dedupe contract uses 4 partition columns: portfolio_id, strategy_id, allocator_id, api_key_id. Each corresponds to a partial unique index `compute_jobs_one_inflight_per_kind_<x>`. The SQL ranks each candidate row by `row_number() OVER (PARTITION BY kind, <col>)` and survives if all 4 ranks are 1 (NULL-skipping). The Python worker has no representation of this 4-tuple — no `PartitionKey = NamedTuple('PartitionKey', [...])`, no enum of partition columns, no list of partition column names anywhere. When a 5th partition column gets added (e.g., 'workspace_id' in a future multi-tenant phase), the migration's self-verifying DO block checks 4 hardcoded PARTITION BY clauses with no Python counterpart to enforce that the worker's job-reading code stays in sync. The audit prompt explicitly flagged 'partition key tuple encoded as Tuple[str, ...] without a named type' — this is the upstream of that: even the Tuple[str, ...] is absent.
- **Evidence**: supabase/migrations/20260428190907_claim_dedupe_partition_keys.sql:103-110 4 row_number() OVER PARTITION BY clauses; lines 167-174 same 4 windows in the priority RPC; no Python types reference these column names as a unit
- **Fix**: Introduce `PARTITION_COLUMNS: Final[tuple[str, ...]] = ('portfolio_id', 'strategy_id', 'allocator_id', 'api_key_id')` in services/job_worker.py with a comment cross-linking to the migration. Add a TypedDict `PartitionKey(TypedDict): kind: JobKind; portfolio_id: str | None; strategy_id: str | None; allocator_id: str | None; api_key_id: str | None`. Add a helper `extract_partition_key(job: dict) -> PartitionKey` so the partition tuple is named once. Future column additions then break the type checker, not silent-correctness.

### LOW (2)

#### G21-049 · TestClaimDedupe._rpc_side_effect uses untyped name: str / params: dict — could be Literal-typed for RPC name
- **File**: `analytics-service/tests/test_main_worker.py:485`
- **Specialist**: `type-design-analyzer` (confidence 9)
- **Summary**: The new TestClaimDedupe.test_partial_batch_from_dedupe_dispatches_survivor defines `def _rpc_side_effect(name: str, params: dict)` and dispatches on `name == 'claim_compute_jobs_with_priority'`. The set of RPC names the worker calls is closed: {'claim_compute_jobs_with_priority', 'mark_compute_job_done', 'mark_compute_job_failed', 'defer_compute_job', 'reset_stalled_compute_jobs'}. A `Literal[...]` type for `name` would catch a typo such as 'claim_compute_job_with_priority' (singular) in test setup — currently the typo would silently fall through to the `return mark_chain` branch and produce a confusing assertion failure downstream.
- **Evidence**: analytics-service/tests/test_main_worker.py:485-490 (per diff lines 485-490)
- **Fix**: Define `RpcName = Literal['claim_compute_jobs_with_priority', 'mark_compute_job_done', 'mark_compute_job_failed', 'defer_compute_job', 'reset_stalled_compute_jobs']` in a shared test helper. Use `def _rpc_side_effect(name: RpcName, params: dict)`. Low-cost guardrail for an entire family of mock-based queue tests.

#### G21-050 · Migration 090's self-verifying DO block omits live regression test; relies on Python mock tests + one-shot deploy proof for cross-row 23505 guarantee
- **File**: `supabase/migrations/20260428190907_claim_dedupe_partition_keys.sql:792`
- **Specialist**: `security` (confidence 9)
