- **Summary**: The DO block performs only structural assertions (function exists, search_path is H-B, body text contains 'row_number() OVER' and four PARTITION BY definitions). A real regression test that inserts two failed_retry rows sharing (kind, allocator_id), calls claim, and asserts ≤ 1 row was claimed without 23505 is deferred to a deploy-time one-shot recorded in `.gstack/deploy-reports/2026-04-28-pr82-deploy.md`. That deploy report is not part of CI. A future refactor of the CTE could pass the structural string match but break the dedupe (e.g. miscoded NULL-handling, wrong partition expression for a freshly-added partition column). The Python `TestClaimDedupe` cases only mock the supabase RPC — they prove the worker tolerates a partial batch, not that the SQL actually dedupes. Net: there is no automated guardrail that the SQL behavior is correct, only that it textually looks correct.
- **Evidence**: supabase/migrations/20260428190907_claim_dedupe_partition_keys.sql:792-861 (structural-only DO block); analytics-service/tests/test_main_worker.py:438-522 (mock-only TestClaimDedupe)
- **Fix**: Add a true SQL regression. The FK obstacle is real but tractable: stand up a `pgTAP` / supabase test (lives in supabase/tests/, not migrations) that prepares its own minimal allocator row in a test transaction with `BEGIN; ... ROLLBACK;` semantics, or use a dedicated test allocator UUID seeded by an existing seed migration. The current 'documented in deploy report' approach is not a control.

## G22 — PRs #85-#90 — Phase 13 follow-ups + a11y + comment-rot strip + long-tail tech-debt

**Summary**: C0 · H7 · M25 · L5 · Total 37

### HIGH (7)

#### G22-001 · cleanup-wizard-drafts: api_keys delete error path (keyErr) is untested — a Supabase delete failure on a single orphan would silently skip and never produce a regression signal
- **File**: `src/app/api/cron/cleanup-wizard-drafts/route.ts:119`
- **Specialist**: `pr-test-analyzer` (confidence 9)
- **Summary**: PR #88 added 14 tests for cleanup-wizard-drafts but the `if (keyErr) { console.warn(...); continue; }` branch at route.ts:119-125 is uncovered. A regression that converts the `continue` to a `return 500` (or flips the !keyErr polarity, e.g., `if (!keyErr) continue`) would silently break the whole cron with no test failure. The route promises 'best-effort orphan sweep should not fail the whole cron'; the count-check error branch IS tested (test 'treats a count-check error as non-fatal') but the symmetric DELETE-error branch is not.
- **Evidence**: grep 'keyErr\|api_key delete failed' src/app/api/cron/cleanup-wizard-drafts/route.test.ts → only 3 deleteKeyByKey: { error: null } seeds, never error: { message: ... }. route.ts:119 `if (keyErr) { console.warn(...); continue; }`
- **Fix**: Add test in src/app/api/cron/cleanup-wizard-drafts/route.test.ts: seed recorders.deleteKeyByKey = { 'key-a': { error: { message: 'fk violation' } }, 'key-b': { error: null } }; assert res.status === 200 AND body.orphaned_keys_revoked === 1 (key-a's failure is swallowed, key-b succeeds). Revert the route's `continue` to `return NextResponse.json({ error: ... }, { status: 500 })` and verify the test fails.

#### G22-002 · Cron's silent api_keys delete failure inflates orphaned_keys_revoked correctness — sums two distinct failure modes into one 'all clean' response · _chain_ · refs: silent-failure-hunter#3, silent-failure-hunter#4, pr-test-analyzer#1, api-contract#6
- **File**: `src/app/api/cron/cleanup-wizard-drafts/route.ts:126`
- **Specialist**: `red-team` (confidence 8)
- **Summary**: Chain of silent-failure #4 + #3 + api-contract #6: when a per-key COUNT check errors, the route `continue`s WITHOUT incrementing orphanedKeysRevoked; when an api_keys DELETE errors on a confirmed-orphan (refCount=0), it also `continue`s without bumping the counter. Both paths produce a 200 response that buries the partial failure in the cron's reply, while leaking raw PostgREST error messages via console.warn that survive in Vercel logs (api-contract #6). An operator looking at `{deleted: 50, orphaned_keys_revoked: 47}` cannot distinguish (a) 'three keys were correctly kept because still-referenced' from (b) 'three keys failed to delete and orphan rows still point at deleted strategies'. The route's response shape encodes a false invariant: response.success === run.success. Over weeks of cron runs, orphan api_key rows accumulate pointing at strategies that no longer exist, breaking the `api_keys.strategy_id` integrity that the user-driven DELETE handler relied on. Combined with pr-test-analyzer #1 (no test for the keyErr branch), a regression that flips `if (keyErr) continue` to `if (keyErr) return 500` would silently change behavior across the whole route without test failure.
- **Evidence**: src/app/api/cron/cleanup-wizard-drafts/route.ts:99-126 (count + delete error paths both `continue`); response payload at :129-132 omits any error counters; route.test.ts (PR #88) seeds keyErr=null in every case
- **Fix**: Track {count_check_errors, key_revoke_errors} on the response payload. When EITHER > 0, return 207 (multi-status) instead of 200 so cron logs surface red. Add a structured Sentry call with key_id tagging so operators correlate which keys orphaned. Add pr-test-analyzer #1's missing keyErr regression test in the same patch to pin the new contract.

#### G22-003 · v2 panel `key={strategy.id}` remount strategy + useLazyPanelMetrics version-counter are belt-AND-suspenders that fight each other — accidentally removing the key prop is now UNDETECTABLE by every existing test · _chain_ · refs: type-design-analyzer#5, performance#3, pr-test-analyzer#7
- **File**: `src/components/strategy-v2/StrategyV2Shell.tsx:108`
- **Specialist**: `red-team` (confidence 8)
- **Summary**: Chain of type-design #5 + performance #3 + pr-test-analyzer #7: PR #86 added BOTH (a) `key={strategy.id}` on 5 panel call-sites in StrategyV2Shell and (b) versionRef monotonic counter inside useLazyPanelMetrics. Either alone fixes the F2 cross-strategy leak; together they create a maintenance trap. A future contributor removing the key prop (citing performance #3's recommendation to drop the remount overhead) would EXPOSE the latent bug class type-design #5 calls out for HeadlineMetricsPanel — which has NO hook-level mountedRef/versionRef guard, just an inline .then closure in handleViewChange. The existing test pins the key prop's presence (Test 6b at StrategyV2Shell.test.tsx:273), but the test asserts the key is PRESENT, not that the underlying race is safe without it. The asymmetry — RollingMetricsPanel/ReturnsDistributionPanel/etc. have hook-level guards, HeadlineMetricsPanel does NOT — is invisible at the type level. The 'belt-and-suspenders' justification at the comment block is correct, but the cost is that the system passes regression tests in TWO DIFFERENT states: with both fixes (intended) and with only the version counter (silently breaks HeadlineMetricsPanel).
- **Evidence**: src/components/strategy-v2/StrategyV2Shell.tsx:80-87 (HeadlineMetricsPanel keyed by strategy.id); src/components/strategy-v2/HeadlineMetricsPanel.tsx:124-139 (handleViewChange uses inline closure, no mountedRef/versionRef); src/components/strategy-v2/StrategyV2Shell.test.tsx Test 6b only asserts key prop presence, NOT race safety without it
- **Fix**: Either (a) factor HeadlineMetricsPanel's log_returns lazy fetch into a useLazyPanelMetrics variant so the guard is uniform across all 5 keyed panels, OR (b) add a Test 6c that specifically reproduces the A→B→A flip race for HeadlineMetricsPanel's Log-returns fetch without `key={strategy.id}` — proving the version-counter alone is insufficient for that panel. Currently the system relies on a contract (parent must key the panel) that the type system cannot enforce and the tests cannot verify.

#### G22-004 · CustomizeDrawer Tab-trap uses document-level keydown listener but ESC uses window-level — different propagation paths give inconsistent suppression in shadow DOM and portal contexts · _new_ · refs: performance#2
- **File**: `src/components/strategy/CustomizeDrawer.tsx:111`
- **Specialist**: `red-team` (confidence 8)
- **Summary**: The drawer wires THREE separate keyboard listeners: (1) ESC on window (line 55), (2) Tab trap on document (line 111), and (3) the slide-in animation timer. The window vs document split is silent: in standard React DOM both fire identically, but when a future component (Radix Portal, Headless UI Dialog, or a third-party tooltip mounted in a sibling tree) installs a stopPropagation on bubbling keydowns at the document or window boundary, ESC and Tab trap will disagree about which events they see. The animation effect at line 117-125 also sets state inside a rAF callback which the comment-rot strip rewrote — the `set-state-in-effect` eslint-disable is preserved but the JSDoc no longer documents the rAF discipline. Combined with performance #2 (Tab handler re-querySelectorAlls every keystroke) this becomes a real-world bug only on touch-screen 'select all + Tab' or in Safari's full-keyboard-access mode. Severity high because it surfaces a class of bug (focus escape from modal) that bypasses screen reader users entirely without a test failure.
- **Evidence**: src/components/strategy/CustomizeDrawer.tsx:50-57 (ESC on window), :85-113 (Tab trap on document); the focus-trap test file added 5 new tests for focus management but NONE cover ESC + Tab interaction or document-vs-window listener inconsistency
- **Fix**: Unify the listener boundary: either both on document (which catches portals and modals correctly) or both on the drawer's own ref (which scopes the trap to the modal subtree but breaks ESC from focused inputs). The current asymmetry is the worst of both worlds. Add a regression test where the drawer is open AND a sibling component installs a stopPropagation on document.keydown — assert ESC still closes and Tab still cycles.

#### G22-005 · LazyMetricsPanelId domain re-encoded in 3 places with no cross-file invariant — drift will not type-check
- **File**: `src/lib/queries-client.ts:12`
- **Specialist**: `type-design-analyzer` (confidence 9)
- **Summary**: The 7-value RPC panel union `LazyMetricsPanelId` is locally redeclared in queries-client.ts as a copy of the same union in queries.ts:686-693, with only a doc comment ('Mirror of LazyMetricsPanelId from queries.ts:441') keeping them in sync. A third local re-encoding lives in hooks/useLazyPanelMetrics.ts:31 where the inline `satisfies Record<LazyPanelId, "returns_dist" | "rolling" | "trades" | "exposure">` clause hand-rolls the 4-value subset without referencing either canonical union. Adding a new panel id (or renaming one) would compile cleanly on all three files independently while silently breaking the RPC contract at runtime — the exact pattern that produced PR #106/#107's silent-dead chips called out in queries.ts:506-513.
- **Evidence**: src/lib/queries-client.ts:12-19 + src/lib/queries.ts:686-693 + src/hooks/useLazyPanelMetrics.ts:26-31
- **Fix**: Move `LazyMetricsPanelId` (or at minimum the 4 lazy-eligible ids) into `src/lib/types.ts` so it is reachable from both server and client modules without crossing the server-only barrier. Then queries.ts and queries-client.ts import the single source, and useLazyPanelMetrics's PANEL_TO_ID can `satisfies Record<LazyPanelId, LazyMetricsPanelId>` against the imported union — drift becomes a compile error.

#### G22-006 · `getStrategyDetailV2`: explicit column projection but `as unknown as Strategy` cast retains the full Strategy shape on access
- **File**: `src/lib/queries.ts:537`
- **Specialist**: `type-design-analyzer` (confidence 8)
- **Summary**: PR #85's MA-1 narrowed the strategy `select(...)` to 9 columns (id, name, start_date, supported_exchanges, strategy_types, subtypes, markets, leverage_range, avg_daily_turnover) for a bandwidth win, but immediately re-widens via `const s = strategy as unknown as Strategy`. The `Strategy` interface contains many fields the projection drops (user_id, category_id, api_key_id, description, aum, max_capacity, status, is_example, benchmark, created_at, trust_tier). A consumer writing `result.strategy.aum` will type-check fine and read `undefined` at runtime — the exact class of bug PR #85's data_quality_flags rescue (queries.ts:506-513) was meant to prevent (PR #106/#107 silently dead chips because PostgREST didn't return the column the typed interface promised). The Strategy shell currently uses only .id/.name/.start_date, so the bug is latent — but the type doesn't encode this invariant.
- **Evidence**: src/lib/queries.ts:503-504,537
- **Fix**: Define `type StrategyV2ProjectedColumns = Pick<Strategy, 'id'|'name'|'start_date'|'supported_exchanges'|'strategy_types'|'subtypes'|'markets'|'leverage_range'|'avg_daily_turnover'>` and cast `const s = strategy as unknown as StrategyV2ProjectedColumns`. Then update `StrategyV2Detail.strategy` to use the projected type — any consumer accessing a non-projected field becomes a type error, and the SELECT column list + projected interface stay in lockstep.

#### G22-007 · LazyMetricsPayload type lies about RPC shape — Record<K,unknown> requires all 12 keys present
- **File**: `src/lib/types.ts:314`
- **Specialist**: `type-design-analyzer` (confidence 9)
- **Summary**: `LazyMetricsPayload = Record<StrategyAnalyticsSeriesKind, unknown> | Record<string, never>` claims the RPC returns either ALL 12 series kinds or zero. Reality (per the migration 087 CASE statement and the panel→kinds mapping in queries.ts:580-590) is that each panel returns a partial subset of 1-3 keys (e.g., panel4 returns just daily_returns_grid; panel5 returns 7 keys; panel7 returns 2). Callers must use optional chaining on every access (data?.daily_returns_grid, data?.rolling_volatility_3m) — the type cannot enforce this because Record<K,V> demands totality. Combined with `return {} as LazyMetricsPayload` casts in queries.ts:733/736 and queries-client.ts:61/64, the discipline is purely conventional. A future consumer writing `payload.daily_returns_grid.length` for a Panel 5 fetch type-checks fine and crashes at runtime.
- **Evidence**: src/lib/types.ts:309-314 + src/lib/queries.ts:733,736 + src/lib/queries-client.ts:61,64
- **Fix**: Replace with `Partial<Record<StrategyAnalyticsSeriesKind, unknown>>` so all 12 keys become optional — the type now matches the partial-projection reality and forces consumers to null-check before access. Even better: a discriminated union keyed by panel id, e.g. `type Panel4Payload = { daily_returns_grid?: DailyGridRow[] }`, so each panel's fetch site narrows to the keys that panel can actually receive.

### MEDIUM (25)

#### G22-008 · PR #90 retired 3 hardcoded-skip Playwright specs (api-key-flow, admin-compute-jobs, bridge-outcome) but no replacement coverage exists — the underlying contracts are now untested at the e2e layer
- **File**: `e2e/api-key-flow.spec.ts:1`
- **Specialist**: `pr-test-analyzer` (confidence 9)
- **Summary**: PR #90 changelog claims `Three hardcoded-skip Playwright specs ... can be re-implemented when its underlying scaffolding is ready.` However, the API-level contract tests inside those specs (e.g. /api/keys/validate-and-encrypt 401 unauthenticated, /api/admin/compute-jobs 401 unauth + JSON content-type) were unconditionally executed (NOT skipped) before the delete and provided real coverage. Removing them silently drops e2e coverage of three authn/JSON-shape contracts. NOTE: at current main these files still exist (audit batch is comparing PR-time snapshots) but if the PR were to re-land, the live deletions would create gaps.
- **Evidence**: In the diff at line 7864-7902, e2e/admin-compute-jobs.spec.ts test 'API returns 401 for unauthenticated request' and 'API accepts filter query params without error shape' are NOT inside test.skip — they run on every CI cycle. api-key-flow.spec.ts has 3 such API-contract tests (line 7935-7975).
- **Fix**: Either: (a) reinstate just the API-contract tests in each spec (drop the test.skip UI tests, keep the request-only contract tests), or (b) move those API contract assertions into vitest route.test.ts files (e.g. src/app/api/admin/compute-jobs/route.test.ts) so the contract is preserved at the unit-test layer.

#### G22-009 · Three E2E specs deleted in PR #90 are still in current main — the PR diff is stale relative to live code, masking the deletion impact · _challenge_ · refs: pr-test-analyzer#8
- **File**: `e2e/api-key-flow.spec.ts:1`

So pr-test-analyzer #8 is HALF-VALID: the bridge-outcome and admin-compute-jobs deletions did land and DID drop their API-contract tests (compute-jobs 401 contract test, bridge-outcome request-only assertions); api-key-flow's API-contract tests are still live. #### G22-010 · StrategyTable.initialWatchedSet collapses watchlist-fetch failure with empty watchlist
- **File**: `src/app/(dashboard)/discovery/[slug]/page.tsx:39`
- **Specialist**: `type-design-analyzer` (confidence 8)
- **Summary**: PR-90's `getMyWatchlist` now returns `Set<string> | null` where `null` means transient DB/RLS failure (distinct from empty starred set). The discovery page reads this distinction at line 38 (`watchlistFailed = watchedSet === null`) and surfaces a banner — but then collapses the failure back via `initialWatchedSet = watchedSet ?? new Set<string>()` and passes a plain `Set<string>` to StrategyTable. StrategyTable's `initialWatchedSet?: Set<string>` type cannot tell 'failed to load' from 'user has zero stars'. So the StarToggle still renders empty stars and a click-to-star (which would normally just succeed against the user_favorites PK constraint) won't surface that the optimistic state is now competing with the real-but-unknown starred set. The failure signal exists at the server boundary and at the page-level banner; it's missing from the table-level type.
- **Evidence**: src/app/(dashboard)/discovery/[slug]/page.tsx:37-40 + src/components/strategy/StrategyTable.tsx:66,136-138
- **Fix**: Either propagate the nullable contract: `initialWatchedSet?: Set<string> | null` on StrategyTableProps and let the table disable the star column (or render a tooltip) when null. Or accept that the page-level banner is sufficient UX coverage and just document it — but the current type erases a fetch outcome the rest of the system worked hard to express.

#### G22-011 · logAuditEvent in admin/intro-request is fire-and-forget — silent on emit failure
- **File**: `src/app/api/admin/intro-request/route.ts:106`
- **Specialist**: `silent-failure-hunter` (confidence 9)
- **Summary**: logAuditEvent(supabase, ...) returns void and runs in `after()`/microtask. Its inner emit() handles errors via Sentry, but the route has no view into emission success; if Sentry wiring lags or fails inside emit, the admin status-change audit silently drops on cold-finish (the audit.ts comment explicitly acknowledges 'the event may still drop on cold-finish here, but that path is non-route and rare'). For an admin-driven contact_request transition, that is a compliance gap rather than a debugging convenience.
- **Evidence**: src/app/api/admin/intro-request/route.ts:106-114
- **Fix**: Either await the audit emission so 5xx surfaces on failure, or document the drop-tolerance explicitly in the route + ensure Sentry instrumentation is in place before this lands in production.

#### G22-012 · Admin POST routes accept unbounded note/review strings — only audit metadata is capped
- **File**: `src/app/api/admin/strategy-review/route.ts:102`
- **Specialist**: `api-contract` (confidence 8)
- **Summary**: strategy-review/route.ts line 102 writes the raw `review_note` (cast string) directly into strategies.review_note (PostgreSQL TEXT, unbounded). The 2000-char cap at line 114-119 only applies to the audit-log metadata copy. An admin (or any caller who passes the admin gate via a session hijack) can write multi-megabyte review notes and bloat the strategies row. Same pattern in intro-request/route.ts line 91: `update.admin_note = admin_note` with no length cap. No Zod schema at all on either admin route — only ad-hoc truthy/whitelist checks.
- **Evidence**: src/app/api/admin/strategy-review/route.ts:62-65 (validation), :100-104 (DB write); src/app/api/admin/intro-request/route.ts:80-92
- **Fix**: Add a Zod schema at the top of each admin route validating { id: z.string().uuid(), action/status: z.enum(...), review_note/admin_note: z.string().max(2000).optional() }. Parse the body with safeParse() and reject 400 on failure. The DB write should use the parsed.data, not the raw body cast.

#### G22-013 · logAuditEvent in admin/strategy-review is fire-and-forget — same drop hazard
- **File**: `src/app/api/admin/strategy-review/route.ts:122`
- **Specialist**: `silent-failure-hunter` (confidence 9)
- **Summary**: Identical pattern to intro-request: admin-driven strategy review status changes call logAuditEvent without awaiting, and the audit.ts wrapper explicitly documents drop-on-cold-finish for non-route paths. For a manager-approval audit, this is the kind of event that compliance reviewers will want a guarantee on — silent drop is not acceptable for an admin action.
- **Evidence**: src/app/api/admin/strategy-review/route.ts:122
- **Fix**: Mirror the route response on audit-emission failure (await emit + propagate 500) or document the drop-tolerance explicitly. At minimum, surface emission failures via a structured Sentry tag, not just console.error.

#### G22-014 · Cron route leaks raw PostgREST error.message to authenticated caller
- **File**: `src/app/api/cron/cleanup-wizard-drafts/route.ts:56`
- **Specialist**: `api-contract` (confidence 8)
- **Summary**: After the CRON_SECRET Bearer check, lines 56 and 83 return `{error: selectError.message}` / `{error: delError.message}` — raw PostgREST messages (potentially including SQL state, table names, FK constraint names, etc.). The accompanying test at route.test.ts:634 even asserts `body.error.toContain('FK violation')` — i.e. raw DB error leakage is encoded as contract. While only CRON_SECRET-holders can reach this path, the secret is shared infra (Vercel cron + manual incident response), so this drift from the generic-error convention used elsewhere (e.g., strategy-review/route.ts:107 returns generic 'Update failed') is observable to whoever can probe the endpoint. Pattern is duplicated in cleanup-ack-tokens/route.ts (pre-existing drift, not introduced here, but newly extended).
- **Evidence**: src/app/api/cron/cleanup-wizard-drafts/route.ts:54-57 (select error), :81-84 (delete error); src/app/api/cron/cleanup-wizard-drafts/route.test.ts:634
- **Fix**: Return generic envelopes — `NextResponse.json({error: 'Cron select failed'}, {status: 500})` etc. — and keep the detailed message in the existing console.error call for ops visibility. Update the test to assert on the generic message and check the console.error spy for the detailed one.

#### G22-015 · N+1 ref-count probe inside `cleanup-wizard-drafts` cron loops one PostgREST call per orphan candidate
- **File**: `src/app/api/cron/cleanup-wizard-drafts/route.ts:98`
- **Specialist**: `performance` (confidence 8)
- **Summary**: After deleting abandoned wizard-draft strategies the route loops over `apiKeyIds` and issues one `from('strategies').select('id', {count:'exact', head:true}).eq('api_key_id', keyId)` per candidate key — classic N+1. With a 30-day sweep on a backlog of abandoned drafts this can easily hit hundreds of round-trips to Supabase serially. A single `from('strategies').select('api_key_id').in('api_key_id', apiKeyIds).limit(apiKeyIds.length+1)` (or one count-by-group RPC) collapses it into 1 query. Even though this runs weekly via Vercel Cron, the 10s/60s function timeout means a backlog of >~300 orphan candidates will start tripping Function timeouts and leaving a partially-revoked api_keys set behind. The per-key DELETE that follows already cannot be batched (it's gated on refCount==0), but the COUNT_REFS scan absolutely can be.
- **Evidence**: src/app/api/cron/cleanup-wizard-drafts/route.ts:98-109 — `for (const keyId of apiKeyIds) { const { count: refCount } = await admin.from('strategies').select('id', { count: 'exact', head: true }).eq('api_key_id', keyId); ... }`
- **Fix**: Replace the per-key COUNT loop with a single batch fetch: `const { data: refRows } = await admin.from('strategies').select('api_key_id').in('api_key_id', apiKeyIds); const refByKey = new Map<string, number>(); for (const r of refRows ?? []) { refByKey.set(r.api_key_id, (refByKey.get(r.api_key_id) ?? 0) + 1); }` then iterate `apiKeyIds` and DELETE only the keys with `(refByKey.get(keyId) ?? 0) === 0`. One round-trip instead of N.

#### G22-016 · Cron count-check error treated as best-effort, allows api_key revoke to wrongly skip a shared key
- **File**: `src/app/api/cron/cleanup-wizard-drafts/route.ts:103`
- **Specialist**: `silent-failure-hunter` (confidence 8)
- **Summary**: When the per-key COUNT_REFS query errors transiently, the route logs a console.warn and continues to the next key (line 108) WITHOUT attempting the api_key delete. That is the safe direction for THIS key (skip orphan revoke if uncertain). But the error is recorded only via console.warn — no Sentry, no metric, no surfaced response field. A cron operator looking at a 200 response with `orphaned_keys_revoked: N` has no way to know that M other keys were silently skipped due to transient DB errors. After enough failed runs, orphan accumulation goes unnoticed.
- **Evidence**: src/app/api/cron/cleanup-wizard-drafts/route.ts:99-109
- **Fix**: Track `count_check_errors` in the response payload alongside `deleted` / `orphaned_keys_revoked`, and elevate from console.warn to console.error when count >= 1 so the cron run shows up red in the Vercel logs view. Better: aggregate as a structured event with the failing key_ids list.

#### G22-017 · Cron api_key delete error logs and continues — orphan never revoked, no operator signal
- **File**: `src/app/api/cron/cleanup-wizard-drafts/route.ts:119`
- **Specialist**: `silent-failure-hunter` (confidence 8)
- **Summary**: When the api_keys delete fails on a confirmed orphan (refCount === 0), the route logs console.warn 'api_key delete failed (non-fatal)' and continues. orphanedKeysRevoked is NOT incremented, but the response still returns 200 with whatever partial count succeeded. An operator monitoring the cron will see `orphaned_keys_revoked: 0` and think the run was clean when in reality the api_keys table is now polluted with orphan rows pointing at deleted strategies. console.warn buried in Vercel logs is not an operator signal.
- **Evidence**: src/app/api/cron/cleanup-wizard-drafts/route.ts:115-125
- **Fix**: Add a `key_revoke_errors` field to the response and bump from console.warn to console.error so the cron run surfaces in error filters. Consider a Sentry call with key_id tagging so operators can correlate which key the FK or RLS failure was about.

#### G22-018 · Notes PATCH route has no rate limit
- **File**: `src/app/api/notes/route.ts:106`
- **Specialist**: `api-contract` (confidence 8)
- **Summary**: PATCH /api/notes (multi-scope user-notes upsert) ships CSRF guard + Zod body parsing but no rate limiter. Comparable mutating routes call checkLimit() (watchlist=mandateAutoSaveLimiter 30/min, admin/*=adminActionLimiter). With the 100 KB content cap per request, an authenticated allocator could upsert ~6 GB/hr of arbitrary text into user_notes (each upsert hits both checkScopeOwnership SELECT + an upsert + an after()-scheduled audit RPC). Pattern drift from every other mutating route in src/app/api/.
- **Evidence**: src/app/api/notes/route.ts:106-188 (no checkLimit / ratelimit import); cf. src/app/api/watchlist/[strategyId]/route.ts:42 + src/app/api/admin/intro-request/route.ts:50
- **Fix**: Add checkLimit(userActionLimiter, `notes:${user.id}`) (or a dedicated notesUpsertLimiter) right after the auth gate, returning 429 with Retry-After before the JSON parse. Add a per-scope_ref dedupe key if you want to allow bursts across scopes.

#### G22-019 · Notes PATCH Zod schema lacks content max — JSON body parsed before size enforcement
- **File**: `src/app/api/notes/route.ts:42`
- **Specialist**: `api-contract` (confidence 8)
- **Summary**: BodySchema.content is `z.string()` with no max(). The byte-cap check at line 133 (new TextEncoder().encode(content).length > 100KB) runs AFTER `await request.json()` has already allocated the body. A malicious caller can submit a multi-megabyte JSON body that the runtime parses, allocates, then rejects with 400 — defeating the purpose of the cap and creating a memory-pressure vector. Next.js route handlers have no default body size limit.
- **Evidence**: src/app/api/notes/route.ts:42-46 (BodySchema), :120-138 (parse then byte-check)
- **Fix**: Tighten Zod: `content: z.string().max(120_000)` (slack vs the 100KB byte cap because UTF-8 multibyte chars take >1 byte; the post-parse byte check stays for byte-exact accuracy). Also consider a content-length header check before req.json() to reject obviously oversized requests cheaply.

#### G22-020 · Notes route PATCH still has no rate limit AND no Content-Length pre-check AND Zod has no content max — three reinforcing DoS vectors · _chain_ · refs: api-contract#1, api-contract#2
- **File**: `src/app/api/notes/route.ts:106`
- **Specialist**: `red-team` (confidence 8)
- **Summary**: Chain of api-contract #1 + #2 + (review fix). All three were filed individually but combine into a single DoS surface: (1) BodySchema.content is z.string() with NO max, so an attacker can submit a multi-MB JSON body; (2) request.json() allocates the full body BEFORE the 100KB byte-cap check at line 133; (3) no rate limiter, so an authenticated allocator can fire arbitrarily many such requests per minute. Combined, a single attacker can submit a 10MB JSON payload that the Next.js runtime fully parses (allocating ~20MB in the JS heap for the parse + string view), the route's TextEncoder allocates 10MB more for the byte-length check, and the request finally returns 400. No rate limit means the attacker can fire 60 of these per second. The Sentry-deferral pattern means there's no telemetry signal. Critical for /api/notes specifically because it's the ONLY mutating PATCH route in src/app/api/ that lacks a rate limiter (api-contract #1 cross-references this); every other route closes the loop.
- **Evidence**: src/app/api/notes/route.ts:42-46 (BodySchema, no max on content), :122-138 (parse → byte-check), no checkLimit/ratelimit import in the entire file
- **Fix**: Three-line fix: (1) `content: z.string().max(120_000)` on BodySchema so Zod rejects oversized payloads before the TextEncoder pass; (2) early `if ((request.headers.get('content-length') ?? '0') > '200000') return 413` so the body never parses; (3) `await checkLimit(notesUpsertLimiter, \`notes:${user.id}\`)` after auth gate. All three are cheap, all three close the loop on the same DoS class.

#### G22-021 · v2 page renders 404 via notFound() when getStrategyDetailV2 returns null — masks RLS/DB error vs. genuine missing
- **File**: `src/app/strategy/[id]/v2/page.tsx:48`
- **Specialist**: `silent-failure-hunter` (confidence 8)
- **Summary**: getStrategyDetailV2 returns null on EITHER (a) the strategy doesn't exist / isn't published, (b) RLS blocks the SELECT, or (c) a transient DB error (queries.ts:447 `if (error || !strategy) return null`). The page treats all three identically by calling notFound(), so an allocator who hits a transient Supabase outage sees a Next.js 404 page instead of an actionable error. The error boundary (error.tsx) only fires when the server component THROWS — not when it returns null.
- **Evidence**: src/lib/queries.ts (getStrategyDetailV2 at ~line 447), src/app/strategy/[id]/v2/page.tsx:47-48
- **Fix**: In getStrategyDetailV2, throw on DB error so the v2 error boundary catches it; return null only on the genuine no-row / status≠'published' case. Then notFound() means 'truly absent' and the error.tsx + Reload-strategy CTA fires for the transient case.

#### G22-022 · AllocatorSyncStatus `syncStatus: string | null` is a 7-state enum encoded as raw string
- **File**: `src/components/exchanges/AllocatorSyncStatus.tsx:36`
- **Specialist**: `type-design-analyzer` (confidence 8)
- **Summary**: The component handles exactly 7 statuses (idle / syncing / complete / complete_with_warnings / rate_limited / revoked / error) — documented in the JSDoc at line 35, mirrored by PILL_STYLES at line 65 (typed `Record<string, ...>` rather than `Record<SyncStatus, ...>`), and pill-label-switched in the function body at line 182. Yet the public prop type is `string | null`. A caller writing `<AllocatorSyncStatus syncStatus='synching' ...>` (typo) compiles cleanly and falls through to the silent `idle` fallback at line 175-178. The `as keyof typeof PILL_STYLES` cast at line 177 is the symptom: it papers over the unsafe widening with no runtime warning.
- **Evidence**: src/components/exchanges/AllocatorSyncStatus.tsx:34-36,65,175-178
- **Fix**: Define `export type SyncStatus = 'idle' | 'syncing' | 'complete' | 'complete_with_warnings' | 'rate_limited' | 'revoked' | 'error'` and tighten the prop to `syncStatus: SyncStatus | null` (or admit the DB legacy via `SyncStatus | 'computing' | null` since the comment says computing is forward-compat). Then PILL_STYLES becomes `Record<SyncStatus, ...>` and the exhaustiveness of the switch is checked at compile time. The forward-compat 'unknown string → idle' fallback can remain via a single typed normalizer at the entry point.

#### G22-023 · useNoteAutoSave race-drop returns void on stale generation — user can't tell save was discarded
- **File**: `src/components/notes/useNoteAutoSave.ts:83`
- **Specialist**: `silent-failure-hunter` (confidence 8)
- **Summary**: The hook's race guard drops stale responses on `generationRef.current !== gen` by returning void with no state update. That is correct for the data path, but the user never sees a signal that 'save was superseded by a newer save'. If the user blurs a field while a save is in flight, then triggers a second save with the same content (no-op), they see the 'saving → saved' state from the SECOND save only. If the second save fails, they see 'error' but have no clue the first save's payload was different. Combined with the comment 'NO unmount flush' on line 18, a user navigating away mid-save can lose data silently.
- **Evidence**: src/components/notes/useNoteAutoSave.ts:78-103
- **Fix**: At minimum, console.debug when a stale response is dropped so it's traceable. Better: surface a small 'Some changes may be unsaved — refresh to verify' hint when navigating away while saveState=='saving'.

#### G22-025 · HeadlineMetricsPanel relies on parent `key={strategy.id}` for fetch-race safety but encodes nothing in its types
- **File**: `src/components/strategy-v2/HeadlineMetricsPanel.tsx:124`
- **Specialist**: `type-design-analyzer` (confidence 8)
- **Summary**: The PR-86 F2 fix added `key={strategy.id}` on every panel that holds per-strategy client fetch state (StrategyV2Shell.tsx:81,109,119,127,134). HeadlineMetricsPanel is one of them — it fires `fetchStrategyLazyMetricsClient(strategyId, 'equity')` in `handleViewChange` and resolves into `setLogReturns` / `setLogReturnsStatus`. Unlike `useLazyPanelMetrics` (which has its own mountedRef + versionRef + isStillRelevant guards at hook level), HeadlineMetricsPanel's fetch is inline in an event handler with no mount or strategyId guard. The whole correctness rests on the parent remembering the key prop. A future component using HeadlineMetricsPanel without the key would silently leak strategy A's resolved log-returns into strategy B's panel — a regression class identical to the F2 bug the rest of the cluster fixed.
- **Evidence**: src/components/strategy-v2/HeadlineMetricsPanel.tsx:124-139 + src/components/strategy-v2/StrategyV2Shell.tsx:80-87
- **Fix**: Either (a) factor the equity fetch into a hook variant of `useLazyPanelMetrics` so the mount + version guards apply uniformly (preferred — moves the invariant into a reusable type), or (b) add an inline `mountedRef.current && strategyIdAtCall === strategyId` guard in the .then/.catch closures so the panel is self-contained. The current contract — 'parent must remember the key prop' — is invisible at the type level and the type system cannot help enforce it.

#### G22-027 · useLazyPanelMetrics error state renders generic banner, no per-panel error detail
- **File**: `src/components/strategy-v2/RollingMetricsPanel.tsx:146`

The panel renders a PartialDataBanner with the same copy regardless of error category: 'Couldn't load this section. Refresh the page to retry.' - **Fix**: Propagate the error category from the hook (e.g., distinguish 'network' / '4xx' / '5xx' / 'parse') and pick differentiated banner copy. At minimum, expose the status code so 'Sign in again' surfaces for 401/403 instead of 'refresh to retry'.

#### G22-028 · Comment-rot strip on the v2 SHELL key={strategy.id} comment is the ONLY thing keeping the maintenance trap visible — and the comment is itself a tombstone for a fixed bug · _new_ · refs: performance#4

Same treatment for the StrategyTable mirror-effect eslint-disable.

#### G22-030 · useLazyPanelMetrics A→B→A flip Test 14 only asserts the bare leak — does not verify versionRef actually increments per strategyId change
- **File**: `src/hooks/useLazyPanelMetrics.ts:42`
- **Specialist**: `pr-test-analyzer` (confidence 8)
- **Summary**: PR #86 SR-4 (versionRef monotonic counter) added Test 14 covering the A→B→A race. The test asserts `result.current.data === null` after the stale resolve, but it never directly verifies that `versionRef.current` advanced by 3 on three strategyId changes. A regression that bumps versionRef on the wrong dep (e.g. `[]` deps once, or only on mount) would still pass the assertion if mountedRef happens to swallow the stale resolve via a separate path. The fix's intent ('monotonic version counter bumped on every strategyId change') is encoded only indirectly.
- **Evidence**: src/hooks/useLazyPanelMetrics.ts:42-44 `const versionRef = useRef(0); useEffect(() => { versionRef.current += 1; }, [opts.strategyId]);` — load-bearing. Test 14 (diff line 2663) only asserts `result.current.data` is null after a flip; it never reads or proves versionRef incremented per change.
- **Fix**: Add a Test 14b that exposes versionRef indirectly: navigate strategyId abc → xyz, resolve the in-flight fetch from the abc instance, assert data is null (already done) AND fire a SECOND fetch from xyz that resolves successfully, assert data IS populated (proves the next-fetch's requestVersion matches versionRef.current). The compound guarantee is what versionRef actually delivers and what a `[]`-deps regression would break.

#### G22-031 · discovery-prefs setItem catch-block console.error logging has no test — silent regression to the original swallow-everything `catch {}` is undetectable
- **File**: `src/lib/discovery-prefs.ts:104`

- **Evidence**: grep -c 'console.error' src/lib/discovery-prefs.test.ts → 0. discovery-prefs.ts:104 `console.error('[discovery-prefs] localStorage write failed:', ...)` is load-bearing for the observability contract.

Verify the test fails when the catch reverts to `catch {}`.

#### G22-032 · discovery-prefs error logging is asymmetric — write-path got console.error in PR #90 but read-path catch still swallows silently, blocking root-cause diagnosis · _chain_ · refs: silent-failure-hunter#9, pr-test-analyzer#4
- **File**: `src/lib/discovery-prefs.ts:78`
- **Specialist**: `red-team` (confidence 8)
- **Summary**: Chain of silent-failure-hunter #9 + pr-test-analyzer #4: PR #90's 'silent .catch cleanup' added console.error to the WRITE path (line 108-111) but the symmetric READ path's empty catch at line 78-80 is unchanged. A user with corrupted localStorage (manually edited, mid-version transition, third-party browser extension touching the storage) hits the bare `catch { return DEFAULTS }` on EVERY page load. They see preferences silently reset to defaults; their saved sort/view/hide_examples vanishes with no diagnostic signal. The write path can succeed on the same session (re-persisting the defaults), so the next read also returns defaults — the user never recovers and the operator has zero telemetry. Combined with pr-test-analyzer #4 (no test for the write-path catch), the entire error-observability surface for this hook is now half-instrumented and zero-pinned. The 'Sentry-deferral pattern' justification cited in PR #90's CHANGELOG argues for console.error specifically because there's no other sink — but applying it asymmetrically is worse than not applying it at all (look at the write path, conclude the codebase IS instrumenting localStorage errors, miss the read path entirely).
- **Evidence**: src/lib/discovery-prefs.ts:46-80 (safeRead's outer try/catch) vs :104-111 (write effect's catch with console.error); discovery-prefs.test.ts has 15 tests, none of which mock a throwing storage on the READ path
- **Fix**: Mirror the write-path treatment: `} catch (err) { console.error('[discovery-prefs] read failed:', (err as Error)?.message ?? err); return DEFAULTS; }` Optionally clear the corrupted entry inside the catch so the next write is clean. Add the missing test from pr-test-analyzer#4 plus a read-path twin that stubs getItem to throw and asserts the console.error fires.

### LOW (5)

#### G22-033 · Watchlist PUT returns 500 on FK violation — combined with security #2's existence-oracle, the rate-limit bucket burns on probes · _chain_ · refs: security#2, api-contract#5, silent-failure-hunter#15
- **File**: `src/app/api/watchlist/[strategyId]/route.ts:67`
- **Specialist**: `red-team` (confidence 9)
- **Summary**: Chain of security #2 + api-contract #5 + silent-failure-hunter #15. Security #2 flagged the FK-existence oracle (200 vs 500 discloses strategy existence to UUID-probing attackers). api-contract #5 flagged the missing UUID format validation. silent-failure-hunter #15 flagged the generic error message strip. Combined: an attacker hits /api/watchlist/<random-uuid> 30 times per minute (the rate limit), 28 fail with 500 (FK violation), 2 pass with 200 (rare hit on a real strategy). The rate-limit bucket is exhausted regardless of probe success — meaning a legitimate user's TOGGLE is now competing with the probe traffic. Each 500 consumes one token; the user gets 429 after the probe drains the bucket. The 30/min limit is high enough that this isn't trivial DoS, but the bucket consumption on malformed UUIDs is wasted because no DB write happened. Add UUID format validation BEFORE the rate-limit check and the entire surface collapses.
- **Evidence**: src/app/api/watchlist/[strategyId]/route.ts:30 (raw strategyId), :42-48 (rate limit), :60-86 (DB call); rate limit consumes a token whether the strategyId is a valid UUID or not
- **Fix**: Reorder the route: (1) extract strategyId, (2) validate UUID format with regex BEFORE checkLimit, (3) return 400 on malformed input without consuming a rate-limit token. Plus security#2's strategy-visibility pre-check (404 on invisible strategy) to close the oracle. All three findings collapse to a single 5-line patch.

#### G22-034 · Watchlist PUT does not validate strategyId existence — UUID-existence oracle via FK error
- **File**: `src/app/api/watchlist/[strategyId]/route.ts:67`
- **Specialist**: `security` (confidence 9)
- **Summary**: PUT /api/watchlist/[strategyId] forwards an arbitrary URL-path UUID into a user_favorites upsert. If the strategy_id does not exist, the FK strategy_id REFERENCES strategies(id) (migration 024:31) fires a 23503 foreign_key_violation which the handler maps to a 500 'Failed to add'. If it exists, the upsert returns 200. An attacker with a valid session can probe arbitrary UUIDs and infer strategies(id) existence by 500 vs 200, even for unpublished/draft strategies the user could not otherwise see (RLS on strategies blocks SELECT but the FK check happens at the DB layer regardless of caller-visible RLS). Combined with PR rate-limit of 30/min, ~43k probes/day per user — feasible against a known-id-space.
- **Evidence**: src/app/api/watchlist/[strategyId]/route.ts:60-73
- **Fix**: Before the upsert, do a supabase.from('strategies').select('id').eq('id', strategyId).eq('status','published').maybeSingle() owner-respecting RLS check. Return 404 (not 400 — same code path as 'strategy not found' on the public factsheet) when the strategy is not visible to the caller. Alternatively, treat the unique-violation/FK-violation distinction internally and always return a generic 400 'Invalid strategy' so the timing/status oracle collapses.

#### G22-035 · StarToggle 429 test asserts wait time at >=2 attempts but does NOT verify Retry-After is honored vs. the 600ms default — a regression to a hardcoded 600ms would still pass the test
- **File**: `src/components/strategy/StarToggle.tsx:78`
- **Specialist**: `pr-test-analyzer` (confidence 9)
- **Summary**: PR #86 added a 429 test ('respects the Retry-After header on a 429') that asserts `fetchMock.toHaveBeenCalledTimes(2)` after the retry wave. The test sets Retry-After: 1 (1 second) and uses a 3000ms timeout, so the assertion would also pass if the route used a hardcoded 600ms delay (ignoring Retry-After). The Retry-After branch (route.ts line 78-87) is therefore not strictly pinned — a regression dropping the parsing of the header would NOT fail the test.
- **Evidence**: StarToggle.test.tsx line 6299-6324: `await waitFor(() => { expect(fetchMock).toHaveBeenCalledTimes(2); }, { timeout: 3000 });` — passes whether the delay is 600ms or 1000ms.
- **Fix**: Replace the loose timeout assertion with a vitest fake-timer: `vi.useFakeTimers();` after the first 429, advance by 599ms, assert fetchMock still called only once; advance by 1ms more (total 600ms), assert still 1 (Retry-After: 1 means 1000ms not 600ms); advance by 401ms more (total 1000ms), assert fetchMock called 2 times. Verify the test fails when the route's `first.retryAfterMs ?? DEFAULT_RETRY_DELAY_MS` reverts to a hardcoded 600.

#### G22-036 · discovery-prefs JSON.parse failure silently returns DEFAULTS — no log signal
- **File**: `src/lib/discovery-prefs.ts:78`
- **Specialist**: `silent-failure-hunter` (confidence 9)
- **Summary**: safeRead's outer try/catch (line 78) returns DEFAULTS on any throw — JSON.parse failure on corrupted localStorage, or any other unexpected throw. The PR #90 cleanup added a console.error for localStorage WRITE failures, but the READ path's empty catch is unchanged. A user with a corrupted entry will silently get DEFAULTS on every visit and never know why their saved preferences keep resetting.
- **Evidence**: src/lib/discovery-prefs.ts:78-80
- **Fix**: Add `console.error('[discovery-prefs] read failed:', err)` to the catch block, mirroring the PR #90 write-path treatment. Optionally clear the corrupted entry so the next write is clean.

#### G22-037 · strategy-ui-v2-flag localStorage read swallows error — returns default true with no signal
- **File**: `src/lib/strategy-ui-v2-flag.ts (PR #87 baseline; file later deleted):265`
- **Specialist**: `silent-failure-hunter` (confidence 9)
- **Summary**: The catch block returns `true` (default-ON) on any localStorage throw — Safari private-mode getItem, security-policy block, etc. The norm-comparison branch was added in v0.17.1 to honor user intent on case variants, but the surrounding try/catch still hides every read failure. A user whose browser blocks localStorage hits the default-ON branch and CANNOT opt out via the persistent flag. No console signal indicates this.
- **Evidence**: src/lib/strategy-ui-v2-flag.ts:265-267 (PR #87 / 0.17.1.2 file state; subsequently removed from main)
- **Fix**: In the catch, console.warn '[strategy-ui-v2-flag] localStorage read failed:' with err.message before defaulting. Note: file appears to have been deleted in a later PR — if it's gone from main, this finding is informational only.
